# Chapter 01 Arrival


## 2nd day of the 2nd tenday of Taraskh, 1492


The Underdark, the hidden realm beneath the surface of Toril, is not a welcoming place, even in the best of times. 


It was certainly not welcoming in 1492, two years after the War of the Dragons ended and only a year after the War of the Giants. 


The events that started with the subversion of the Cult of the Dragon and ended with the re-establishment of the Ordning of the Giants were well and truly over. 


New adventurers, however, still tried to ply their trade. And there was always a need for someone to deal with a problem or two. 


And if you can’t find adventure above ground, there is always below ground. 


Or at least that’s what the half-orc Gyrgum thought to himself as he sat in a prison cell - again. 


At least this time, he wasn’t alone; there was Daz, the Drow Elf Magic User, Thorin Giantfriend, whose experience with giants was radically different than his, and the very quiet Zalthir, a dragonborn monk. 


The adventure had been going so well. They had this cave to explore, and there was some gadget they were supposed to get, and then - boom, they fell down a chute. And even then, it wasn’t so bad because they were a group of heroic adventurers, and Bahamut had his back. 


Except this time, there was a bigger mission at play. 


A group of Drows found them unconscious in the chute. When they woke up, they were without weapons or armor and being led deeper into the Underdark. 


“Menzoberranzan is our final destination,” remarked Daz. 


“Is that good?” asked Thorin. 


Daz shook his head. Daz explained that the City of Menzoberranzan was a city where the Cult of Lloth was very powerful, and enslaved people didn’t have a very long and healthy life. Drow who were apostates tended to have an even shorter life than other slaves. And apostates that were male Drow Elves, the shortest-lived of all. 


Gyrgum sighed and thought, “Not again.” 


The journey through the Underdark took two, or was it three days? With no sunlight to guide them, the only things that gave him a sense of time were the long periods of rest and the feeling of exhaustion at the end of the day. 


“You will be dropped off here,” said Welnaste Mizzrym, the caravan leader. “This is Velkynvelve. I have secured a reasonable price for you. Another caravan will come to pick you up in a ten day or so to take you to Menzoberranzan.” 

Grygum looks up and sees Velkynvelve. It's a Drow outpost high in a cavern 100 feet above the rocky floor. The outpost consists of small caves in the cavern walls and four hanging towers. These are hollowed-out stalactites connected by walkways, stairs, and rope bridges. The towers are concealed by the thick webs of giant spiders that stretch below them, so only the lowermost parts of the stalactites are visible from the cavern floor. 


As they climb up, he notes that the small amount of dim light used in the outpost, shielded from the cavern floor below, allows one to walk the entire length of the cleft without becoming aware of the outpost overhead, hidden in the darkness above the ranges of torches and lanterns. 


Daz points out, “There are giant spiders. If someone should arrive in this cavern, they can lower themselves and attack from above. Drow soldiers probably have stockpiles of spider silk that they will use as a rope to drop down as well.” 


At the main entrance to the outpost, Welnaste shouts, “Ilvara, I have the shipment.” 


Ilvara steps forward. She is a haughty, arrogant, well-dressed, and coiffed female drow cleric. Daz snorts, “fits the type.” 


Next to her is another cleric and two male drow fighters. One of them has a disfigured face and is missing two fingers. 


Ilvara turns to the disfigured Drow: “Jorlan, take them to the cell. We will use them until the caravan arrives.” 


Welnaste looks at Ilvara and mutters, “Remember, house sister, money has been exchanged, and you will be held to account if they are lost or die before the caravan arrives.” 


Grygum then is made aware of Drow soldiers surrounding the group and putting bags over his friend's head. Before he can protest, a bag is placed over his. 


### Zalthir


The dragonborn had taken a vow of silence. Not so much about not speaking but only speaking if he had something to say. And right now, he wasn’t quite sure what to say. 
Looking around, he saw ten fellow prisoners - a fish man, a mushroom with legs, two deep gnomes that looked like twins, a deep gnome that didn’t, a derro, a hulking quagoth, a half-orc, another drow that was covered in some kind of fungal rot, and a dwarf. 


He was carefully considering what to do next and how to get information about his cellmates when Grygum decided to ask. 


“How novel?” he thought. 


“I am Topsy, and this is my brother, Turvy; we’re twins.” 


Turvy mumbles. 


“He says a pleasure to meet you too, Grygum. And I am pleased as well. By the way, everyone is looking at the other Drow.” 


Zalthir had noticed the stares and wondered why. Again, he thought to ask, but the deep gnome just gave away information—“They’re all wondering if you are like Sareth. Sareth was convicted of the murder of one of his fellow drow. The problem is he got caught.” 


Sarith reacts to that comment - “I didn’t! It was a setup! Or was it? Maybe I did do it. Maybe they’ve imprisoned me and are gonna send me to Menzo to be sacrificed or turned into a DRIDER!” 
![image]()


Zathir notes Daz’s shudder and can read his body language; Sarith is not sane. 


Grygum approaches Zarith and mutters, “And he’s not a spy. He’s a prisoner just like us.” 
### 
Thorin


“A fellow dwarf! We must plan our escape,” says the other dwarven prisoner. 


![image]()


Thorin is delighted to meet one of his kind but speaks with an unmistakable Giant accent. Eldeth is taken aback when he hears of his story. She explains that she’s not quite sure what to do. The war of the Giants has devasted the world above, and she’s not one of those who believes that Giants can make peace with what they call the “little folk.” 


“But here is an example of such a possibility.” 


The derro, intently staring at Thorin, finally speaks in a thin, raspy voice. Eldeht scowls at his intrusion, muttering something about Derro’s being some kind of dwarven perversion. 


Conversely, the derro looks personable, gregarious, and talkative. He introduces himself as Buppido. 


“We must escape from this place. It is part of the divine plan.” 


Grygum intrudes, “Divine plan? Yes, it involves many dragons.” 


Buppido smiles, “You are a cleric and a follower of gods. In the future, perhaps, we will work together. And shortly, perhaps, we will work together to escape. For I know that the divine plan tells us, there is only one path forward!” 


Eldeth tries to avoid rolling her eyes, but Thorin catches her. 


### Daz 


“I have not seen a Kuo-Toan in a long while. They are a curious race of fish-people who were corrupted by the mind flayers. They can create gods from the power of their imaginations. Dangerous and very mad. I must be careful as I speak to them.” 


Zalthir steps before him, sensing that the Kuo-Toan is a monk. 


The fish man speaks soothingly and introduces himself as Shuushar the Awakened. 


“I have found enlightenment.” 


Buppido coughs, “He’s a Kuo-Toan; they always go mad.” 


“My people indeed go mad, but I have found a way to stop that. I was on my way to my Sloobludop near the Darklake. I have navigated those winding roads for years and can surely find my way back.” 


Daz wonders if they can rely on this person to escape. He seems sane, but he is a Kuo-Toan. 


The Drow mage has been trying hard not to be noticed by the Quaggoth. The Drow Nobles of Menzoberranzan have taken an interest in recruiting and training the creatures, encouraging their ferocity while strengthening their obedience. Such a creature, here, is very odd. It could tear them all apart without thinking. 


“So why hasn’t it?” 


Suddenly, the creature speaks with a rarefied accent, typically heard only among the upper kingdom's most powerful elves. 
This shocks Daz, for the Quaggoth were hunted to extinction by the surface elves. The other reason the Drow use them as troops is because they hate surface-dwelling elves almost as much as the followers of Lloth.  


“I am Prince Derendil of the Kingdom of Nelrindenvane in the High Forest. My crown was usurped by the evil wizard Terrestor, who trapped me in this form and exiled me from my people. I would be much obliged if you treated me with the respect my station commands.” 


Daz knows in an instant that Prince Derendil is a liar. He traveled through the High Forest, but no Kingdom of Nelrindenvane existed. He thinks about confronting the fake Prince, but then he thinks that the Fake Prince may be a useful ally as they try to escape. 


Just then, the mushroom speaks, “I am stool. I am a member of the circle! My circle is called the Neverlight Grove.” 


Daz stares at him, uncertain of what he is—and surprised to see a mushroom with legs that talks. 


He is repulsed but can tell this is a child of whatever species it belongs to. 


### Grygum 


“A fellow orc,” he thinks. 


The orc introduces himself as Ronc and is disappointed when he discovers that Grygum is a cleric but not Gruumsh. Ronc had fought poorly and was looking for absolution from his god. 


Eldeth sneers at him and mocks him - “You and your kind were defeated at Gauntlygrym. The Shield Dwarves captured their castle, and we will keep it from your kind.” 


Grygum sighs. The dwarves can be so bigoted. 


“We should go there, to Gauntlygrym. It’s the best place for us to escape!” 


Just then, the other deep gnome speaks, “Wanna bet?” 


Buppido sighs, “Not that again. He keeps bEttin g every day on anything.” 


“You won’t take my bets on your divine plan.” 


“We never bet on the divine plan that would sully the plan.” 


Topsy shouts, “That’s Jimjar, always pretending he’s better than us. He’s from our town, you know.” 
Turvy mumbles something to her; she pauses and then shouts, “We should go to Blingdestone!” 


Jimjar smiles and says, “I’ll make you bet nobody agrees to go there.” 


Eldeth then turns to Grygum, “The mushroom is a Myconid. A conscious form of mycelium.” 


“Yes, I am a Myconid. And my sovereign is mighty. And he will be thrilled to see me. And I can get you to the Neverlight grove! And it will be safe.” 


Grygum hears no sounds and is about to ask how he heard that when Bupido explains, “They release these spores that allow them to communicate without speaking.” 


### Thorin 


He approaches the door, “We can so break this door down.” 


Daz looks at it and says, “I have a better plan.” He prepares to cast a spell when Eldeth shouts, “The room will not allow you to cast magic. It’s pointless to try.” 


“So break it is.” 


Eldeth turns to Thorin, “I like your spunk. And it’s a good look. But there are nine drows, a bunch of Quaggoths, and who knows how many giant spiders there are?” 


The “Prince” adds, “And there are three Drow guards right across the door.” 


Grygum turns to Thorin, “Maybe we rethink the charge at a pack of drow with no weapons a little more?”


Buppido then whispers, “Let’s send Runc ahead. He can distract them, and the rest of us can escape.” 


Thorin asks, “Why don’t you do it?” 


“I am more of a big-picture thinker. And frankly, if I reveal my power, then …” 


Grygum is frustrated, “Time to do the big reveal?”


“No.” 


Thorin gets frustrated when Jimjar starts speaking, “Oh man, the Drow polycules are such a mess.” 


The group stares at him. 


“The Drow with the ugly scratch marks on his face, Jorlans is his name, used to be the number one squeeze, but now Shoor is the primary squeeze after Jorlan got injured. Jorlan used to have a wand of globs. Meanwhile, Ashar’s angling for the top job.”


Serith, seeing how Jimjar has become the center of attention, shouts, “I too have information.” He starts to speak and then begins to mutter. Thorinth then watches as Grygum reassures the Drow, who explains, “At the bottom of the cave is a gray ooze in the pools. If we escape that way, we have to be careful.” 
# Chapter 02 Exploring the prison


## 3rd day of the 2nd tenday of Taraskh, 1492
### Gyrgum


The prison door creeks open, and a voice rings, “Wake up.” 


Gyrgum opens his eyes. “How much time has passed?” he wonders. From his time as a prisoner the last time, he’s learned not to worry about how much time has passed. 


The voice speaks in undercommon—a language Gyrgum doesn’t understand. 


But he can gather from the gestures that Ront and Prince Derendil, the deluded Quaggoth, are to follow this Drow. 


He is worried. The Kuo-Toan Suushar the Awakened notices and tells him to relax, “These are daily chores, nothing more. The Drow who took them is Beremil. They will be carrying water.” 


The next Drow appears and points to Zalthir, Buppido, Jimjar, and Eldeth. 


“Balok runs the winch. They will be helping with loading and unloading of cargo.” 


Another Drow points at Daz, Sarith, and Stool. Daz has a very sour expression. 


“Oh dear, Guldor has the dirty job of cleaning chamber pots. I wonder what he failed at.” 


Then, at last, it’s Gyrgum’s turn. A Drow appears and points at Suushar, Topsy, Turvy, and Gyrgum. Suushar smiles, or his mouth spreads in a way that might be a smile, “Excellent, Imbros wants us to cook.” 


## ![image]()
### Zalthir


The first thing that Zalthir noticed was that the Drow outpost was 100’ in the sky. A direct drop would be suicidal. Perhaps if we has a more powerful monk, he could fall safely, but he is not. 


He looks a little bit more carefully and notices a spider web. Below the spider’s web, he notices a pool of water. 


That looks more promising. 


Across from his prison cell is a stalactite. There is a door, and two very bored Drow are past the door. 


He could easily sneak past them, “But to where?” 


Jimjar, next to him, mutters, “Wanna bet on who would die first when we splat on the ground?” 


As he crosses the bridge near the waterfall, he watches the “Prince,” Ront, and Thorin filling buckets of water. 


Jimjar turns to anyone, “Wanna get some action on how many buckets will be filled?” 


They march on until they see the basket. 


Attached to the edge of the barracks platform is a winch-and-basket device consisting of a giant swinging arm that carries a thin cord of strong spider silk. The cord runs through several pulleys from a hand-cranked horizontal spool to a heavy woven basket suspended at the end. The basket is kept up on the platform except when it is in use.


Balok shouts, “Stop.” 


He turns to his new slaves and points to the apparatus: “You will clean and unload. If you steal anything, then there will be consequences.” 


Jimjar again tries to make a bet, “Wanna bet on how many people will come up? How many will come down?” 


The other prisoners, familiar with the chores, pick up the rags and clean the basket. 


Two quaggoth attendants remain by the lift, waiting for a signal from below to lower the basket. 


As the four prisoners enter the basket, Balok pulls a stopper, and the basket flies over the chasm. 


The two quahogs let it drop. The other prisoners are startled but seem to have been expecting this. 


Balok is laughing. 


Jimjar shouts, “Wanna get in on some juicy action on how many times they’ll do this?” 


As the basket bounces, Zalthir notices a piece of paper with some names of people who owe a favor to the person who has the paper. It’s unclear where, which city, what favor, and why. But he pockets the paper. 


He notices that Elspeth sees him pocket the paper. He notices that she finds a comb. She pockets the comb. He has little use for combs. 


As the basket comes up, he notices Grygum entering a cave. 
### Gyrgum 
. 
As Grygum walks towards the mess hall, the orc thinks, “Not speaking undercommon is awkward, but then again, understanding the language of your captors may be a problem. And anyway, I’ve got plenty of folks around me who can translate.” 


Just before the mess hall door, he can hear Balok laughing as a basket appears to bob up and down. 


He sighs and walks into the hall. The cave serves as a gathering and eating place for the drow warriors of the outpost. It has four circular tables carved from zurkhwood, each surrounded by five chairs. Part of the hall is used as a food preparation and storage area, containing stocks of dried and fresh fungi, dried fruits, cheeses, preserved meat, and a few clay jars of spices. A heavy iron brazier provides cooking heat and dim light, but much of the food is served cold.


There are a pair of Drow sitting at a table, looking hungry. Suushar mutters: “Jaezred and Kalannar”


Guldor sits with them. 


Topsy and Turvy whisper to each other. Suushar turns to Grygum, “The twins wonder if you could create a distraction by talking to the drow while they steal some food?” 


“I don’t speak undercommon.” 


Suushar mutters, “I see.” 


The drow speaks, and Suushar turns to Grygum, “Can you cook? That would be a better distraction.” 


The drow laughs and says something. 


Suushar translates, “Something tasty.” 


“I don’t speak undercommon, but he used many more words.” 


“Yes. As part of my attempt to find spiritual balance and cope with the madness of my race, I have chosen not to repeat offensive words.” And then Suushar proceeds to translate every insult the drow used. 


Grygum smiles at the Drow, “Yes, I am the inferior race.” 


He then turns to the kitchen, looks around, and realizes that he’s not a great cook and that many ingredients are unfamiliar, but he can put on a great show. 


And it's a great show he does. 


As the lunch progresses, Grygum notices a knife and tries to steal it. Guldor notices and Grygum explains that he is just trying to sharpen the knife. Guldor takes the knife and says a bunch of words whose intent is quite clear. 


Suushar translates, “They will do awful things to you if you steal a  knife.” 


Grygum again realizes that Suushar has left out many details. 


### Thorin


Thorin is standing on the other side of the bridge south of the prison cell. He looks down at his feet and sees buckets and a slippery path leading to the head of the waterfall. 


He notices that if he were to jump into the waterfall, he could quite easily land safely into the pool of water below. 


Beremil shouts, “Fill the buckets and then come.” 


As he fills his bucket, he notices Zalthir walking by. 


Beremil then shouts, “Now, we take water to Ilvara.” 


Thorin recalls how Ilvara was in charge when they first arrived here. 


Prince Derendeil mutters, “ I remember how she greeted me when I arrived. She was robed in silken garments and flanked by two male drow, one of whom had a mass of scars along one side of his face and neck. Mistress Ilvara liked to impress her will with a scourge in hand and remind her slaves that our lives now belong to her. Every time, she would end her pep talks with the phrase - ‘Accept your fate, learn to obey, and you may survive.’”


Water in tow, Ronk, Thorin, and Prince Derendeil enter the uppermost level of the largest hanging tower, called the priestess’s tower. Dark silken mats cover the floor of this circular chamber with a pale web-strand pattern woven through them in silvery thread. In the middle of the chamber (at the center of the web) stands a broad pedestal carved from zurkhwood, with a 10-foot-high sculpted spider at its head. 


This place is a shrine to Lolth, the drow’s spider goddess. The altar is flanked by a pair of heavy silver candlesticks worth 25 gp each. They hold thick black candles and are unlit. 


The eight “eyes” of the spider statue are eight pieces of polished jet — four small ones worth five gp each and four larger ones worth ten gp each.


“Something for later.” 


A rope ladder leads down from the shrine into this chamber.


Ilvara is there. She smiles and has her scourge handy as she flicks it toward her prisoners.  “This is my quarters. I am the high priestess of Lloth and commander. Do not spill any water, do not touch anything, and fill my bath.”  


Inside, the walls are hung with black mesh resembling a spider’s web, extending from a central spot on the ceiling to the walls, then draped down like curtains. Thick, woven mats cover the floor, while a low platform is covered with cushions and pillows to make a broad, divan-like bed. One side of the chamber contains a small table and two chairs, while the other holds a small shrine to Lolth draped in white silk. A heavy chest of black-stained zurkhwood sits at the foot of the bed.


As Thorin stares at Ilvara some more, he realizes there is something manic about her. As a dwarf, even one raised by Giants, he knows that Drow is calculating and cold, not mad. And this one looks a bit crazy.


To prove the point, when Prince Derendil objects to being a chamber enslaved person, Ilvara pulls a knife and points at him and explains in excruciating detail how she will treat him if he doesn’t bring the water. 


### Daz


Daz and his crew collect the chamber pots from each tower. Guldur explains that they collect the filth from each tower in a bucket and then take the bucket to the lake, where they dispose of it and clean the filth. 


Their first stop is at the cave to the north, which they notice is a quaggoth barracks. Peeking in, Daz notes one of them resting. 


The next stop is the tower of the high priestess. There, Daz notes that Thorin has a better job.


Finally, he arrives at the winch. Goldur informs Daz that he will be down before they can run if they try any funny business. Daz notices Zalrith and thinks the monk will have some unpleasant fun cleaning up after he comes up. 


Daz, Stool, and Serith walk to the edge of the lake and notice that it is pretty clean, which is odd given the amount of filth being deposited. They look around and see nothing. 


Later that day, Daz is back in the prison cell, surrounded by his fellow prisoners. Jimjar is making more bets. The stool is happy to be talking to everyone and has spread his spores so that everyone in the prison cell is in a group mind. 


Daz notes that this allows them to coordinate any plans without being discovered. 


Topsy and Turvy are very excited about Gyrgum’s cooking. Even Suushar seems excited, although he cautions the orc, “If you were to show this cooking to my people, they might imagine a god like you.” 


It’s then that Buppido speaks, or instead projects his mind, “The Divine plan says we must collaborate and share information.” 


Gyrgum has a peculiar expression as Buppido says the word divine. Later, Daz learns from the cleric that Buppido thinks he is some kind of god, or he is a god. 


After sharing the information, Buppido says, “The divine plan requires that you create a distraction while I escape.”


Thorin corrects him, “We escape?” 


Buppido looks surprised, “We?”


Thorin, who also picked up on the derro’s insanity, says, “Well, how else will we protect you so that you can fulfill the divine plan?” 


The derro stares at Gyrgum and says, “You are quite right. You have pledged your swords and your spells! And your lives.” 


Daz thinks, “At least we have that.” 


Daz asks, “What is the plan?” 


Bupiddo, like any mysterious god or charlatan masquerading as a god, would say, “In due time.” 


## 4th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh
### Gyrgum
The next day, Gyrgum goes to the kitchen again. This time, six Drow soldiers are present. 


Suushar explains that they heard about his fantastic show and wanted to experience it themselves.


The orc is pleased but wonders how to steal a knife. Topsy and Turvy look at him and wink. Seeing how they successfully stole food, he guesses they might be better placed to steal a knife. 


As Gyrgum, with theatrical flair, tosses ingredients into the air, moves like a dancer, and hums a tune, Topsy and Turvy steal several knives. 


The drow soldiers, delighted at this entertainment, ignore the two deep gnomes who make off with a knife. 


### Zalthir


 The dragonborn monk is once again detailed to the winch. And he again has to clean the mess that Daz, Stool, and Sarith create.


This time, though, he uses the cleaning to examine how he can damage the winch to aid their escape. 


The two things that attract his attention are using spider silk to hold the basket and the winch and gears that the spider silk goes through. 


Daz had remarked that he could use his cantrip to turn water into ice, and such an effect could break the gears. 


“But I breathe fire, and fire breathing is a simpler way to cut a rope…” 


He takes a small piece of rope to test its resistance later. 


### Thorin


Stool once again releases spores, and once again, everyone is talking. Thorin remembers all these free-for-all conversations when he was younger. Everyone was talking over everyone, everyone was shouting, and everyone was not listening. 


As he waits for the food to arrive, he is surprised to see a member of Ilvara’s polycule bring it. 


Sethir says, “That’s Jorlan. He used to be the number one, but after he got hit with acid, his face was disfigured and he lost a finger, Ilvara’s dropped him, and now Shoor is number one.” 


Jorlan turns to Thorin, “If I made it possible for you to escape, would you try?” 


Thorin connected to his friends via the spores and asked, “How do we know that he isn’t here to entrap us?” 


Prince Derendeil explains, “Well we know that there is no abolitionist movement amongst those who worship Lloth. It has to be for his benefit.” 


Jorlan senses the hesitation, “I don’t care if you succeed. I just want you to try. It will make Shoor look ridiculous, and make Ilvara realize what a terrible mistake she’s made. And if you do make a mistake, she’ll be embarrassed and need my help to find you and realize what a mistake she made.” 
Thorin is satisfied. “What’s the plan?” 


Jorlan smiles, “I can sense you don’t trust me. You are wise not to trust me.” He bends closer, “I will leave the door to the prison open, create a distraction. The path to the armory will be unguarded. Grab the weapons and flee.” 


“Where to and how?” 


“Must I explain everything to you? Use the waterfall to slide down, or jump into the spiderwebs and then jump into the pools of water.” 


“And then where?” 


Buppido smiles, “To Gracklestugh, my homeland!” 


Stool objects, “No to the great circle! My people!” 


Topsy says, “We should go to Blindengstone. I know there is a way out of the Underdark from there.” 


Suushar objects, “Yes, but the direct path is through Menzoberranzan. We will have to go to Darklake first, and we must visit my people to share the enlightenment! From there, the path is good.” 


Jimjar adds, “Who wants to bet on which path the new guys will want to go? Will they go with the myconid kid? The enlightened kuo-toan? The Destiny Weilding Derro? Or trust the two deep gnomes?” 


Zulthir asks, “We have no money; how do we pay our debts?” 


“Oh, don’t worry, I have perfect recall. Just make your wager, and when you have money, I’ll collect.” 


 Sarith nods. 


Zulthir says, “You seem to be confident we will escape and live.” 


“Wanna bet?” 


Gyrgum asks, “Where will we find safety?” 


Eldeth laughs, “Safety? This is the Underdark.  There is not enough resources or space for anyone. Survival depends on your wits. People tend to distrust outsiders and view them as a resource to be used.” 
Thorin thinks for a moment, “I know where our stuff is. It’s in the chest in Ilvara’s room. The Drow leader probably keeps all the loot for herself. And if any other Drow had our stuff, they would taunt us.” 


The dwarf turns to the Drow and says, “Your deal is accepted. When?” 


“After a long rest, before you go on your assigned tasks.”


## Dreams
Everyone’s sleep in the slave pen is troubled and fitful, filled with strange dreams and disturbing images. Dark shadows seem to move and reach out toward them as the characters wander lost through endless mazes of tunnels. Oily tentacles slide to brush up against them while a great buzzing and howling rises in the distance. Suppurating wounds burst open in clouds of spores or crawling masses of maggots or insects. At least one or more of the prisoners wakes in a cold sweat from these nightmares after every rest, feeling as though something is out there in the dark depths — something far worse than the drow.


Daz wakes up and remembers, “Right, Sethir said there is a grey ooze in the pool. That’s how the waste gets processed.” 


# Chapter 03 Stealing weapons
## 
4th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh 1493
Stool, the myconid, releases his rapport spores. 


Then, everyone starts talking in each other’s heads. At first, the experience is disorienting and debilitating. Slowly, everyone learns to focus on who they want to talk to. For the most part, there is privacy, but there is no guarantee that someone won’t accidentally overhear a conversation.


Zalthir peeks outside and observes that it’s very dark. Fortunately, he has Darkvision. He plans to sneak into the tower, then quickly climb up to the top floor, arm himself, and bring whatever weapons he can carry back to the prisoners, who can then use the arms to attack. For backup, he’s relying on Daz. 


Like the great Sage Vof Klownits described in his opus, an opus that Zalthir never read, “No plan survives encounter with the enemy.” 


Zalthir trips. Daz is startled and tries to help Zalthir, kicks the goblet that Zalthir tripped on. The goblet shatters. 


The guards turn towards Zalthir and Daz.


Daz shouts in Thorin’s brain, “Plan B.” 


Thorin shouts back, “What is Plan B?” 


Zalthir mumbles, “Get in here and help us?” 


Thorin rushes into the small chamber, climbing over a sprawled Zalthir and Daz. The chamber has two Drow guards and one of the more elite Drow male fighters. It contains a zurkhwood table and three chairs, a smaller side table, and spider-silk webbing set with hooks for hanging equipment. The table is set with the Drow game Sava. 


He tries to overpower the elite warrior, whom Serith identified as Imbros but fails.


Imbros is, in turn, amused by the turn of events and is tempted to kill Thorin but chooses not. A prisoner revolt is not something new, and killing prisoners is a very costly business. So he tries to subdue the dwarf and knock him unconscious. 


Zalthir stands up and tries to shove Imbros as well, and Imbros, trained in Menzoberranzan from a very young age, deftly dodges the attack. Or so Imbros would choose to believe. Zalthir, who has spent several days in captivity, tried to go to for a classic opening move but forgot to position his hand, and instead of pushing Imbros, he caressed him. 
The rest of the prisoners, led by Bupido, take advantage of the distraction, rush into the chamber, and scramble into the armory. The Drow warriors are unable to react. 


Prince Derendil declares, “I am already armed in this hideous form, and it would bring me great joy to kill this drow.” He then charges at Imbros. 


Gyrgum decides that an armed cleric is better than a disarmed cleric and follows his fellow prisoners to the armory.


Imbros realizes that this revolt has become much more dangerous. He strikes Thorin, who falls, bleeding and unconscious. 


Daz focuses his mind on Imbros and speaks the incantation of Mind Sliver, but the Drow is unaffected. 


Seeing Imbros boxed in by the Prince, Zalthir tries to strike one of the two drow guards with his unarmed fists. His fists land ineffectively. 


Just then, an armed Serith comes down and attacks the same guard that Zalthir flailed at. As the Serith strikes his erstwhile comrade, he curses him in a unique way that makes the Drow curse each other. 


Then, from the opening in the roof where the armory is, Eldeth, Bupido, Shuushar, Jimjar, Topsy, and Turvy attack using hand-held crossbows. Eldeth and Topsy hit the remaining Drow guard. Ront, who prefers a straight-up fight, squeezes into the fight and strikes at the guard, killing him. Suushar aims at Imbros and hits. Buppido and Jimjar miss. 


“You should have taken that bet,” everyone hears Jimjar say. The Deep Gnome has mastered Spool’s telepathy and forces everyone to listen to him. 


Grygum descends from the armory and walks towards Thorin. Grygum stands over the dwarf, and then, with a moment’s incantation and a gentle touch, bloodless flesh becomes rosy, gashes close, and broken bones knit instantly with a rush of magical healing. Flush with renewed vigor, the formerly injured Thorin is ready to face the world once more.


Daz has recovered from the disastrous opening gambit and remembers how magic missiles work. It’s not one dart, but three darts. 


Imbros reels from the magical attack.  


Realizing that fighting unarmed against Imbros is foolhardy, Thorin slips out of range of the Drow, climbs upstairs, and puts on some armor. 


Imbros now realizes he’s fighting for his life and realizes that if he doesn’t stop these slaves, Ilvara might decide his fate should be precisely like Serith’s. He’s tempted to call for help and remembers what happened to Drow, who failed. “No, better to deal with this on my own.”


Imbros strikes Prince Derendil twice; this time, he uses the Drow Poison. Prince Derendil is injured, and the poison stings. 


Zalthir again tries to strike Imbros and misses. 


The fellow escapees armed with hand crossbows fire at Imbros, who is struck three times. 


Imbros is still standing. 


Grygum points his finger at Imbros, and the dolorous sound of a bell fills the room. Imbros, for a moment, feels the necrotic power consume him but rejects the spell’s powers. 


Daz strikes with three more magic missiles. Imbros looks battered and barely alive, but he is still snarling. 


And an injured Drow is still a deadly Drow. Prince Derendil’s journey ends with being stabbed to death by Imbros. 


Serith suddenly goes mad. He is about to start screaming at the top of his lungs. For some reason, this death affected him deeply. 


Grygum notices and reaches into Serith’s mind to tell Serith to focus on his spirituality and how much better things will be if he chooses to focus his rage on the divine rather than on the material. 


Serith is confused and calmed. 


Grygum smiles. The lessons of his cult have served him well.


And Serith smiles, too, when his sword cuts Imbros down. 


The fight took less than a minute. And the victory was far from certain. And one of their fellow prisoners had died. But they had weapons. And they were in a better place now than they were before. 
# Chapter 04 Escape 
## 4th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh 1493


The body of the dead drow litter the floor. The large corpse of the deluded Prince Derendil stands as a silent monument to the price of the victory. 


Zalthir shows no sentimentality and quickly scours the bodies for any weapons. The rest of the former prisoners do as well. 


Sarith arms himself with studded leather armor, picks up a shield, and places one of the hand crossbows in a strap on the armor. Equipped with the Drow weapons, he looks every part of the warrior caste of the Cult of Lolth. 


Grygum finds some poisoned hand crossbow bolts and a vial of what Serith explains is Drow poison. He hooks them into a loop on his armor. 


Daz stares mournfully at the armor and mutters, “I will not be wearing armor.” 


Thorin opens the door to the guard room, peaks outside, examines the area past the rope bridge where Ilvara’s residence is, and mutters, “We need to get our stuff.” 


The prisoners debate the relative merits of securing their stuff or escaping. Should they escape and risk not having their weapons and gear and face the elements while they travel the Underdark, or should they risk their lives and freedom now? 


Daz feels a thunderous drone, a discordant, raw hum that sets his teeth chattering.  He pokes his head and looks and sees four black, bloated flies. He can see these massive and terrible things, larger than a pony. Barbed legs dangle from their bulbous forms while their elephantine proboscis probes are hungrily forward.


For a moment, he worries that they are looking at him with their multifaceted eyes and breathes a sigh of relief. They are fixated on two other creatures. He wonders what they are, and Just then, a blood-curdling screech pierces the air. He looks at the source and sees a creature with stretched-out feathered wings attached to a back covered in fur, calling out with its jagged beak


Daz knows these monsters and is surprised. So many demons in one place is very odd. He turns to his fellow prisoners, “Demons: four chasme and two vrock.” 


Topsy and Turvy look around and shout, “We could get your stuff  for you for a price.” 


Zalthir stares, “How?” 


Thorin looks at his Drow weapons and decides that leaving everything behind is good. A good, fresh start. He shouts, “Nah, let’s take advantage of the distraction.”


Grygum agrees. He remembers when some Giants’ prisoners tried to steal goods from them instead of escaping, and the prisoners made a good meal. 
![image]()
Topsy and Turvy sigh and then transform into rats. 


Zalthir grabs some silk ropes on the pegs and prepares to drop down into the spidery web below. Buppido clicks his tongue and points out that there are spiders—very large spiders. 


He sighs, “So do we run, or do we first burn the place down?” 


Sarith, who seems to be overcome with bouts of madness, mutters, “The faster we get out of here, the better. Ilvara will be honor bound to pursue us. And let’s not give her more motivation. But -,” and he cackles, “revenge is so tasty.” 


With that, the prisoners decided that escaping now was the best option. So they rushed from the tower to the waterfall and slid down, landing in the water. 


Although aware of a gray ooze, the creature is invisible until it strikes. And strikes it does, landing a pseudopod with a crushing blow on Thorin. 


Above, the demons are fighting amongst themselves and the Drow. On the cavern floor, Grygum takes stock of the options. To the north is Menzoberranzan, a city full of Drow Cultists. Going south to Blingdenston would require going through the pitched battle between Drow and Demons. He sees Topsy and Turvy transform back into gnomes and head down the passage that leads to the Darklake. 


Grygum silently shares his thoughts with his friends and the other prisoners. They all agree, disengage from the ooze, and run towards the tunnel to the Darklake. 


Even Thorin, tempted to smash the creature with his sword, decides it’s not worth it and rushes off. 


The grey ooze thrashes in the water behind them, extending pseudo pods into the air, and then settles down. 


As Daz crosses the cavern floor to the tunnel, an injured vrock lands on the ground. From this close, Daz notices its abnormally long arms, dense with lean muscle, that end in raptor-like claws, scraping the ground. The creature extends its wings, feathered wings out and then back. 


Although excited about the opportunity to study a vrock up close, Daz is more interested in escaping with his life and flees before the creature can strike him down. 


Every other prisoner does the same, except for Ront. Ront is still angry at his cowardice. He still feels that he must prove something. And killing a vrock would redeem him. His first blow cuts through the creature's hide and the gangrenous blood-like substance that oozes out gives Ront hope that he has killed the monster. But he hasn’t. The demon, with startling speed, kills him with one taloned hand, then grabs the lifeless body with the other while it’s beak envelops the head and snaps it off. 


Daz watches as the creature swallows the head and then flies off. A few moments later, as he makes it to the safety of the cave, he hears the thud of the now headless body land on the ground behind him. 


The escapees are now feeling safe in the tunnels of the Underdark. 


Although Jimjar disrupts their feelings of safety, “Anyone wants to make a bet about how many of us will die before any of us escape?” 


Buppido laughs, “The divine plan says I will make it Gracklstugh.” 


Jimjar stares at him, “Put your money where your mouth is?” 


“Yes.” And a wager is made. 


Daz turns to the group, “Anyone know where we are?” 


Sathir perks up, “Yes. I do. Before I was unfairly and unjustly imprisoned, I was a member of the warrior caste, and I have explored this area quite thoroughly.”


They all turn to him. 


“We need supplies. If our destination is Gracklstugh, the fastest way to get there is to go through the Darklake.” 


The overbrighters stare at him, confused about the word “Darklake.” 


He sighs and explains, “The Darklake is a network of underground rivers, natural tunnels, and canals that connect innumerable water-filled caverns and chambers. This vast waterway stretches over a hundred miles across, with ceilings that are miles high in some places and depths that are unfathomable.


Long ago, duergar engineers extended and widened many of the interconnecting passages of the Darklake. They also constructed locks for raising and lowering watercraft to different levels within it, opening up large portions of the network for travel. Many Underdark creatures are experienced in navigating the Darklake, including the kuo-toa.” 


“We can get to Gracklstugh, Blingdenstone, or wherever we want from the Darklake. If what Shuushar says is true, the town of Sloopdopblop is just eight days away, and we can find a navigator and a boat.” 


There is a moment of silence, and then they all agree. 
## 5th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh 1493


The group begins the long march through the darkness after the long rest. The tunnels alternate between pitch-pure darkness or lit with the surreal magic of the *Faerzess (*Fay-YERR-zess).


As Grygum marched, he took note of his new friend. When he woke up, Stool, whom they had met as a fellow prisoner in Velkenyvelve, was curled against him. When the orc tried to push him away, the myconid cried. 


Stool explained that he was lonely, scared, and terrified. He remembered Grygum's inspirational speech yesterday and knew Grygum would bring him home. He knew he wanted to be Grygum’s best friend. 


Grygum stared at the creature. Although its behavior was different, he could tell when a child was looking for an adult figure to protect it. He sighed and told the creature that they could be friends. When stool extended his hand, Grygum took it. And so they marched. 


But it wasn’t only altruism. Having a myconid would allow the group to surprise enemies using the telepathic powers Stool imbued his allies with. 


They moved at a normal pace, trying to find food and water. 


“Well, look at this,” shouts Jimjar. 


The group stops and stares at the fungus he is pointing at. Thorin thinks it looks like a giant’s tongue. 


“Is it edible,” Thorin asks.


“Tastiest thing in the world,” says Sarith. 


Thorin is distrustful and asks Shuushar, who answers, “It is said that when you eat this mushroom, you connect with the gods.” 


Thorin is dubious but chooses to eat the mushroom. He gets the vague impression that it has a psychedelic effect, but he doesn’t feel any different afterward. 


“You know, that Myconid thing probably tastes delicious. And Shuushar, you really  have big eyes.” 


Everyone stares at him, and then the prisoners from the Underdark start to laugh. Buppido asks Thorin, “So tell us the truth. Is it true what they say about Giants?” 


And Thorin attempts to lie but tells the truth. 


And then everyone laughs even harder. 


When the laughter subsides, Shuushar explains, “*The Tongue of Madness* will compel its eater to say the truth.” 


Seeing that answering a question is the only danger, and Thorin is not compelled to respond, the rest eat the mushroom and sit silently. They are all unwilling to reveal anything. 


Zathir stares at the group, ats the mushroom, and declares a vow of silence. 


Buppido looks at him, funny. 


Once they have eaten, the group continues their journey into the dark. They arrive at a large cavern, and as they stretch their arms, a tremor can be felt. And then, before anyone can react, rocks fall. 


Once the dust has settled, Zalthir looks around. Topsy, Buppido, Jimjar, Eldeth, Grygum, and Shuushar are trapped under the rocks. Grygum shouts that he’s fine, but Daz is silent.  


Zalthir examines the mage and concludes that he’s unconscious. And will die if he doesn’t get him out in time. 
# Chapter 05 Pursuit


Zalthir notices that Sarith is not under the rocks and thinks, “We have not lost the guide.” He sees Thorin reach for Grygum and thinks, “We need the healer.” 


He looks at Daz, “If I don’t get him  out of there, he will die.” He braces against some rocks and shoves them out of the way. Daz is injured and unconcious but alive.


Stool is relieved to see that Gyrgum is alive. Gyrgum tells the frightened Myconid child, “Go help Shuushar.” 


And Buppido shouts, “The divine plan said you would rescue me, Sarith!” 


In the darkness, something shifts, legs clicking. Zalthir sees the bulbous shape of a massive, ghastly insect leaving behind a meal of exhumed remains. The thing clicks its mandibles, feather-like feelers probing the darkness for its next meal. It screeches, and the smell of rot and loam overwhelms him. Before the centipede-like creature wraps its entire, staggering length around him, he breathes fire and runs behind Thorin and Grygum. 


So, the creature wraps its tentacle around Grygyum, knocking him out. 


Sarith, Buppido, Topsy, Turvy, and Sarith shoot the creature with hand-held crossbows. The bolts land on the beast, which, in its attempt to avoid gEttin g hurt, exposes its soft, fleshy parts to more bolts. 


Thorin strikes with his short sword, cutting into the carapace. Zalthir tries to burn the creature again, but his fire doesn’t perform. The beast sensed his arrival and twisted away. 


The enraged monster bites Thorin, but the dwarf’s armor protects him. He then tries to grapple Sarith with his mandible and fails. 


Thorin shouts to the twins, “Save Eldeth and Jimjar.” 


Buppido and Sarith kill the creature with their bolts. And then Sarith shouts, “Rations!” 


Zalthir wakes up Daz and Grygyum. When Daz hears about Thorin’s decision, he mutters, “Good decision. Maybe, just maybe, our traveling companions will see our actions and choose to help.” 


An hour later,  Daz tells Zalthir, “Did you notice that?” 


Zalthir nods. 


Daz thinks, “We are being followed.” He hears the careful footsteps of a drow scout, a sound he is very familiar with. He turns to Zalthir, “Drow.” 


Zalthir remembers the particular gait of one of the Drow soldiers, Nym, and mutters, “It’s the Drow from Velkynvelve. These are their scouts.” He remembers reading the story of one of the monks of his order who was trapped in the Underdark and pursued by Drow. The monk, Korrh Erann, had been part of a group pursued for days. Some of their group hoped that killing the scouts would slow the Drow down. Korrh insisted that this was a dangerous gamble and chose to run. He was the only survivor. 


Zalthir, remembering the story, shouts, “We have to run!” 


Because Stool moves very slowly, Thorin shouts, “Get on my back!” 


Stool jumps on and releases his rapport spores. A few moments later, he asks everyone, “Was that a good idea? I think it was a good idea.” Before anyone can respond, he says, “I’m really glad you liked my good idea!” 


Zalthir dashes off ahead, using his monk training to speed ahead. As he runs, he looks for anything to use as a weapon or a hiding spot. He sees a tunnel and chooses the one veering left. As his lungs burn, he’s about to give up when he notices a space behind some stalagmites that they could hide behind. Using the mind link created by Stool, he lets the group know. 


Thorin, Daz,  Grygum, and the remaining prisoners run to the hiding space. 


Meanwhile, the pursuing Drow, hearing the running, start sprinting and, in their haste, barely avoid a sudden drop in the cave tunnels.


Soon, the Drow scouts arrive at the stalagmites. They hear a large thump. Zalthir has fallen from his hiding place. Nym draws his weapon. He looks around. Then, he feels a tremor. Worried that this cave will collapse and seeing no evidence of the prisoners, he turns to leave. As they leave, Nym mutters, “I told you it was the other tunnel.” 


What Nym didn’t know was that Grygum’s Thaumaturgy was the source of the tremor. 


Sathir whispers in their skulls, “Ilvara has found us and, worse, has caught up with us. We must put some distance between us and them. Or we can keep going slowly and have someone cover our trail.” 


The dwarf whispers, “I was taught to cover our tracks in the Underdark.” 


Grygum asks, “Where are the drow? Are they ahead of us? Behind us?” 


Sarith mutters, “Overbriters that cannot fly are the easiest prey in the Underdark.” He then explains, “The Underdark is not flat. And the tunnels don’t move in a straight line. They twist, and they turn. Worse, the tunnel system is constantly changing. And so an enemy can appear far away, only to appear in front of you. What’s important is that we move. And we hope no tunnel gives them a shortcut to find us.” 


Grygum thinks, “Like a Maze?” 


The Drow soldier nods.


And so they run. As they run, Jim Jar mutters, “I was going to make a bet that I was going to find food, and you guys weren’t. But the silent one,” and he points at Zalthir,” wanted us to run. So nobody is going to find food.” He pauses, “Wanna bet?” 


### 6th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh 1493


As they run through the Underdark, they rush through a cave with plenty of *Faerzess*. Suushar seems uncomfortable as they run through the odd glowing substance. As they run out, Suushar mutters, “That was odd. It was the first time I had felt so strange. The *Faerzess* was just a light, but now it seems to be a poison.” 


Jim Jar mutters, “That’s what happens with Kuo-Toans, who think they aren’t mad. They are insane, but their madness seems reasonable. The *Faerzess* has never affected a living thing. Its only magical power is to prevent teleportation spells.”


Sathir mutters about the need to find a path through the cave to the next tunnel and is about to give up when Grygum shouts, “Is this what you are looking for?”


Sathir mutters, “Yes, I saw that.” He looks annoyed, “I didn’t need your help. But it’s good that you can help.” And then rushes down towards the tunnel that Gyrgum saw. 


As the day ends, Sathir explains, “We did well to put some distance. But we have no water. And if we don’t find some soon, things will get unpleasant. Tomorrow, we must go slow. Eldeth, it’s up to you to hide us.” 
# Chapter 06 Arrival at the Silken Paths
## 
7th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh 1493


As the caravan of escapees moves through the Underdark, the problem of storing liquids rears its ugly head. 


At the time, ditching their gear and making a break for it seemed like a good idea. But now, the lack of a water bladder is creating problems. 


Daz then proposes an ingenious solution. When they next find water, he will use his ability to shape water to transform it into a block of ice. The block of ice can then be carried. Every hour or so, the water can be refrozen. If someone needs water, a block can be chipped away, and the water can be consumed. 


“All we need is some water,” mutters the monk. 


Fortunately, the escapees find both in the form of a few Barrelstalk mushrooms. Jimjar explains that the Barrelstalk mushroom can produce 1-4 gallons of water and five to 10 pounds of nutritious food. 


Eldeth covers the rear as they travel, trying to obscure any evidence of their travels. Buppido seems particularly interested in her tricks. 


Daz, Gyrgum, Thorin, and Zalthir try to help the dwarf. Eldeth tries not to be annoyed at all of the help. 


As the day progresses, they arrive at a narrow passageway lined with bioluminescent green moss. This moss grows in warm and damp areas and is particularly common near steam tunnels and vents. 


Jimjar explains that it is a fungus called “Ormu. In addition to shedding a dim light for 5 feet, it can be harvested, dried, and made into a phosphorescent powder or pigment.” 


Zalthir collects some fungi - “Never know when you need that kind of pigment.” 


As they exit the narrow passageway, Zalthir turns to Jimjar, “You’re good at hiding things.” 


Jimjar nods. 


“How about you block this passageway in a way that does not look like we were the cause?” 


“Wanna bet that I can?” 


“How much?” 


“5 gold.” 


“I have a pound of food?” 


“I want gold.” 


“Are you not interested in avoiding the drow?” 


“Wanna bet?” 


“We could leave you behind; it would improve our odds.” 


“Wanna bet?” 


“WE HAVE NO MONEY.” 


“That’s okay, we’ll have some later.” 


“And if we don’t, then?” 


“Then you never pay up.” 


Zalthir is gEttin g progressively more annoyed. 


Sensing this could get violent, Daz steps in, “It’s my understanding that Zalthir vowed never to gamble again when he became a monk. And such a bet would violate his oaths.” 


Jimjar is stunned, “I’m so sorry. I didn’t know.” 


But then Grygum steps forward, “I’ll make that bet.” 


Jimjar gets to work and, a little bit later, announces, “You won the bet.” 


“I did? Which side did I bet?” 


“You bet that I could do it.” 


Zalthir is baffled and intrigued, “He bet against himself even though he knew the odds of winning that bet were terrible. His willingness to make these bad bets implies he will make further bad bets going forward.” 


Grygum turns to Zalthir, “Interesting.” 
Zalthir tries to test his theory, “I’ll bet you can’t fly to the roof of this cavern?” 


Jimjar laughs, “I am a gambler, not an idiot.” 


Zalthir can only see that Jimjar is an infinite cash machine. If he can only figure out how to make Jimjar take the side of bets, Zalthir is most likely to win. 


As the group settles into sleep, Daz notices Topsy and Turvy talking to each other. But they are too far away for him to understand what they are saying. 


## 8th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh 1493


Sarith rouses everyone in the morning, “We must continue.” 


And so they do, deeper into the Underdark, hopefully heading to Sloopbludop. 


After an hour of marching, Torin finds a pool of water. Daz immediately starts creating blocks of water for the group. When all the blocks are made, there is no more water. 


A little bit later, Grygum finds some more Trillimac. Jimjar, a botanist, explains it is a mushroom that grows to a height of four to five feet and has a broad gray-green cap and a light gray stalk. The cap’s leathery surface can be cut and cleaned for use in making maps, hats, and scrolls (its surface takes on dyes and inks well). The stalk can be cleaned, soaked in water for an hour, then dried to make a palatable food akin to bread. 


“That one will be worth 6 pounds of food.” 


“How much water will we need?” 


“I don’t know.” 


Zalthir glares at him. 


The rest of the crew cannot find any more of the mushroom. Eldeth shouts at Grygum, “Will you look?”


The half-orc interrupts his reverie and looks around. He shouts, “There!” 


And indeed, there is more Trillimac, enough to make 20 pounds of food.


“But how much water do we need?” 


Shuushar sighed, “Soon, we will be at the Darklake, and we will have more water than we ever knew what to do with it.” 


Zalthir would pull out his hair if he were a humanoid with hair, but he isn’t.  


And so the march continues. 


Sathir shouts, “YES!” 


They all look at him. 


“We have arrived at the Silken Paths. We are heading in the right direction.”


Buppido asks, “Although I know what they are, what do you think they are, Sathir?”


“The Silken Paths are a network of spider webs crisscrossing a 500-foot-deep, 2,000-foot-wide chasm that stretches for nearly five miles. The major strands of the web are traversable. Still, the Silken Paths are ever-changing because old webs disintegrate over time and the giant spiders inhabiting the chasm constantly sping new ones.” 


“So how do we get across?” 


“We start walking and hope we find a way through this maze.” 


Sathir is about to head out when two goblins appear. They are dressed in relaxed, comfortable shoes, baggy pants, and shirts whose button reaches just above their knees, whose sleeves are particularly wide, and their heads are covered with beanies. Their bodies are covered in tattoos written in draconic. The spelling is wrong. And it’s only through happenstance that Zalthir realizes they are writing goblin words using a draconic script. 


The first one, whose color motif is orange, introduces himself, “My name is Yukyuk.” 


The second jump, whose color motif is pink, speaks with an odd accent: the R’s are rolled, and the vowels are clipped oddly. “And I am Spiderbait. We can be your guides at a nominal price of 2 gold per day.” 


Daz admits, “We are destitute.” 


Thorin grabs Daz and nudges Stool to use his spores. 


Then he turns to his allies, “Look, we don’t have the money, and we don’t know how. How about we ask them to demonstrate how to navigate the web? We’ll take notes and then politely decline.” 


Zarith mutters, “Jimjar, you seem to have a knack with words.” 


Jimjar then turns to the two goblins, “I’ll bet you 20 gold you can’t navigate the spiderwebs.” 


“Done!” 


As they head to the web, Grygum realizes that the Jimjar doesn’t have 20 gold. He wonders whether to say anything to the goblins and realizes that Jimjar will pay when he has money. “And they are goblins; we could easily deal with them if it comes to that,” he thinks. 


Thorin observes them coat their shoes with a peculiar substance and start running. 


Grygum stares at them, slides on the strands, and mutters, “They are good at surfing the web.” 


Daz nods, “It’s almost as if we are on a Safari that surfs the web.” 


Grygum asks Jimjar, “Do they know which side of the bet they made?” 


He looks at the cleric and, with a twinkle in his eye, says, “No.” 


When the goblins return breathless and pleased, they turn to Jimjar. 


He nods his head and says, “You won.” Jimjar then looks into his pockets and mutters, “But I am a bit short of cash.” 


Angered, Yukyuk tosses his beanie on the ground and starts marching to the web. Spiderbait, however, has an idea: “Jimjar, how about we be your guides and hang around until you have the 20 gold you owe?” 


Jimjar acts like this was the most awful idea he had ever heard, then pauses and sighs, “I suppose that will have to be the plan.” 


Just as they are about to follow them onto the strands, Zalthir tries to figure out if these two peculiar web-surfing goblins can be trusted. And although he is distrustful, he feels there is no subterfuge about them. 


And with the deal closed, the stiff, formal nature of the two goblins dissolves. Yukyuk turns to Topsy, “  Oh, yeah, man. That was fun. Did you see me nail those tough strings? There was this one moment when I was taking a curve, and the strands broke, but I managed to do that twist and flip, and that's super cool.” 


Topsy stares at him, confused. 


Grygum, always excited with new forms of speech, shouts, “That was an amazing triple spin!” 


Spiderbait, seeing Grygum’s interest, mutters, “Yukyuk took the easy route. I went around the spider and through its legs.”


Zalthir takes note of the spider and asks, “Spiders?” 


“Not the small kind, but the giant kind. You get extra points if you spin a spider.”


Zalthir is now, perhaps the word isn’t worried, but something in the environs of that sentiment, “That sounds fascinating, but given the complexity of your moves, how are we supposed to get across?” 


Yukyuk looks at Zalthir confused and then laughs, “Oh man, you’re not surfing. You’re walking.”


Zalthir then stares at the web, “How attached are you to these webs? Can we burn the web down?” 


Spiderbait looks hurt and then laughs, “Do you remember that crazy Drow wizard who wanted to burn this place down? But the spiders kept rebuilding it faster than he could burn.” 


Yukyuk slaps his forehead, “Oh yeah, man. And then, when the webs were burned, you had to climb down these gnarly cliffs. And then climb up some other cliffs. No, man, the web is the way to go. Just gotta avoid the spiders.” 


Zalthir stares at them, “But when we walk on the web, the spiders will hear our vibrations. Won’t that attract them to us?” 


Yukyuk says, “Yeah, dude. But there is so much stuff bouncing on the webs that they won’t notice your bouncing scales.” 


Zalthir feels compelled to add, “If we don’t make it out alive, we won’t be able to pay.” 


“Yeah, man. We’re, like, the best guides, and, like, all our clients make it out.” 


Spiderbait walks up to Yukyuk and high-fives him. He then turns to the group and says, “We are the best. We are going to have so much fun going through the web with you. And you are an awesome group.” 


Buppido mutters, “I am not sure the divine plan had anything about relying on two semi-sentient goblins for our safety.” 


For once, Zalthir agrees. 


Sathir, seeing that the deal has been made, tells the two goblins where to guide them, “Take us to a passageway that will get us quickly to Sloopbludop.”


The two goblins start the hike through the maze of webs. As they walk, they explain that fire can burn through the web, but when it does, anyone within 30 feet of the burning point will likely fall to their death. 


Zalthir asks, “And can we mitigate that fall?” 


The two goblins shrug. But Eldeth, who has done some spelunking, mutters, “We can tie some of the silk rope around each of us. That way, if one of us falls, the others can try to arrest his fall.” 


This innovation intrigues the goblins, who take many mental notes as the escapees tie themselves. 


Spiderbait asks, “But what if the other guy can stop the fall?”


Eldeth answers matter-of-factly, “Well, then the next person must.” 


“And what if he fails? And what if you all fail?” 


“Then I suppose we all die.” 


“Gnarly.” 


After an hour of walking, Daz notices a cocoon. Zalthir notices it is moving and humanoid-sized. He turns to Stool, “We need those spores.”   


Stool is very excited, “I’m helpful, aren’t I? I love being helpful.” 


Grygum turns to him and smiles, “And we love you for it.” 


“Are you going to come with me?” 


Grygum smiles at Stool and says, “Yes, I will. Now let’s go together.” 


So Stool and Grgygum advance on the cocoon, and then they hear the voice of a still living halfling in their heads. “I am Fargas Rumblefoot.” The voice turns demanding, “Can you please get me out of here?” 


Grygum is about to cut through the cocoon when Thorin says, “Perhaps we should have him tell us who he is?” 
Grygum stops, “He can't be evil with a name like that. But you’re right.” 


“I was a member of an adventuring band looking for a lost tomb. Gnolls attacked us.” 


“A gnoll?” 


“Yes, gnolls. Feral hyena-headed humanoids attack without warning, slaughtering their victims and devouring their flesh. It is said that spawns are put into a hyena, and when the spawn is born, it rips out of the hyena's body. It is also said that hyenas are one of many species that can be used to store the spawn of gnolls. It is also said that they were created when the demon lord Yeenoghu found his way onto Faerun and ran amok.” 


Thorin turns to his allies, “I wonder if he’s already been infected? Like, do we free him, and we get a gnoll?” 


“I am not infected.” 


“That’s what everyone thinks, and then it’s the apocalypse.” 


Zalthir - “Why aren’t you infected?”


“Because I escaped. Most of the time, the gnolls just eat their victims.” 


“And what are you doing here?” 


“I am spider snack for later. Can you please stop talking and get me out?” He pauses, “Shit, I can feel the spiders coming.” 


Thorin turns to the guides, “What should we do?” 


“Get out of here?” 


Fargas suddenly realizes he might not be freed,  “I have information. We were coming to look for a tomb. I know the location of the tomb. And more importantly, I know the location of the treasure.” 


Zalthir turns to Thorin, “Can you carry him, or will we need to spend minutes to free him?” 


Thorin takes his blade, saying, “I can cut him loose in a few seconds.” 


Grygum, Zalthir, Daz, and Thorin take a look around. Spiders are walking on strands. Those strands can be cut with fire or a blade. They can stop the spiders and escape if they cut the strands in the right places. They will get trapped if they cut the strands in the wrong place. 


They remember this as a game from their childhood called ‘Cut the Graph.” 


# Chapter 07 The Silken Paths Continued
![image]()
## 8th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh 1493
The rules of “cut-the-graph” are pretty simple. The two players sketch out a series of rivers on paper. Each takes a turn to draw a line. Then, each player adds a bridge. The number of bridges and rivers drawn depends on various factors and is unimportant. Once the bridges and rivers are drawn, both players try to advance their tokens to the other side. A river can only be crossed at a bridge. Players must choose which bridges to destroy to defend themselves and which bridges to use to attack. Most of the time, the game ends in a tie. 


A particular variation played in Cormyr, where militaries are far more sophisticated, allows the attacker and defender to build bridges with special magical units. Most people in the North don’t have much experience with that game. And those who do feel it changes the game in a way that doesn’t make it as challenging. In fact, in several gaming halls across Faerun, playing with the Cormyr rules will get you expelled from the gaming hall. 


This is why when Zalthir cuts one of the strands, he’s surprised by the reaction of the Spiders. Instead of trying to attack from very away, they use their web-spinning ability to build new bridges and advance along those bridges. 


Thorin is particularly annoyed at the Giant Spiders, who are simply not playing the game as it was meant to be played.


As the Spiders advance on the group, the group starts running and cutting strands, which causes the Spiders to keep creating strands. Making a strand means they can’t also attack, which the escapees view as a positive development. 


Fortunately for them, the Giant Spiders are somewhat territorial. If they run out of their domain, they will stop pursuing them. 


The combination of swords and Daz’s magic missiles slows down the Spiders long enough to allow everyone to escape. 


As folks sigh with relief, Yukyuk and Spiderbait offer suggestions for next time. Yukyuk says, “Like dudes, that was cool. But you might want to have thought about sliding -under- the spiders and cutting the web from the other side. That would have been so much cooler.”


Spiderbait adds, “And like, using Magic is okay, but like, it’s kind of a cheat. I mean, I get why you did it, but next time, you should like stick to your skills.” 


Zalthir then turns to the halfing, “About the treasure?” 
Fargas Rumblefoot is tempted to deny what he said, but the look on Zalthir’s face dissuades him. 


Furthermore, Grygum pulls out a scrap of paper, says, “I took notes while you were talking,” and then repeats what Fargas said. 


The halfling adventurer sighs, “I suppose I should keep my end of the bargain.” He sits down, picks some spiderweb still in his hair and his equipment, and begins - “In ages past, at the height of Faerûn’s great empires of magic, the half-elf sorcerer Brysis of Khaem was interred in a floating tomb. After the fall of the empire of Netheril and its flying cities, Brysis’s tomb plummeted into a crevasse and wound up in the Underdark, where it has remained for centuries.”  


Grygum looks up from his notes, “And it’s full of treasure?” 


Thorin asks, “Is it full of Bris?” 


Fargas sighs, “Yes and No. What is essential is that I know about the false tomb. When other treasure hunters arrive at the tomb, they find a sarcophagus and a burial chamber.  And that is a fake burial chamber. The real treasure is hidden in another chamber that you reach from a secret passageway from the servants' tomb.” 


“And the tomb is?” 


Fargas shrugs, “I don’t know the precise location. But I do know where it is -sort- of. It’s on the eastern edge of the Darklake.”


Sethir perks up, “Tell me more.” And the two talk for a bit, at which point Sethir announces, “I know where it must be. I can get us there.” 


Zalthir turns to his fellow escapees - “It is interesting that he said he knew where it was previously but doesn’t know now.” 


The monk realizes that Fargas’ claims were either made out of desperation or bravado, but he is uncertain if Farga is lying now. 


Grygum looks at Fargas, takes a measure of how the halfling speaks, and declares, “Fargas wasn’t -lying- and he isn’t lying.” 


Zalthir then walks up to Fargas and touches his belly. The halfling is very miffed. “What was that about?” 


The monk announces, “No gnoll spawn.” 


At this point, the Zalthir turns to Serith and asks, “Can you explain how you know where it is?” 
Serith sighs, “Probably best if I draw a map.” He uses the Ormu that Zalthir had collected from the narrow tunnel they had squeezed through. 


“Now, this isn’t a map of the tunnels, but it will give you an idea of where we are and where we are going.” 


![image]()


“We started in Velkynvelve. We have been heading towards Sloobludop. We are at the Silken Paths. The Darklake is a large body of water. Unlike the overbrite, it doesn’t have a surface in the conventional sense. It’s a large water balloon in the Underdark, where intersecting caverns, caves, and tunnels allow navigation. After we get to Sloobludop, Bupido says we should go to Gracklstugh. Gracklstugh is a large Derro city. I agree with him. That’s where we can get weapons and gear. The tomb is on the way.” 


“How many days are we from Sloobludop?” asks Grygum. 


Sethir answers, “Three days.” 


Thorin looks at the map carefully, “The map doesn’t reflect the relative distances accurately.”


Sethir glares. 
With that, the escapees continue their trudge through the Silken Paths. Zalthir asks hopefully if the Drow pursuers will be slowed down by what happened with the Giant Spiders.


Spiderbait explains, “Depends if they have good guides. And there are hundreds of ways of going through the Silken Paths. Yukyuk and I just happen to know the best way. If they have a good guide, no. A bad guide? Yes.” 


A few hours later, as they walk along a strand of web far removed from other strands, a floating sphere with a gaping maw and a single great eye, set within four eyestalks, floats up to meet them. 


It reaches out with its mind and starts talking - “I bring warnings!” 


Grygum, always friendly, asks, “What warning?” 


“I have escaped from my imprisonment to a long-dead drow wizard.” 


Zalthir adds, “Us too.” 


The large eye and one eye stalk focus on Zalthir, and the other three eyestalks focus on Grygum, Thorin, and Daz. 


“I bring warnings of Demons,” it broadcasts. 


“Where and what kind of demons?” asks Grygum 


“Why do you want to know?” It pauses and then stares at Zalthir, “Maybe you are a demon! Maybe you weren’t prisoners of the Drow but worked for the Drow. Maybe that Drow is your master!” 


Two eyestalks now stare at Daz. 


Zalthir reaches out through the mind network of the myconid and wonders who can try to convince this creature of its benign intent. 


Grygum says, “Jimjar, I’ll make a bet you can’t convince him that we are not demons and not enemies.” 


Jimjar takes the bet and fails. 


He shrugs. 


The creature, later revealed to be a Spectator, a kind of Beholder is quite mad and attacks. It uses a confusion ray on Thorin. Unfortunately for the creature, Thorin charges at it and attacks it. 


Daz strikes with magic missiles. 


Zalthir runs towards Thorin, who is blocking his approach to the creature. He looks at the strand and realizes he can go under it by holding onto the spider webs. While hanging on the spiderweb, he attempts to strike the creature. Unfortunately, the effort to hold on and attack is too much, and he misses. 


Grygum mutters to himself, “I need better-ranged spells.” He then takes his handheld crossbow and fires at the creature. 


One of the eyestalks, meanwhile, emits an eerie green ray, and Zalthir is now paralyzed. 


A blue ray from another eyestalk strikes Thorin, but Thorin is unaffected. 


Thorin swings his sword, leveraging an old battle technique called a hill strike, which he learned from a hill giant battle master. Usually, the creature would be knocked prone, but the Spectator is stronger than the dwarf expected. 


A few curt words and a swift gesture are all it takes to unravel an arcane knot in Daz’s mind and unleash swift darts of pure magic. Glowing teardrops of blue-white force sizzle through the air, swooping swift as starlings, unerring in their flight.


The Spectator is dead. 


With the danger gone, the two goblin guides slide into view. Yukyuk is very impressed with Zalthir, “That was some next-level spider walking. Like going underneath the spider web and attacking the creature.”


Zalthir is still paralyzed and can only think of choice words to use. 


A little bit later, the escapees see the edge of the cavern wall. Along the strand they are walking, they see a large chest. 


There is a momentary desire to see if it’s a treasure chest, but all agree it’s a mimic.


Even Buppido agrees. 


Jimjar wants to make a bet, but nobody wants to test the theory that it is. 


Once past the mimic, the group is on ston,e, and the endless tunnels of the Underdark beckon. 


Yukyuk asks, “You guys got our money?” 


Jimjar smiles, “I am good for it, but not right now. I promise you’ll get your money.” 


“When?”


“The minute I get it.” 


Yukyuk and Spiderbait are tempted to abandon the escapees, but Zalthir's slick, kick-ass move elevates them in the two guides' imaginations. And so they decide to stay with the escapees. Both of the goblins seem to be in awe of Zalthir. 


Zalthir privately wonders if they could convince the two guides to get the gold from the mimic. 


But Daz mutters, “They might prove useful as fodder in a battle.” 


Buppido overhears the two and turns to Zalthir, “What an interesting idea, Zalthir. Perhaps you can be part of my divine plan.


Zalthir wonders whether the Spectator thought Buppido was the demon, but he pushes that idea aside as the escapees move forward. 


# Chapter 08 Murder most foul 
## 9th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh 1493
The Silken Tunnels are behind them now, and the dark depths of the Underdark are ahead. Their group expanded to include two members, the curious goblins Yuk-Yuk and Spiderbait. They were promised 20 gold, and Jimjar convinced them to follow him into the dangerous tunnels. 


The tunnel journey is slowed as the group forages for food. They find some Ripplebark that, despite its rotten fresh appearance, is entirely edible in its raw state and could be roasted to improve its nutty flavor. Scorched or burnt ripplebark turned black but was still edible. It could also neutralize disease germs.


Near a pool of water, the Eldeth smiles. She has found waterorbs. As she explains, the Waterorb is a fungus that grows in the Underdark in shallow water. When mature, it was bulbous in shape and bigger than a human head. If squeezed and wrung out, it yields about a gallon (almost four liters) of potable water. The remaining husk was bland and chewy like a sponge but edible, providing about


But more importantly, it can be used to store water. 


This part of the journey takes you through tunnels and caves rich in the Faerzess's eerie magic. Yuk Yuk and Spiderbait find the colors somehow different than they are used to. And Sethir seems particularly affected. 


But it is Thorin who suddenly loses it abruptly. He starts screaming, laughing, and weeping. After about ten minutes, during which no one is sure if he’s suffering from PTSD, whether the stress of the Underdark has become too much, or whether this is some religious ritual, he recovers. 


“I have no idea what happened. But I am fine now.” 


Suushar the Awakened sees Thorin’s bout of madness and remarks that perhaps in Sloopbludop, the archpriest Ploopploopeen can help. “Ploopploopeen is a follower of the Sea Mother, and she will be most welcoming of my awakening to the end of our people’s madness.” 


Grygum hears the name of the archpriest and mutters, “That’s quite a bit of tongue twister.” 


Suushar is confused - “It isn’t. It’s pretty simple to say. Ploopploopeen, Ploopplooppen, Ploopploopeen!” 


Grygum raises an eyebrow and is about to speak, but the tunnels turn left, and he finds himself in a massive cavern with what appears to be a bottomless gorge. 


Zalthir mutters, “If only I could fly, I could get across. But I don’t, and there is no way to climb across it.” 


Buppido rolls his eyes and looks upwards. 


Zalthir looks up and suddenly realizes he’s in a cave with a ceiling that allows anyone to climb over the gorge. 


Thorin volunteers. 


As Thorin is about to start his climb, Grygum asks Jimjar - “Wanna make a bet?”


Jimjar smiles, “That’s the spirit. He makes it, or doesn’t it?” 


“Makes it.” 


Thorin overhears the bet and shrugs. He takes a rope, ties it around his waist, and then begins the hazardous sport of climbing to the roof of the cavern and then the gorge. He drops down as he gets to the other side of the gorge. 


Thorin shouts, “We don’t owe you any more money, Jimjar.” 


Unfortunately, the darkness does not permit him to notice several humans hiding on the other side of the gorge who attack him with their crossbows. 


While Thorin secures the rope, the other escapees rush over to the other side to help. 


The fight is short, brutal, and victorious. The attackers appear to be desperate bandits dressed in a mix of armor and clothing and armed with scimitars and crossbows. Their equipment suggests they have been in the Underdark for some time. 


Zalthir is pleased to discover many vital pieces of adventuring gear on the corpses, the most important of which are water bladders.


Jimjar, however, is excited about the tinderbox - “Toasted Ripplebark, the best thing in the Underdark.” 


Zalthir turns to the locals, “Do we leave the bodies here, and will the ecosystem of monsters impede our pursuers? Or should we dispose of the bodies because it will be a trail?” 


That triggers a massive debate. What to do with corpses is a significant ecological, Phylosophical, and existential problem in the Underdark. Because corpses are food, unwanted creatures are attracted and will eat them. This creates pockets of disturbance in the local ecosystem that a clever group of trackers can use to identify the presence of violent combat. 


Jimjar, Topsy, and Turvy believe that the monsters will be a hindrance. Suushar feels that the notion that trackers can discern anything from what the circle of life is is absurd. Buppido is emphatic that this will leave a trail. 


For some reason, Zalthir believes Buppido. There is something about the Derro’s conviction. And so the bodies are dropped into the bottomless gorge. 


As the group watches the bodies fall, Stool shouts, “That’s a cool mushroom!” He calls the mushroom a  Nilhogg's nose. The young Myconid explains, “You can eat it, but it won’t fill you up.
