But after eating it, you can smell better and find good mushrooms and other smells. It’s like the smells become so much more. But if you smell a bad smell, it hurts you a lot more.” 


Zalthir collects a bunch. 


In the evening, Thorin tries to talk to Eldeth. But the shield dwarf finds Thorin’s relationship with giants to be offputting. The War of the Giants that happened after the War of the Dragons ended in a peculiar stalemate. Although the Ordning was re-established, the giant civil war continued. And the effect on the people of the North was devastating. 


Thorin says - “But they were different giants!” 


She seems unconvinced. 
## 10th day of the 2nd Tenday of Taraskh 1493


“Another day in the dark,” mutters Eldeth. Her frustration at trudging through the dark will not stop her from finding plenty of food. 


Her success as a forager has made her indispensable to the group. Her ability to hide their tracks may be why they are still alive. 


The Drow of Velkynvelve is now almost forgotten. 


“Stop,” she shouts. 
She is standing in front of a cave covered with mushrooms. She shouts, “Tinmmasks.” 
Everyone looks closer and sees a field of squat toadstools growing to about two feet in width and height. They are grouped in clusters, with no more than four in a cluster. The mushroom has a beige-colored cap crossed with red and orange stripes.


Thorin asks if they can be eaten. 


“No.  If it is heavily damaged or killed by uprooting, it spews a cloud of spores out to a radius of 15 ft. All those within the cloud may be poisoned for about a minute and, when poisoned, are affected by the same effects of a confusion spell.” 


She looks at a corpse, “that’s what happened to that guy.” 


The escapees loot the corpse, and as they loot them, they realize he is the bandit who escaped from the ambush near the gorge. 


“He had friends,” mutters Buppido. 


Later that day, as the group settles to sleep, Buppido’s analysis proves correct. The friends show up. 


A group of bandits arrive under the flag of truce, offering information about how to get out of the Underdark. 


The bandit leader explains, “We were exploring a dungeon and made one too many wrong turns, ending up deeper into the ground than we wanted to.” 


Grygym, Eldeth, and Zalthir realize that the story is a fabrication and that the details are not that important. 


He offers the information for food. The deal is agreed upon, and he shares with him that the best chance of escape is through the town of Blingdenstone. 


Topsy and Turvy find the name off-putting. Jimjar is mildly disinterested. Sethir insists they should check out the lost temple and find the treasure. Buppido insists on going to Gracklstugh first and suggests they can purchase the equipment they need to make it to Blingdenstone. Sethir observes that traveling along the Darklake is less treacherous than traveling in tunnels.


Suushar says he has no interest in traveling past Sloopbludop but may be willing to help with travel in the Darklake. 

The debate continues, but eventually, everyone tires of it and falls asleep. 


Grygym, enjoying the taste of toasted Ripplebark, asks Jimjar, “Wanna bet that we’ll find monsters in the tomb?” 


Jimjar mutters, “It’s a lost tomb; of course, we will; the better question is -what kind of monsters-.” 


“Undead?” 


“Boring.” 


“Skeletons and Zombies?” 


“I’ll take that bet.”


“What are we bEttin g?” 


The two of them are told to be quiet by the rest of the group as it tries to sleep. 


## 1st day of the 3rd Tenday of Taraskh 1493


The group wakes up to the sounds of screaming. 


Spiderbait is staring at the ground at his friend Yuk Yuk. The rest of the group examines the ground, and there is the corpse of Yuk Yuk, his throat cut with a blade. 


Grygum examines the cut and notes, “It’s a shortsword. Any one of us could have done it.” 


# Chapter 09 Buppido is uncovered! 
### 1st day of the 3rd Tenday of Taraskh 1493


Grygum mutters, “I am so upset that the person I have known for a day is dead!” 


Spiderbait screams at Jimjar, “Give me money. I am leaving now!” 


Jimjar quiets him down and reassures him that he’s more likely to live if he stays around. 


Zalthir, whose pleasant dream about what Monks dream about was interrupted, looks around, trying to figure out why everyone is in an uproar. Then, hearing the screaming, he stands to attention, ready to kill. 


“Are we under attack?” 


Shuushar whispers, “No. Yukyuk was murdered, and Spiderbait is very upset.” 


Grygum looks around and says, “Well, we have no other option but to continue and be alert.” 


But Daz, who finds mysteries to be interesting, thinks otherwise. “I want to figure out what happened.”


First, he questions Spiderbait. 


“Would anyone want him dead?” 


“Yukyuk was the kindest, gentlest goblin you could imagine. He and I were pals.”


“Did he have anything of value?” 


“Other than the kindest heart, no.” 
     
Then Spiderbait glares, “I’ll tell you who I think it is - Shuushar. Kuo-toan’s go mad. And when they go mad, they snap, and then they kill people!” 


Daz turns to Zalthir, Grygum, and Thorin - “What do we know? Buppido always talks about the divine plan. Sethir seems a bit off. Topsy and Turvy are lycanthropes. Jimjar makes bets all the time. Eldeth is trying to keep it together and make sure we all arrive in one piece. And Shuushar claims to have figured out the cure to Kuo-toan insanity.” 


Just then, Shuushar approaches them and says, “ I propose we head to Sloopbludop, where we can meet the arch-cleric of the Seamother, who can cast the zone of truth, and we can learn what happened.”
Grygum mutters, “That’s the easy way out. Let’s do it the hard way by applying intelligence, deduction, insight, and perception.” 


Daz shrugs, “I guess I could ask Buppido.” 


“Do you know what happened?” 


Buppido looks at Daz and says, “This was all part of the plan!” 


But Daz knows something’s off. 


“Sounds like a non-answer.” 


Buppido sweats, “Yukyuk’s death was necessary for the divine plan.” 


“Who was responsible for his death?” 


Buppido tries to evade the question, “Who can say? I cannot be held accountable for the divine plan. 


Daz gets annoyed and pushes past Buppido. He examines his equipment and notices that the shortsword may have blood on it from a victim. 


Buppido tries to protest that he’s not a maid, and that’s why it’s got blood on it. 


Daz is fed up, so he casts a mind-sliver on the derro, stares him in the eye, and makes it clear that it could get a lot worse. 


“Ouch!! That hurt. It wasn’t me! It was the agent of the divine plan.” 


Grygum looks at him and says, “That’s what they all say.” 


“It’s not my fault,” Buppido whimpers. 


Another mind-sliver is cast, and the derro whimpers even more. 


Sarith walks up to Daz and says, “That’s an excellent torturing technique. However, I have other more effective ones that I was taught as a member of Lolth’s guard. We could remove his eyes, nails, and other things.” 


Daz looks at him, somewhat annoyed but somewhat pleased: “I am not torturing him; I am providing motivation.” 


Zalthir perks up, “Motivation?” He thinks that in his many years, he had never heard anyone refer to torture as motivation. “Perhaps I should reconsider my prohibition of it.” 


Daz turns to Buppido, “So?” 


“It wasn’t me.” 


Daz stares at him, wondering if he is mentally ill or just different. He has had enough experience with the judgmental overbrighters who assume all Drow are evil to be willing to give everyone a chance. But he realizes that this isn’t someone who has a different perspective; Buppido is mad. 


“Let’s cut him loose.” 


Shuushar says, “No, no. I want us to tie him up. I can try my techniques of mental sanity on him as well!” 


Buppido looks genuinely horrified. 


Daz turns to the derro, “We are going to tie you up, and if you can’t keep quiet, gag you.” 


A few minutes later, a gagged Buppido walks next to Shuushar, who talks endlessly about this technique called Kuo-toan-fulness. The goal is to create a space between the moment an impulse comes to your mind and the moment you take an action, and in that moment, wonder if that impulse is a reaction to the real world or just a response in your mind. 


Buppido pleads for a mercy killing, but all that everyone can hear is the muffled moans. 


# Chapter 10 Leemooggoogoon vs Sea Mother! 


An hour or so later, the group is ambushed by eight kuo-toans—four creatures attack from the front and four from the rear. 


At first, the escapees are worried that they have met their end, especially when they see a Kuo-Toan monitor. A Kuo-Toan monitor is a special kind of Kuo-Toan leader who provides structured organization over a Kuo-Toan group. Shuushar explains that the monitor’s primary role is to deal with any sudden break of insanity. And that when the monitor is defeated, the Kuo-toans are less likely to keep fighting. 


During the fight, the group discovers that the body of the Kuo-toans releases a particular liquid that causes any melee weapon to stick to their bodies. Only the application of strength can from a weapon from the glue.


In the end, they realize that a collection of hand-held crossbows, combined with a united team, can create a powerful enough force to take down even a formidable group of enemies.  


Three of the Kuo-toans flee into the Underdark, including the monitor. 
Shuushar sighs, “Such an unnecessary battle. Why would this be happening?” 


Sethir mutters, “Should we continue?” 


“Yes,” the Shuushar the Awakened says. 


An hour from Sloopbludop, another kuo-toan party appears. This time, Shuushar is very excited and starts talking to one of them. 


Just then, his interlocutor casts a spell, and suddenly, not only is their language clear, but also the nuances of their communication and body language. 


“This is Ploopploopeen, archpriest of the Seamother.” 


Grygum finds the name very funny and tries not to laugh out loud.  


The archpriest is excited and says, “The Seamother has answered my prayers!” 


It’s then that the fish origins of the Kuo-toans become apparent. Ploopploopeen has come with other members of her kind, and as she talks, she walks around. They follow her like a school of fish, walking here and there in circles. 


The effect is surreal because, like in a school of fish, the other Kuo-toans will go in front of her, around her, and stay in the back. And yet, it all seems very well choreographed. Shuushar follows her as she walks around, yet doesn’t always stay next to her, even as she seems to be talking to him. 


Ploopploopeen explains that the inhabitants of Sloobludop have lived in harmonious service to the will of the Sea Mother for some time. There were occasional “visionaries” who stirred up trouble (at this, he might cast a walleyed glance at Shuushar) but nothing of any great concern. A few weeks ago, Bloppblippodd, Ploopploopeen’s daughter, experienced a powerful vision of “Leemooggoogoon the Deep Father,” proclaiming him the new god of her people. She has backed up her claims with a tremendous increase in magical power, and new followers have flocked to her.


“We are split in two,” Ploopploopeen explains, “fighting among ourselves.” The followers of the Deep Father have been making an increasing number of offerings on his altar — killing blood sacrifices then casting bloody chum into the waters of the Darklake, where it is consumed by … something.”


A bit bored, Topsy asks, “I hear about your problems, and that sounds like a you problem, not like a me problem. What can we help with you?” 


“Oh that’s easy. I wish to use you as bait.” 


Zalthir looks at her, unimpressed. 


The archpriest of the Sea Mother explains he wants to use them as bait. The archpriest of the Deep Father needs humanoid sacrifices, and the party represents a prize collection in that regard. Ploopploopeen will offer them as a “token of peace and reconciliation” to get closer to the archpriest of the Deep Father — except the adventurers will not be helpless prisoners but infiltrators. Ploopploopeen wants them to disrupt the upstart faction’s rituals, allowing his true believers of the Sea Mother to cut off the head of the cult. The archpriest promises that the characters will be “well rewarded” for their aid.


Grygum mutters, “Oh great, pit one weird religion against another!” 


Ploopploopeen is offended. “The Seamother is not a weird religion. It is the traditional faith of the Kuo-toans! It is Leemooggoogoon the Deep Father that is the real evil!” 


Daz interrupts the archpriest, “We need to have a quick chat amongst ourselves.” 


The escapees huddle in a group. Daz mutters, “If Ploopploo-whatever is going to keep talking endlessly like that, maybe we should kill them?” 


Shuushar is aghast, “No, no, no. The Sea Mother is an old god, the Deep Father, that is who we should fight against. The Deep Mother demands humanoid sacrifices, not the Sea Mother.” 


Daz is unmoved, “I don’t want to listen to this drivel all the time.” 


Shuushar thinks momentarily, “Perhaps we should talk to his daughter before we take action? I have learned that one must open themselves to all points of view and then only then make decisions and judgments.” 


Shuushar continues to drone on but thankfully walks away. 


Zalthir shouts to the archpriest, “You said reward?” 


Grygum adds, “I am all about the spiritual stuff, but the temporal have needs too.” 


The archpriest promises 500 gold and two potions of healing. But she sees how they are unimpressed, “Two boats and guides to navigate the Darklake?” 


The escapees nod in agreement. 


Daz asks, “How many members does the other faction have?” 


“Do not worry yourself about that. All you have to do is distract Bloppblippodd enough. I will take care of her, and my followers will take care of the followers of this false god.” 


# Chapter 11 The Village of Sloobludop 
### 1st day of the 3rd Tenday of Taraskh 1493


Ploopploopeen, the archpriest of the Sea Mother, stares unblinkingly at the escapees. 


And they are confused. Yes, there is a reward, but why should they sacrifice themselves for these fish people? 


Ploopploopeen realizes that the Tongues spell didn’t translate his intent as well as he would like. The escapees think they will be required to fight. 


“No, this is wrong. You will arrive in Sloobludop and stay in my quarters. I will send message to the followers of Leemoogoogon that I have an offering for him. In the morning, my daughter, Bloppblippodd, the high priestess of the Deep Father, will demand to see the offering. I will present you to her, and I will insist that I come with you. She will accept. And then all of my followers will attack. Your role in this will be over.” 


Grygum finally understands, “This is like a flag of parley. Have you considered a white flag?” 


“I tried that, but she didn’t bite. She needs sacrifices for her false god.”


Grygum tries to probe if the sacrifice must be willing. 


“I am not certain how your rituals work, but in the rituals of Leemoogoogon, the sacrifice is essential, not the provenance.” 


Grygum nods, “Yes, our rituals are different.” 


Thorin probes, “But willing sacrifices are sweeter?” 


“No. An unwilling sacrifice is better. This is an evil god.” 


Grygum looks at Plooploopeen and wonders what he has heard. He and his daughter have problems with their relationship, and it’s also unclear if a god named Leemoogoogon even exists. 


Topsy and Turvy, on the other hand, realize that a free-for-all is an excellent opportunity to steal. 


Zalthir wonders why they should bother. They have their problems, and the issues of these two warring tribes are not their concern. 


But Daz sighs, “Man, we’ve been running for days. Having a purpose in life is a good thing. We busted out of prison, and then what? Ran. We’re being chased, and we keep running. One of our group got killed by another of our group. Having something to focus on would be much less depressing than just doing what we are doing.” 


Zalthir shrugs and the group accepts Ploop’s offer. 


The remaining journey to Sloobludop is uneventful. The tunnels eventually end up on the village's western side of about 500 kuo-toans. There is a wall made of nEttin g guarded by Kuo-toans. They snap to attention when Ploop arrives and lets everyone through. 


Thorin notes that the nEttin g isn’t an effective wall against a determined invader. 


Past the walls are the huts of the kuo-toans, and at the other end of the town, almost 500 feet away, is another wall of nets. 


Between the two walls to the south is the cave wall. To the north, between the two nEttin g walls, is the Darklake. Between the walls of nEttin g, the cave wall, and the Darklake is the village. There are over a hundred houses of various sizes. Each home has mud walls, and the ceilings are made from an unidentified dried vegetable matter. 


The Darklake side has docks. Some of the docks have boats. Some are empty. Walking along the docks are groups of Kuo-Toans. These leader types that Shuushar explained are responsible for ensuring that the madness of the Kuo-Toans doesn’t rip the society apart. 


In the middle of the town is a large statue 


Ploop stops in front of the sizeable nine-foot-tall statue. The statue is roughly carved from wood in the shape of a humanoid female, its head and forearms formed from the severed head and claws of a giant albino crayfish. These parts are lashed on with strands of gut and emit an overpowering stench of rotting shellfish. Shells, brightly colored stones, mushrooms, and rotting fish are piled at the statue’s feet and strung in garlands around its neck. 


Four stern kuo-toa slowly circle the statue, alert and on guard, while a few others move about, gazing up at the statue and bowing repeatedly while chanting.


Grygum recalls from somewhere that the Deep Sea Mother is a scavenger goddess and that regurgitating and spitting on her altar is perhaps the perfect form of offering. 


Ploop is delighted when Grygum and Thorin both spit on the altar. 


Meanwhile, Daz, overcome by the rank smell, has his hand over his mouth and tries to rub the smell out of his nose with his thumb. Ploop looks at him, and he smiles weakly as he pretends his nose is itchy. 


“We must eat!” he shouts. 


Thorin is worried that this will be some raw rotting food, but Ploop, perhaps sensing that, assures him that Kuo Toans eat cooked fish. 


At this, even Zalthir is convinced that perhaps helping the Kuo-Toans isn’t a bad idea. 


After eating, Ploop falls asleep. As is the case with Kuo Toans, he stands up and walks outside. 


At this point, the escapees notice that many kuo-toans just walk around with their eyes open, sleeping. And that some other kuo-toans are moving about as schools of fish. 


At this point, they decide to go check out the altar of Leemoogoogon. They sneak out just close enough to see the idol of Leemooggoogoon the Deep Father. It consists of a large hide cut roughly in the shape of a manta ray and stretched out on cords between two support poles. A dead, splayed-out manta ray is pinned to the center of the hide. Two dead octopuses are draped across the top, their tentacles pinned and artfully arrayed, their heads tied together and painted with red and blue pigments. The idol reeks of decay and the broad stone altar below the idol is stained dark with blood. 


Unfortunately, their attempt to be quiet is anything but. And the kuo-toans circling the Deep Father notice. 


“I say we beat a hasty retreat,” whispers Thorin. 


“These guys are spooky. Let’s get out of here,” mutters Zalthir. 


Safe inside Ploop’s house, another Kuo-Toan stares at them. Uncertain if he is awake or asleep, they ignore him. 


He says, “My name is Glooglugogg. Gloog is what my friends call me. I do not approve of Father’s choice to have outsiders meddle in our affairs, but you showed respect to the Sea Mother, and thus, I see that you respect and understand our ways. Our society is torn to pieces by my sister Bloppblippodd. Father has shown her too much deference, offered her too much, and let her get away with too much. She has no respect for our ways. And she has fallen prey to this madness.” 


Gloog’s dislike for his sister becomes increasingly apparent as he enumerates her ills and flaws as a sister, daughter, and former cleric of the Sea Mother.  


Zalthir asks, “We saw a dozen near the altar. Is that all her support?” 


Gloog burps, “Her hard-core supporters are few, but how many in the village are on our side? Her side is unknown. This is why it must be dealt with now. While we still have the support of the majority.”


Zalthir, again, clarifies his role, “So when we go there, our job is just to sit around and do nothing.” 


Gloog looks at him, “Of course not. You will help us as you, too, see the righteousness of the Deep Mother.” 


“But we won’t throw the first punch?” 


“No, that would insult the honor of my father and our people. This is our problem, and we must resolve it.” 


Zalthir is satisfied. 


Gloog turns to him, “Now get rest. In a while, we will have to fight.” 


As Gloog is about to sleep, he mutters, “You didn’t choose just to give us the derro whom you tied up? That is both honorable and odd.” 
### 2nd day of the 3rd   Tenday of Taraskh 1493


In the morning, twelve kuo-toa led by a kuo-toa monitor arrive at Ploopploopeen’s quarters. The archpriest of the Sea Mother admits the monitor and informs him that he, his whip, and the prisoners will accompany them to see the archpriest of the Deep Father.


# Chapter 12 Demogorgon nee Leemoogoogoon
## 2nd day of the 3rd tenday of Taraksh
The archpriest of the Sea Mother steps forward across the span of the altar toward the kuo-toa, waiting for him there. “The time has come,” he says, “for us to acknowledge and welcome your divine vision. I have brought these as offerings.” He gestures toward all of you, standing within a circle of guards behind him. “Will you not accept them?” “You are wise, father,” the younger archpriest replies. “I accept your offering in the name of the Deep Father. May their blood nourish and strengthen him!” A burbling cheer rises from the surrounding kuo-toa, their fists raised.


The escapees are wondering if they are about to be betrayed. 


Just then Thorin notices a duergar. He looks at the creature. And then remembers the stories of the deep dwarves. Whisperwind, a giant friend, warned him of the deep dwarves. 


From the shadowed depths of the earth, where light fears to tread, crawl the duergar or deep dwarves, a grim reflection of their mountain kin. No warmth graces their granite hearts, and no laughter echoes in their echoing halls. Instead, a gnawing hunger, bottomless greed, drives their every deed. Gold, not glory, fuels their forges, and the clang of hammer on steel is a dirge, not a song. They are masters of the craft, yet beauty withers beneath their touch, replaced by cold, utilitarian perfection. Each creation is a testament not to artistry but to acquisition, a step on the endless climb to hoard more than their brethren.
Their faces, etched with the lines of ceaseless toil and bitter resentment, rarely soften. Kindness is a forgotten word, and mercy is a weakness they despise. The suffering of others, a twisted reflection of joy, brings a fleeting smile to their lips. They are bound by clan, yet kinship is a hollow word, for trust is a bauble they cast aside long ago. Each duergar toils in their designated role, a cog in the great machine of their subterranean empire, individuality crushed beneath the weight of conformity. They envy those who have more and scorn those who have less, their hearts poisoned by the belief that the world owes them a debt they can never repay. To a duergar, life is a brutal, unending struggle, a journey from the cradle to the grave spent in joyless labor, a hollow echo of the dwarven spirit. Even the treasures they amass bring no satisfaction, only the gnawing need for more, a hunger that can never be sated. They are the gray dwarves, and their existence is a testament to the darkness that can fester in the heart of even the most steadfast race.
“Please help me. Do something.” 
Grygum answers, “We were told we would have to do nothing.” 
The duergar looks at Grygum, surprised yet somehow comforted. His desire to live overcomes his innate cultural cynicism. “What? You are just going to show up here and die?” 
Grygum realizes that this creature doesn’t know the plan and recognizes that this may be an opportunity to take advantage of this poor creature, “There’s more than meets the eye.” 
The duergar sighs, “Very well. Tell me when to act. And if we get out of here alive, find me in Gracklstugh.” 
“Your name?” 
“Hemath.” He spits out blood. “I am an arms dealer and got caught up in this madness. I promised weapons to the Archpriest of the Deep Father, and she said that my sacrifice would be weapon enough.” 
Meanwhile Kuo-toans parade around the altar in a wide circle as they chant. Part of their path sends them splashing and wading through the shallows of the Darklake. 


Zalthir,  who has been observing everyone, can’t tell one faction of fish-folk from the other but sees the archpriest of the Sea Mother and his whip moving toward the altar.


Just then, he hears Bloppblippodd call for the sacrifices to be brought forth. One kuo-toa per escapee jumps to do her bidding. They prod Zalthir and his fellow escapees with their spears, herding them toward a slight depression 20 feet from the altar, with a large grate at its center. 
Jim Jir mutters, “Wanna bet on how many of us will come out of this alive?” 
Daz announces, “We’re all going to come out of this alive.” 


Buppido mutters, “ahd m.” 


Daz nods. 
Zalthir observes that the stonework in the depression is marred by the blood of countless sacrifices, accompanied by the gentle sound of the Darklake lapping against the grate. 
The chanting grows louder.
Grygum looks around and wonders how the sacrifice is going to be performed. 


Thorin mutters, “If this is a fireball.” 
Grygum concludes, “No, this is going to be one of those conventional slit-their-throats with-knifesacrifices. Normally, the victims would be disarmed, but I guess they figure that part of the ritual is some of the cultists dying in the attempt?” 
It’s just then that Thorin realizes that if Ploop and Blopp are working together, they have all the necessary spells to paralyze them. He admits to himself that Ploop might have been playing them, and if so, between the two archpriests, enough hold persons can be cast to hold him indefinitely. 
As Thorin considers the possibilities, he is brought forward. Bloppblippodd gestures toward the altar and shouts, “Bring me the knife!” 
Thorin wonders if this is the end.


Ploop has betrayed his daughter, not the escapees, and attacks her along with his allies.
Thorin looks at the guards who surround them, and they are surprised. 
And then he looks around and realizes it’s a free-for-all. Kuo-Toans are attacking other Kuo-Toans. And the sacrifices are now ignored. 
Grygum examines the situation and decides that fleeing is the better part of valor. He also decides it's time to take a side and will go behind Ploop to heal any of his warriors. 
Daz notices the cleric running and runs after him. Blopp screams at one of the Kuo Toans to stop the escapees from running. Her second in command advances to block one route of escape. 
Jimjar, Eldeth, Buppido, Spiderbait, Shuushar, Serith, Topsy, and Turvy take advantage of the confusion of the melee to run towards Grygum. 
Jimjar mutters, “We all made it alive.” 
Grygum looks at him and thinks, “It would be cheating to let one of us die. Would he cheat?” 
Zalthir, Daz, and Thorin arrive, where all the escapees are huddled. The Kuo Toans engaged in the melee ignore them. 


Grygum looks around and notices docks and boats attached to them. He also notices Kuo-Toans fishing in the water beside the docks. Finally, he observes Kuo-Toan monitors standing on the docks, seemingly guarding the boats. 


He points to a boat in the far eastern part of the cave, guarded by a small group of isolated Kuo-Toans. 


Daz shouts, “We should check to see if we can find any supplies anywhere.” 


Grygum nods, “Let’s see if there is anything we can take from Ploop. After all he promised to pay us.” 
He runs into Ploop’s thatched hut. Once there, he pilfers whatever treasure he can find. Daz had suggested they try and find supplies, but gold and magic would have to do. 


The battle continues to rage, with Blip and Ploop shouting curses at each other and casting spells. The other Kuo-Toans, the followers of the Sea Mother and the followers of the Deep Father, are engaged in a genocidal battle to eliminate the other. 
Daz observes the madness and walks towards the boat with a confident swagger, looking as if he knows what he is doing and that nobody should mess with him. His chest is puffed up and out, his arms sway, and his stride is big. The other escapees, seeing that, mimic him. They walk towards the boat, away from the battle, with the swagger of righteous, powerful, and dangerous adventurers. 
Thorin then notices several Kuo-Toans who were previously in the water fishing and are now screaming. It appears that the fish people are trying to fight some underwater enemy. And then, just like that, the screaming stops, and the water foams with blood. The fish people are no longer. He looks around some more and realizes that there are several patches of blood in the dark lake. 
Grygum, his arms full of treasure, rushes towards the group. Everyone is both pleased and disappointed - “Gold to buy things and nothing to buy?” is how the cleric of Bahamut puts it. But, as his mentor, Gorg’Bahamut, said, “A hoard is always a valuable thing and a blessing from Bahamut.” 
Just then, he hears the young archpriest of the Deep Father call out, “Leemooggoogoon!” just as her father strikes a final, fatal blow. Blopp drops, dead, before the profane altar.
Grygum thinks for a moment and realizes that the ritual is complete. Usually, when an evil cult completes a cruel ritual, something terrible happens. 


He pauses and listens. And then thinks, “Yep, evil outcome of evil ritual,” as he hears another sound rise above the burbling cries of the Kuo-toa. He looks out onto the dark lake and notices the water's surface bubbling and beginning to foam. “Not to worry, just water effects,” he prays. And then a thick, oily tentacle bursts forth, followed by another. “I take that back; this is bad.” He stares at the point in the lake as two monstrous heads break the surface, resembling hideous, enraged baboons with wickedly curved tusks. Both heads are attached to a single torso, and the monster’s red eyes blaze with bloodlust and madness. 
“This is bad, but it can’t be what I think it is,” he mutters.
The creature emerging from the Darklake stands thirty feet tall, with water cascading down its back and shoulders. Upon reaching its full height, it throws back both its heads and lets out a mighty roar!


“Bahamut, save us; that’s Demogorgon,” he shouts. 
Thorin asks, “Demo-who?” He recalls Shuushar saying that the Kuo-Toans could create gods with the power of their faith, and he knows that the archpriest said Leemoogoogoon, not Demogorgon. 
In many ways, it’s amazing how the brain will convince you that the thing you are seeing is not what you are seeing because the horror of that being in front of you is too terrible. 
Thorin was experiencing that. 


But Grygum remembers from his training who and what the entity they were seeing was. He remembers his mentor, Grog'Bahamut, and what he said of the foul creature one evening. 
"Demogorgon.  The very name is a blasphemy against creation, a festering wound upon the fabric of reality.  He is a creature of pure chaos, a monstrous embodiment of the Abyss's insatiable hunger for destruction.  Two heads, each a font of corruption, embody the duality of his vile nature: one whispers insidious lies, tempting the weak to embrace the darkness, while the other roars with primal fury, reveling in carnage and despair.  His form is a grotesque mockery of life, a twisted amalgamation of reptilian savagery and demonic power.  Tentacles replace hands, dripping with the venom of chaos, while his twin necks support heads that mirror the fractured nature of his soul.
He is the antithesis of all Bahamut stands for: justice, order, and compassion.  Where Bahamut offers protection and guidance, Demogorgon sows discord and ruin.  Where Bahamut inspires hope, Demogorgon revels in despair.  He is a predator of souls, a corrupter of the innocent, and a destroyer of worlds.  He commands legions of demons, each a vile reflection of his depravity, and his influence spreads like a plague across the planes.
To face Demogorgon is to confront the ultimate darkness, the purest form of evil.  Yet, even in the face of such horror, we, the followers of Bahamut, will not falter.  We will stand against him, armed with faith and righteousness, and we will fight to protect the innocent from his insidious grasp.  For even in the deepest shadows, the light of justice can prevail."
Grygum thinks now is not the time to delve too deeply into this topic and shouts, “Demogorgon, Prince of Demons, powerful, dangerous, and we need to run.” 


# Chapter 13 Flight.
## 2nd day of the 3rd Tenday of Taraskh


Demogorgon roars. And while Leemoogoogoon’s followers cheer in ecstasy, the followers of the Deep Sea Mother are either terrified, driven mad, or planning to stand their ground and fight the demon lord. 


It's too much for Daz, who collapses in tears and moans. 


“We need to get out of here,” mutters Zalthir. 


He’s about to run when he notices that in addition to Daz, Eldeth, Topsy, Turvy, and Shuushar are also screaming and wailing. 


“To the boat?” he overhears someone say. 


The way out on the ground means gEttin g through the mobs of Kuotoans in the village of Sloopbludop. And even if they get through the Kuotoans, Demogorgon is advancing in that direction.  


If they can get to the boat, they may slip past Demogorgon. 


But what about his friends and allies? 


Fortunately, the group figures it out. 


Jimjar picks up Daz, Thorin grabs Eldeth, Topsy and Turvy are carried by Grygum, and Spiderbait carries Shuushar. 


The group arrives at a dock where several Kuotoan monitors stand, guarding. 


Grygum advances boldly and tells them that the Archpriest of the Sea Mother commands them to help the rest of their community.


The Monitors seem relieved to have a purpose and rush off.  


And with that, they board the boat and float away, paddling quietly not to be heard. 


From a distance, they can see Demogorgon destroy the town of Sloopbludop—the screams of the Kuotoans echo in the darkness. 


Shuushar, finally recovered from the sudden appearance of the demon lord, mutters, “Enlightmnet is necessary! We must change as a people. Our imagination brought into existence, Leemoogoogoon.” 


Eldeth mutters, “That was Demogorgon. He’s in the prime material plane. That is not possible.” 


Thorin stares at her, “I am not sure what you think is or is not possible, but I saw what I saw.” 


As the boat floats on the lake, the puzzle pieces all click in Thorin’s head. 


But it’s Grygum who says it out loud - “The spectator warned us about demons. And we saw the demons in Velkynvelve. Demons have made it to the prime material plane in large numbers!” 


Daz reflects on his knowledge of the arcane and his time in the Underdark, “Demons do not just appear in the Underdark. They must be summoned. And the spell to summon a demon lord is some mighty magic.” 


Spiderbait wails, “This is so not good. The Underdark isn’t a friendly place! And rampaging demons and demon lords!” 


Eldeth concurs, “The danger to all of Faerun is undeniable. Even if we escape the Underdark, these demons won’t stay down here. And to think someone summoned demon lords! We need to get a warning to the surface worlds. Dwarven miners are at risk!” 


Sathir mutters, “Where to next?” 


Buppido, who is no longer gagged, says, “Gracklstugh! I know people.” 


Thorin stares at him, undecided. Grygum, however, helps the group decide, “We need better equipment, and we now have the money to buy it.” 


Buppido sighs, “Yes, and I know people who can help you.” 


Jimjar looks at him, “Wanna bet?” 


A few days pass in relative quiet. Shuushar acts as a guide and navigator, pointing out where they can find water to drink and food to eat. 
## 4th day of the 3rd Tenday of Taraskh 1493
### Daz 


Standing on the front of the boat, Daz looks into the darkness. His eyes can see the water and the cave above him. 


A slight current pulls the boat, and the rowers are somewhat relaxed. 
Daz almost misses the rocks that stand out as stone teeth. He shouts.


The boat crew looks at him as he shouts, “Rocks! We need to dodge these rocks.” 


Everyone is confused and starts shouting. Daz realizes he needs to tell everyone what to do: “On my say, heave port or starboard!” 


The boat is heading straight for the first rock, and he shouts, “Port!” The ship turns, and he notices another rock, “Starboard!” The crew moves across the boat again. Daz is about to breathe a sigh of relief when he sees another pair of rocks. He must get between them, so he shouts, “Port! Starboard!” to line up the boat through the space. 


This goes on for a few more seconds, and then the rocks are behind him. 


He looks carefully for any sign of new rocks, then relaxes slightly. 


## 6th day of the 3rd Tenday of Taraskh 1493
### Thorin


Thorin reaches up and touches the cave's ceiling, which is only three feet above the water. He wonders what will happen if it gets any lower. 


He looks at Zalthir, Shuushar, Grygum, Daz, and Sarith, who are uncomfortable sitting down and lowering their heads to avoid banging them on the ceiling. 


“It’s good to be short,” Thorin notes as he sees how everyone else isn’t inconvenienced. 


Unfortunately for Thorin, he thought too soon, and the boat jerked, and he fell in, along with Grygum and Daz. 


As he splutters, he notices that the Darklake isn’t empty. 


The same creatures that were feasting on the kuotoans are here. They look like manta rays, whose jaws, instead of being used to filter plankton, have powerful jaws for rending the flesh of their victims. 


Fortunately for himself and his two companions, Daz and Grygum, there are only four. And unlike the Kuotoans, they are no match for them. 


As he climbs out of the water, he thinks it’s probably not good that a demonic fish is floating around with the local flora and fauna… 


## 8th day of the 3rd Tenday of Taraskh 1493
### Zalthir


“The ability to cast magical darkness and see through it opens up so many tactical opportunities,” he muses. 


Just then, he hears a shout from the watch: “There’s another boat ahead with some Kuotoans.” 


Zalthir stops and thinks and listens. The dragonborn is annoyed that he got caught up in a religious ritual that may or may not have summoned Demogorgon and is now floating through the Darklake in a tiny boat.


And the boat is a tight fit. 


Hemeth seems to be reading Zalthir’s mind when he suggests, “Maybe we take that boat from them? Like the last time I talked to Kuo-Toans, I almost got sacrificed. I was just trying to sell them weapons. I didn’t think they would think sacrificing me was a weapon. Crazy fish people.” 


Before Zalthir can agree, Suushar and Grygum have already decided that talking with more Kuotoans is the right answer. 


Zalthir  steps back and gets ready to attack, just in case. 


The Awakened shouts out to his kinsmen. Shuushar is very excited; at least, it would appear to Zalthir, Shuushar’s excited. 


Finally, their Kuo-Toan companion turns to the group, “They are from Sloopbludop and have seen the danger of the Kuo-Toan madness. And they are receptive to my message! They want to create a better Kuo-Toan world where we are no longer driven mad by our need to create a new god! I have found my calling! And I must leave you!”   


Before Zalthir can point out that Shuushar’s insight into the map of the Darklake is critical to their survival, Thorin says - “Follow your bliss!” 


Then Shuushar turns to his fellow escapees and thanks them for their help: “I have found my people, and we will build a better world!”


Zalthir stands off as he watches the tearful goodbye of Thorin, who is giving him a hug, Grygum spitting into the lake, and Daz looking indifferent. 


As the other Kuo-Toan boat floats off, Shuushar says thank you! 


As they stare into the Dark Lake, Sarith mutters a few moments later, “Erm, guys, I have Shuushar’s instructions, but I am not so sure I can follow them correctly.” 


# Chapter 14 Journey Through the Darklake
## 9th day of the 3rd Tenday of Taraskh 1493
### Grygum


Jimjar stares at Grygum and asks, “Why are you a follower of Bahamut?” 


And Grygum sighs. 


He has always been a bit of a mystery to other folks—an orc cleric of a dragon god. 


Those from the more civilized parts of Faerun ascribe it to the strange story of Protanther and the Dwarf and a chess game. 


The Dwarves and the Dragons had a long history of not seeing eye to eye. And although they found ways to acknowledge each other’s existence begrudgingly, they were not friends. 


After the events of the Well of the Dragons, the Dwarf Stroud had gone on a bit of a speaking tour, talking about his victory over the Gold Dragon Protanther and how the Gold Dragon saw that as a sign. He would spend hours walking folks through this thought process, the board, and the inspiration he had when he made the move. 


Many a chess grandmaster stared at the board, dumbfounded, that Protanther did not see the move on a board he had been studying for 400 years. They were also confused by Stroud’s explanation of the move because it would appear that he barely had a passing knowledge of the rules. 


Those who believe in the intrinsic goodness of the Gold Dragons believe Protanther chose to lose. He saw an opening to side with those who opposed Tiamat and made it sound like a sign from the gods. 


Some saw Stroud as the personification of the right humanoid at the right time and place, doing the right thing. It was proof that the individual had agency and that a single person could change the world, 


But others believed that Bahamut moved Stroud’s hand and hid the move from Protanther. 


And so the dragon god, who was never one to seek faithful among those who were not dragons, has gained quite a following among those who saw in his actions a divine plan. 


Jimjar was fishing to find out what Grygum believed, and Grygum was tired. And it was dark, and he didn’t want to get into another argument about free will, the will of the gods, and whether the scale color of a dragon defined the intrinsic goodness of a creature that lived for a millenia. 


Grygum smiles and says nothing. 


Jimjar stares back. 


## 10th day of the 3rd Tenday of Taraskh 1493
### Daz 


The boat suddenly stops, and Daz is tossed forward. 


Sarith shouts, “A sandbar!” 


Daz looks into the war and sees a swarm of those demonic Manta Rays floating in the water.


Zalthir shouts, “Anyone got oars?” 


Sarith laughs, “It would have been useful a while ago…” 


Daz watches as Grygum and Thorin prepare to get into the water to push. 


And then a flash of inspiration hits him, “Stop, I can do this.” 


They look at him, and he smiles, “Shape Water.”


Everyone groans. They have heard Daz explain how he can use Shape Water, and every time, the promise far exceeds what is delivered. He remembers an old saying from his days as an apprentice, “Overpromise and under-deliver!” But the last few days have made him question his memory.  


Daz is aware of their doubt, but this time, he is confident. 
He casts the spell and uses it to push a small wave over the sandbar. The extra water is enough to move the boat forward. He keeps doing it, and pretty soon, the ship rises over the sand and is free. 


As it floats down into the murky darkness, he turns to the group and says, “So?” 


And he enjoys a brief moment of applause and congratulations. 


# Chapter 15 Greengrass Day
### Thorin


Somehow, Thorin remembers that today is Greengrass. 


The festival of Greengrass was a tradition of the farming communities near the giants he lived with. 


The wealthy farmers would bring flowers to the poorer farmers in a peculiar spring festival to encourage the gods to usher in the summer.


The giants always found the festival peculiar. It was a strange obsession of the little people. 


But after the end of the War of the Giants, King Hekaton had decreed peace with the little people, and so peace it was. 


His reverie is interrupted when Zalthir shouts - “rocks ahead.” 


He looks a bit further and sees a boat. A boat that is abandoned.


Daz mutters, “We could use the oars!” 


Thorin agrees and is about to join the war when Zalthir stops him. “Isn’t it a bit ominous?” 


Thorin smiles; ominous sounds fun.


Daz shouts, “You have a point. They probably fell into the water.” 


### Zalthir


The dragonborn sighs. He wonders how Thorin managed to stay alive all of these years. In fact he’s beginning to wonder if he will survive next to Thorin, Daz, and Grygum. 


“We could check to see if there is any blood or gore on the boat?” 


He then looks at the castaways they collected and asks, “Do any of you recognize the boat?” 


The duergar looks at it and says, “Yes, it’s  Duergar Keelboat. You can see the crates.” 
Zalthir is about to say something when Thorin suddenly wises up, “Are they big enough to hold people? I am worried about an ambush.” 


Hemath laughs, “Yes, that would be a good thing to worry about. The Duergar can become invisible for a whole hour.” And he turns invisible. “I will be hiding here.” 


Then Thorin, who, to Zalthir’s pleasant surprise, is becoming a lot more paranoid, asks, “Can’t we do something to detect them, like splash water?” 


Zalthir groans inwardly because Daz will be excited.


“I have shape water!” 


And a few moments later, water is sprayed around the boat, and the outline of a humanoid appears. 


Zalthir is annoyed. They were about to have the element of surprise. If only Daz had carefully timed his water use so that Zalthir could take advantage of that action. 


But it is done. 


He scans his surroundings, eager to spot something, and he succeeds. He invokes Darkness and plunges into the water to attack the foe. Even though the opponent is invisible, Zalthir can pierce through the magical darkness, nullifying its advantage. 


The Dragonborn’s initial strike misses, but the second strikes home with a thud. 


### Thorin


Zalthir has disappeared into the Darkness. Thorin can sense another creature in the water and is tempted to use a handheld crossbow, but he rejects the idea. Diving into the water, he swims next to Zalthir and strikes the invisible creature, wounding it. 


Thorin hears two scorching rays hit the water and hiss harmlessly. He’s about to lose hope when he hears the scream of a Duergar in pain. 


Thorin thinks the creature is still alive. Then he hears Grygum's magical words and the telltale sound of a belch. He ducks. The Duergar is not so lucky and dies. 


Then he hears a scream. He can hear someone from the boat being grappled and pulled overboard.
Two more members of the crew are grappled. 


Thorin swims out, and Jimjar shouts, “You know what the Duergar do for a living?” 


Thorin wonders why the gnome would want to talk about anthropology now, “Nothing good?” 


“Yes, they capture slaves that they sell in Gracklstugh.” 


Thorin overhears Zalthir shout, “At least it’s where we were going.” 


Thorin approaches the boat and notices that Eldeth is not one of those captured. He sighs, relieved. The dwarf checks the others and sees that Stool has been captured. He attacks the Duergar. And the Duergar release Stool. 


Then the area is covered again in Darkness, and he hears the thuds of the Dragonborn’s fists on the Duergar. 


Thorin waits to see if the Duergar is dead. It is not. 


### Daz


“The darkness is annoying,” thinks Daz. He then mutters to himself, “I will need area-of-effect spells.” He smiles as he sees two targets. "The magic missile will do just fine here.”


The Duergar is struck by glowing teardrops of blue-white force sizzle through the air, swooping swift as starlings, unerring in their flight.


It howls in pain and drops the prisoner to flee. 


Daz notices Buppido has his hands over his eyes and asks, “What are you doing?” 


“I am invisible.” 


Daz rolls his eyes, “No, you are not.” 


“Yes, I am!” 


In the water, he can hear the splashing of Thorin’s swimming and then strikes the Duergar, dragging Spiderbait away. 


### 
Zalthir


Zalthir again moves the darkness to cover the enemies. He can hear Daz groan. 


As he swims towards them, he hears Eldeth curse them out as “Demonic spawn of dwarven corruption. Slave trader who deserves to be sent to the nine hells as punishment!” 


Zalthir mutters to himself, “I sense some racial animus.” 


His fists strike the creature that had Spiderbait, killing it.  


Daz shouts, “Leave one uncovered!” 


Zalthir shouts, “It protects you!” 


He can hear Daz’s sighs, and the burst of magic bolts kills the other creature.  


Another belch sounds, and another Duergar dies covered in acid. 


A few moments later, the last of the Deurgar is immobilized, and Zalthir is tired and happy. 


He floats to the keelboat and looks into the casks and the chest. He finds some gold and a jug that he learns later can be used to generate any liquid. The first liquid they generate is mayonnaise. After eating bland mushrooms, mayonnaise will make anything taste much better. 


As he digs through the contents, he can hear the debate on the Kuotoan boat about who should question their Duergar prisoner. 


Buppido shouts, “I have particular expertise and talents.”


Sarith explains, “The Lloth’s guards trained me. I am an expert, but having seen Daz’s approach, I recommend that he be given the first crack at extracting information.” 


### Grygum


The orc has been puzzled by Eldeth’s venom directed at the Duergar. He thinks there might be some rivalry between the Duergar gods and the Dwarven gods, but then he remembers something he read: that religious conflict is not always what it seems. The Dwarves and the Duergar compete for the same resources, and political conflict may matter more than any religious principle or dogma. “This is not the will of any god. This is the will of the people,” he mutters.  


## 9th day of the 1st Tenday of Myrtul
### Daz


The long journey through the dark waters of the Underdark has led him here to the metropolis of the Duergar in this part of the Underdark. 


Over the past few days, Hemeth has said a lot about his home, which sounds unpleasant. It’s a strictly regimented, xenophobic city. Non-Duergars are only permitted to move freely in the Darklake district. Within the city, everyone obeys the laws. The Duergar can become invisible at will; you never know who is watching. And finally, it’s a city of slavers. 


![image]()
And yet, despite everything Hemeth said, Daz is unprepared for what he sees. The city is so unlike the Drow cities Daz has heard of. The Duergar prize order and work over art and beauty. There is none of the opulence and refinement. Instead, the buildings are plain and functional. Whereas the Drow would have decorated their homes with etchings and art, the walls of the Duergar homes are plain. 


And the ambiance is just that of work. The sound of hammers warping metals, the stench and heat, and the light of the smelters make all of Gracklstugh appear as one large work camp. But the acrid smoke makes breathing hard and burns through his sense of smell, which he will remember most from his time here. 


Gyrgum asks, “So what are we doing here?” 


Daz looks at him and is about to answer when Jimjar whispers, “Buy equipment so we can survive more easily. Get information on how to get out of the Underdark.” 


Sethir mutters, “We plan to get equipment and then go to the Lost Tomb of Khem, where we will find treasure!” 


Daz notices that Grygum is satisfied. 


Daz remembers what Hemeth had said about the Blade Bazaar: 


“This marketplace is named after the most abundant goods the duergar offer, but the shops here sell almost everything available in the city, along with stalls set up by visiting merchants. The din of people arguing, mainly in Dwarvish, nearly drowns out the hammering coming from the city’s forges, and the crowds here offer a good chance to slip away from pursuers.”


“To the Blade Bazaar,” he says out loud. 


## Thorin
But before they can get to the bazaar, they must reach the docks. And before they reach the docks, Thorin remembers some castaways. He looks at Brannum Redmarch and Buppido and says, “What are we going to do about them?” 


Realizing that his time as a free person may be ending, Brannum pleads, “You wouldn’t turn me into the guard?” 


Zalthir has been thinking about some magical items he wants and was disappointed when Hemeth said that magical goods could be purchased in Gracklstugh but not in the Darklake District. He asks, “Could you purchase some uncommon magical items?” 


Brannam lights up, “Why didn’t you ask? That’s my business.” 


Hemeth, upon hearing that, grumbles, “I am a weapons trader, and you would go to him?”


Zalthir asks them, “Can either of you get me Eldritch Claw Tattoo?” 


Hemeth shrugs, “No.” 
Brannam lights up, “Yes! I know a guy. But it will take a few days. And then the slate is wiped clean?” 


Thorin realizes that Zalthir is very good at negotiating a deal, but sometimes muscle is needed to terrorize people, “And just so we are clear, if we don’t get what we want, and you betray us, there will be consequences.” 


Brannam shrinks, “Yes, of course.” 


Thorin then points at Buppido, “What about this guy?”


Buppido mutters, “Look, I made mistakes. It was the divine plan. Just let me go. I won’t bother you again.” 


Spiderbait, still seething with rage, wants to kill him on the spot, and although Thorin is tempted, he wants to see what everyone else has to say. 


Zalthir is unsure. “Perhaps he will betray us.” That logic sways Thorin and pulls his sword. “So we kill him?” 


But Grygum intervenes, “There are so many people who will kill us that I am not so sure we should worry about him.” 


Thorin lowers his weapon, uncertain. He looks to Daz, and Daz says, “I vote that we get as close to a guarantee as we can and then, as we leave, let him loose in the city.” 


Buppido is desperate and pleads, “I made mistakes. I was mad. The divine plan called me, and I realized it was a mistake. I have learned from Suushar that I was mad. PLEASE!” 


Thorin is now very confused. 


Then Zalthir hands him a mushroom, The Tongue of Madness, and says, “Eat.” 


And Buppido does and starts talking.


“I just wanted to return to my bolt hole in the caverns near the city and praise the Divine Plan.” 


And then he starts expressing his true opinions of his companions: “You all have been so annoying. Daz has foul-smelling breath. Thorin thinks his muscles are impressive. Eldeth is -not- interested in him.”


At that, Thorin decides he’s heard enough, but Grygum stops him. 


“Zalthir’s scales haven’t been cleaned in ages.” 


Grygum has heard enough, “I am done.” 


But then he says, “Jimjar’s bEttin g is so annoying! GIVE IT A REST.” 


Zalthir smiles, “I like him.” 


And that settles it with Thorin. He turns to Jimjar - “You all need to keep an eye on him.” Jimjar smiles, “Wanna bet?” 


### Zalthir


But just then, Zalthir remembers something, “So - wait, I mean, can he summon Demogorgon like the Kuo-toans?


Jimjar roars with laughter. 


Zalthir can’t help but think Jimjar is judging him. 


Then the gnome sighs, “Obviously, you do not understand the first thing about interplanar or gate travel. There are a great many things Buppido could do, but that is not one of them. The great powers of the outer planes in the Time of Trouble could enter the Prime Material Plane at will. And that created havoc. Aos, the overgod, has ended that era with the Second Sundering. And so now, bringing the avatar of such a power requires powerful magic and artifacts.” 


Jimjar then sighs and stares at Grygum, “The Cult of the Dragon almost brought Tiamat into the realms, and that required artifacts and rituals. No, Buppido has no such powers. But, Zalthir, it does beg the question - who did?” 


### Grygum


The cleric of Bahamut approaches a stall in the Blade Bazaar and tries to engage a merchant in a deal. The merchant, Dulgir, asks if he wants to buy or sell.


“Sell this mace?” 


At that, the Duergar starts cursing Grygum, accusing him of things that, in a different sEttin g, might have provoked a violent reaction. 


Grygum pauses and decides that he should start by buying, and the Duergar suddenly shifts, speaking with the stilted tongue of a Baldurian patriar. 


A few minutes later, he is the proud owner of a new mace. 


As he toys with his mace, he notices Zalthir looking at a list. “I found this list of names earlier.” 


Grygum shrugs.  “I think they might be worth looking into.” 


Grygum shrugs again. 


Zalthir is annoyed that he has nothing more definitive to say and mutters, “They could be people who could help us.” 


Grygum then notices that Dulgir is not the only one acting strangely. Many duergar merchants give different prices to buy or sell the same items whenever they are asked and insist that the buyers they deal with change their terms.


Near a food stall, a merchant suddenly turns invisible during a transaction but keeps speaking as if nothing has happened.


Across the aisle, another weapons merchant threatens a customer, and when the customer protests, the merchant denies ever saying so. 


Next to him, a cloth merchant suddenly stops mid-negotiating and starts talking to someone he refers to as his brother. When the customer asks who he is talking to, the merchant says, “My brother!” 


Grygum asks Dulgir, “I guess his brother is invisible.” 


But Dulgiar answers, “His brother doesn’t exist.” 


The answer disturbs Grygum, who is convinced that some madness afflicts the city, perhaps the same madness that consumed the Kuotoans. 


He steps away from the Bazaar and looks down a road to see if it’s happening elsewhere. The gates at the end of the road keep the Darklake District isolated from the rest of the city. It looks calm. 


And just then, the rhythmic hammering of the city’s forges is drowned for a second by a thundering roar and the sound of crumbling rock. Duergar and visitors alike turn to look as a two-headed, gray-skinned giant burst through a gate, howling madly and lashing out left and right, littering the plaza with rock and stone debris. As he bellows, one of his swings connects with a duergar soldier, whose broken body flies through the air and crashes near you with a sickening crunch.


Grygum thinks, “That’s an illusion!” But a piece of debris hit his toe, and he mutters, “No, it’s not.” 


Thorin, who overhears the giant, shouts, “Stone giants never talk. And they certainly don’t bellow. Something is wrong.” 


Grygum looks at him, “And the two heads?” 


“Two heads is more normal than bellowing.” 


For a moment, the priest of Bahamut wonders if he should just run. “What is in it for me?” he asks. And then he remembers the teachings of Bahamut that when you do a good turn for someone, they may do a good turn for you. 


A sign for Bahamut appears: a Duergar patrol racing towards this giant. 


“If I fight him, we may get some friends.” 


He turns to his companion, raises his holy symbol, and prepares to attack. 


With that, Zalthir and Thorin race into combat. 


Daz strikes first with magic missiles that streak from his hand. 


Zalthir places his circle of darkness just before the giant and enters it. Stepping up to the giant, he strikes with a flurry of blows. But he misses. The giant, although blind, dodges him. So Zalthir uses his power to focus his mind and strikes again. This time it is a glancing blow. 


Thorin rushes after Zalthir; with blindsight, he approaches the mad giant and strikes him with his sword. 


Grygum speaks the words of power that Bahamut has taught him, pointing his holy symbol at the mad giant who burns with necrotic damage and the power of Bahamut. 


The giant roars and smashes Thorin, but Zalthir, using his awareness of the monk, deflects the attack just in time. 


Daz is pleased, and Zalthir places the darkness so that he can still strike him. His fingers move in the air, the incantations are spoken, and bolts of power fly from his finger, striking the giant. 


Zalthir strikes the giant once, focusing his mind on striking again and striking the air. If the giant could see, he would see a dragonborn attack the air. And perhaps the giant would laugh. But this giant is mad and blind and misses this moment of joy. 


Thorin feints and strikes the giant. The creature howls. 


Gyrgum raises his holy symbol again and speaks the words of power, and the giant again burns. 
# Chapter 16 Wanna Bet on Who Dies First?


## 9th day of the 1st Tenday of Myrtul 1493
### Grygum


The stone giant with the two heads burned and wavered but did not fall. Bahamut’s magic did not kill him. 


A flash of flame engulfs the giant from two duergars that have come to join the battle. 


Startled, Grygum notices that the fire comes from a device they are holding. It is a tube that connects to a bottle on their back. At the front of the tube, a small flame sits outside the tube. He realizes that the flame is produced from some kind of magic concoction lit by the tiny flame when the duergar operator pulls a lever. 


“Don’t kill him! There’s something wrong with this giant! Let’s try and subdue him,” shouts Thorin. 


A few bolts of magic streak from Daz’s hands. 


Grygum looks at Daz, and then looks at the giant, and thinks, “Well, I guess Daz chose to weaken his spell purposely.” 


Grygum hears from within the darkness the sound of Zalthir’’s fists hitting the giant and the blade of Thorin, but still, the giant stands. So Grygum rushes in to strike with his mace. 


But the Giant stands. 


The Duergar, unconvinced by Thorin’s entreaties, kill the giant. 


Grygum watches as a distraught Thorin whispers prayers for the dead. 


\*pop\*


Grygum looks up, and the enlarged Duergars have shrunk to their standard size. 


### Thorin


Although Thorin is unfamiliar with the patterns of behavior of the Duergar, the madness of a stone giant is unheard of. The Stone Giants don’t move. They are taciturn to a fault. And so he needs to learn more. 
He turns to one of the Duergar, “Are there more crazy people about?” 


The Duergar stares at him, confused. “Crazy?” 


Thorin remembers that the Duergars are literal people but is uncertain how to continue. 


The guard sensing that asks, “Someone who does not follow orders and engages in anti-social behavior, but does it in a way that will bring them no profit and certain doom?” 


Thorin breathes a sigh of relief, “Yes.” 


The Duergar turns to the others on his patrol, briefly discusses, and says, “We have noticed that there have been significantly more incidents of this kind of behavior. As a result, the work of the militias has increased.” There is a pause, “And we know of no underlying cause. Although a clan leader may have information they have chosen not to share with us.” 


Before Thorin can ask a follow-up question, another Stone Giant appears, flanked by Duergar, armed with curious stone weapons. 


The Stone Giant stares at Thorin, whose body and blade show that he fought and perhaps killed the two-headed giant. Thorin remembers that Stone Giants are not talkative and may take a long time before they initiate a conversation as they ponder all possible things.  He begins the discussion by asking about some stone giants he has heard of. 


The Stone Giant doesn’t smile, “No. But then again, I don’t know many. Who are you?” 


And Thorin explains his curious relationship with giants and how he got here. 


The Stone Giant pauses, then speaks, “I am Dorhun, and this is Rihaud. We were both apprentices to Stonespeaker Hgraam. Did you kill him?” 


Thorin explains how he tried not to kill but subdue him and that it was the Duergar. The Stone Giant confirms his story and sighs again. 


“We have qualified immunity if a Stone Giant is rampaging through our city,” one explains. 


The Stone Giant sighs. 


Then he says, “I ask you to visit me at Cairngorm Cavern before you leave the city.” Turning to the Duergar with the stone weapons, he says, “Stone Guards, you are to let them through.” 


The dwarf watches how the Duergar gives the Stone Giant the briefest of scowls, showing how much they don’t want to give this non-Duergar permission to visit their city. 


## Zalthir


Zalthir is trying hard to protect himself from being burned alive, crushed by a giant, or arrested. 


And he’s feeling good about his chance when he hears a voice and a body materialize behind him.


“I gotta get me some of that ability,” he thinks. 


A Duergar appears right behind him. Zalthir immediately notices the scars on his ears, four notches that don’t look self-inflicted. 


“I am Gartokkar Xundorn, and these are my Duergar.” 


Just then, a few other Duergar approaches to see what is happening. Gartokkar flashes a bade of some kind, and the other Duergar move away quickly. 


Zalthir thinks, “And that, too.” 


“I am the Custodian of the Flame, the chief of the Keepers of the Flame, who tend to Themberchaud’s needs.” 


Zalthir stares, confused. 


“The furnaces of Gracklstugh must be kept hot, and instead of using a large amount of kindling, we use a fire dragon that burns stone hot that then is used to keep the furnaces running.” 


Zalthir hears Daz ask while holding down a snigger, “So he’s a lighter?” 


Gartokkar is a Duergar, and he is literal and misses the sarcasm, “Yes. The Keepers of the Flame tend to the dragon’s needs. And we are the most prized of the Deepking’s advisors. We need someone like you.” 


Zalthir hears Grygum’s joke, “We do have some kindling here.” 


Gartokkar laughs. “ A joke. I have not heard a good joke in so long.” 


Then, he becomes serious. “Your skill set would be of great value to the city of Gracklstugh. If you were to come to the Keepers of the Flame headquarters and do me a service, I could give you safe passage through the city. And as long as you did nothing that the Deepking would disapprove of and would not require me to do too much, I could keep you out of the prisons.”


There is a moment of hesitation, “The offer expires tomorrow. And if you don’t accept the offer, I cannot promise we will be so friendly when we meet next.” 


Gartokkar disappears. 


## Daz


The story of this dragon intrigues Daz. 


“How does a dragon end up turning into a lighter? What’s in it for him? Red dragons are not exactly known for their willingness to serve. They want to build a hoard or something. A dragon that flies around lighting fires is odd.” 


His friends look at him, and he looks back. 


“Well, we should find out what we can do before we help him. Perhaps we can go to the brewery?” 


And so, from just outside the Blade Bazaar, Daz and his odd collection of travelers arrive at the Darklake Brewery.


The Brewery is closed to non-Duergar, and Daz is disappointed until Grygum, who sneaks a quick peek, says that inside is a pretty dour place where people talk only in hushed whispers. 


Just outside is a Drow and Halfing, and they are drinking beer. Daz and Grygum approach them. 


The halfling looks at Grygum, “You must be new.” 


“I’m just glad you see an orc and don’t run off scared.’ 


The halfling laughs, “I am in the Underdark. I see so many scary things. You are the least scary thing I have seen this week.” He pauses, “You won’t turn invisible?” 


He laughs and, after being introduced, asks, “You haven’t gotten in trouble with the law?” He looks at them and says, “Of course not; otherwise, you would be in the Overlake Hold and not hear talking to me.” 


“Say, you wouldn’t be the people who took down the crazed giant?” 


Daz acknowledges that. 


“Good for you.” In a conspiratorial tone, he says, “Did any of the factions approach you for a job? You would be crazy to join them, and they are trying to kill each other. It all began with the Deepking’s madness.” 


Daz describes the madness of the merchants, and the halfling shrugs, “Yes, that kind of madness. However, in Deepking’s case, the laws are more arbitrary. We’ve always had laws in Gracklstugh, but they made sense. Now, they don’t. It’s as if he is detached from reality.”


The halfling again whispers, “You must have met the Keepers of the Flame? They are in a pickle, what with the Gray Ghosts and the Crown.”


“How do you know so much?”


“I’m an outsider. And what do I know? Not very much. And as long as I stay an outsider, no one considers me a threat. And I can share what I know with those not in the game. And you are not part of the game, nor am I.” He pauses, searching for a phrase, “What is that expression? It's -- Not relevant to the game.” 


Daz wonders, “Can you come with us to the meeting with the Keepers of the Flame?” 


“No, I won’t. That might make me appear like a player in the game. I like to watch. I would avoid such encounters and actions. Although, it might be impossible to stay alive, anyways.” 


At that, Daz asks about the dragon. 


“Yes, the Red Dragon. The city has had one for ages. The red dragon keeps the stones hot enough for the furnaces to burn. Are you wondering about its horde? The keepers of the flame give him a horde, and they pamper him. The problem, and you’re right to wonder, is that Red Dragons dislike playing second fiddle. And so, at some point, the Dragon discovers it’s not in charge. Then, the Keepers of the Flame have to kill the dragon. There is also the problem of the dragon becoming more powerful over time. So the Keepers must kill and replace the dragon with a new one.” 


Daz is about to ask why but remembers how Dragon eggs can be purchased and hatched. 


At this point, the Drow sitting next to the Halfling splutters, “Look, friend, I am from Menzoberanzan. The backstabbing and politicking are nothing compared to the Duergar. I mean, we will do it with style and finesse. Here, it’s just slaughter. No torture, no speeches, no art, and I mean no style. It was just a brutal struggle. They just engage in violence for violence’s sake. It’s disgraceful if you ask me.” 


At this point, Daz wonders if they should interview the various factions to find out which one they should join or whether they should join any of them. 


### Thorin


Thorin downs his Darklake Brewery Stout, burps, and then sees a group of Duergar with curious stone weapons approaching. 


“I am Errde Blackskull, captain of the Stone Guards on the lake, and I must ask that you come to my office so we can talk.” 


Daz stares at her, “Are you threatening us?” 


Thorin grabs his sword and wonders where exactly they will run to because it’s not clear how they can beat the entire stone guard, but the effect Daz was hoping for is achieved. Errde is taken aback and smiles, “Of course not. It is a friendly conversation.” 


Thorin, worried that some faction might think they are joining with the Stone Guards, shouts, “It’s just a friendly meeting. Not that kind of meeting!” 


The Halfling smiles and touches his finger to his head as if to signal that Thorin has made the right move. 


A few minutes later, they are in the Overlake Hold, the local guard house. Errde brings them to a sitting room. Like everything in this town, it is austere. The chairs and table are made of stone. There is no color—the light is grey. And the room is just cold enough to make one feel they are deep underground. 


A subordinate brings some pastries and some warm liquid to drink, and after they have eaten, she speaks. 


“I have been tracking a particular Duergar named Droki. He lives in the West Cleft District, where the Derro live. If we were to go there in force, it would provoke a violent reaction. So we need someone who isn’t us to find him.”


Thorin is tempted to say yes, but Daz holds his arm, “Of course, but we would need remuneration for all of that plus our time.” 


“You want me to pay you?” 


“It makes it sound dirty, more like helping us help you.” 


Thorin is unconvinced. He is tempted to work for the Stone Guards. After all, they are friends of the Stone giants, but the warnings of the Halfing worry him. 


“Are we helping you? Or the city?” 


Errde’s face suddenly darkens. “There is something very wrong going on in my city. Some kind of corruption eats at the heart of the Deepking’s court. Droki is the key to uncovering that corruption. He is linked to the Council of Savants and maybe even elements of the Clan Lairds. Discovery of this conspiracy will earn me great favor with the Deepking. And when that happens, I swear you will get free and safe passage out of the city.”


Thorin pauses, “Look, we want to know if this is for the Stone Guards or the City?” 


“It is my job to protect the city from corruption. So yes, it is for the city.” 


She pauses, and Thorin notices that there seems to be something odd about her, “Do you have any proof of corruption?” 


Daz asks, “What is corruption?”


Thorin stares at him, confused, but remembers the previous encounter with the Duergar. 


Errde smiles, “ Things were not proceeding according to the rules of the market, of the bazaar. It starts with not obeying the rules. Then it proceeds to grift, then chaos, and then destruction.” 


Daz smiles, “Yes, there was much of that going on.” And he repeats the behaviors at the Blade Bazaar. 


Thorin is confused, and Daz mutters, “In this authoritarian, strict-as-rules city, what we saw is corruption.” 


Errde smiles, “You have found me proof!” 


Thorin says, “Yes!” 


“Excellent. As a reward, I offer you 175 gold pieces of equipment from our armory. When you bring me Droki and the proof I need, then I will give you 175 more.” 


She then smiles very evilly, “And I can offer one more thing.” 


Thorin looks at her, “If a particular group of Drow were to come looking for some escaped slaves, I could tell them that they are not here. As you think about which group to work with, remember I am the one that can guarantee your freedom.” 


# Chapter 17 Triple Agents
## 9th day of the 1st Tenday of Myrtul 1493
### Grygum


Grygum watches as Erdde Blackskull stands. She has an aura of paranoia fixated on her person, and seems disappointed. 


Armed with the scrolls he found amongst her goods in the armory, Grygum prepares to leave when she says something very odd, “I would appreciate it if you were to look for the empty scabbard killers. My underlings have reported their presence after finding bodies with puzzling wounds.” 


Grygum is perplexed. 


Erdde, almost as if she doesn’t want to draw too much attention, tries to act utterly nonchalantly, “Oh, just an old wives tale to frighten children. They kill people with their minds.” She pauses, “Of course, this is nonsense. They are just another figment of the people’s imagination. It’s more likely that they don’t exist, and instead, assassinations are being conducted by some agency in the government, and this is a cover.” 


The dwarf is intrigued and tries to probe some more. But Erdde is unwilling to reveal much. 


“I can’t look for what I don’t know.” 


That does the trick, and Errde brings one of her subordinates into the room, Grimholl Forgebrand.


“Holl to my friends, and you are not my friends,” he announces. 


Holl explains that the bodies were found with no exit wounds or entrance wounds. 


Grygum further probes and learns that two victims were Errde Blackskull’s clan members. 


Errde dismisses the idea that these are assassins, “My uncle could have died for any of many reasons: poison, old age, a bad heart. The clerics found no evidence of that on their bodies.” 


She then pauses, “Look, I am not foolish enough to believe they weren’t assassinated, but some children’s fable come back to life to kill them? Nonsense.”


Grygum is perplexed: dead bodies with no entrance or exit wounds, no evidence of foul play, just dead bodies. 


Daz, known for his fondness of novels, reads voraciously and has managed to get a copy of Milo Goodbarrel’s book detailing the events surrounding the war of the dragon. He notes: “Milo describes this kind of attack as a psychic blade attack. It leaves no trace. There is this one moment where the Kenku Whistler used the psychic blades to fake an attack by Milo on an enemy.” 


Grygum stares at him. 


“I liked the books. They were well written.” 
## 10th day of the 1st Tenday of Myrtul 1493
### Daz


The Ghohlbrorn’s Lair, to Daz’s refined sensibilities, offers the kind of accommodations one could expect from a Duergar: unpleasant, cold, and austere.         


There is a large, cold, damp dining room and communal chambers where you can sleep. 


The other escapees, except for Topsy and Turvy, have gone missing. 


“Wererats,” thinks Daz. 


Buppido continues to be bound and seems resigned to his fate. 


Jimjar has made a few friends and asks - “When do you expect us to be able to leave?” 


Daz explains that he wants to learn about the Keepers of the Flame, and Grygum wants to know about this Red Dragon that is kept in some kind of peculiar captivity by the Keepers of the Flame. 


When Jimjar tries to explain that they came here for supplies, and judging from the equipment the group has, they have them and that, “Perhaps we should leave?” 


Daz dismisses him, “I think gathering intelligence is just as important.” 


Jimjar shrugs and slumps into one of the beds. He sighs, “Very well.” 


Zalthir turns to Daz, “And I don’t think we want to cross Errde. She said she could set the Drow on us.” 


Daz leaves the inn and walks to the piers near the “inn.” On one of the piers, a Duergar man appears, looking into the darkness of the Darklake. Like most Duergar, his clothes are dark and plain, but there is the occasional flourish of wealth and taste. 


“And perhaps that’s why,” Daz thinks, “he’s being attacked.” 


Daz thinks that and realizes he’s not just thinking that but watching that. Two assassins, wearing face coverings and wielding glowing weapons, strike the other man. 


“Psychic weapons?” he wonders. 


As Daz watches, Grygum rushes one of the assassins, trying to toss him into the water. He fails. 


When Daz utters the mystical words, motes of light appear above his hand, and three fingers point at one of the assassins. A silent rush of air accompanies the flight of the magic missiles, and when they strike, a burst of light and a crackling sound fills the area. 


Daz watches as Zalthir covers the area with Darkness. 


“I can’t see. And this is why area of effect spells are useful,” he mutters.


Grygum rushes into the fight, and so does Thorin. 


Daz can judge where the Drow is, even in the Darkness. He speaks the words for scorching rays and feels the rush of intense heat as the fiery energy is manifested. He points with his index finger, uses his thumb to sight, squints, and lets the rays loose. They travel quickly, leaving a streak of heat haze. Zalthir’s darkness hides the flash of bright light, but the smell of burning flesh is not.
