### Zalthir


Zalthir stares at the merchant and the dead assassins. Zalthir is uncertain if they made the right decision. 


Thorin mutters, “We assume we picked the right guy. For all we know, he’s the evil dude.” 


The Duergar merchant has no wound on his body.


Zalthir scrutinizes him and concludes that Holl may not have been lying. 
Before Zalthir can stop him, Grygum heals the Duergar. 


“Thank you! I have no idea why they attacked me,” says the heaving Duergar. “Did they target me? Are they assassins?” 


Zalthir looks around for the weapons, finds none, but does find a charcoal drawing of the merchant on one of the bodies. 


He presents it to the Duergar. 


“Oh my, I was.” There is a pause, “I am Werz Saltbaron. And you did me a good turn. Come by the Shattered Spire tomorrow, and I will reward you. Today, I have places to be.” 


Zalthir watches as the Duergar becomes invisible. 


“Convenient.” 


Zalthir starts to rifle through the assassins' corpses and finds some coins, a pair of bloodstained gloves, and a box of candles. 


He notices they have a pleasant smell and passes them to Thorin. 


The dwarf smiles, “Scented candles!” And then he says, “God, what I wouldn’t do for a bath and listening to whale sounds.” 


Zalthir chuckles, “I could create that illusion for you.”


Thorin hoots. 


Just then, Zalthir hears a body falling into the water. Grygum has pushed the first corpse into the water. 


“We must get out of here before the guard shows up.” 


Zalthir agrees and helps push the other body into the water.  


The group finds a quiet corner and sits far away from the battle scene. And after resting, he heads out to the Keepers of the Flame.


Errde Blackskull’s passes let him and his friends through the gates that keep all non-Duergars out of the city. The guards who look at the passes are surprised but are not so surprised as to ask any questions. 


The Keepers of the Flame are in the far southeastern corner of the cave, and the journey is uneventful. 


As Zalthir walks, he reflects on the city's quiet and how the monks would be astounded at how peaceful it could be. “Having invisible ruthless guards helps.” He wonders if such a regime could be implemented. 


Finally, he arrives at the entrance, and there is Gartokkar. The Duergar priest wants to lead him to a building carved from stone just outside a monumental cave entrance. But the ground trembles slightly just then, and a thunderous voice echoes against every wall.


“Gartokkar,” the voice calls as a reptilian behemoth comes into view. It scales the color of lava, its bright yellow eyes glowing in the cave's shadows before coming into the light. You didn’t say I was having surfacers for dinner today.”


The dragon chuckles at his wit. His massive body gives the distinct impression that he is overweight, indicating eating habits that don’t bode well.


“Foreigners,” the duergar priest says with great reverence, “meet the Father of Flame, the Everburning, and the Foundry’s Heart — Themberchaud, the Wyrmsmith of Gracklstugh.”


The dragon roars, “I wish to speak to them alone.” 


Zalthir notices how Gartokkar isn’t pleased but points him forward. 


The dragon’s cavern is filled with a hoard of gems and coins. Sitting on top of it is a plump, overweight red dragon. 


Zalthir is stunned. He’s never seen such a thing. 


The Dragon bellows, “If I catch anyone spying, I will kill them.” 


And with that, he breathes fire in a circle around the cavern. When nobody dies or screams, the dragon laughs. 


The dragon turns to Zalthir, “You are a gold dragonborn?” 


“No, a bronze.”


“Good. I never liked gold dragons.” 


Zalthir stares at him and wonders how this fat, obviously out-of-shape red dragon ended up like that. And then, he wonders whether this red dragon could survive in the wild. It is so pampered that it probably has forgotten how to hunt. 


He questions Thorin and Grygum and seems satisfied with the answers. 
When it’s Daz’s turn to be questioned, the dragon asks if Daz is from Menzoberranzan. Zalthir wonders as well. Daz says he is. But Zalthir isn’t convinced that is the truth. 


The dragon laughs, “Excellent! You have no family associations and nobody that can be blackmailed.” 


Grygum shouts, “We have people who will come looking for us!” 


Zalthir nods, “Of course.” 


The dragon laughs, “Very well. I am Themberchaud, and I wish for you to be my agent. And as my agents, you will have my protection.” 


Zalthir overhears Daz and asks Grygum, “Do you think this dragon also plays chess? According to Milo Goodbarrel’s memoirs, chess played a significant role in negotiating with the metallic dragons.” 


“Deals with red dragons are never good deals,” thinks Zalthir. 


Daz is curious, “What must we do as agents?” 


The dragon whispers, “Your first mission is to do whatever the Keepers of the Flame ask you to, but report to Themberchaud first.” 


### Thorin 


Having lived with giants, Thorin has picked up the peculiar antipathy towards dragons that giants have. And this red dragon is triggering him.


But even he notices that Themberchaud wasn’t asking him to be an agent; he was telling him he was an agent.


“Its ego is so fragile that it can’t even wait to hear an answer of yes.”  


The dragon roars, “Gartokkar, come.” 


And the Duergar priest shuffles insides, “Yes?”


“Give these humanoids some of the gold badges,” growls the dragon, inches from Thorin’s face. “And the rest of you do what Gartokkar says.” 


Gartokkar hands out some gold badges. Thorin weighs it in his hands. Daz turns to him and asks, “How much gold is this?” 
Thorin follows Gartokkar outside the cave and asks Daz, “Did we find ourselves working for a faction without much choice?” 


Daz, who has experience with the twisted, machiavellian politics of the Drow, replies, “The faction thinks we are working for them. Whether we do is up to us.” 


Grygum, standing next to Thori,n mutters, “I suppose we are double agents, or is it triple agents? We work for the Stone Guards and the Keepers of the Flame.”


Thorin is exasperated and almost shouts, “I am sorry, I can’t deal with these factions. I can’t keep track of who we are working for and which faction we are double-crossing. I want to be my faction.” 


But he manages to keep his frustration bottled up just long enough to make it to Gartokkar’s chambers.


The Duergar priest sits down in his chamber and says, “I am so delighted to see that you accepted Themberchaud’s offer to be an agent of ours.”


Thorin is about to explode, but Daz gets their first, “We never technically accepted an offer. He assumed we accepted. We would like to understand the nature of the offer?” 


“What are the rights and responsibilities for this position?” growls Thorin, outraged to be working for a dragon. 


Gartokkar begins - “The powers of the Keepers of the Flame derive an equal measure from our psionic abilities, the leadership of the Deepking, and our influence over Themberchaud. We lost face when the Gray Ghosts stole the valuable red dragon egg that would hatch Themberchaud’s replacement. Our war with the Thieve’s guild has been ongoing. The Gray Ghosts stole the egg and created a great disturbance in the Underdark. It feels like a hole has been torn through the world.” 


Thorin thinks the words about holes are just a flex of vocabulary by psionics and ignores them. Instead, he asks, “Does Themberchaud know about this egg?” 


“He doesn’t.” 


“But we were hired by him?”


Gartokkar smiles conspiratorially, “Themberchaud thinks we work for him. What Themberchaud doesn’t realize is that he works for us. It’s good that you told us this about Themberchaud. The egg is for when Themberchaud moves on. His replacement.”


“Moves on? How does he move on? Do you kill him?” 


Gartokkar looks appalled, “Of course not! Eventually, the Dragon moves on because he wants to see more of the world.”


Grygum turns to Thorin, “It’s like when parents say that the pet puppy left even when it dies.” 


Gartokkar continues, ignoring the comment, “We have identified an agent of the Grey Ghosts. His name is Droki.”


Thorin remembers that this is the same person Errde, Captain of the Stone Guards, is looking for. 


Gartokkar says, “As you have already accepted to work for Themberchaud, let me give you this holy symbol of Laduguer and these gold pins featuring Themberchaud’s profile. With them, you can travel within Gracklestugh, but there are limits.”


Thorin is annoyed, “What if we say no?” 


“Well we will turn you over to the Stone Guards.”


“Under what charge?” 


“Very well. As Gartokkar Xundorn, Custodian of the Flame, let me enumerate a list of potential transgressions that the dwarf, Thorin, has committed, which could warrant significant punitive action within the laws of Gracklstugh.


Let me see; I can prepare just such a document. He pulls out a piece of parchment and starts to read off it, adding Thorin’s name in the blank spaces. 
1. **Public Disturbance and Disorder:** Thorin was involved in the altercation with the deranged stone giant. While he claims to have wanted to subdue the giant, his actions could be interpreted as contributing to the ensuing public disorder. Creating such disturbances within the city is a serious offense.
1. **Interference with City Watch:** Thorin attempted to influence and direct the actions of the Duergar City Watch during the aforementioned incident with the stone giant. While he claims he was trying to help, any interference with the watch's official duties can be seen as obstruction and a challenge to their authority.
1. **Questioning Authority:** Thorin has repeatedly questioned the authority and motives of various Duergar individuals and factions, including the Keepers of the Flame. Such questioning can be perceived as dissent and disrespect, which is not tolerated within Gracklstugh's hierarchical society.
1. **Unauthorized Access:** Depending on his movements within the city, Thorin may have entered areas restricted to non-Duergar citizens without proper authorization, even with the passes. Any unauthorized access to restricted areas is a violation of city ordinances.
1. **Association with Undesirables:** Thorin has been seen associating with individuals of questionable character, including other surface dwellers and individuals who may be considered enemies of the state. Such associations can raise suspicion and lead to accusations of conspiracy, aiding, and abEttin g.
1. **Possession of Unauthorized Items:** If Thorin is found to own any items considered contraband or restricted within Gracklstugh, such as certain weapons or magical items, he will violate the law.
1. **Suspicion of Espionage:** Given his questioning and interest in the city's affairs, including the Keepers of the Flame and Themberchaud, Thorin is suspected of espionage or gathering intelligence for potentially hostile entities. This is a grave offense with severe consequences.
1. **General Suspicion:** As a non-Duergar, Thorin is already subject to suspicion and scrutiny within Gracklstugh. Any deviation from expected behavior or any action that could be interpreted as threatening to the city's stability can lead to arrest and imprisonment.
According to the penal code, the interpretation and enforcement of these laws are at the discretion of the Duergar authorities. Even seemingly minor infractions can be used to justify imprisonment if deemed necessary.’


Gartokkar pauses, “Is that enough?” 


Thorin stares at him. “I am just putting all of our cards on the table. So if we get arrested, we will have to tell the Stone Guards about the egg, right?” 


Gartokkar turns dark and then smiles, “You joke? Sharing that would be a disaster.” 


“For whom?” 


Gartokkar looks at him, “Just find me the egg and the proof of the Gray Ghosts.” 


As they stand outside the building that houses Gartokkar’s office, Daz turns to Thorin while looking at his collection of badges, “So we flash the right one at the right time?” 


Thorin nods. And then he has a peculiar glint in his eye. He turns to Grygum, “I have an idea. These factions are all trying to play us against each other, and this Dragon is one of us. So what if we ride this Dragon out of here, laying waste to everything behind us?” 


Grygum smiles, “As a cleric of Bahamut, I am appalled at how they treat Themberchaud. Let’s do it.” 


# Chapter 18 Badge of the Wyrmsmith: Now Accepting Application
## 10th day of the 1st Tenday of Myrtul 1493
### Thorin 


“The plan to lay waste to Gracklstugh and its slavers is a good plan,” thinks Thorin. But before he can do that, he must see the Stone Giants. 


“Perhaps they can help,” he thinks.


From Thermbechaud’s cave to the Cairngorm Cavern, Thorin and his friends must traverse through the city of Duergar, where no one but the Duergar is allowed.


But the badges of the Keepers of the Flame or Stone Guard are enough to stop anyone from asking too many questions. 


A long tunnel opens in the eastern wall south of Laduguer’s Furrow. The tunnel is gigantic, even by the massive size of Gracklstugh. And the rock is well polished. And sitting on a rock is a very large and very venerable stone giant. 


Thorin stands in front of him. He remembers that Stone Giants are not one to be rushed into a conversation.


The giant stares at him. And then raises an eyebrow. 


Thorin realizes this is his opening and tries in his best giant to offer his condolences again. 


The giant sighs, “Yes, it was a tragedy. You did not try to kill him. But you did try to stop him. He was driven mad.” 


Just as Thorin is about to ask another question, Daz asks - “Do you know what’s driving everyone mad?” 


And the giant stares at Daz, and for a moment, Thorin worries that the Giant will never speak again, but he sighs, and says - “Something evil stirs in the Underdark. The rock itself cries in pain and horror, and a madness creeps from the blackest depths. Pay heed to the signs surrounding you. A cave with two faces. Rock devoured, and the land overgrown. The pebble believes itself flesh. The earth rejects its wards, and the tunnels shake in fury. By these portents, you shall know of evil’s presence and of evil’s face. This is what the stones tell me.”


Thorin tries not to roll his eyes. Stone Giants are cryptic in the best of times. 


The giant turns to Thorin, trying to show his disapproval to Daz’s impetuousness. “Do you have any questions that I may answer?” 


And so Thorin learns from Hgramm that the best way to the Dreamlands is through the city of the Deep gnomes. Thorin is pleased to have Jimjar's claims vetted. He then asks about the tunnels underneath the city. 


Hgraam sighs again. 


“Many have told the Deep King that what goes underneath the city affects what goes on in his city. And what goes on in his city affects what goes on below. And much of what goes on below is evil. The Deep King has tried to keep order and control, and the more he trie,s the more the order escapes and tries to take the city from him.” 


Thorim immediately understands what’s going on. The Deep King has relied on his secret invisible police to control the city, and so opposition has gone underneath it. Thorin also understands why they are underneath the city. To get to the tunnels, the Duergar would have to go through the Derro, and that would trigger a bloodbath. 


Zalthir turns to Thorin, “The Stone Giant is particularly attuned to the rocks? So what we have seen as localized appearances of demons is not localized. The demons at Valkenvylve, the Beholder in the Spidersilk caves, the demonic manta rays, and Demogorgon, all of this is no coincidence.” 


Grygum whispers, “The end of the great sundering ended the era that allowed the gods to walk in Faerun freely. It’s why the Cult of Tiamat had to resort to such an extraordinary ritual to bring her into the prime material plane. That so many demons are walking freely is not normal. There is some kind of powerful magic that has enabled this.” 


Thorin wonders if this has anything to do with the Faerzess, which has affects his sanity. 


“What about the Grey Ghosts?” 


Hgramm sighs, “Grey Ghosts? The Deep King creates so many enemies. He used to be so calm. He and I would watch the stones grow. But something has happened to him. He has become paranoid towards old and new friends.” 


Thorin asks, “Is there some new advisor?” 


“Yes, Shal, an advisor of his. Ever since they became friends, The Deep King has been unwilling to listen to any sage advice.” 


Daz asks hopefully, “Do you know anything about him?” 


“I have asked to meet Shal, but they refuse.” 


The giant stands up, looks at Daz, “You are too hasty. And I have rocks to tend to. But before I go, I have a gift.” His assistant brings a 19 inch shard of quartz crystal. Thorin looks at it confused. 


![image]()


“This is the stonespeaker crystal, with it you can cast Speak with Animals, Speak with the Dead, and Speak with Plants. It will also help you cast divinations.” 


And with that, he heads back into his cave. 
### Zalthir 


Zalthir likes the stone giants. They speak little. They ponder and then they consider their words. Perhaps there is something that even his monastic order could learn from their subtlety and patience. 


He must bring that up when he returns to the surface world. 


But now he must find Droki. 
From the Cairngorm Cavern, Laduguerer’s Furrow is just a short distance. Looking around, he notices how this is so spotlessly clean in its style. At either edge of this Furrow is an entrance. And past that entrance, he can see a slum. 


Droki, he is told, is to the west. 


So to the west he goes. 


As he walks, he thinks how curious it is that this Derror is a courier for so many factions. But when he gets to the Derro slums, it’s obvious why. The Derro slums are dangerous to anyone. Even from here, it’s evident that the homes of the Derro are mostly burrows carved into the walls and simple structures piled atop one another. The district's dirty and cluttered streets clearly formed as dwellings spread and came together, not as a product of planning. The contrast with the clean, perfect Duergar dwellings is obvious. And the resentment and hatred become apparent. 

And now, why Errde Blackstaff and the Keeper of the Flames were so anxious to find a non-Duergar to come here is clear. 


He observes, “Droki is someone all of the factions trust and can get to the Whorlstone Caverns safely through that.” And he points to the Derro slums. 
### Grygum


“Let’s get Buppido.”  


Zalthir urges caution, but Grygum is determined. 


And so they head back to Ghohlbrorn’s Lair, where they find Jimjar playing a game of chance. The gnome hears that they want Buppido and points them to a room out back, where a sad Buppido is still tied up. 


Thorin asks Buppido if he knows who Droki is, and Buppido laughs. Grygum is a bit embarrassed when Thorin asks the question, thinking that not every Derro knows every other Derro, but Buppido knows him. The reason is that Droki can be trusted to deliver messages to the groups in the Whorlstone caverns and keep secrets. 


Grygum asks him if can tell them something about the Derro community. At that, Buppido becomes enraged. He screams about the Council of Savants who promised freedom and failed to deliver freedom. 


“I have to get back to save my people. The divine mission requires that I go back! The Council of Savants will fail my people. I must go and save them!” 
Grygum turns to his allies, “We need to get him to show us the way to the Whorlstone caverns. If we go around poking for things, it’s unclear what could happen.” 


Zalthir is unconvinced. Thorin mutters that Buppido has already committed murder once. 


As Grygum cuts him loose, Thorin whispers, “If you betray us, I will gut you.” 


Buppido smiles, “The divine plan tells me I must help you!” 


And so he leads them to the western gate of Laduguer’s Furrow. He mutters, “The duergar built a series of guardhouses to keep an eye on their derro slaves living in the West Cleft. These were abandoned when Deepking Tarngardt, grandfather of the current monarch, who liberated the derro, allowing them to spread from the West Cleft District into the East Cleft District. The guardhouses now stand empty and are an excellent vantage point for us to wait for Droki.” 


And so Grygum waits. 
![image]()


As he is about to doze off, Buppido nudges him, “There.”


The dirty derro is easily recognizable: a pale face under a floppy hat fitted with two tentacle-like things that bob up and down in time with his brisk pace. He mutters a repetitive series of phrases at different volumes, failing to notice Grygum. “Droki is late! They will be so angry! Stupid, stupid, stupid! Delays, blocks, procrastination, obstructions, pfah! No time, no rhyme, not mine! No! Time!”


Grygum gets up and follows Droki into Derro city. 
As he passes through the gates, the stench in the air changes from acrid and metallic to fetid and repugnant, the fires of industry replaced by squalor. The homes in this part of Gracklstugh are crudely carved from the rock or are just holes in the walls, arranged in no apparent order. The chatter in the air is unnerving, with hundreds of derro muttering, screaming at each other, and otherwise reveling in their insanity. Those who spot Grygum look at him with a burning hatred.


Grygum is relieved he has Buppido, whose presence seems to temper the anger. 


As for Droki, he isn’t in a rush. But he is walking too quickly for a Derro, as if there was something magical about his pace. Grygum observes that Droki also doesn’t seem to care if anyone is following him. 


Droki wanders between the various houses and merchants of the Derro, as if there is no purpose to his walking. He mutters to himself and to any Derro whom he says. 


And then Droki stops between a cluster of hovels in West Cleft and turns. Grygum follows him. Against a wall are some scraps of cloth, sheets of canvas and moldy boxes. Droki lifts the scrap of cloth,  pushes the gray sheets of canvas to the side, revealing a narrow fissure in the chasm wall. He steps over the moldy boxes, and jumps into the crack. Just as he disappears into the cavern, a wisp of eerie fog floats out. 


At that point, Buppido rushes towards the entrance.


Grygum is tempted to stop him, but he notices that there are many eyes on him and that detaining a Derro could turn into a fight. 


For a moment, Grygum wonders what to do, and then, realizing that standing in front of a secret entrance isn’t the best place for an Orc, ancestral enemy of the Dwarf, he moves quickly into the caverns. 


### Daz 


Daz ponders how the Duergar deal with their slaves and compares it to how the Drow of Menzoberanzan do it. 


He shakes his head. There is no good way to have slaves. Slaves are always a problem. “Free people are the basis of any society,” he concludes. 


The narrow corridor from the West Cleft opens into a long cavern lined with stalactites and stalagmites. Water drips from the stalactites, forming small pools on the floor. The glow of faerzress casts an eerie soft light across this cavern, swirling into spiral patterns and casting dancing shadows from the jagged pillars lining the walls. The air smells and tastes slightly metallic, and the sound around you is strangely muted. The dripping of water makes no echo, as if Daz stood in open air.


Daz hears footsteps to the north and looks. There in the distance is Droki. He’s tempted to race after him, but notices that Droki's path is very well worn and marked with junk that the Derro drops. The Derro’s predictability is precisely why everyone uses him. 


Droki heads through a cave to the north-west of the main entrance cave. Daz looks into a cave that leads to the southwest.  As he ventures into the cavern, a stench of rotting meat rises. The floor is carpeted with humanoid remains in varying stages of decomposition, arranged in a spiral pattern around the cave’s center. An off-key humming comes from a hunched figure working busily at something on the floor.


“Oh, there you are!” The figure is Daz’s old friend Buppido. Buppido wipes his hands on his vest and smiles viciously. “I didn’t expect you to find me here, with my shrine nearly finished! And power! My faithful are finally honoring me! Are you …? Yes. Yes, I sense that you are ready to receive my truth into your hearts!”


Daz is flabbergasted. Zalthir asks, “Weren’t you with us just a few seconds ago?” 


Buppido smiles, “Do you want to see my shrine?” 


Daz approaches warily. Thorin has his sword drawn. 


Alright, let's get back into the action and narrate the battle with Buppido in the caves, from Daz's perspective, in the present tense and third-person:


Daz shifts his weight, taking in the scene. Just moments ago, they were following the muttering Droki, and now, they’re facing Buppido, who has somehow manifested a macabre altar of bones and skeletons. Buppido's earlier eccentricities have morphed into full-blown madness, and Daz feels a knot of apprehension tighten in his gut. This is escalating quickly, and not in a good way.


Buppido shrieks, his voice cracking with manic energy. He brandishes some makeshift weapon and charges, a wild glint in his eyes. "You will finally give me the worship I deserve!" he yells, his words echoing in the cavern. Daz knows this is no longer just strange behavior; this is a dangerous threat. The chaotic brawl is about to begin.


Knowing his strengths lie in spells, Daz focuses. He observes the cluster of skeletons around Buppido; they’re practically begging for an area-of-effect spell. With a practiced gesture and a muttered incantation, Daz casts Fairie Fire. Suddenly, three skeletons are marked, and an ethereal glow surrounds them. Daz knows that anyone who attacks these specific skeletons now has an advantage. He’s just given his allies a crucial edge. “The three you see marked,” Daz announces, “your attacks are with advantage.”


Thorin, eager as ever, wastes no time. The dwarf charges forward, closing with one of the skeletons. Daz watches as Thorin lands a solid blow, adding to the chaos. Zalthir, never one to shy away from unusual tactics, plunges the area into darkness. Daz understands the intent—to disrupt the skeletons and disorient Buppido. It’s a bold move, and the flickering light and deep shadows add to the unsettling atmosphere.


Confusion reigns for a moment. Some of the skeletons blunder blindly in the darkness, stumbling around aimlessly. One skeleton, however, manages to take a shot at Grygum with its crossbow. Daz sees Grygum flinch as the bolt hits, a testament to their constant danger. Buppido rushes at Thorin with a hooked spear but misses wildly, his attack fueled more by fury than skill.


Grygum, ready with his holy symbol, prepares to turn undead. Daz knows this could be a game-changer, but Zalthir's darkness complicates things. A brief exchange leads to Grygum holding his action, waiting for the darkness to shift so that more skeletons are visible. It's a clever coordination, and Daz appreciates the tactical thinking. 


And it works. The cleric’s words of power overwhelm the skeletal minions of Buppido. The battle was evenly matched, but now it will become a slaughter. 


With the chaos still unfolding, Daz knows it’s time to deal directly with Buppido. He focuses his arcane energy, feeling the familiar surge within him. “Magic missiles,” he thinks, visualizing the shimmering darts. With a flick of his wrist, three bolts of magical force streak through the air, each unerringly finding its mark on Buppido. The derro cries out in pain and then dies. 


Daz stares at Buppido’s corpse and mutters, “Your divine mission is now over.” 

Session 19 
## 10th day of the 1st Tenday of Myrtul 1493
### Grygum


The blood-spattered remains of Buppido lie scattered amongst the bones that made up the crazed Derro’s hideout. 


“He was a crazy one, but he was our crazy one,” mutters a sad Thorin.


The cleric of Bahamut nods. 


And as he prepares to pray for Buppido’s soul, a ghostly head pops up. The head is that of a Svirfneblin, whose appearance is hurt by the gaping wound that looks like it was made just yesterday.


“He’s dead?” 


Grygum tries not to stare. 


The head rolls around, flopping into place, and stares at Buppido’s corpse, “Wonderful!” 


The ghostly gnome emerges from the ground and announces his name, “Pelek, at your service if you will be at mine.” 


Grygum, whose interest in linguistic studies and origins of names and how they intersect with cultures across the ages, is startled by such an odd name. He then recalls that the Gnomes tend to name themselves after things and that many of their names are onomatopoeia of the sounds of those things, and he thinks that perhaps it’s after a pick or an axe. But he’s uncertain so he asks, “What does that name mean?” 


The ghost affects a blushing expression. And then begins to explain - “My father, god rest his soul, never liked the name. My mother named me after an actor. And well, there was always this doubt about the origin of the name and my lineage, which created a lot of friction in my family. And since you asked. I had a delightful childhood, except when it came to my name. My father was always very jealous, and there was always an undercurrent of hurt and shame in my name and how it affected my parents. I suppose that’s why I ended up as a merchant, and became friends with Buppido and ignored the tell-tale signs of his incipient murderous rampage.” 


“Are you an actor?”


“Why, thank you! Yes, I tried. But I never had the knack for it. Or was I worried I had too much of a knack for it and would engage in self-sabotage?” The ghost notices Grygum’s traveling companions are exasperated. It shifts the conversation: “But the story of my parents and their marital strife and the circumstances of their marriage, although fascinating, are not my most pressing topic. I need a favor.” The ghosts floats over some bones and points at them, “These bones are my bones, and I would appreciate you folks collecting my bones and bringing them to Blingdenstone.” 


Thorin sighs, “Classic Buppido.” 


The ghost is delighted, “Yes! He killed me and cut my body up into the pieces you see here. And I have been stuck here ever since. We were business partners. He was working with a faction of Derro known as the Council of Savants. Buppido said he could move product out of the city without dealing with the Duergar taxes. And well, he needed a supplier who could act. And well, you know, that tickled me pink. He promised to prove his point and brought me here.” 


Grygum wonders, “Did something happen?” 


“Now that you mention it. I did notice that the Faerzess glowed brightly, and after that, Buppido’s temperament changed. He became convinced he was some kind of divine figure. The derro do go mad, and I assumed it was that. But the Faerzess glow was unmistakable. It was almost as if it was being sucked out, and went dark and then came back brighter than before. No one knows what the Faerzess is. And so I assumed it was something that happens.”


Grygum gets excited - “When?” 


“A few months ago. Why? And this is unimportant. What’s important is that you will get my bones to Blingdenstone.”  


Grygum looks at Daz, Daz looks at Grygum. Daz wonders out loud, “So the Faerzess is a substance that makes teleportation into a region impossible.” 


“Yes.” 


“Then if it blinked, could it have - I dunno - broken the walls between the planes?” 


Grygum looks at Daz. 


The ghost sighs, “That sounds like a ghost story. The Faerzess blinked, and then monsters from the Abyss appeared. Next, you’ll tell me it was part of some mage’s plot involving demonic powers and the world's end.” 


Grygum coughs, “About your bones?” 


“Excellent, my bones. And my hand. Seems it went off scurrying about. There is a family ring on it, an obsidian ring of some value. You can keep it if you find the hand.” 


“Do we need the hand?” 


“Oh no. A few bones will be fine.” 


### Thorin


The dwarf is annoyed at the ghost. He feels he is being taken for granted and nothing has been offered in return for this help. 


“Is the ring magical?” 


“No. But if I said otherwise, would it encourage you more?” 


Thorin growls, “It wasn’t powerful enough to keep you alive.” 


“I was surprised.”


“How long have you been here?” 


“I don’t know,” he shrugs his shoulders, and his head flops off. He sighs apologetically, puts his head back on his neck, and continues, “Less than a year? Telling time in this cavern is hard. And being unable to move more than 30 feet from your bones makes it harder. And as a ghost, the usual time markers don’t apply.”  


“Do you know anything about Droki?”


“The derro messenger? No. I was told that he works for the Council of Savants. He’s very peculiar. Some say he’s mad. I know many people like that. My cousin always wears the same clothes, follows the same path, and does the same things.” 


Thorin sighs.


“Look, I have been trapped here for some time with a madman. I had to take stock of my life, and have been working to improve.”


“Always working on yourself.”


Pelek sighs, “Yes.” 


“It’s a struggle.” 


“And when you are a ghost, it’s a bit harder, what with my fixation on stopping being a ghost?” 


Thorin mutters, “This guy wants us to take his bones to Blingdenstone and hasn’t helped us.” 


He takes mental notes: "He’s confirmed that something weird has happened in the Underdark, and that it’s connected to the Faerzess. But I knew that. And it’s not like he’s given us any useful information. Time for this to change.” 


So Thorin puffs himself up to his full height, walks up to the ghost and shouts, “Now listen here!”


The ghost laughs. “Overbrighters.” 


Seeing the ghost laugh, Daz tries to scare him, but that scary face works better with his younger siblings than with a murdered ghost. 


The ghost sighs, “Look, I don’t want to possess you. It’s awkward. And frankly, I like you. The city of Blingdenstone is your exit. There are many routes to the Overbrite from there. And to help you a little bit, when you get there, make sure to deny any association to Lolth, or Menzoberanzan, and make any references to the number eight or spiders.” 


Thorin looks at him, “How do you avoid the number eight?” 


“Just don’t have anything on your person that counts - obviously - to eight.” 


“Now, can we work together, and will you collect my bones?”
### 
Zalthir


Zalthir doubles back to the entrance of the cave where they found Buppido. To the northeast is a cave with a pool of water. To the north is another cave and the obvious trail of Droki. 


“Following the path of the quarry is the center of …” he mutters and stumbles, unable to remember the appropriately vague and incomprehensible teaching of his monastic order to refocus his attention after enduring the endless banter between the ghost, the dwarf, and the orc. 


He walks into the northern cavern and sees Droki’s obvious trail. The Derro is a creature of habit.


A well-trodden path ends at a crack in the wall, with mushrooms to either side of the crack. The crack is too small for anyone to fit into. Zalthir looks around and realizes that the Derro ate some mushrooms. 


“I don’t see how we go past this.” 
Thorin marches past Zalthir, ‘I am going to smash our way through.”


Zalthir stops him. He thinks, “This place used to be where hippies hid out. Now it has become a den of vipers aimed at the mad Deepking.” But he says, “We must be quiet. There are many enemies about.”


He can tell the dwarf has heard him, as he sits down deflated. 


Grygum pulls out a bone, “Hey Pelek.”


“Yes?” 


“Can you look into the crack?” 


“Why yes, yes I can.”


Zalthir stares at the ghost as it merges into the rock, and then waits for it to reappear. 


The ghost sighs, “A tiny tunnel. Tiny all the way through.” Then the ghost pauses, “Oh, look at that Pygmywort and Bigwig.” 


Zalthir looks at him, “And?” 


“Pygmywort is the mushroom with a one-inch-long stem and a stubby blue cap with white dots, and Bigwig is the four-inch-tall mushroom with a thin stem and a wide purple cap. The first one shrinks you, like the effect of a reduce spell, and the latter grows you, like the effect of an enlarge spell.” 


Zalthir wonders what to do, and during that time, Grygum impulsively swallows a Pygmywort and shrinks. 


Unfortunately, he can’t squeeze through the crack.  


Zalthir stares at the crack. “We are at a dead end.” 


Pelek nods, his head flopping off. “I am so sorry.” He puts his head back on. “Yes, Buppido mentioned that there were tunnels that the derro used to go through the whorlestone tunnels. He also talked about these magical mushrooms. It's quite fascinating.” 


Zalthir wonders why a monastic order devoted to silence only taught him how to make people blind, and not how to make them silent. 


### Daz


“It is my time!” announces Daz. 


The drow mage marches towards the lake in the cave where they found Buppido and the cave with the crack that Droki used. 


He walks down the tunnel, which slopes downwards, towards the edge of a vast expanse of water. 


This is no mere puddle but a large pool filling the cavern ahead, stretching nearly one hundred feet to the opposite shore. The most striking feature of this pool is its unnervingly black water. The darkness is absolute; nothing can be seen beneath its surface, hiding whatever lies within its murky depths. Despite its dark and foreboding appearance, the water is surprisingly heated by a thermal spring, making it pleasantly warm to his touch. 


Then, casts a spell with a flourish, and the water freezes. He turns to his friends, “Well, come on!”


They stare at him and quickly jump on the ice. He then proceeds to cast another block of ice, and they jump from block to block, eventually landing on the other side of the lake. 


As they land safely, he smiles. 


And he waits for polite applause. There is none, but Thorin slaps his back. A friendly slap on the back.


And Grygum can’t stop saying “Wow!” 


As for Zalthir, Zalthir is quiet. 


Another patch of Bigwig and Pygmywort mushrooms and Droki’s trail is on the other side of the lake. A trail that heads east through a thicket of fungi. Blocking the tunnel juncture is a dense fungi forest. The path ahead vanishes into a thicket where the tallest specimens reach about five feet, creating a wall of fungal life that requires effort to pass through.
This isn't a silent place; as Daz approaches, a hissing sound begins to rise. It sounds like uncounted tiny voices whispering in tongues he doesn't understand.” 


Daz wonders if he should advance.


Thorin turns to Pelek, “Look, I am not saying why I know, but there are some kinds of mushrooms that may have a psychedelic effect so I would hold our breath.” 


Pelek hears Thorin’s comment and laughs, “There’s nothing psychedelic about that sound. It’s the normal effect of wind blowing through a fungal thicket.” The ghost then, as politely and contemptuously as possible, says, “Overbrighters.” 


Daz is unnerved by the auditory experience caused by air simply whistling through perforated mushrooms within the thicket, and let’s Thorin lead on. 


As they advance, Daz notices that the thicket is full of mushrooms. “Food for later,” he mutters and pulls out his blade. He picks up some barrelstalk, a large, cask-shaped fungus that stores water, bluecap for making flour, ripplebark that tastes good toasted, trillimac that can be used for scrolls and makes a bread-like substance that can be rolled up, waterorb for storing water, and zurkwhood for making things. 


As the group navigates the forest, he points out Nightlights—mushrooms that grow to 15 feet and shed light in a 15-foot-by-15-foot circle. When they are touched or cut, they stop glowing.


“It is so unlike the ormu,” he reflects on silently. “That can be crushed into a paste and used as a light source. Not the Nightlight.”


“Watch out,” he shouts to Thorin. The dwarf was close to a two-foot-tall toadstool with orange and red stripes across its beige cap known as “the devil’s mushroom,” or a timmask. Uprooting the mushroom can cause madness. An effect he remembers all too well.  


Zalthir asks about a two-foot-tall mushroom, and Daz smiles, “Why, that’s a torchstalk. It has a combustible cap and can burn for 24 hours when lit.”  


Although the experience of finding such a rich collection of fungi is a delight for Daz, who, as a magic user, has been trained to learn about all of the magical and near-magical properties of fungi of the Underdark, it is a delight, centipedes ruin it. 


Not one centipede, but swarms of them.  


Daz watches as the centipedes emerge, a shiver running down his spine. Zalthir is quick to act, throwing punches at one of the swarms. "Brave," Daz thinks, "or reckless." He decides to try his hand at spellcasting. "Toll the Dead," he mutters, focusing his magical energy. He watches intently as the spell is cast, but his hope quickly fades as the centipedes seem unfazed. 


"No!" Daz exclaimed inwardly, "They saved!" He can't believe it; his attempt has failed completely.


The centipedes, now emboldened, began to swarm over Zalthir. Daz winces, imagining the crawling, tickling sensation on his skin. It is a sight he finds deeply unsettling. Grygum then steps up, casting "Tasha's Caustic Brew." Daz watches with anticipation, but once again, the centipedes somehow manage to avoid the brunt of the spell. "Seriously?" Daz mutters under his breath. Were these bugs unusually lucky, under the protection of some bug god, or was he just having an off day?


Just then, Thorin charges in, swinging with his weapon. Daz perks up as Thorin actually manages to strike one of the swarms, dealing a significant blow. "Yes! There you go!" he thinks, a glimmer of hope returning. But even with Thorin's success, the centipedes keep coming, relentless and unsettling. Daz finds himself scanning his spell list, second-guessing his choices. "Maybe 'Burning Hands' would have been better?" he muses, or perhaps something with a wider area of effect. He feels a slight unease, wondering if his spells are just ineffective or if he needs to re-strategize. All the while, he keeps scratching at his arms, feeling the phantom sensation of bugs despite knowing there were none on him.


# Chapter 18.05 A Long List of Potential Transgressions
## 10th day of the 1st Tenday of Myrtul 1493
### Thorin
The Centipedes are dead. Thorin, kin of giants, stands over them. Their crunchy, small bodies splattered and smashed. 


The rush of the battle is over, and although he knows a barbarian who will rage until every living thing dies, that is not him. 


“Are there any more?” 


Zalthir mutters, “No.” 


“I need a rest.” 


And just as he is about to rest, the cleric speaks, “Let me help with that.” The words of prayer to the cleric’s dragon god fill the forest, and a few moments later, it’s like he has rested. 


“Where to now?”


Zalthir mutters, “We were chasing Droki.” 


But Droki’s trail is anything but difficult to follow. The Derro is a creature of habit. 
### Zalthir


The cave to the southwest beckons. And so he heads out to see what can be found. 


The tunnel opens into a natural cave, where several fungi dance to a silent tune. Three are five feet tall, and the others are half as tall. One of the small ones stands apart from the rest. 


“These are myconids. And those little ones are sprouts, like stool.”


He stares at their movements, “Stool described myconids and never described them as dancing frantically.” 


The madness of the Underdark has affected them as well. 


Behind the myconids are two spore servants; from their looks, they are quagoths. For a moment, he remembers Prince Derendil, the mad quagoth, who was a polymorphed elf. 


“They look harmless enough.” 


When he tells his allies of his discovery, they agree that perhaps this is an adventure for another time. 


And so he continues through the eerie fungi forest, following Droki’s trail.  


As he exits the forest, a curious creature appears and follows the cave north. The creature looks like a mushroom cap with two tentacles that have eye sockets at their end. And below the mushroom cap are tentacles that float. The creature vents gases, making a “flumph” sound. 


It smiles and starts speaking directly into his head. 


The voice is high-pitched and pleasant. 


“Hello!” 


Zalthir masks his feelings well. The monks taught him how to do that, and he was very good at it. 


“You see a creature you have never seen before and have nothing to say? At the very least, don’t you want to know why I am speaking directly into your skulls?” It then giggles.  


Thorin starts speaking: “Everybody we come across here in the Underdark has tried to kill us, so we are wary.” 


The creature turns dark blue. “Understandable. Well, I am known as a flumph. Or at least that’s what others call us because we make a flumph sound when we move.”


The creature turns pink, “You didn’t make the obvious joke! How wonderful!” Then it pauses, turns green, “You don’t know what a flumph is?” 


Zalthir turns to Daz, “Perhaps he does?” 


Thorin blurts, “I am not trying to assume every Drow knows every creature of the Underdark, because that would be racist, but … Daz?” 


The creature turns pink. “How amusing.” Then it turns light blue, “I am a flumph. And my kind feeds on the psychic energy of creatures. We aren’t parasitic like the Mind Flayers; we feed on the residual background energies. And we do tend to meet one too many Mind Flayers. And Gith. Only the evil creatures.” 


Zalthir has heard that one before, but the Flumph answers Thorin's question of how they determine what is evil by saying, “Well, the evildoers are typically torturing, abusing, feeding, or doing other horrible things.” 


He notices that the creature turns a dark blue. 


Zathir wonders, “Have you seen anything evil?”


And just then, Zalthir’s head is flooded with images. 


“There you saw it! A chamber with a circular pathway and a pyramid. The one known as Plinki has found this mighty and tasty obelisk and has been trying to make it do something evil.” 


Grygum’s horror at the egg breaks into his voice, “What are the strange markings on the egg?” 


“Plinki has recently converted to the Cult of Demogorgon and wishes to turn the egg into a dual-headed dragon that he can give to his master to ride!” 


Just then, the Flumph takes on the teal color. 


“I feel so much better!” 


Zalthir can sense that Thorin is unhappy when he says, “You just trauma dumped on us!” 


“Trauma Dump? Why yes! That’s what I do. I let out all the unpleasant memories inside and into the heroes' minds, and now I feel better!” 


The creature turns green. “You will deal with them? You are heroes?” 


It then turns purple as it waits for an answer. 


Zalthir senses an opening, “Perhaps you can tell us where they are?” 


![image]()
And he learns more. There are two ways into the cave with the Obelisk: the main entrance and a side passageway. Through the side passageway, he sees a chamber with a derro that carries the insignia of office of the Council of Savants and the Gray Ghosts. 


And then he gets hit with more sadness. The creature is Trauma Dumping. He learns that the caves were once a hippy place, where Derro and Duergar would come to chill out, party, and be friends. Some months ago, the permanent twilight of the Faerzess stopped, and the cave complex became dark. Everyone was afraid, and the Faerzess blinked on brightly and then was off. And then it blinked once more, and then it returned to its usual color. But something had changed, and soon the various hippy friends stopped being friends. Instead of being a place of friendship, a place where folks could be happy, it became a place of murder and death and conspiracy. The mesa (Area 5) was once a place where folks got together to get drunk and party, but now it was a war zone between the forces of the cult of Demogorgon and the empty scabbard killers.


### Grygum


The trauma dumping seems to affect Thorin, but Grygum is an orc, and a practical creature, and quite frankly, he’s seen worse. 


He looks at the creature, and it’s once again turned teal. He noticed that it had turned dark blue just before the trauma dump and then, as the trauma dump ended, became teal. 


Grygum takes note of this. 


“Did you say assassins?” 


“Yes!” notes the Flumph. And again, it trauma dumps. This time, Grygum learns that the Flumph had found a tasty snack in the psychic energy released by a mind flayer. 


“A mind flayer?” 


“Yes, they are quite dangerous! But you are heroes!” 


The flump then shows how the mind flayer lives down a hallway. 


“Who else lives there?” 


The creature turns Magneta, then says, “I survive by not lEttin g mind flayers know I exist. I just know that the Mind Flayer is there, and that the assassins are also there. The ones you said had a magical light blade that tried to kill that duergar Werz.” 


Grygum snorts, “I never said that.” 


“Oh, right. You didn’t. You thought it.” 


Grygum pauses, “Can you help us?” 


“Absolutely. And don’t worry, although your deaths will be sad, I will absolutely trauma dump on someone else and feel better!” 


Thorin glares. 


Grygum stares at Zalthir, who interrupts his train of thought - “What are we trying to do here? I was just trying to kill some time before I got some magical equipment. Saving the Duergar from a mad king and defeating another cult of Demogorgon is not what I am here for.” 


Grygum nods, “I agree, but the egg. As a cleric of Bahamut, I must save the egg.” 


Flumph turns Green, “Why?” 


Grygum explains that Bahamut is the god of good dragons. He is committed to the principle that dragons have free will and that the pigmentation of their scales doesn’t pre-determine their personality. This idea that chromatic dragons are evil is the greatest evil. 


“We need help,” he mutters. Grygum turns to his friends. “We have the rest of the crew holed up in a seedy bar. We could get them weapons from Errde. She was willing to give us a lot of weapons. But we need a reason. And I think we do. We found evidence of the Grey Ghosts doing something evil. And we found evidence of the assassin’s guild. The only problem is how to convince her.”


He smiles and turns to Flumph -  “Flumph, I’ll need you to trauma dump on someone.” 


The creature turns pink, “That would be so good. I have so much trauma.” 


“We should be able to get support from Gartokkar Xundorn and the Keepers of the Flame.” 


Grygum says to Flumph, “Make that two trauma dumps.” 


“Won’t that be enough evidence?” asks Zalthir. 


Daz, who has been quiet, says, “No. Without physical evidence, the word of a Flumph won’t be taken seriously.” 


Zalthir shrugs, “So, can you tell me what was written on the papers in the obelisk room?” 


Flumph looks at him, “No.” 


“What about the Gray Ghosts and the Council of Savants? Can you tell me anything about them that would convince Gartokkar or Errde?


The Flumph sighs, “Well, look, the Council used to be these nice people, and then after the blink, they became crazy. And now they are working with Plinki to try to summon Demogorgon or make him a two-headed dragon mount! Look, I don’t read their minds. They are psychics, and they use psychic energy, and I feed on it. Ever since my friend Buppido went stark raving mad… ”


Grygum is silent.   


“How well guarded is this Council person?” 


“She has four guards.” 


Thorin growls, “We don’t have the resources to mount a full frontal assault. So we could just return, give the information, and then boogie out of here. We still have a boat. But I still like the  plan of escaping on the back of Thermbachaud.” 


Grygum mutters, “Bahamut commands that I save the egg.” 


### Daz
Daz, a thoughtful magician and long-time student of magic, was inspired by a commentator on Milo Goodbarrel's practice of writing daily. Milo had mentioned in his book that that practice made him such a good writer. Daz, impressed with Milo’s writing and wanting to improve, began mentally composing entries as if he were writing in a journal back home. This practice became a regular habit since his escape from Velkynvelve. 


*As we leave the Derro hovels and re-enter the city of blades, Zalthir’s question of what to do next is pressing. *
*
First, the factions hiding in the caves will not notice the deaths of Buppido and of some minor fauna. *


*Now let’s consider our putative employers and their objectives: *


1. *Errde of the Stone Guards believes the Council of Savants and the Grey Ghosts are behind the increasing madness of the city. She is also pretending not to think that assassins have targeted her clan. She believes that Droki is somehow helping the Council of Savants, and she wants proof of the Council of Savants' involvement with the corruption in the city. She also wants any actual evidence about the Empty Scabbard Killers.*
1. *Gartokar Xundom of the Keepers of the Flame also wants the Grey Ghosts dead. But more importantly, wants the egg. The egg is their insurance policy against Themberchaude. The Keepers of the Flame consider the Council of Savants their worst enemies. And are engaged in a secret war with them. They, too, want the Council of Savants exposed. *
1. *Themberchaude, the red dragon, believes that the Keepers of the Flame have plans and is not convinced his position is as secure as he wants to believe. More importantly, he’s not sure that he’s in charge. And he wants information about what’s going on. *


*Gartokkar and Errde can’t get into the Whorlestone Caves without triggering a war. For Gartokkar, the need for war would reveal the loss of a crucial pillar of his power. In Errde’s case, it would expose her incompetence as the city guardian. *


As Daz pens the last paragraph, he smiles. The path forward was clear, and indeed, it was very profitable. 


And so he returns to this journal - 


*Grygum led us to the Keeper of the Flame. Once there, the Flumph trauma dumped on Gartokkar, who seemed curiously relieved. Then, he began making demands that we fetch the egg. *
*
This is how I remember the dialogue: *


*Grygum - “We need some help.” *


*Gartokkar - “You had some helpers, use them.”*


*Thorin - “You are not employing them.” *


*Gartokkar - “I could give them badges!” *


*Zalthir - “I think we need some compensation.” *


*Gartokkar - “Compensation? COMPENSATION.” 


The duergar smiled slyly when he realized we were as mercantile as he was. *


*Gartokkar - “I want proof of the involvement in demonic worship. Bring me the statue of Demogorgon.” *


*And then I realized what this madman wanted. He intended to use the proof of the theft and the proof of the demonic worship to convince the Deepking that it was time to eliminate the scourge of the Derro from the city. He was planning to engage in a genocidal war against the Derro. *


*I was horrified and curious. As for payment, Gartokkar was not against paying for a service—“2000.” *


*It was then that Thorin and I entered the negotiations. First, we secured an upfront payment of 30% of the 2000 gold. Then we secured a confidentiality rider worth another 1000 gold. We attempted to raise the upfront fee to half of the 3000, but Gartokkar was not biting. In fact, for a moment, he looked like he would go mad and attack us. *
*
But he chose not to. *
*
As he counted the money, he said, “If you betray me, there is no cave, no pool of still water, no river, no place in the dark that I will not find you and hunt you down.” *


Daz smiles, “Time to talk to Errde and negotiate terms with her.” 


# Chapter 18.1 Alliances, betrayals and the Trauma Dump
## 10th day of the 1st Tenday of Myrtul 1493
### Daz


Daz has a lot of experience in dealing with leaders suffering from delusions of grandeur, paranoia, and megalomania. If he considers the average Drow leader of the Cult of Lolth, it’s almost a prerequisite. 


He remembers what the mages said: Lolth became Lolth through betrayal and subterfuge. Correlon, the chief elvish god, was her consort, or she was his, it’s unclear, and the story depends on how it’s written. Regardless, she wanted his power, so she created an avatar, Lolth, and convinced some elves that their destiny was to rule. Correlon didn’t find out until it was too late, when Lolth’s followers tried to kill his priests.  


Revealed for what she was, Correlon banished her, and the elves banished her followers. The ancient word “Drow” was used to describe the followers of Lolth. What it means has been lost even to the wisest of Elves, but there are many opinions. 


Daz always wondered if the Drow were only on Toril, but according to the clerics of Lolth, the banishment occurred in the Feywild, and from the Underdark in the Feywild, the Drow fled to every part of the multiverse. 


And in each part of the multiverse, the Drow are both a strand and a spiderweb. A strand of Lolth’s web, and a web of intrigue whose only purpose is to destroy the followers of Correlon. 


In the cities where Lolth’s cult dominates, society is organized around noble houses. And there is a ruthless competition to climb higher. And every so often, a noble house will try to destroy another house. And if it fails, then the other noble houses will ruin it. 


Daz remembers, or was it a story he heard, of a noble house destroyed by the combined might of the other noble houses because one child survived. 


For the Drow, you either exterminate your enemy or don’t try. Lolth is still touchy about her followers' failures from eons ago. 


And so now he is on his way to Errde’s office. And the stench of paranoia runs deep. And the desire for power is palpable. But he knows that she and her followers don’t understand the importance of planning, of preparation for the kind of strike that a Drow faction would organize. Errde would die a miserable death, and the city would kill her in the most gruesome way possible, and her supporters would suffer for their failure. 


Daz understands that societal norms differ, and the Duergar's deviation from Drow norms makes their city more perilous. Unlike the Drow's swift executions, conflict here is protracted.


He knows what she wants. She wants proof of the Grey Ghosts' alliance with the Council of Savants. She wants that proof to kill as many Derro as possible. And he knows what she wants, not evidence that the Empty Scabbard Killers exist, but who has decided her clan members must die. 


Why does she want the Derro dead? Daz has seen that look on many a Drow leader. The desire to kill a group of people, because the leader thinks that is why everything is broken. The leader is convinced that this poor, helpless group is why everything is falling apart. She is blinded by her conviction that the Council of Savants, a ruling group of the Derro, is corrupting the Deepking. 


He knows those groups. They are a fig leaf of autonomy for races controlled by those in power. Buppido, before he became mad, as The Flumph, complained about how the Council was more interested in staying in power than freeing his people. The Council of Savants is innocent, thinks Daz, or worse, they are victims of the machinations of yet another power. The idea that they have so much control over the Deepking makes Daz laugh. 


But he knows that the Keepers of the Flame and Stone Guard want the same thing: the destruction of the Derro. 


And Daz may have the information they need to provoke a slaughter. 


“Given how many Derro there are, how defensible their enclaves are, and how deep the tunnels go, I am not so sure that the Duergar will win this war.”


He shakes his head - “We are sitting on a volcano. We can trigger a slaughter if we provide the wrong information to the wrong group. But I do have an alternative proposal.”


The group stares at him. “I have seen this before, everyone convinced that the leader is a victim of some outside influence, and a need to destroy the outside influence. No one wants to confront the reality that they want power, and they are too afraid of the leader to try and seize it from them. If we can get rid of the Deepking, or focus everyone’s hatred on him, then the Duergar would slaughter each other.” 


Grygum gives him a look, and Daz smiles, “Being a Drow, you pick some stuff up.” 
### Thorin 


“Guys, we have everything we need. Why are we here?” 


Thorin had survived the War of the Giants when the ordning fell apart, and the giants pursued ambitions of a genocidal war against the little people. 


Zalthir jumps in, “We have made quite a bit of money. Let’s grab our magic and get out of here.” 
Daz mutters, “If they think we are alive, then they will come after us.” 


Thorin nods, “So we fake our deaths and run.” He then thinks about being on the run, “We have some Drow after us, and I am not sure having another society after us is a good thing.” 


“Everyone is threatening everyone because they are all looking for a trigger to go on a bloodbath.” He pauses and smiles, “The fact they are all want to kill us, means we are safe.” 


Thorin mutters, “Not sure it works that way.” 


But Zalthir, to Thorin’s surprise, agrees. 


Thorin looks at Daz and Zalthir and decides he’s had enough of subterfuge and lies. He wants to be radically transparent, to say it as it is. He liked his giant tribe; they didn’t invent complex plots and plans. They were direct and to the point.


### Zalthir


The monks who taught Zalthir the importance of being discreet, of hiding in the shadows, and of avoiding frontal conflict. 


Zalthir's monastic teachers emphasized discretion, the value of hiding in shadows, and avoiding confrontation. He sees no upside to doing anything but running. 


But Grygum insists that they must honor their commitments.


Zalthir sighed and followed the group to Overlake Hold to talk to Errde. 


In her chambers, Daz encourages the Flumph to trauma dump on her. 


The Flump mutters - “I need more trauma. These dumps are no longer as satisfying.” 


Zalthir raises an eyebrow to Thorin’s response, “Don’t worry, we’ll get you some.” 


Errde is not right. 


“I knew the Grey Ghosts and the Council were working together!” 


Zalthir is not entirely comfortable with where this is going. But Daz, who has been here before, knows what to say. 


“I don’t know that’s the case.” 


Errde stutters, “But the flumph showed me.” 


“He showed you that they are near to each other. People being near each other doesn’t mean working together on everything. Like I am talking to you and advising you, but are we working together on all things?”


Zalthir stares at Errde, and the madness disappears. “You present me a conundrum. I need more information.” She stares at Zalthir, “You must go back.” 


Zalthir wonders why she’s looking at him.  


But then she turns on Daz. 


“Drow, you knew this was not enough. Why didn’t you bring me the papers?” 


Daz looks like a Drow explaining things to a child: “We did some searching and ran into trouble. The caves are not as safe as they once were. We ran into some trouble.” 


Grygum then interjects, “We needed reinforcements.” 


Errde glares at Grygum, “I can’t send my Duergar troops into the Derro slums.” She thinks, Zalthir stares at her, and then says, “You have a crew. I can arm them.” 


Zalthir is about to leave, when she once again hisses, “When will I have what I need?” 


Zalthir can see the feigned irritation in Daz’s eyes, “When I have it. To keep our mission secret, we will be seen talking to other people; that way, when we are seen going into other caves, people will think we are working for them, when we are, in fact, working for you.” 


Zalthir is impressed and worried. Daz seems far too comfortable in this nest of scorpions. 


She claps in her hands, “A fantastic idea. You must talk to Clan Ironhead or Clan Xardelva. Clan Ironhead is forbidden from taking weapons directly and may only take surplus orders from Clan Steelshadow. The Deepking has been sending all orders to his clan, Clan Steelshadow. Clan Ironhead is upset with the loss of business. As for Clan Xardelva, they are worried that their work will be seen as too similar to weaponsmithing, and Clan Steelshadow will take them over. Both of these clans are seen as opposing the Deepking. As the head of the Stone Guard, anyone who sees you talking to them will assume we cannot work together.”  


Zalthir looks at Daz, Errde, and then walks through the door. A thousand times the darkness of his spells than the plots and fogs of the plots of the Drow and the Duergar. 


### Grygum


Grygum stands in front of the Tavern known as the Shattered Spire, where the merchant Werz insisted they meet. It is built on a broken stalagmite that juts out from the Darklake about forty feet from the shore. This stalagmite forms the foundation of a tavern built with fungi stalks in a manner similar to a log cabin. 


Grygum has to cross a bridge woven of rothé wool to get to it. 


Once there, he sees Werz sitting by himself at a table. The Duergar smiles. 


As they sit, he hands Grygum and each of his companions a gemstone worth 10 gold pieces.


Grygum asks, “What about the Flumph? And our ghost?” 


Werz is happy to be alive and gives the Flumph a gem. The Flumph turns light blue. Then , when it turns green, it picks the stone up and plays with it in its tentacles. After a while, it turns magenta, and the stone falls to the ground. 


As for the ghost, Werz hands Grygum the gem. 


When no one is looking, Grygum picks up the Flumph’s gem and puts it in his bag. 


“My saviors, I want you to know that I have already spoken to the owner of the Gholbrorn’s Inn, and I will take care of everything.” 


Grygum can tell that Daz knows something is up, but the Drow is silent. 


“Assassins! I thought they were a story told to frighten children.” 


The unimpressed cleric explains that just because someone tried to kill him is not proof of an assassin’s guild. “Why, if I tried to kill you, that would not make me a member of the Assassin’s Guild, unless someone paid me.” Grygum pauses, “I guess that would get me into trouble with any actual Assassin’s Guild.’ 


Grygum wants to know more. But Thorin is eager to talk, so Grygum is silent. 


Thorin asks, “Why did they try to kill you?” 


“Because somebody paid them.” 


Grygum rolls his eyes. “Do you have any enemies other than assassins?” 


The Duergar merchant shrugs, “First, assassins are not your enemies. They are professionals. And before you ask, I did try to offer them a higher rate, but they are professionals.” 


Once again, Grygum notices that Daz has seen something. 


Grygum turns to Daz, and Daz, through Flumph, speaks directly into Grygum’s mind, “Maybe he ordered somebody to assassinate somebody, and now somebody else found out and they have ordered somebody to assassinate him. He played, he fucked around and now he’s in the find out phase.” 


Thorin asks, “Did you go to the Stone Guards?” 


Werz looks uncomfortable. “They would never believe me. The assassins are a children’s fable.” 


Grygum is enjoying watching Thorin’s bluntness, “So you want us to kill a bunch of professionally trained killers?” 


Daz twists the knife well, “Are you trying to create a new assassin's guild?” 


Werz turns pale, “I don’t know why I am on the list.” Grygum smiles, “Then I guess we’ll leave.” 


Werz grabs his hand and urges him to sit, “I am a merchant. And it’s my job to make deals between people. The Deepking has forbidden any weapons deals with any clan other than his clan, Clan Steelshadow. As a merchant, I can't walk away when I see two sides of a deal that I can profit from. And perhaps, I helped some clans make deals they shouldn’t have.”


Grygum looks at him, “I suppose we could use you as bait.” 


Werz snarls and then looks at Grygum, “You are overbrighters. And you are looking to get to Blingdenstone. The gnomes have been trying to make deals with the clans for weapons. I can help facilitate such a deal. I can promise I will make that deal.” 


Thorin coughs, “Let’s talk about our optional NDA.” 


Werz looks at him, “NDA?” 


Grygum points to Daz, who explains the concept of a Non-Disclosure Agreement, a critical part of any Drow deal. Daz adds, “The NDAs of the Drow promised all kinds of horrible outcomes to the party that revealed anything. We can only promise the haunting of a ghost.” Werz stares at the phantasm and shudders. 


“How much will it cost?” 


“1250 gold is our normal NDA price. But since you did offer a favor, if we needed one, we would be willing to go down to a flat 1000,” says Daz.  


“That’s highway robbery!” 


“Or we can choose not to be bound by secrecy.” 


Grygum tries not to laugh when Thorin explains, “I don’t like NDAs because they don’t allow for radical transparency and honesty in relations. So I get why you wouldn’t want one. We should tell everyone about our deals with you.” 


Werz coughs, “A thousand?”


Grygum admires how Daz snarls, “I told you it was 1250.”


The merchant whimpers apologetically, “I am a merchant, I have to question every price.” 


“If you question it again, it goes to 1100.” 


“But my good friend, I wasn’t questioning your generosity, but would it be rude not to bargain?” 


“1100,” snarls Daz. 


Grygum is impressed with Daz's cold calculation and watches as Werz hands over the coins. 


As he hands over the money, Werz says, “Since we are business partners, let me tell you about some information you might find helpful. As a merchant, I know how the clans feel about the Deepking. Clan Ironshadow’s clan leader is willing to wait out the Deepking’s madness, but other clan members are unhappy. Clan Tharzgad has been complaining about raids by the Grey Ghosts. Although many clans are dissatisfied, some, like Clan Xundom, will support the Deepking if war breaks out.” 


Grygum yawns. 


Werz then whispers to him, “There are rumors of the Stone Guards taking bribes.” 


“I thought they were incorruptible.” 


“They were until a few months ago when the madness of the Deepking took over.” 


Grygum takes note of the timing and the blink of the Faerzess but keeps silent. 


As they are about to leave, Werz warns him, “This city is ready to explode. Provide the wrong faction with the wrong information, and you will have all-out war. Remember, Werz doesn’t care about politics; he only cares about trade. And I only care about gEttin g rid of my assassin's problem.” Grygum gives him a funny look, “And I would like the problem not to be solved with my death.” 


Werz prepares to leave. 


### Daz


“Hold on.” 


Werz looks at the Drow. 


“We didn’t discuss the fee for gEttin g rid of the assassins.” 


“You just got 1100 gold!” 


“Yes, to not reveal our discussions. We didn’t discuss the fee to get rid of the assassins.” 


Werz turns pale, “I am broke!” 


Daz picks up his copy of Milo Goodbarrel’s book, thumbs to a page, and reads. Then he turns to Werz: “There was this guy called Ezra, and he kept saying he couldn’t pay and always could. And you know why? Because he needed the First Faction more than they needed him.” 


The merchant sits down and opens a bag, “Here are some gems. Before you sell them, go to your gnomish friends and ask them about their value.” 


Daz is tempted to press the topic, but even he knows when a rock is bled dry. 


A little bit later, he’s in the Ghohlbrorn’s Lair, where the rest of the crew sits at a table. 


He explains the deals they have made, and that to get out of Gracklstugh, they will have to go into the Whorlstone Tunnels and find the evidence for at least one of the many different factions. 


After he does that, he hands Jimjar a gem. Jimjar whistles, “Now that is something I didn’t expect. These are empty spell gems. There is an alchemist in Bligndenstone who can turn these gems into gems of immense magical power. If you bring these to Kazook Pickshine, he will pay a lot for them.” 


### Zalthir 


The dragonborn then talks to Stool about the myconids to see if he can learn anything. 


Stool is very confused. “Myconids don’t dance. We should find out what’s wrong with them.” 


Zalthir then mutters about another sprout who looks upset and isn’t dancing. Stool demands Zalthir describe him. And then stool becomes super animated: “That’s my friend Rumpadump. Something’s wrong. We must go save him!” 


The dragonborn rolls his eyes and then hisses, “The sprout is not as concerning as the myconids.” 


“Myconids won’t attack unless they are attacked.”


“What about the quagoths?” 


Sprout is nonpulsed. “They must have attacked. They are savage monsters.” 


Zalthir looks at him funny, but Sprout continues, “Quagotths are bad, mean creatures. The quagoth attacked, and those Myconids had to kill him.” 


Thorin coughs, “A bit of biological determinism there?” 


“Bio what? 


Zalthir interrupts, “Never mind. Why do we have to save Rumpadump?” 


“Because he’s from my circle. And the dancing Myconids must be from our circle. And he can tell us what is going on! We have to save him!” 


Zalthir sighs, “We are already knee deep in so many obligations that I am not sure we can do that, my friend.” 


The sprout starts to sob, or what Zalthir thinks is sobbing. He’s unmoved. But Thorin is not. Zalthir groans as he realizes that they will have to do more thing. 


“We can do it after we deal with the assassins?” 


Zalthir nods, defeated. 


Towards the evening, the Duergar Brannam shows up with the magical weapons and items Thorin and Zalthir requested. 


Zalthir sews the tattoos on his body. He thinks that perhaps now he won’t die. 
## 1st day of the 2nd Tenday of Myrtul 1493


The following day, Jimjar, Spiderbait, Sarith, and Eldeth walk to the Underlake Hold, where Errde arms them. 


From there, the entire group heads to Clan Ironhead and asks to speak with the clan leader. The clan is initially unwilling to talk to them. Still, their badges get them an audience with Thangus Ironhead, who explains that Clan Ironhead approves of the Deepking's policies and agrees that the Deepking's clan needs to be pre-eminent.  


Zalthir is unconvinced of Thangus Ironhead’s honesty. Daz, who listened to him, scoffs, “He’s lying and trying to survive.” 


As they leave the Clan stronghold, a female Duergar approaches them. 


“My name is Grinta Ironhead. I know you are trying to go to the overbrite through the city of the gnomes. The Deepking has raised prices to astronomical levels for the Deep Gnomes. Now, if the Deepking were unseated, Clan Ironhead would be free to do business with the gnomes, and we would be willing to do so at a discount of our normal prices.Greetings. My name is Grinta Ironhead. I am aware of your intent to traverse to the surface world via the gnomish city. Be advised that the Deepking has imposed exorbitant pricing upon the Deep Gnomes. It is my proposition that were the Deepking to be deposed, Clan Ironhead would be afforded the liberty to conduct trade with the gnomes, and we would willingly extend a discounted rate relative to our standard tariffs.”


Zalthir tries to look confused, but she has already left. 


Daz smiles, “They all know that we are going into the Whorlstone tunnels, and they all hope the information we provide will help them. The question is, how do we get the information and profit most?” 


Grygum coughs, “And free Thermbachaude.” 


# Chapter 18.2 
## 1st day of the 2nd Tenday of Myrtul 1493
### Daz
Daz looks at Flumph, Jimjar, Sarith, Stool, Elbeth, and Spiderbait, armed with Errde’s weapons. “Perhaps they will help us” as they follow him, Zalthir, Grygum, and Thorin, into the Derro slums of Gracklstugh. 


As he walks he reflects on the image of the egg that Flumph shared. 


The lettering on the egg rings a bell. 


“It’s too late.” 


Grygum stares at him, “What do you mean?” 


“A demon has already possessed the egg. There is no dragon there.” 


The cleric of Bhamut is saddened. Daz detects a resolve to hurt the Derro magician. Daz is pleased. 
### Zalthir


Zalthir marches the group back through the same path they took last time, going over the lake, and then through the fungi forest. He then follows the path towards the Raucus Mesa. 


As he approaches the intersection that leads to the assassin’s lair, two Derror materialise.


They introduce themselves as Grimgrim and some unpronounceable Derro. The Drow not named Grimgrim explains that he can be called - “Rust.” 


Zalthir tries to determine the wisest course of action, but Thorin blurts out, “Are you the assassins or the dudes trying to become besties with Demogorgon?” 


Zalthir notices how pleased Rust is, who says, “You are the enemies of Demogorgon?” 


And Thorin explains, “So you must be the assassins?” 


Zalthir cringes. 


Rust speaks in a serious tone, “Yes. We are the empty scabbard killers.” 


Zalthir, who learned the art of saying little, wonders if he can rip Thorin’s throat out when the dwarf asks, “How do you kill people if you have an empty scabbard?” 
The orc piles on, “ Well, it's easier to kill someone if the scabbard is empty?” 


Zalthir wants them to stop. 


But Thorin won’t, “Oh, is it because you have your weapon in your hand, or is it magical?” 


Rust asks them to move along. 


Zalthir remembers that they had to help Werz. What Werz wants is not to be a target. Killing the assassins is not what he wants. 


Then he remembers what Errde craved, proof that the assassins killed her family.  


Zalthir turns to Thorin, “Maybe we can do them a favor and take care of the cult, and they will drop Werz as a target?”  


Thorin looks at him, “What favor?” 


“Get rid of the cult of Demogorgon.” 


Daz whispers through the telepathy of Stool, “I like the idea of collecting all of the information and then distributing it to all of the power brokers of Gracklstugh simultaneously. We could stab them all in the front simultaneously and flee in the chaos.” 


Thorin turns to Rust and Grim, “Hey, we would love to compare notes on the cult of Demogorgonn and see if we can help each other out.” 


Rust shouts, “Let me confer with my leadership to see if they agree with this plan.”
### 
Daz


The Duergar assassin returns and says, “The boss wants to see you.” 


Daz overhears Thorin telepathically asking if Flump will join them. Flumph says, ‘I want to observe a tragedy, not be in one. I will stay here.”  


Jimjar moves to follow Rust, but Rust turns to him, “Only these four will come, the rest of you,” pointing at Spiderbait, Jimjar, Sarith, Stool and Elbeth, “can wait here.” 


And so Daz, Thorin, Zalthir, and Grygum enter the chambers of the assassins. Rust marches them into a cave that is 70 feet long and 70 feet wide at its widest point. Inside is a large garden. Standing in the garden is Duergar with an eye patch. 


Daz takes note of a desk to the north with papers. 


He also notices three soul blades, the name the Duergar assassins give themselves, standing behind what appears to be their boss. Behind Daz, the mage can feel Rust and Grim standing. 


“Violence is not the answer,” he thinks.  


The Duergar with an eye patch speaks, “My name is Eldgrim. Rust says you may have a deal for us. And in exchange, we are to let you through our territory.” 


Daz collects his wits, “Do you have a hit on a guy named Werz?” 


Eldgrim laughs, “Small potatoes. I can cancel the contract for a small fee and permanently brightlist him for a small fee.” 


“Brightlist?” 


“Yes, put him on a list that will protect him. It’s called bright because we can always see it.”
