Thorin whispers to Daz, “Ask them if they have a talism that we can use for safe passage?”

Daz looks at Thorin, “So we can use it to prove they exist later.” 


Daz asks Eldgrim, who in turn laughs. “An assassin’s guild with a card?” 


The mage shrugs and turns to Werz, “So what is the  fee for Werz?” 


“You get rid of my demogorgon problem, we could move Werz to the allow list for, shall we say, 20 gold?” 


Daz is outraged, “We are going to deal with your problem, and you want 20 more gold?” 


Before Eldgrim can speak, Thorin blurts, “I don’t think a group of demon worshipers is only worth 180 gold, the imbued value based on the calculation from the proposed discount.” 


Daz stares at Thorin, and Thorin shrugs, “I learned about contracts. The Giants needed somebody to make deals with the locals, and I made contracts. It’s easy to make a good contract if the choice is a contract or a bunch of giants raid your town.” 


Thorin then turns to Daz, “Have him sign a contract, we can use that as proof!”  


Eldgrim stares at Thorin, “Daz, that’s what they said you were called. I made a business arrangement with others. If I were to eat that contract, then folks would look at me as weak. But the offer of killing Demogorgon’s followers would remove a source of ongoing cost to my operations. So, although I don’t like it, if you get rid of them, I will move Werz to the brightlist.” 


Daz sensing an opportunity to get proof, asks, “Perhaps we should sign a contract? With a confidentiality agreement to make sure that we keep things quiet.”  


Eldgrim sees through Daz’s efforts, “You want to prove we exist? Do you want to show this contract to someone, and do you really think they will believe that we exist and not think it's a forgery? You’re a fool. Anyone who sees any proof of our existence and knows we exist will deny our existence, and everyone else will laugh at your credulity.” 


He pauses, “As if a group of strangers can come down here and find proof of something that nobody has found, ever.” 


While Eldgrim arrogantly dismisses the mage, Daz notices a piece of paper on the desk that has a mark that looks like a mark from someone with power. 


He turns to Eldgrim, “You are right. Nothing I say or show will prove anything. And I wanted the contract for my selfish reasons. I have been writing a collection of stories that I hope to publish as a book later. It would be nice to jot down your name on a piece of paper so I can include it correctly. Could you do that? 


Eldgrim is flattered and says, “The legend of our guild will spread far and wide.” The other duergar looks at him oddly, and he says, “And if you spread anything but our legend, well then, perhaps we will have to take care of a certain author.”  


The assassin chief walks up to his desk, pulls a piece of paper from the desk, and scribbles. 


Meanwhile, Thorin turns to Grim and Rust and starts asking them about the empty scabbard moniker in an attempt to distract them. 


Daz takes the contract while Eldgrim is distracted, but he knows that if it goes missing, then the assassins will come after him. 


So he starts to cough. 


He motions to Zalthir to come over. The dragonborn marches over and thwacks Daz on the back. Daz whispers to him, “When I hit you, breathe fire at the desk.” 


Daz stops coughing and shouts with a sense of real relief, “I thought I was going to die. My allergies.” Zalthir is still confused. And then Daz slaps him on the back and shouts, “Thank you!” 


Zalthir, on cue, breathes on the desk, burning the papers on it. 


Eldgrim screams - “Fool! I should kill you.” But then he looks at the burned papers and mutters, “Contracts that I have committed to memory. Better destroyed.” 


He then turns to them, “Now go get rid of my problem.” He pauses, “And if you don’t, then you will die. It will be a free contract that I will enjoy fulfilling.” 


### Thorin 
Once outside of the assassin’s redoubt, Thorin turns to Daz, “So show me!” Daz tells him to wait. And Thorin once again takes note of the Drow’s paranoia that is so useful in the Underdark. Two more soulblades were invisible in the caves, some 50 feet north of the entrance to the assassin’s. If they had looked at the contract when he wanted, they would have been caught. 


After passing them, Thorin takes the contract from Daz’s hands. 


Thorin reads it, 


***“Faster this time. Faster! I want to hear heads rolling by the***
***time the ink dries on the tip of my quill! Or veins bursting***
***black with poison, or lungs filling with water, or faces melting***
***in forges… I don’t care how you do it, just do it faster!***
***THANGUS IRONHEAD!!!!! HOW DARE HE TRY TO***
***ENCROACH ON MY FAMILY’S BUSINESS???? BOIL HIM! BOIL***
***HIM IN OIL AND FEED HIM TO ROACHES!***
***WERZ SALTBARON THAT SNIVELING SQUEALING***
***WRITHING LITTLE RAT! BIND HIS FEET AND THROW HIM***
***OFF HIS BELOVED DOCKS!***
***Captain Blackskull… I’ve smelled treason on her since she***
***was but a lass. She’s always had an eye on my throne, but she’ll***
***never get it! All she’ll get is what’s coming to her. Yes, that’s***
***what she’ll get!***
***His Arrogance, His Rotundity… the Pampered, the Portly,***
***the Scheming Red… Freeze the Wyrmsmith until his heart***
***turns crystalline, then smash it to bits!***
***LINGRICK XARDELVAR MY MOST GASEOUS ALLY!!!!!!*****”**


He turns to Daz, “I think we have what we need.” He reads it out loud to Daz, Thorin, and Grygum. He then adds, “There are dozens more with one or two words of description, most of which are petty insults: 'Commoner,' 'Ugly,' 'Poor,' 'Wretched,' and so on.” 


Daz asks him, “But who wrote it?” 


Thorin points to a mark on the document bearing the personal seal of the Deepking and the royal seal of Gracklstugh. 


Daz mutters, “Yes, we do.” 


Thorin, whose interests in contracts stand in contrast to his focus on brutal strength, smiles. He’s seen many contracts that people should never have signed. He never wrote those. 


Zalthir decides that rather than go through some door that they may not be able to open, it’s safer to try a different route. There is a tunnel entrance that goes past two caves. The caves have  Derro inside. One of the Derro is a member of the Council of Savants. 


Thorin turns to Flumph, Jimjar, Sarith, Stool, Elbeth, and Spiderbait and commands them to be quiet. He demonstrates by walking on his tip toes. 


He then overhears Zalthir’s sigh. The sound of Thorin tiptoeing could wake the dead. Zalthir proposes a new plan: “I will cover you in Darkness and you will just be quiet.” 


### Grygum 


Past the caves they sneaked through, is a much larger tunnel, some 80 feet wide and hundreds of feet long. To the west, the tunnel opens up into a massive cave, glowing with faerzress, bioluminescent fungi, and shafts of white light that fall. GEttin g closer, he sees naturally formed shelves along the walls as well as a rocky mesa at the center of the cavern. His eye is drawn to crudely formed ramps connecting the different levels of the mesa up to the height of its two topmost tiers, which are linked by a sturdy bridge. 


“The egg,” he mutters. Atop one of those tiers sits a large red egg. 


“The obelix,” he notes when he looks atop the other tier. There stands a 50-foot-tall obelisk made of smooth black metal with a few noticeable imperfections, as though small parts of it were somehow chipped away.


A female derro stands close to the obelisk, gently patting and stroking its surface. The obelisk flashes once, the glow of faerzress around the cavern flaring in response. The derro squeals with glee as she snatches an object up from the ground, then writes something down in a small notebook.


# Chapter 18.3 A Journey Deeper into the Underdark


Beyond the narrow, winding caves through which they had cautiously advanced, a significantly larger tunnel stretched before them, an impressive passage spanning roughly eighty feet in width and extending for what seemed like hundreds of feet into the subterranean darkness. To the west, the tunnel dramatically opened into a colossal cavern, a breathtaking space illuminated by an eerie, pervasive glow. This light emanated from the mystical faerzress that permeated the Underdark, mixed with the soft luminescence of various bioluminescent fungi clinging to the cavern walls and floor. Adding to this subterranean spectacle were several shafts of pure white light, piercing down from unseen openings far above, casting ethereal beams across the vast expanse.


As he cautiously moved closer to the cavern's opening, the explorer's gaze began to discern the natural formations within. He noted a series of naturally formed shelves that tiered the cavern walls, creating ledges and recesses along its perimeter. Dominating the center of the cavern was a substantial rocky mesa, a raised plateau that formed a distinct feature within the immense space. His attention was soon drawn to the crude but functional ramps that snaked their way up the sides of the mesa, connecting its various levels. These ramps led upwards to the height of the mesa's two topmost tiers, which, remarkably, were linked by a sturdy bridge that spanned the distance between them.


A thought escaped his lips, almost a reverent whisper: “The egg.” His eyes had locked onto a large, distinctly red egg that rested atop one of the mesa's highest tiers. Its size and vibrant color made it a focal point within the dimly lit cavern. And even from afar, he can sense it’s corruption. 


Shifting his gaze to the adjacent topmost tier, another exclamation followed, this time a statement of observation: “The obelisk.” Standing sentinel on this second tier was a towering structure, a fifty-foot-tall obelisk crafted from a smooth, jet-black metal. Upon closer inspection, he could discern a few noticeable imperfections marring its otherwise flawless surface, appearing as though small fragments had been somehow chipped away over time.


Near the base of this imposing obelisk stood a lone figure: a female derro. Her actions were curious; she stood close to the black metal, gently patting and stroking its cool surface with an almost reverent touch. Suddenly, the obelisk emitted a brief flash of light, a pulse that caused the ambient glow of the faerzress within the cavern to momentarily flare in response, intensifying the eerie illumination. The derro reacted with a sharp squeal of glee at this display. Immediately following the flash, she bent down and snatched an object from the ground near the obelisk. With the object now in hand, she produced a small notebook and began to diligently write something within its pages, her brow furrowed in concentration.


Grygum coughs, “I am a cleric of Bahamut, and I am drawn to this egg.” 


He points to the egg. 


Plinki looks at him, confused. 


But something about his demeanor made her excited, “A cleric of Bahamut to see my creation! Excellent! Then it has worked!”


She shouts, “Come here!” 


Grygum circles the mesa, finds a ramp in the back, and starts to climb. 


As he walks, he notices that Thorin, Daz, and Grygum follow him from a distance. 


Plinki is ignoring their presence. Instead, she motions to several other Derro to come to the egg. 


Grygum counts them, “six.” 


Once standing in front of the egg, Plinki points to Grygum’s friends and asks  , “Who are they?” 


“They are my companions. They are not as enlightened as I.” Grygum looks at the egg, and can feel its evil. “Tell me about this egg?”  


“The Grey Ghosts stole it from the Keepers of the Flame. And then I brought it here. I have been using this magical artifact to infuse it with the spirit of a demon in honor of Demogorgon.” 


Grygum looks at Plinki and realizes that the poor Derro is confused about his sub-sect of the Cult of Bahamut. Unlike traditionalists who view the color of scales as the defining characteristic of Dragons, and that Dragons are fixed in their temperament, Grygum believes that Dragons have freedom of choice. And thus, for Grygum, there is no good or evil dragon because of its scales, but goodness and evil flow from the choices of dragons. 


As Grygum reflects on this, he also notices that Plinki has gotten closer and that the other Derro have surrounded him. So when Plinki declares, “The beating heart of a cleric of Bahamut will seal the ritual!” He’s not surprised. 


Grygum shouts, “The Drow hates dragons and will destroy the egg if you do not back down!” 


Plinki hesitates. 


Thorin shouts, “What would a dragon omelet taste like? And would this one have two yolks?” 


And then Grygum is enveloped in Darkness. Zalthir has enveloped the entire top tier in his magical darkness. Grygum hears the thuds of Zalthir’s fists on the crazed Derro. Plinki shouts, “Let me go!” Grygum smiles. Plinki has been grappled. And since he is grappled, Grygum will show him the true power of Bahamut. He utters words of cruel power, rakes his hand through the air before Plinki. Magic follows, forming a great claw that glimmers in the air for the blink of an eye. This necromancy seeks to rend armor, unstitch flesh, crush bone—to do whatever it must to destroy your enemy.


# Chapter 18.4 The Flumph Trauma Dump


*The Flumph was traumatized by the entire battle scene. Fortunately, it found a willing receptacle for a trauma dump that we share here. *
Oh! Oh, thank goodness, a fresh mind! You have to listen, you just *have* to, I feel like I'm going to burst! It was... it was just the most awful, chaotic, LOUD thing I have ever had to feel!
So there they were, my heroes! Standing before the mean lady-derro, Plinki. And the orc-cleric, Grygum, was trying to talk to her, something about choice and dragon gods. His thoughts were so... earnest and golden-yellow! But Plinki, her mind was just a screeching, red mess of "Sacrifice! Power! For the Big Baboon Demon!"
Then everything went wrong all at once! *Flumph!* Sharp little pings of malice from the dark! The nice lady-dwarf, Eldeth, her thoughts just went *AAAAH-PAIN!* and it was like gEttin g stabbed with a rusty-tasting needle!
And then Zalthir—oh, Zalthir, the quiet, scaly one, his mind is usually like a still, cool pond, you know? But he just decided—no more light! *FWOOMP.* And the whole world went psychically gray and muffled! It was like trying to taste soup through a wool blanket! I couldn't get a clean read on *anything!* Just jumbled bits of "Where are they?!" and "Kill them!" It was so confusing!
The Dwarf, Thorin, he just charged right into that black cloud. His mind was a simple, bright axe-blade of "HIT THE BAD THING." Very pure, but so loud!
But then the *other* floaty-eye-thing came! Ugh! It's mind tasted like curdled milk and mindflayer static! But Daz, the clever Drow, his thoughts are like a spiderweb, all intricate and patient. He said, "Maximilian's Earthen Grasp," and the ground just reached up with a big muddy thought and *SQUEEZED* the eye-thing! Oh, the rage! The indignation! The *squeezed* feeling! It was horrible!
And Zalthir! He was in the middle of it all! His thoughts weren't shouting like the others. They were sharp and cold, like little shards of ice. I heard him think, *"The leader is the lynchpin. Neutralize Plinki."* And then he opened his mouth and the thought turned into ROARING-HOT-AGONY-FIRE! Plinki's mind just... went out. Like a candle flame. A bright, nasty, red shriek and then... nothing. A void. It was so sudden it made me flinch!
All her little followers felt it, and their minds just shattered into a million panicked pieces! And that's when Zalthir... oh, it was fascinating and awful! He moved so fast! I heard him think, *"This one is the most dangerous. Their skill is a threat."* and he just... grabbed the thief-derro! The thief's surprise was a sharp, lemon-zest tang of "What-?!" and then Zalthir, so silent, so focused, *threw him off the ledge!* The feeling of falling, the brief moment of weightlessness, was followed by a CRUNCH of pain that tasted like biting on stone! Then Zalthir was on him, and it was just... *thud, thud, thud.* No anger, no rage, just... methodical dismantling. The psychic texture of it was terrifying! It was like watching a glacier move, unstoppable and silent.
And the poor ghost, Pelek, he tried to get in the thief's head! It was like trying to pour hot tea and cold water into the same cup, all sizzle and steam and wrongness! The thief's mind was like a fortress and just pushed him out!
The battle was just a soup of ugly feelings after that! The wizard, Daz, his mind went all silvery and he just... wasn't there anymore! A little psychic *poof* and then he was by the egg, and the anxiety coming off him was a physical wave! *"Get it, get it, get it, get out!"* his thoughts screamed. He grabbed the egg and *poofed* away!
And all the other derro felt it at once! Their minds exploded in a chorus of "WHERE IS THE EGG?! THE EGG! WHO HAS THE EGG?!" It was a psychic tsunami of panic! I felt it wash all over me!
They just... fell apart after that. Zalthir and Thorin were a wall of quiet violence and loud violence. Zalthir was like, *"This one is off-balance. Strike here."* And then, *whump*, another one gone. He never wasted a thought, never wasted a move. So efficient!
*(The Flumph shudders, its glow flickering before settling into a soft, exhausted teal.)*
...Phew. Oh, my. That... that really helps. Just gEttin g it all out. It was just so much. But now... now I feel much lighter. Thank you. Thank you for being such a good, quiet place for all that... noise.


# Chapter 19 The Ember Vanguard
## Zalthir


He stands in the darkness. He hears nothing. Then he hears a shout. 


“Is everyone okay?” 


Zalthir recognizes the voice; it’s Eldeth.


Thorin shouts, “Yes, we’re all fine.” 


Zalthir sighs and dispels the darkness. 


Daz shouts, “I have the egg.” 


And then an unfamiliar voice of a Derro shouts, “My goodness, this body is uncomfortable.” 


Zalthir tenses. 


“Oh, yes, I am Pelek. I seem to have occupied this body.” 


“The ghost,” he thinks. 


The monk looks around. The upper levels of the mesa are covered in blood and the broken bodies of the derro. Where Eldeth is, near the tunnel entrance is a spectator, a creature similar to but different from a beholder. 


He looks to where the egg should be. There is no egg. There are two dead derro. 


Grygum shouts, “Where is the egg?” 


Then Daz shouts back, “I have it.” 


Zalthir jumps off the mesa and heads to an alcove in the northeast corner. There, he picks up the statue of Demogorgon. 


“Leemoogoogon, Demorgogon, two-headed baby dragons - …” he thinks to himself.


While Daz and Pelek exchange pleasantries, and Grygum searches the bodies he heads to the northwest corner where there is a desk with some papers. 


He finds a journal by Pliinki. 


Pliinki's Journal
Here are some journal entries from the perspective of Pliinki, detailing her macabre experiments and fervent beliefs:


### Pliinki's Journal
**Day 17 – The Stone of Diirinka**
The Obelisk. Such a magnificent, fractured thing! Hidden here by Diirinka himself, I am certain. Its black metal hums with quasi-magical energy, a power just waiting to be unleashed. I have tried the Thrazgad ore, as Narrak suggested, to mend its cracks, but it merely sits "discarded and forgotten" next to my workbenches. Foolish duergar, not to understand the true purpose of this ancient power! It will conquer Gracklstugh, just as I plan. Today, I touched it with a spark of my own will, and it flashed! A mere flicker, but a sign! A squeal of glee escaped me. Soon, my Prince, soon.
**Day 25 – The Prince's Gift Arrives**
The Gray Ghosts delivered it! The Red Dragon Egg! What a marvel! The Keepers are in a panic over its loss, but they don't understand the true glory that awaits this "replacement". This is no mere insurance policy; it is the vessel for my greatest creation, a gift worthy of Demogorgon himself. The Deep King will be "delighted" when he sees it, though he knows nothing yet of its true destiny. My work begins at once. The notes are spread, the circles drawn.
**Day 38 – Mutagenic Progress!**
The experiments are progressing gloriously! The egg pulses with new life, and my notes confirm my suspicions: the mutations are taking hold. I've surrounded it with the finest reagents: hair, scales, fungi from the tunnels, and... other, more precious viscera. My goal is clear, a two-headed wyrmling, a perfect "Prince's gift" for Demogorgon, to serve as his mount. Grygum, the cleric of Bahamut, spoke of "freedom of choice" for dragons, but what he doesn't understand is that true choice lies in serving the Prince of Demons. The transformation will make it *perfect*.
**Day 47 – The Obelisk Responds**
I returned to the Obelisk today, feeling the madness and corruption of the city seep into my very being. The constant war between the Keepers and the Council, Gartokkar's paranoia, Errde's "conspiracy theories" – it's all part of the spiral. I pressed my hand to the Obelisk again, channeling the energy of the Whorlstone Tunnels into its fractures. It didn't just flash this time; the very air around it flared! It hungers for more power, more chaos! This monolith will be the instrument of our ascension, allowing us to conquer Gracklstugh and deliver it as a sacrificial gift to Demogorgon.
**Day 54 – Anticipation and Destiny**
The egg is nearing its time! Weeks, they say, until it hatches. I can already feel the dual-headed presence forming within. My "creation" for Demogorgon will soon be revealed. The Obelisk, too, senses the coming shift. Its purpose, alongside the egg, is to herald the Prince's arrival and the "genocidal war" that will cleanse this city. All the pieces are falling into place. The path forward is clear, and it is glorious.


He also finds some letters 


### Letter 1: From Pliinki to Uskvil (Gray Ghosts Leader)
***To: Uskvil, Master Thief***
*The Egg has arrived! Your operatives, those foolish Gray Ghosts, delivered it precisely as planned, though they do not comprehend the true glory of their retrieval. The Keepers of the Flame are in a panic over its loss, believing it merely a "replacement" for their bloated wyrm. They are so blind! This is no mere insurance policy; it is the vessel for my greatest creation, a gift worthy of Demogorgon himself.*
*The mutations are taking hold, just as my notes predicted. Soon, the two-headed wyrmling will be ready to serve as our Prince's mount. How fares the Thrazgad ore? Narrak mentioned you were assisting with its application to the Obelisk. It refuses to accept the material so far, stubbornly sitting "discarded and forgotten" next to my workbenches. We must find a way to mend its fractures, for it is the key to conquering Gracklstugh and offering it as a sacrificial gift to our Lord.*
*Continue your diversions. The city's destabilization proceeds apace, fueled by the Deepking's escalating paranoia and erratic edicts. Keep the Deep King "delighted" in his ignorance.*
*By Diirinka's Fractured Stone, Pliinki*


### Letter 2: From Aliinka (Council of Savants / Gray Ghosts) to Pliinki
***To: Pliinki, Most Devoted***
*Your updates on the Prince's Gift are... stimulating. The Keepers of the Flame remain obsessed with their "missing" egg, a truly delightful piece of chaos we've unleashed upon them. Uskvil confirmed the successful retrieval of both the dragon egg and the Clan Thrazgad ore, as ordered. The Deepking remains blissfully unaware of his true vulnerability.*
*Our operatives, under the guise of the Gray Ghosts, continue their work in the city, ensuring the whispers of dissent spread like contagion. The Deepking's increased reliance on the Empty-Scabbard Killers for his wanton assassinations only serves our purpose, drawing attention away from our true agenda. Captain Blackskull of the Stone Guard, in her own misguided paranoia, is actively searching for "corruption", unwittingly aiding our efforts to sow discord.*
*Narrak is pleased with the Council's continued indoctrination; almost all members have now embraced the true path, thanks to our careful placements of the 'Y' carvings. The city spirals precisely as we planned, preparing for the true glory that awaits it.*
*For the Coming, Aliinka*


### Letter 3: From Pliinki to Uskvil
***To: Uskvil, My Resolute Assistant***
*My frustration with the Obelisk grows. That acid-resistant ore from the Thrazgad Clan, which you so expertly acquired, has proven useless in mending its cracks. It still sits "discarded and forgotten" next to my workbenches. The quasi-magical energy it leaks promises so much, but its fractures defy my touch. How are we to fully harness its power to conquer Gracklstugh if it resists simple repair?*
*Meanwhile, the egg flourishes! The two-headed mutation is nearly complete, a testament to the Prince's foresight and my dedication. I can feel the life within it, pulsing with demonic potential. This "creation" for Demogorgon will be flawless, a true measure of our devotion.*
*Ensure the Deepking's hit list remains in the assassins' hands. The chaos it creates serves to further erode his authority and prepare the populace for what is to come. Our sacrifices will be glorious.*
*The Stone Hungers, Pliinki*


### Letter 4: From Narrak (Cult Leader) to Pliinki
***To: Pliinki, My Inspired Disciple***
*The seeds we've sown are bearing fruit, Pliinki. The madness and corruption spread throughout Gracklstugh. The Deepking, in his senile paranoia, continues to issue edicts that weaken his own authority, and his reliance on the Empty-Scabbard Killers to eliminate "opponents" is a gift. Errde Blackskull is consumed by her own "conspiracy theories," hunting phantoms while the true power shifts beneath her feet.*
*The Keepers of the Flame are utterly distracted by the loss of the egg, a secret they guard jealously from the Deepking. They have no idea it is destined to serve a far greater purpose than simply replacing their fat dragon.*
*Your work with the Obelisk and the egg is paramount. This ancient monolith, once repaired, will be the instrument of our ascension, allowing us to conquer Gracklstugh and deliver it as a sacrificial gift to Demogorgon. The path forward is clear: destabilize, corrupt, and then, offer the city to our Prince. All of Gracklstugh will be a fitting tribute, and the "genocidal war" against the derro that Gartokkar so desires will merely be the first cleansing.*
*The Prince Awaits, Narrak*
*        *
Zalthir knows he has enough to condemn the Derro and Duergar to a genocidal war that will result in the utter destruction of the city of Gracklstugh. 


“But is that the right thing to do?” he wonders. 
## Grygum 


Grygum reads what Zalthir has found and is disturbed. And the egg disturbs him further. As he sits there, he remembers some text from the temple where he learned of the power of Bahamut - 


*"When the egg, crimson-hued, promises but a shadow's ride, does one mend the shell, or seek to free the spark within? The true wyrm's form is not etched by fate's first breath, nor by sorcerous hand. It is the choices that twist the spirit, or set it soaring. To break the chains of another's dark design, even when madness fuels the crafting, is to affirm the very freedom Bahamut cherishes.” *


He scratches his head. He remembers how Bahamut’s clerics never gave him a straight answer. 


The egg is no longer a dragon. It is a physical manifestation of a demon. The egg should be destroyed. 


“We shall return the egg to Gartokkar,” he declares. 


Zalthir stares at him, confused, “What?”


“This is no longer a dragon. And so when this abomination hatches, the dragon Themberchaude will have its revenge on those who would think to control it.” 


\*rattle\* 


Grygum stands at attention and turns to the rattling sound.


There is Thorin with a baby rattle. A giant baby rattle that looks like it would fit a dragon. 


Thorin shouts, “Look what I found.” 


Grygum approaches him, “This is a baby dragon rattle. How curious.” 


He examines it further, “It says made by clan Thrazgad.” 


“How curious. Why would they make a baby rattle for a dragon? Why would this rattle be here?” 


Thorin rattles it some more, “We should get a baby dragon. I would like to have a dragon. It would be so cool if we had a dragon.” 


Grygum is appalled. Zalthir is a dragonborn. And Dragonborn are considered, by some, a draconic abomination. 


Grygum coughs. He watches as Thorin stares at him and realizes what he said, “I’m sorry. I didn’t mean that we don’t have a pure dragon, and that I wanted a pure dragon.” He pauses, “Okay, that sounded worse. I am going to stop now.” 


Grygum watches Zalthir clench and unclench.  


## Thorin


“So what do we do? I am still partial to the ride Thermbechaude out of this place.” 


But the loss of Buppido, and the death of the derro, and the destruction of the dragon in the egg, and the near death of Eldeth have made the idea of leaving Gracklstugh a smouldering inferno less appealing. 


Zalthir mutters, “I vote we get out of here as discreetly as possible, creating the least amount of chaos as possible.” 


Thorin sighs, “Yeah.” 


Grygum pulls out a scrap of paper, “I’ve been taking notes on all of the deals we have made. And it seems to me that the best choice we have is to give the egg to Gartokkar and then use him to escape from Gracklstugh. We tell Gartokkar that the Derro didn’t steal the egg, but some other crazed group. We also explain that we need his help to escape because of the deal we made with the Stone guards and that if Errde were to imprison us, we might be compelled to change our story under torture.” 


Thorin stares at him. 


“I take notes. It’s what I do.” 


Thorin nods, “Let’s do it.” 


And so they are ready to leave the chamber of the Obelisk. 


But Thorin stops them. “We need a name.” 


Everyone stares at him.


“A what?” asks Zalthir.


“A name! Like the First Faction was the legendary heroes that saved the North! And then there are the legendary heroes of the War of the Giants, the Three Half Pints and the Pint (3HPP)! We need a name!” 


There is a moment of silence. 


Grygum mutters, “The Second Faction?” 


Thorin looks at him and arches an eyebrow, but Daz says what he is thinking, “Too derivative.” 


And then he smiles, “I have it - The Ember Vanguard.” 


Thorin looks around and notices that Zalthir is nodding, Daz is smiling, and even Grygum seems pleased. 


“The Ember Vanguard, Onwards!” 


The groan from his companions is noticeable. But he doesn’t care. From the cave entrance, they choose not to circle back the way they came. As Zalthir explains, “The Empty Scabbard Killers might want to kill us.” 


Thorin agrees, so they go down a different cave tunnel, which leads to a pair of double doors. 


In front of those double doors is a small squad of derro. 


“Do we attack?” 


Daz turns to him, “No.”  
## Diirdeklin the Derro


Diirdeklin has been at this guard post for days. Pliinki has promised him that this is part of some plan that will free the Derro from the bondage of Duergar. But Diirdeklin has heard that before. 


There is a noise coming from the north. That’s odd. It doesn’t sound like Derro. He’s worried. 


The creatures are advancing, as if they own this place. Well, he’ll show them. 


He reaches for the alarm. And then he hears a booming voice - “The people you are trying to warn are dead.” 


Diirdeklin’s hand drops the alarm bell and grabs his weapon more tightly. 


It’s then that he sees a Drow Archmage who has summoned a meteor swarm. This is no ordinary group of mercenaries; this is a powerful raid by the Drow of Menzoberranzan. 


He stops. He just wants to live. 


The Drow shouts, “We are The Ember Vanguard, and you will let us pass!” 


Diirdeklin worried that Diinarnnmyr might foolishly try to fight,   shouts, “Yes, pass!”


And as they leave the cave, he thinks, “A Drow incursion! This is not good. And if they killed Pliinki, that means that they have bigger plans.” 


As they leave Diinarnnmyr mutters, “The Ember Vanguard - the Drow are now working with the Duergar to subdue us!” 
## Daz


Daz is very pleased with his use of dancing lights and the effect it had on the Derro. His friends congratulate him. 


Thorin shouts, “The Ember Vanguard are in the house!” 


The mage likes the idea of being a feared group of mercenaries instead of a pathetic group of adventurers who are running around trying to stay alive. 


He has found purpose. He is the feared mage of the Ember Vanguard!  


Once past the doors, Thorin leads them west, instead of south, where the Empty Scabbard Killers live. 


After walking in the enormous 20-foot-wide cavern for a few minutes, Thorin hears a yelp. 


He turns around and sees Grygum enveloped by a creature that looks like a manta ray. 


Grygum shouts in pain. 


Daz ponders his spell list and has some intriguing ideas, but realizes that the old standby, Magic Missile, is probably the best bet. 


He watches as Zalthir and Thorin attack the creature, trying to get it to release Grygum.


Daz grits his teeth as he hears Grygum’s muffled sounds of pain and watches as the Orc can’t escape. 


So he casts silvery barbs to help Grygum escape, and then Daz follows up with the deadly chimes of the spell toll the dead. 


Zalthir strikes the creature a few more times with his fist, and the beast dies before Grygum can take advantage of the spell. 


But the Orc is grateful, but he looks unhappy as he is covered in the acid slime of the Trapper. 


# Chapter 20 The Derro like Demogorgon
## Grygum.


The battle was terrifying. But I am alive. Wounded. But alive. So let me do a bit of Divine magic and heal myself. And that friendly dwarf, the one Thorin likes. 


“May the power of the platinum dragon cure us all!” I shout. That’s a bit of theater that I created for the believing. 


I should be honest, it’s theater I created for myself. Bahamut is boring. Stroud was exciting. Bahamut, not so much. 


## Daz


A good rest is always beneficial, but we need to get out of here.


Zalthir, the good old monk, is scouting ahead, keeping us safe. Good for him. 


“Something’s up ahead.” 


I have to assume it’s not good. So I follow Grygum and Thorin around the turn of the tunnel and see a single Derro standing over a pit, with an unbelievable smell emanating from it.  


I look at him carefully.  He  has blue, gray skin and pale eyes that lack both irises and pupils. He has thin, stringy hair, dull white, constantly looking greasy and unkempt. The creature is wearing scraps of tattered leather and cloth stained with grime and the foul odors of wherever he has been working. Now that’s interesting, he seems to be muttering to himself. Bah, it’s a common trait among the irrevocably insane of the Derro. 


Wait, that’s interesting, he’s got an amulet of Demogorgon. 


I stare at him. I wonder is he the true-believing kind that has warped his world view? Or is he just a dummy that needs someone else to think for him and is therefore a true believer?


I look at him carefully to see some spark of genius. I see nothing. He’s a dummy. I recall the stories of the Derro, creatures that served the mind flayers and had their minds destroyed. They are not well in the best of times. 
## Grygum 


I approach the poor creature. And examine what he is doing. 


Well, that’s interesting. He appears to be tossing body parts over the ledge into the pit. 


The Derro looks at me with fear. Good. 


“Don’t mind me, I am just looking to learn about how the big project is progressing. Are you on schedule?” 


“The great project of Ulnara of the Council of Savants!”


“Yes! Is it on schedule?” 


The creature whimpers before me and pleads, “But Pliinki promised Skiit a better job.” 


I smile, “Only if you succeed at this one, Skiit. I see a lot of zombies.” 


Skiit  looks at me and then points at Spiderbait, “Can I kill that one over there?” 


I am worried, but I know how to deflect, just double down on his anxieties, “I am not going to hand you new body parts because you can’t keep up!” 


I tried to intimidate, and failed. Maybe it is my gentleness from all my time at the temple, because instead of this thing cowering, it puffs itself up and says, “I am a follower of Demogorgon! Pliinki has said that anybody who follows Demogorgon is making the Derro proud and powerful. And we’re going to be great again!” 


And it gets worse. 


“I don’t believe you guys work for us. I think you work for the Duergar or the Mindflayers!” 


Seeing the zombies below, they do need some new body parts, and this one Derro, would be a fine addition. 


I push him over the cliff. At the same time, Daz unleashes a light show. 


## Daz


I approach the ledge, and the first thing that hits me is the smell that reeks of death and decomposed flesh. I open my eyes and absorb how enormous it is. The glow of faerzress is everywhere, seeming to flow like fog around dark shapes shambling across the pit. A crack in the southeast wall of the pit leads to a narrow tunnel, flanked by mounds of fungi and offal.


From there, a voice and an Ogre Zombie emerge. 


“What is the meaning of this? Who are you? Who do you think you are?” 


“We are the Ember Guard,” shouts Grygum. I smile. I like that name. 


“Who do you work for?” she shouts. 


I pause and try to answer. However, we have struck numerous deals with various other parties, and I'm no longer sure what to say. 


Grygym answers - "Ah, my friend, you've just asked him a simple question: "So, Grygum, who do you work for, truly?"


He looks at her with a mix of weariness and a peculiar Orcish amusement. "That is a question that requires more than a simple answer. It is, in fact, a Divine Scrutiny, a profound act of investigation into the very threads of our intertwined fates, here in this churning city of Gracklstugh."


I know what will come next: a long, meandering discussion of the nature of the Divine Scrutiny and how a Divine Query is necessary, and how he must consider Aspects of the Truth and that he must consider the Divine Ledgers or Celestial Archives from which the truth will be drawn. 


Or he could just give them an answer. 


Clerics of Bahamut. 


Now let’s take a look at her more closely. She’s the necromancer in charge of this operation. But she’s a cultist of Demogorgon, and she’s a derro, and fear works well for keeping these creatures at bay. 


The Derro named Skiit, which Grygum tossed into the pit, is starting to wake up. I know what to do. 


I cast Maximillian’s Earthen Grasp and start to crush the poor unfortunate creature. 


Ulnara looks at me, and she has that look of someone who thought they had all the cards, and understood what was going on, and realizes she doesn’t anymore. Her arrogance disappears, and her sniveling, subservient persona emerges. 


The transformation is stunning. 


“Your lordship! Or was it the Ember Vanguard? What a wonderful name for such a powerful group. Do not worry, after he’s dead I will turn him into a zombie and he will seve the cult of Demogorgon forever!” 


I snap my fingers, trying to kill him, but the derro escapes. 


So I cast Toll the Dead, and the deadly chimes echo throughout the caves, but only it’s intended target hears them, and his heart stops, and he dies. 


I look at Ulnara, who realizes that I am Drow. And that the Drow do not mess around. 


“Thank you for this new supply! I know you will tell Pliinki that I Ulnar,a did much to help the Ember Vanguard!” 


“We shall, certainly,” says Grygum in his preacher’s voice. 


## Thorin


The caves go on. We arrive at a door, and we rest. Resting is good. 


A little bit later, we arrive at a door. It’s a big door. However, we have a lot of people, so we open it up and continue. 


“Left or right?” I ask. 


The discussion begins, and I am too tired for this, so I say - “East.” 


Ahead, I see what appears to be a break in the tunnel. I stop because the smell is just awful.


Don’t these guys know how to take a bath? 


Seeing how we will overcome the violent urge to vomit, I go closer. The smell is coming from cages assembled from scrap iron on both sides of the chamber. A spiral path circles into the center of the room, marked off by small stone pylons.
.
I notice two Derro in front of a tent, near a tent. Both are talking while ignoring each other. They are not well. 


“ More of this, always mor,e the mastery demands. Many contributions, the prince is hungry, always hungry,” says one. 


The other intones as it stares intently into the murky bubbling cauldron, tracing an invisible pattern with a dirty finger, “Water it chips, not like the dark lake. There, I pulled something from the dark ones, A scale smooth, this polished obsidian, but it shimmered like madness. In the dim light came from the deep, the deepest part with voices seeing.”


Grygum mutters, “They are mad.”


Zalthir asks - “Do we need to fight them?”


I squint at the tents and the room and say, “No. There is nothing of value here.” 


We agree and move on. 


And so we continue on our journey through the caves, when a Derro patrol stumbles on us. 


Daz insists we march as if we own this place. And it works. The creatures are fearful and somewhat deranged. 


Just a few more yards and we will be past them. 


But Grygum notices something, and he can’t keep quiet. 


“I worship Bahamut!” 


The moment that Grygum mentioned "Bahamut," I knew we were in for it. These Derro, bless their simple, deranged minds, don't take kindly to anything outside their two-headed deity. And sure enough, they immediately attack. 


Grygum shouts, “I thought we could have a deep Phylosophical conversation!” 


I roll my eyes. 


The Derro are Dwarves that were slaves of the mindflayers, who corrupted their fundamental nature until they are barely Dwarves. They are mad. These are not creatures to reason with. 


I moved forward, my heavy armor clanking, but I ignored the sound. My focus was on the nearest Derro. He was a scrawny one, probably thought he was tough. I swung my longsword, a satisfying *thwack* as it connected. "Take that, you blithering fool!" I yelled, though I'm sure it was lost in the chaos. A hit, but not enough to drop him, but enough to know he'd messed with the wrong dwarf. 


The Derro themselves were predictably clumsy. One swung at me, but my armor held. The other landed a hit on Grygum, but our allies were quick to retaliate, dealing a good chunk of damage to him. Zalthir, bless his arcane heart, summoned his darkness, enveloping a couple of them. Then, in a burst of brilliant speed, he critically struck one of the Darrow. Impressive.


Daz, always quick with a spell, launched his magic missiles. A flurry of arcane energy streaked across the tunnel, and the DerroI had struck, already reeling, and fell. One down. Good.


The remaining Derro, true to their limited intellect, continued their mindless attacks. One swung wildly at Zalthir, missing entirely. Another charged Grygum, screaming some incoherent babble about their master. My armor held, and I parried his pathetic attack. "One head is better than two!" I roared, pushing him back.


My chance came again, and I didn't hesitate. I brought my longsword down hard on the Derro, attacking Grygum. The sword cut through his flimsy armor and into his chest, and it dropped like a sack of rocks. Dead. "This is how the Bahamut walks!" I declared, standing over his fallen form, ready to take on the next fool who dared challenge us.


But they were all dead. 
## Daz


Our journey continues until we reach another cave entrance. And this one we must go through. 


And yes, the unspeakable stench that seems to follow the Derro emanates here. This time it is the smell of brimstone and chemicals.


The Ember Vanguard will march in, but we tell our companions to wait outside. Jim Jar, Spiderbait, Sarith, Eldeth, and Stool look at me worried, but I motion for them to stay. 


I walk in quietly. We don’t need light, because we can all see in the dark. 


As I walk in, I can see the light of campfires. 


Grygum shouts, “Watch it!” 


I look down at what he is pointing at, and it’s a poorly disguised pit trap. Whatever is here is at least trying to keep out outsiders. 


Further within, the cavern is cast in an eerie, hellish red glow that swirls into spiral patterns on the walls, creating dancing jet shadows. The air is muted, and the dripping water makes no echo, as if one stood in open air. Fungi grow rampantly in large patches on the floors and walls, adding to the oppressive atmosphere.


And I finally spot the inhabitants, some Derro and Death dogs.


They don’t notice us, so we continue. 


The cavern floor rises to form a natural 5-foot-high platform. A glowing ritual circle dominates the top of the platform. Around the platform are books made from Trillimac. I look carefully and notice a few of the titles - “The Spiraling Descent: A Treatise on Duality and Madness,” and “The Prince's Gift: On the Creation of Favored Spawn”, and “Rituals of the Two-Headed Beast.” 


Errde Blackstaff wants evidence of Demogorgon’s influence, and here it is. And amongst the books are various papers. Knowing these creatures, there is probably enough evidence to convince Errde of whatever she wants. 


I might not want to give it to her. But I know her type; if she doesn’t get evidence, she’ll invent it. 


Just then, one of them picks up a book and starts to read from it. 


Another asks, “Narrack, what are we doing?” 


I look at this Derro, who seems to be the orchestrator of the disturbing scene before me. This is Narrak. His pale, derro features are perpetually contorted, twisting into a grotesque mask of terrifying, spiraling madness. His eyes, perhaps unnervingly bright in the dim light, dart about with a frenetic, almost desperate energy.


He gestures wildly at a few apprentices. There’s an undeniable, warped intellect simmering beneath his frantic movements, but it is utterly consumed by the chaotic evil that seems to radiate from his very being. His presence in this space is deeply unsettling, a chilling testament to the insidious influence of the demon lord he serves. 


He shouts - “We are conducting experiments!” 


They chant back at him - “For what purpose!” 


He screams - “The only purpose that matters! The elevation of the Derro, the Triumph of Demogorgon, and the destruction of the Duergar!” 


## Zalthir


I observe everything and say nothing. My mind is clear. I act without speaking. I do because I know. 


# Chapter 21 The ritual

What’s that in the middle of the platform? 


A statue of a stone giant with a second head emerging from it.*

*I need to think.

*“Hear me, you two-headed fools! *
*His madness flows, our city drools! *

Fortunately, Grygum notices something, or has a divine inspiration, or lies like so many of Lolth’s priests. We are told that Hgraam should be able to reverse whatever ill effects on the Stone Giants.

I look at him confused, and I show him the statue on the platform. He sighs as he realizes it is only 2 feet tall.   


I try not to laugh. 


### Zalthir 


We are once again at the final resting place of Bupido. It’s a grim place, full of dead bones, and an altar to some demonic power or some mad idea. 


I look forward to meditating when my thoughts are interrupted. 


“We should go talk to Rump-a-dump.” 


It’s the childlike voice of the Myconid. The spores allow us to communicate in certain tactical situations silently, which makes her abilities valuable, but. 


I feign ignorance, but the creature continues, “We went over this last time, Zalthir. Rump-a-dump is a sprout from my circle who is unhappy. We need to go talk to Rump-a-dump, find out what’s going on, and bring them back.” 


“If I recall, there was this crazy group of ape-like creatures?”


“Yes Zalthir! It’s totally related to that and the spores and everything. And if Rump-a-Dump is there, it’s totally okay. Like nobody has to die.” The creature pauses, “In fact we shouldn’t kill anyone! Cause they are myconids. And they are like me. And we need to get Rump-a-dump.” 


Another thing for another day, “Sounds good. Let’s put a pin in it and revisit later.” 


I think the matter is settled, and prepare to meditate. And the creature once again enters my head, “Zalthir, you never listen to anything I say. It’s not fair. Why don’t you listen to me!” 


“I listen. There is some ambiguity as to whether the myconids are friends or foe.” My patience has worn thin. And at this time, in the monastery, the young children would have learned to be silent, I wonder if this creature can learn to be quiet. 


“Zalthir, they aren’t enemies. They are zombies. Well, what you would call zombies. We have this process that allows us to convert our dead enemies into zombies.” 


“I would like not to become a zombie.”


That startles the creature, which seems to want to cry, “Rump-a-dump would never let them do that! You don’t want to help my friends, and so why should I help you?” 


My need for quiet is intense, and I would appreciate it if this creature could be quiet. I think back to what the parents would say. Ah, yes, “I think that our current focus should be on surviving, so let’s focus on gEttin g some slee,p and we will take it from there.” 


And the creature falls asleep. 


I look at sleeping and shrug, wondering why parents complain so bitterly about their children. 


### Grygum


I prepare to say my prayers when the Pelek, who now possesses the body of Derro, asks if we would tie him up. He’s concerned that he might lose control of the Derro, who might try to kill us. 


At first, I am confused and uncertain. More to the point, are we safe with this ghost? 


Daz, however, explains that there is no such danger. And that they would all be safer with the ghost tied up. The last time they trusted someone, Bupido killed one of their group. 


As we tie Pelek/Derro up, JimJar again offers one of his silly bets. He bets me that my knots won’t hold. 


## 2nd day of the 2nd tenday of Myrtul


### Grygum


And when we wake up, Pelek/Derro is still tied up. And I collect my winnings. 


As I untie him, Pelek mutters, “I haven’t had a good night's sleep in ages. Although it’s unclear I if I am sleeping … There is this whole question about whether death is a form of sleep. I suppose I will find out.” 


This is a good time to engage in a deep debate on the nature of the afterlife, but the Ember Vanguard must get ready for battle.  


And so we head out from Bupido’s lair and find ourselves once again outside of the cultist cavern. And once again, we have managed to sneak into the room. There is a derro who, by all rights, should see us, but he seems to be preoccupied with a death dog, desperately trying hard not to be noticed. 


Thorin points to a statue of another two-headed stone giant. I reassure Thorin that Hgraam will take care of this, and our job is to end this cult. 


He seems good with the plan. 


And so we approach the platform and see a furious head cultist is chortling, “We have successfully converted another of Hgraam’s giants to a two-headed monster. Now we shall convert one more, and by golly, they will lay waste to Gracklstugh!”


He motions to all of the Derro to surround him and begins, “First, you will take the same positions as yesterday.”


One of the Derro raises a hand, and asks where, and the head cultist shouts, “OVER THERE!!!” 


The Derro nods. 


They all move to their positions. 


 “Now, I will begin by chanting.


"Hear me, you two-headed fools!

But the Derro only do so half heartedly, at which point the one I assume is Narrak, like every choir director ever shouts, “Silence, you blithering half-wits! More vigor! This city's doom, a ritual! Dig it!"


Zalthir turns to me and says, “I want to watch!” 


I raise an eyebrow. 


Narrak turns to his group, “Clearly, we have not learned our lines, and the ritual will not work if we can’t say our lines. And with fervor.” 


The Derro groan and gather around him. 


Zalthir turns to the Ember Vanguard, “They are bunched up; it’s time to attack.”

I know that look, the look of a priest trying to get the members of his temple to practice the rituals.

I nod. 


The last thing I hear Narrak say is  “ More vigor! This city's doom needs a ritual. Dig it!” 
### 
Daz


I finally understand why that Derro, who should have seen us, has not noticed us. He’s trying to avoid being seen by Narrak. 


I’ve seen that before, when the various Priestesses of Lolth would get angry, and everyone tried hard to be invisible. A high-level cleric can kill you very easily.  


Zalthir and I had discussed what we should do. He plans to use his darkness, and wants to know who I will target. I say the Ettin . He nods and soon all the derro are covered in his magical darkness.


From inside it, Narrak shouts - Demogorgon’s madness flows through me! You will embrace it or *break *trying!”


I'm not sure what the point of that comment is. 


Zalthir rushes into his darkness and breathes fire. 


He seems disappointed with the outcome. 


And of course, Narrak has to provide a running commentary, “Fire is nothing compared to the awesome power of Demogorgon!” 


One of the Derro rushes out of Zalthir’s darkness, notices Grygum, and strikes him while chanting, “You shall die! You shall die!” 


The Derro misses. 


Another creature attacks Zalthir in the darkness. It took shrieks something intelligible. I don’t hear the sound of weapons making contact with flesh, so I assume the monk avoided gEttin g hurt. 


And then I hear Zalthir shout, “There’s some kind of effect that the circle has on those who enter it. Some kind of madness gripped my mind, but my monk training allowed me to stop it. Be careful!” 


And then I hear Grygum moaning in pain, then in incantation. There is a violent heaving. I look at him as he straightens and vomits forth a wave of acid.


This is not a spell I wish to cast. 


Instead, I will use my scorching rays. Three spears of flame, raging hues of orange and red, appear above me. My skin prickles and sweats under their intense heat—but I am not frightened. I feel invigorated. Empowered. These are the vessels of my inner fury. They roar like fierce beasts as I hurl them toward the Ettin . 


Narrak shouts, “What’s going on here!” 


The Ettin  points at the three of us outside of the darkness, but Narrak can’t see anything. 


Another Derro rushes out of the darkness and attacks Grygum, missing. 
Finally, Narrak emerges and shouts, “I will use fear!” He takes a white feather and points at Thorin, Grygum, and Zalthir, says the magic words, and the three members of the Ember Vanguard look terrified. 


As the fear takes over, he shouts - “Beyond you creatures!” 


This is not good. 


The Ettin  raises his battle axe and strikes the frightened Thorin, and misses, but the morning star hits. Thorin looks battered.  


If I am left alone, this will not be good. 


And then Zalthir has a brilliant ploy. He moves the darkness over Narrak. As the source of the Ember Vanguard’s fear is no longer visible, they are no longer affected by it.  


A guiding bolt from Grygum strikes the Ettin , and it groans and then smiles. I don’t think the spell hurt him as badly as we need. 


But Thorin has a better chance to strike the creature, and he does. 


I stare at the battle, and then think that Narrak is still in the darkness, and I could keep them there with a spell. And so I cast Maximillian’s Earthen Grasp on where I think he is.


Narrak screams in rage - “You cannot stop the inevitable... the curse spreads!”


# Chapter 22 Defeating Narrak, ending the ritual, and next steps. 
### Grygum 
The air is thick with the foul stench of these Derro, their maddening chant of 'die, die, die' echoing in my ears. Gru Manga, the hulking Etten, roars before us. As a cleric of Bahamut, my duty is clear: protect the innocent and smite these wicked creatures. I focus, channeling the Platinum Dragon's justice, and my acid spell lashes out, catching three of the chanting Derro. But then Gru Manga's roar fills the cavern, an enraged bellow directed straight at me, convinced I am the source of his pain. Before I can react, a Derro bursts from Zalthir's darkness, its hook sphere striking me. The hit throws me off balance and I am knocked prone. Worse, the impact shatters my concentration, and the acidic mist I'd conjured dissipates.
### Zalthir
While Grygum struggles, pinned and prone, I act. My monastic training calls for calm and precise action, even when faced with unexpected turns. I activate my Eldritch Maul, transforming my hands into a writhing mass of tentacles that extends a terrifying fifteen feet. It is unsettling, even to me, but undeniably effective. With swift motion, I move the sphere of darkness, enveloping Gru Manga once more, depriving him of sight. Now, with him blinded, my tentacles lash out, striking the Ettin. I press the assault, channeling a focus point for another strike. Drawing on the skills I learned in the monastery to grapple folks, a skill that proved useful in a tavern brawl once,  my tentacles wrap around him, and Gru Manga is grappled, held tight in my grasp. The Ettin fights no more on his terms.
### Daz
The Ettin is grappling with Zalthir's tentacles, held tight in that strange new form of his. Grygum is back on his feet now, and I see him preparing another spell. Good. Zalthir moves his darkness, so my ocus shifts to another Derro. They are a nuisance, but some are weaker than others. I call upon the simplest, yet most reliable, of my spells: Magic Missile. Two bolts streak towards the weaker Derro northeast of Grygum, and the third unerringly finds its mark on a stronger one. The weaker Derro crumples, **dead** instantly. It is a clean kill, one less chanting maniac to deal with. Just then, Narrak's voice, strangely cutting out, booms, 'fools, your sacrifice is but a step toward glory!' Empty words from a cultist who underestimates the effectiveness of direct force.
### Grygum 
I pull myself up, shedding the prone condition with a determined heave, using half my movement to regain my footing. My previous acid spell was disrupted, but I still have more slots to cast Tasha's Caustic Brew. I unleash a stream of corrosive acid, spraying all three Derro. Two manage to dodge its full effect, but one does not and now suffers at the start of its turns. I let them feel the burn of Bahamut's righteous wrath. Narrak speaks. His words hold dark meaning, perhaps they are part of the ritual, a ritual that needs to be stopped. We have to end this.
### Zalthir


Gru Manga, despite my latest strike, is still clinging to life, but barely. This Ettin is a stubborn brute, but his time is up. I deliver the final, decisive blow. Gru Manga falls to the ground. Narrak again screeches, 'Your sacrifice is but a step towards the glory,' though his conviction is, clearly, waning. One major threat is neutralized. My gaze then sweeps to another Derro, and with another efficient strike it diesl. Efficiency in action, that is the way.
### Daz


Narrak, the foolish cultist of this twisted scene, attacks Grygum, although still restrained by my Maximilian's Earthen Grasp. He attempts to break free of my grasp, but fails. Now, it is time to press the advantage, to ensure he remains our captive. I command the earthen hand to squeeze him further. Narrak might talk of glory and sacrifice, but he is currently just a victim of my magic. Thorin heals himself, ready for another push, and I know we are nearing the end of this chaotic dance.


### Grygum


Narrak strikes at Thorin with a short spear. The evil cult leader will die soon. So I focus my intent, casting True Strike, honing my aim for the next blow. Then, I bring my mace down on a Derro, but it is still standing. Thorin observes that it’s nearly dead. I smile, I know it won't last long. We have control, and the enemy is faltering.


### Zalthir


The fight ends swiftly after Grygum's last strike, with Thorin making the final, grim decision to kill Narrak, his last words a desperate plea: 'No, the ritual cannot be undone!'. It seems his 'glory' has indeed ended here. All enemies are now dead. While I prefer discretion and the avoidance of unnecessary conflict, the efficiency of our group in battle is undeniable. We are no longer mere prisoners; we are a formidable force. The 'silent spell' from earlier dissipates, and the true scope of this strange ritual, involving the two-headed stone giant statue, now presents itself. My thoughts, usually calm, ponder the true nature of Narrak's work: the statue, the "Rituals of the Two-Headed Beast," and the madness it induces in stone giants. We acquire some peculiar, yet potentially useful, items from Narrak's person and his chest, including gold, Keoghtom's Ointment, and strange texts. 


Four different factions sent us into these caves looking for evidence to bury the other. This evidence can bury this entire city in blood if we release it. 


We have the evidence that the king has been working with assassins to kill Eldeth’s clan,  an egg that would help the Keepers of the Flame or the Red Dragon, and proof of the Derro perfidity and support for Demogorgon. 
### Daz


Narrak is dead, silenced by Thorin's decisive blow. His frantic final words about the ritual are just the weak words of a follower of a demonic power. It is always about the rituals, isn't it? The air clears, and the silence of defeated enemies is a welcome change. My tactical mind immediately shifts from combat to intelligence gathering. There is still a Derro unnoticed in the background, a detail for later consideration, perhaps. I examine the two-foot-tall statue that is the ritual that turned one of Hargaam’s giants mad. 


I find a 'bunch of texts,' including 'The Rituals of the Two-Headed Beast,' which Narrak was reading. This confirms his role as the orchestrator. 


But what to do.


And then the curious JimJar speaks. He observes that we have this evidence that we can keep. He wants to make a bet that it would be helpful to us later. Jimjar's advice to 'hold onto these' for later usefulness is wise, as always. We have survived, and now we have leverage. The idea of 'installing democracy' is floated, but I laugh. The Duergar and their innate invisibility create a level of paranoia that prevents any kind of civil debate. 
### Stool 
“Hey, Zalthir? Grygum? Can we go save Rump-a-dump now? PLEASE!!!!!” 
# Chapter 23 The Dark Lady 
### Zalthir
The small myconid has become increasingly demanding that we save his friend Rump-a-dump. 
He says that his friend would never threaten him, and then talks about zombie creatures that were harvested from the dead. 
While he whines, the adults have more pressing concerns. We have enough information to create a civil war at best, or a genocidal massacre at worst. 
Jimjar suggests we hold onto it, even betting that we will find it very useful in the future. I find that notion absurd. Once we are out of the Underdark, I do not intend to come back. 
The group is conflicted about what to do, but I calmly remind them of our plan and its wisdom. 
And after some prattling and discussion, they agree that we will hand over the egg to Gartokkar and then escape via the ports. 
“Zalthir, why won’t we go save Rump-a-dump?” 
Daz, who demonstrates the cold detachment of the Drow, is indifferent. But Thorin Giantfriend seems determined to help Stool’s friend. 
At the monastery, children like this would be sent to a room and told only to return when they could understand why they must be silent. 
I patiently explain to Thorin that what we know is that these bipedal mushrooms can mess with people’s minds and control their bodies. 
Stool, of course, insists that his people are harmless. 
As his obstinacy does not affect me, he turns to Thorin for support. 


Which is a good strategy. 


Thorin explains that it is splitting. 
I sense a strategic awareness on the part of the small creature that suggests it is far wiser than I have given it credit. 
Unfortunately, Stool is too successful, and Thorin is off. 
Stool looks at me, and I am convinced that if he could, he would be sticking his tongue out at me. 
I again encourage my allies to prepare themselves against any of the powers of the Myconid. And it is then that Daz explains that we have nothing to fear. 
“They have the power to release spores. The dangerous spores are only hazardous in melee range. They can only turn creatures they have killed into Zombies. Until you are dead, the zombie process doesn’t work.” 


## 3rd day of the 2nd Tenday of Myrtul 


### Thorin 
We soon arrive at the cave with the Myconids, who seem to be dancing as if at a Wandering Veil concert that he attended.


My allies seem confused, and I realized that not everybody is aware of The Wandering Veil. So I explain that this eclectic troupe of bards and mystics has roamed the realms for decades, their music a swirling tapestry of haunting ballads, raucous tavern shanties, and spellbinding improvisations that seem to bend the very fabric of reality. 


Grygum looks at the Myconids and looks at me, and is still confused. So I explain “The Veil’s performances are never the same twice; each show is a living ritual, a communal experience where the lines between audience and artist blur, and even the most hardened adventurer finds themselves dancing beneath a sky painted with arcane light.” 


As we stand there, Serith suddenly starts walking towards the Myconids as if compelled. 


He shouts - "The call... the Dark Lady is calling me! Can't you hear her? She sings in the spores, a song of becoming! Of true purpose! I... I must go to them! They know the way to the bloom!"


Zalthir notices this and stops him. 


Sarith protests, "I... I can feel her now! The whispers... the glory! The pain, the madness... it's all part of the becoming! We must join the Lady's dream! There is no other way now. She commands it. She calls!"


Sarith tries to resist, but seems conflicted. 


Zalthir while holding Sarith looks disapprovingly at Daz and says, “We are seeing effects that are stronger than 30’” 


And just then, Stool starts jumping up and down as he shouts to another sprout, Rump-a-Dump. 


### Rump-a-dump


I stare at my friend Stool and the humanoids he has brought. I sigh. Stool, once again, is speaking constantly, generating words and sounds, and not giving me a chance to think. 


Whereas he attempts to convey with an avalanche of words, I believe in a tersely worded comment that is precise and restrained. 


I shift my weight, looking towards the dwarf, then glance at Stool. I decide his enthusiastic bounciness is not helping but hindering. When I speak, I can hear the worry in my voice. 


"Greetings. I see Stool found you. \*\*Something is not right here.\*\*".


I gesture with a thick, stubby appendage towards the dancing myconids, then point to a taller figure among them. 


"It's Voosbur. He released strange spores... and everyone changed. They started... this.".


### Grygum 


The creature looks uncomfortable and very worried. 


"We were all very happy in Neverlight Grove," His thoughts briefly show a serene, glowing cavern before clouding with confusion. "Then Voosbur's spores came, and the next thing we knew, we were \*here\*. It was... a sudden jump. The others... I think they ate the silly mushrooms\*\* after we arrived.". His thoughts flicker to the shrinking/growing mushrooms you've encountered.


"I did not eat them. That is why I am not... like this.".


Thorin is shocked and asks, “Isn’t that Cannibalism?” 


Rump-a-dump stops and stares, “A mushroom is not a Myconid. It is my understanding that you eat other creatures that are like you? Are you cannibals?” 


I am cringing. 


Daz has his hands in his face, embarrassed and muttering, “Overbrighters. They understand nothing about the complex ecology of the Underdark.” 


"These are not our old dances. And the way they speak... about 'the Lady's dream,' it is confusing. Stool does not understand it either. It is not the way of myconids. We do not dance like this. This is... forced.".


"I am worried. I need to get back to Neverlight Grove. What if Voosbur's strange spores... infected the rest of my myconids back home?". "My Sovereign there, they might know a way out of here... if they are still themselves.".


I sigh, “Another race gone mad.” 


Thorin, who has started to dance as if he were at a Withering Veil concert, says, “I like these Myconids, basically don’t mess with them, they don’t mess with you.” 


Meanwhile, Sarith, who was never sane to begin with, says,  "We will rise! We will transform! This is the only way to escape... to truly live! The Dark Lady... she offers liberation... revenge for all that has been done!"


Zalthir recalls that Sarith’s urge to go to the Myconids increased when he was closer to them, and so pulls him back, and mutters, “The knowledge of the Drow …” 


As I stare at the situation, and mull over the words, “The Dark Lady,” I remember something from my teachings about a demonic power known as the Dark Lady in the holy text The Platinum Chronicle: Discourses on the Abyssal Blight. 



**Excerpt from The Platinum Chronicle: Discourses on the Abyssal Blight**
**On the Blight of Zuggtmoy, Demon Queen of Fungi, Lady of Rot and Decay**
This fiend, Zuggtmoy, the Demon Queen of Fungi, the Lady of Rot and Decay, is a grievous affront to the very essence of creation. Her being is the antithesis of justice, order, and compassion, for where the Platinum Dragon, Bahamut, seeks to foster life and free will, she yearns only for chaos, madness, and utter destruction.
Her powers are not born of strength, but of insidious corruption. She seeks ever to infect the living with her spores, transforming them into her mindless servants, destined to become naught but decomposing hosts for the mushrooms, mold, and other fungi that are her abhorrent spawn. This "gift" she offers is a perversion of life itself, a descent into a perpetual state of rot and decay, where the mind is consumed in a twisted, communal dream.


Let it be known to all who walk the paths of Bahaumuy: Zuggtmoy’s song is not of liberation but of forced perversion. She seeks to extinguish the freedom of choice that Bahamut cherishes for all creatures. To resist this Demon Queen is to champion life against the encroaching rot and madness. Thus, vigilance is paramount against the creeping influence of the Lady of Rot and Decay
I explain to my friends that this Dark Lady is, in fact, the Demoness. 


Zalthir looks particularly clever to be so far away from these Myconids. But Bahamut commands me not to walk away. 


I wonder aloud if it’s possible that whatever controls Voosbur can control us, but Daz explains that, as this is a Demonic curse, the method of propagation is not natural but magical. And in most likelihood requires consent or some exchange of bodily fluids. 


Zalthir, if he were here, would wonder if visiting the Neverlight Grove would be wise. After all, there is a chance that Zuggtomy is there. 


Thorin, terrified or reckless, mutters, “You throw a stone here, you hit a demon.” 


I nod.


And then turn to Thorin, “All roads lead to Voosbur. We must talk to him to discover what is going on.” 
### 
Daz


We approach the Myconid, and it stops its frantic dance for a moment. And then it continues its dance, but we hear it’s voice in our heads. 


“Hey, beautiful souls, you’ve been groovin’ through the dark for a while now, yeah? Dig this — there’s a far-out place, a hidden trip where the Lady herself spins the vibes. It’s like the ultimate underground rave, but in your mind, man. No noise, just the pulse of the spores and the rhythm of the earth.


Thorin laughs, “He’s so totally at a Wandering Veil concert.” 


I ask about the infection, and his voice changes. 


“She’s no infection. She’s the mama of the mushrooms, the queen of the dreamscape, and she’s got a gift — a ticket to ride through her cosmic garden. It’s not an infection, it’s a wild ride, a mind-expanding journey where you can see the world in a whole new light, feel the beat of the Underdark’s heart.


But hey, this ain’t no Sunday picnic. The Lady’s dream is deep, heavy, and real — like a psychedelic trip that changes you forever. You ready to drop in, tune out, and dance with the spores?


Come on, let’s take that trip together. Peace, love, and mushrooms, man. Will you groove with the Lady’s dream?” 


The creature’s hand is outstretched, and I shrug. I have seen the ecstatic drug-fueled madness of the cleric of demons, and have no interest in participating. 


But Thorin, who has a “fuck-it-all” attitude, takes the creature's hand. 


Grygum mutters, “This reminds me of that time. Well, I’ll be going around to make sure it isn’t a bad trip.” And he too is holding onto Voosbur’s hand. 


I step back. 


And then both Grygum and Thorin stop moving. 


Voosbur assures that all will be well. 


I am not sure. 


### Thorin


I open my eyes and realize I am in a different cavern, my heavy boots sinking slightly into the soft, mossy floor. I squint, taking in the scene. 


"Well, now. This air's thicker than a giant’s forearm, feels almost alive, humming softly like a forge that's lost its bellows. Mushrooms, taller than any giant I've ever seen standing straight, stretch right up to the cavern ceiling, their caps glowing in all sorts of fancy colors—violet, teal, amber. They're casting light all over the place, soft and shifting, making patterns on the ground."


I  try a step, my brows furrowing as the ground beneath my feet pulses faintly.


"The ground here feels... squishy, like it's breathing. Odd. And all these tiny spores drifting about, shimmering like motes of dust in a sunbeam. Looks pretty, I suppose."


I take a cautious sniff, then shake my head slightly. A familiar feeling of unease stirs within me.
"Smells earthy, a bit too sweet, with a musk that's starting to make my head swim. Just a little. Like that Tongue of Madness mushroom, but not as direct. All these glowing fungi, pulsing and fading, like the slow beat of some silent drum. The whole place is like… a Veil Concert. Beautiful, but there’s definitely something strange, something otherworldly, lurking beneath it all. This ain't natural, not by a long shot."


I take a deep breath, trying to clear my head. As I do so, I feel my face form a faint frown as the glade's silent song seems to tug at my thoughts, threatening to pull me deeper into its strange rhythm.


I mutter out loud, “Just a trip, Thorin, just a trip."


The experience is too much, and I start breathing shallow breaths. Is it fear, or caution, I don’t know, but I rush down the cavern. 


As I do so, I touch some mushrooms and they start to pulse, as if to warn me not to touch them again. 


I don’t. 


As we leave the cavern, I find myself in another, very different one. 


"Hmph. This looks like a giant, festering wound. There are thick, twisting vines and fungal tendrils, woven together like the pulsing veins of some colossal, subterranean beast. Not a sight for a dwarf with an empty stomach."


I take a deep breath, cough, and swat at the air.


"The air's heavier here, damp and warm, like standing too close to a fire giant’s hearth, but without the fire. And there's this faint, rhythmic thumping, like a slow, steady heartbeat echoing through the stone itself, as if the very walls are breathing. Unsettling."


"And these vines... they twitch sporadically, their surfaces slick with a glistening, translucent slime. Spores that glow cling to the tendrils, casting eerie shadows that dance and flicker with every subtle movement. This all makes it hard to tell what's solid and what's just a ghostly figment."


I take a careful step, and as cautious as it is, my boot still makes a faint squelching sound.


The ground beneath my feet is uneven, tangled with root-like growths that seem to reach out and try to snare a boot. And the smell! It's a blend of damp earth, rot, and something faintly metallic. Not the honest smell of rock and ore, that's for sure.


Every step in here feels like walking through a living maze, and these vines seem almost sentient, watching, waiting for a misstep—too much life in a tunnel for my liking. Give me solid stone any day over this… this thing. 

I turn to Grygum and urge caution and quiet. And for a time, it works, and we go through the vine forest. 


Some thirty feet from the exit of this place, Grygum is making too much noise. The vines start to move to close the path forward. If we don’t make it to the exit, we will be trapped in this nightmare. 


We dash, vines try to lash us and miss. We arrive at the edge of this cave and can see behind us the once clear path covered in vines that are moving, pulsing, and crunching. 


I step outside. 


And into another cave. 


Well, this looks like a blighted festering pit, unfit for any living creature, let alone a dwarf. There's a throne, but it's nothing but fungal growths twisted with bleached bones and decaying wood. 


My gaze sweeps across the looming shapes around me. 


"These giant mushrooms... they stand like sentinels, silent and still, but they ain't natural stone. Their caps are mottled with sickly patches of mold, and their stalks are twisted into grotesque shapes that defy any honest growth. Unnatural. Completely unnatural."


"The air itself feels heavy, thick with… something. And the colors here are muted—sickly yellows, dull browns, and shadowed grays. Like the very life has been sucked right out of the rock."


My eyes fix on the spectral figure at the center, a flicker of grim certainty in their depths. 


And there she is. The 'Dark Lady,' the Demon Queen of Fungi, the Lady of Rot and Decay. Shimmering into view like a fever-dream. They talk of beauty and decay, allure and menace, but I see naught but corruption and the promise of a slow, blighted end. She's a demonic power, that's what she is."


Her face is… unsettling. Delicate features, but framed by tendrils of glowing mycelium that pulse with a sickening inner light. Her eyes shine like twin lanterns, radiant yet hollow, drawing you in with a pull that feels more like a cold, hungry grasp on your mind.


I notice her crown, a halo of glowing spores drifting lazily, casting an otherworldly glow across that twisted fungal throne.


I think that these must be the same spores she uses to turn the living into mindless servants, into decomposing hosts.


I take a look at more closely. Her smile is slow and knowing, a curve that speaks of ancient secrets and fathomless power she shouldn't wield. When she moves, it's as if the very air bends around her, and the stench of damp earth and decay follows in her wake. Her voice, when it reaches my mind, is a haunting melody—at once soothing and commanding, like a lullaby sung by a hungry cave bear after it's caught its prey. It promises to 'bloom beyond the bounds of flesh and time,' but that bloom is a perversion, an infection that steals your very self."


This is it, then. The 'heart of the Lady’s dream,' a place where power and corruption are so tightly woven they're inseparable. Every breath here feels heavy with ancient secrets and dark promises of what she offers.


Just a trip, Thorin, just a trip. 


And then she speaks to me with a soft, melodic tone. 


“Welcome... wanderers of flesh and bone…” She pauses. And then continues with the same tone, *“*You stand at the edge... between waking and dreaming… Where life... and decay... entwine in endless dance…” And she pauses again.
