And I feel fear in my bones and she once again uses that haunting voice, * “*I am the pulse... beneath the stone… The breath... within the spore… To walk my dream... is to touch the heart… Of all that grows... and all that withers…”


She then looks at me with her eyes, “Do you fear the rot... or do you understand its song?”


I think about this for a moment. Grygum reminds me that every deal with a demon is a curse. It gives you power, and it robs you of your understanding of the need to avoid using power. 


The temptation is there, but I don’t know what will happen and it’s too dangerous. 


“Not this time? I have too many responsibilities on the outside.”  


She looks at me, disappointed -  We would bloom beyond the bounds of flesh and high. You could have lingered with me and found your heart entwined with me, forever. As part of the endless mycelium.” 


I can feel that mindless infinite eternity, and then just as much as I feel it, I am awake.


### Daz
Grygym and Thorin wake up. And they don’t appear to be covered in some kind of rotting mycelium, so that’s good. 


Voosbur sighs, “I guess you guys didn’t want to join us. You still can if you want. But hurry.” 


Spores fly out of him, they glow, and then the dancers walk towards the moss on the edge of the cavern and disappear. 


I hold onto Thorin and Grygum, worried that they will follow. But they don’t. 


# Chapter 24 The Wall 
### 


Daz
![image]()
Grygum and Thoring, after recovering their senses, to the extent that is possible for the dwarf, explained that they saw Zugtomy. And that she had made them an offer, an offer that Thorin refused. 


“Good,” I said. Deals with demons are rarely pleasant. 


With Rumpadump and Stool chatting, and the rest of our gang following us, we leave the Whorlestone caves and once again enter the slums of the Derro.


The Derro are particularly on edge. If I could express it, it would be a sense of pre-revolutionary violence. 


I think that we need to get out of here. 


Everyone agrees, so we head out quickly to the city of the Duergar, Gracklstugh. 


As we approach the gate, the Derro thin out until we find ourselves alone, some 50 feet from the entrance to the West Cleft District. When we came, this guardhouse was abandoned; now it’s not. 


Some thirty feet from the entrance, a Duergar guard materializes and asks, “Your business?” 


I notice behind him a poster that says, “The Ember Vanguard, wanted dead as long as we can raise them or aliave.” 


A spelling mistake and a grammar mistake, so typical of the Duergar. 


The picture of the Ember Vanguard, most certainly, doesn’t look like us. The drow wizard is an ancient Drow wizard. The golden dragonborne, Zalthir, is now red. As for Thorin, the likeness is flattering. And as for Grygum, they made him far more fierce than he really is.


I look past the guard and stare at the wall. The walls are covered in a faint sheen of dust. On the walls, I can hear the sound of armor clanking and see the shadows of visible Dueragar. 


This is no mere checkpoint. It’s a gauntlet where power, politics, and peril converge. One wrong step, and we will be trapped between a Duergar assault force, and the Derro looking to wage war on their oppressors. 


The guard scrutinizes me, and the rest of our group, and declares, smugly, “You are a Drow.” Turning to Thorin, then Grygum he says, “You are a dwarf and you are an orc!” 


Grygum turns to me and says, “He’s good at identifying species.” 


And finally, he stops in front of Zalthir, “And you are not red.” 


The Duergar sighs, “Then you must not be,” and points at the picture of the Ember Vanguard, “the Ember Vanguard.” 


“Who are these fearsome warriors, the Ember Vanguard?” asks Thorin.


The Duergar has already turned away and mutters, “Grogluk will wish to speak to you. Follow me.” 
### Zalthir


The Duergar of this city seem to live under the misconception that the color of a dragon’s scales has anything to do with its perspective and morality and choices. Although, to be fair, the only dragons they know are the red dragons of the Keepers of the Flame, and Themberchaude is not doing dragonkind any favors. 


I follow him into a passageway that is 10’ wide and 30’ long with 20’ side walls. At the far end of the passageway is a gate, and on the walls are more guards. I wonder how they could have assembled this so quickly, and remember that the Duergar are kin of the Dwarves, and magic can always help make the construction of walls go faster. 


Grygum whispers to me, “There are at least five more invisible guards we can’t see in this hallway.” 


I nod. Grogluk’s defiant and proud demeanor is an act. He’s not alone. He just pretends to be.  


Grogluk is about 4 feet tall; he has the typical ashen grey skin of the duergar. His face has scars and a few tattoos. His lips curl into a thin, unsettling smile, and around his neck is a crude pendant. 


It’s a familiar token of the Underdark, a clenched fist that expresses loyalty to the ruler. 


“This Duergar works for the Deepking.” 

The Duergar looks at him, “Yes, I do. And are you the Ember Vanguard or are you its prey?” 


Grygum looks confused and says, “I don’t know who these guys are, and given how fearsome they look, we would like to get back into town as quickly as possible.” 


Grogluk lip curls and asks the rest of the group, who all follow Grygum’s lead, acting very confused. 


Disgusted, he looks at us and shouts, “Turn back. No one shall enter the city of the Deepking.” 


I show him the passes of the Stone Guard. 


Grogluk stares at them, annoyed, “Passes can be forged. Show me proof that you are not the Ember Vanguard! It is well known that the Derro get details wrong. Perhaps the Dragonborne was gold?” Grogluk chuckles at the thought, a gold dragonborne causing so much havoc.


Daz whispers to me, “I have seen so many guards of despotic rulers living among the Drow, and they all want the same thing, a bribe.” 


Before I can react, Grogluk smiles, his curled lips forming a sneer with the scar on his face that stretches across his body, “If you are innocent, lay down your weapons and magic items for inspection or speak the secret message of the stone guard.” 
### Grygum


Remembering a simple salute is no challenge for a cleric of Bahamut. The seventeen steps of the night prayer to the Platinum God are more challenging than this simple ritual. 


But I also know that creatures like him are no different than the orcs in my tribe, whom you could terrorize with some names of their superiors. 


And I tell him of our mission from Errde. And I can see him sweat. 


Daz, always read for a plan B, readies a spell. I hope it’s a good one. 


I turn to Grogluk, stretch, and limber up, and then perform the ritual perfectly. 


“You are not the Ember Vanguard!” 


“Fuck those guys,” I add with emphasis. 


And then he asks for the bribe, “But I do have some guards, and it would be a shame if I could not spread some coin.” 


I size him up and give him 20 gold. He smiles and shouts to the others here that we are to pass through. 


It’s always interesting how the poorest part of a city is next to a wall, and on the other side is the wealthiest. We stand in Ladueger’s Furrow. Here’s where the richest and most powerful of the Duergar live. 


As we stand there, Jimjar asks, “I wager that Thorin will do something embarrassing. Anyone want to take the bet?” 


Thorin takes the bet and accidentally unbuckles his belt, and his pants fall. We all laugh. 


Jimjar smiles as if the goal wasn’t to win or lose the bet but something else, to change our mood. 

Our mood is better, so we decide to visit the giants.  


### Daz 


Gracklstugh is a city of furnaces, bellowing heat, a toxic fog, and haze that blocks out the light. Visibility is constrained as we move about. The comparison with the filth of Gracklstugh and the beauty of Menzoberanzan is jarring. 


The Drow would not reduce the suffering in this place, but at least it would have clean air. 


The atmosphere at the gate has put me on edge. The balance that kept the peace is tilting towards madness. 


As we sneak about, I notice another grey-skinned duergar, leaning against the wall, eyeing us with cold calculation.


If something is going to happen, I would rather have a hand in it happening, and so I walk up to him. 


He looks me over and tells us that the Stone Guard is on edge and about strangers in the city. “Any group with a Drow would probably want to be very careful. Everybody’s been on edge since the Ember Vanguard killed several members of the Derro High Council.” 


Thorin mutters, “We killed several members of the high council?”  


I glare at him, “You mean the Ember Vanguard? I do believe they did.” 


The Duergar sticks out his hand and demands a gold piece, and we pay him off. 


This is not good. The Derro we killed were not just madmen; they were part of the overall power structure of this city. And with them dead, the possibility of a civil war has suddenly increased.  


### Thorin


We end up at Hgraam’s cave and explain to him that there was a secret ritual that was transforming his giants into two-headed monsters. 


I reassured him that the ritual was the actions of mad men. That the Derro as a people had nothing to do with it. 


The stone giant sighs. And he offers us a small pile of coins. And then asks us to leave, declaring that the entrance to his cavern would be closed for a while. 


Knowing Stone Giants, it could be a very long time.


Before we leave, I ask him about a route to the surface world. He scratches his head and says, “I know of no such place. I do not know if such a place even exists. And I would not know what to do with a world that had no stone over my head.” 


As we leave Craingorm’s Cavern, Zalthir uses his sphere of darkness to hide the group. We figure that the haze and darkness will allow us to proceed unmolested. 


And it works out great. And we are soon at Gartokkar’s house. 


When I knock on his door, he looks surprised.  


“You have the egg?” 


Grygum steps forward and announces, “Yes, we have the egg and it is glorious!” 


Gartokkar's eyes light up, and I become worried about his expectations, “We’ll give you the egg as we found it, but we make no promises about the viability of the egg. We rescued it from a mysterious ritual.” 


The Duergar takes the egg and notices the strange occult markings. He is worried. 


Before I can reassure him further, he turns to Grygum and asks him as a cleric of Bahamut, “What do you think?”


Grygum finds the tiresome confusion among the masses that the evil of dragons is a function of scale pigmentation to be very annoying, but sometimes it can be handy. “I am a cleric of the Platinum Dragon. I know much about metallic dragons. But this is a chromatic dragon, and I know very little other than it will become evil.” 


Gartokkar is pleased. 


Which is good?


He smiles at me and says, “A deal and a non-disclosure agreement is a deal.” He leaves the main room and comes back with a bag full of coins. 


I nod my head and say, “I don’t know what kind of deal we made or who we made it with!” 


With our business transacted, I start to walk out, but Gartokkar suddenly stops me. “I heard the Deepking’s agents are everywhere, looking for a mercenary band so fierce that the Stone Guards are afraid to face them head-on. They are not mere adventurers, more like shadowy assassins from Menzoberanzan with powerful magic and blades that can rend souls.” He pauses and stares at me, “How did you manage to survive them?” 


“We appeared small and insignificant.” 


“Very wise. Be careful. The Derro are on edge, and the Stone Guard are on edge. Everyone is worried something is going to happen, and some want it.” 


Gartokkar is warning us. He is, which is odd. Which means he is afraid. But why would he warn us? Because he’s worried that if we do anything or say anything, we could cause this entire place to explode. 


As I walk out, I remember that we had a deal with Thermbechaude. And then I remember, Thermebechaude thought he had an agreement with us. We never had a deal with him. 


With this warning, we head out towards the Darklake. As we walk through an alley, trying to be inconspicuous, a group of Derro surrounds us. They announce that the Grey Ghosts will have their revenge for the murder of the High Council. 


I try to explain that we are not the Ember Vanguard. The Derro won’t listen. 


A few moments later, there are five dead Derro. 


As I pick through the coins in their pocket, I find a note. 


To all - 


The Deepking’s agents—the four shadows, The Ember Vanguard, who walk among us, wielding dark magic and unmatched skill—have brought death and dishonor to our kin. They are the ones who crushed our leader and stole what is rightfully ours: The Egg.


Your mission is clear:
**
Stalk them relentlessly.** Let the city itself become their cage.,
**Strike from the shadows.** Use invisibility, illusions, and sudden, whispered strikes.,
**Leave paranoia in their wake.**  Allow no escape, no peace.,
**Recover The Egg.** It belongs to the Gray Ghosts.,


This is not merely an order; it is a cold, cruel vendetta for our fallen leader. You carry death with you for these trespassers. They believe they can outrun shadows, but the dead do not rest, and neither do we.


Failure is not an option. Be swallowed by the shadows, or make them so. 
# Chapter 25 Leaving Gracklstugh, going to a wedding, and picking up a gift along the way, just in case. 
### Grygum


Here I am, Gyrgum, half-orc cleric of Bahamut, and Gracklestugh is what makes an orc camp look pretty. 


Any escape will require some "clever and insane scheme" to get through the barred gates of Laduguer's Furrow. 


And when you think about it, I seem to keep having to escape from some prison, whether it’s the prisons on the overbrite, or the prisons of the Drow, or the prisons of the Duergar. I have a gift for this. I suppose. 


The dead grey ghosts litter the street, and we start wondering how we will find a way into the Darklake District. We have passes, but Eldeth will demand to see what we found. And if we share with her what we found, that will trigger violence. 


Suddenly, a massive shadow falls over us. My eyes, accustomed to the gloom of the Underdark, pick out a dragon, a young red dragon, flying above. By Bahamut, he looks on the chubby side. It's Themberchaud, the Wyrmsmith of Gracklestug, and he's dive-bombing right for us! My first, most practical thought is that "we're not a match for a dragon". I quickly suggest we try to "talk to him" while positioned "Near something I can duck into". 


A parley is always better than a fight against impossible odds.


Themberchaud lands with a shuddering impact. The landing lacks any of the grace of a dragon. It looks like a bag of potatoes that landed and the bag barely broke. As he stands up, he resembles a farmer trying to steady the bag, stuffing the potatoes into position so it can stand properly. 


I look closer.


The typical taught and defined muscles of the dragon are nowhere to be seen. I wonder why, and it’s obvious, he is a predator who doesn’t hunt. And then I look at him more closely, and his scales are shiny. Someone has been carefully keeping them polished. And his claws are painted. They have none of the telltale signs of rending and destruction that they should have. He looks like a pampered toy, a pet, not the fearsome predator that he is. And he doesn’t realize how ridiculous he looks, fat and pampered and dolled up. 


The dragon’s voice booms and declares to us that we are his “agents, bound by my protection."


He raises his head, and I can’t help but notice the second chin.


 He then declares to all, "The keepers in the flame and their short-sightedness would have you waste precious time navigating checkpoints and patrols." And then he surprises me when he offers his "express service to where you must go next". 


I look at him, confused. And he shouts, playfully and authoritatively, "Climb aboard, unless you wish to question the will of your wormsmith". And I start to wonder. Themberchaud’s maturity has been adversely affected by the peculiar role he serves in Gracklstugh as a glorified lighter. I wonder why the Duergar chose a Red Dragon? Surely magic would be cheaper and less dangerous. 


But enough about that. 


The prospect of riding a dragon is too tempting. It feels "dangerous and stupid," but a dragon ride? So… I'll do\]. I even attempt to flatter him, addressing him as "Great Themberchaud".


We all clamber onto his voluminous back, easily finding space. Themberchaud takes off with a powerful beat of his wings, proudly declaring, "I need to show you my realm". He flies us through the cavern, proclaiming it "my town". It's clear that he "thinks he's in charge". Yet, I know the truth: he's merely a "glorified lighter" for the Duergar forges. My Bahamut-trained sensibilities are appalled at how they treat Themberchaud. To see such a powerful creature so manipulated is a travesty against dragonkind.


But this is not the time to reveal anything. 


### Daz


A young dragon would not have enough space for our gang, but this is a very large dragon. Not a very old dragon, a very large dragon. 


The creature groans as it flaps its wings, and then we are airborne. To fly on a dragon in the overbrite is one thing; to fly on a dragon in a cave in the underdark that is covered in thick clouds of the forges of the Duergar is quite another. 


The dragon shouts, “Where to?” 


Grygum looks at me. Thorin mutters, “We should just tell him everything. Nah.” 


I am relieved. I do not want to have a dragon destroy a city while I am on its back. 


After conferring, we agree that the right place to go is the docks. 


Themberchaude is unimpressed - and roars -  “My agents have more pressing matters than to loiter among the common rabble and petty traitors of the Dark Lake.”


Grygum tries to persuade him but fails. I begin to worry. 


Grygum asks the dragon, “Where do you think we should go, oh Great Themberchaud?” 


As I guessed, he has no idea what to do. He pouts, “Well, I have many agents, and they have many places to look. You're my most recent agents, and you've been out and about for a few days. Where do you think we should be looking for information?


I again insist that we should go to the Dark Lake District, and again, he seems unconvinced. It’s his ego. 


“Are you suggesting I am missing something important?” 


Grygum shouts, “You’re not one of the peons who understands the little things. But we are as little as you get, adn we can find the little things that are big for us.” 


Zalthir, having seen abbots like this dragon, who just want a face-saving gesture, shouts, “There was an attack on the docks, so there might be new intelligence. Your agents didn’t miss it; they just haven’t been there recently.” 


The dragon agrees and tries to make a turn. But he’s fast, and his belly rolls instead of gliding, and then I am falling. 


Not for long, that’s what Misty Step is for. 


And as I look down, I notice Grygum and Thorin falling. Zalthir has sprouted wings. He catches Thorin. 


The ghoul Jimjar shouts, “Anyone want to make a bet that Grygum is going to survive?” 


Grygum seems to shout, “I’ll take the bet.” 


And it would have been a good one for him to take. Jimjar throws a rope and catches the falling orc. And then the group pulls him onto the dragon, which is frantically trying to catch his agent. 


### Thorin 


The flight on the back of a dragon is fun. But I agree with Zalthir that we really should have tied ourselves up rather than just sit on Themberchaud’s back. 


Just then, the Dragon shouts, “Oh, wait, there’s a forge that needs some fire!” 


I'm not sure if we should do this, but Themberchaud looks excited. And he approaches the forge and shouts, “I am Themberchaud the Wyrmsmith, bringer of flame!” 


And he breathes fire. 


Daz turns to me, “The Duergar are rolling their eyes. They don’t take him as seriously as he takes himself.”


I nod. 


And then Zalthir sounds a little bit more worried, “They recognized us. Look at their panic. They weren’t afraid of Themberchaud but when they saw Daz, they suddenly freaked out. They think we are the Ember Vanguard.” 


“So what do we do?” 


“I don’t know. But I can see many of the Duergar rushing around as if they are trying to send warnings.” 


I look down. It is as Zalthir said. The Duergar were unafraid of Themberchaud, but now they are pointing in our direction and moving frantically. 


“What do we do?”


Zalthir looks at me, “They think we are this all-powerful group; we take advantage of it.” 


Themberchaud has not heard a word we said and shouts, “Alright, one more flyby and to the docks!” 


### Zalthir


As we land on the docks, everyone flees except one lonely Duergar Stone Guard who stands in front of us. 


Gartokkar has warned us that everyone is on edge. The Stone Guard is looking for the Ember Vanguard, the powerful mercenary group, and the Grey Ghosts are looking for the Ember Vanguard, and the Deep King is worried. And now that we have come off of Themberchaud, this poor guard must think we are the Ember Vanguard. 


He clears his throat and tries to hide the quaver, “Halt in the name of the Deep King!” 


That’s a surprise. The guard didn’t think we are the Ember Vanguard. Maybe we can get out of here without bloodshed.  


Before I can react, Grygum says that they come in Thembersham’s name. 


The guard still refuses to let us pass. 


“Shall I recall him?” asks the cleric. 


I stand next to Grygum to make myself look as scary as possible. And we fail. The guard is unimpressed, but then he looks at a poster of the Ember Vanguard, and whispers, “I know you, you are the Ember Vanguard! I must warn Captain Errde at once!” 


We have to kill him. As I explain, “In the interest of avoiding mass bloodshed, I think we must.” 


Thorin mutters an old giant saying, “To save the village, you must smash the village.” 


Grygum walks up to the guard and whispers that we are impersonators trying to flush out the Ember Vanguard. “We are not them, but we are on a vital mission.” 


Thorin turns to Grygum, “Deputize them!” 


Grygum nods and pulls out a caltrop, “This is a symbol of our mission. Guard it and keep it secret.” 


The Duergar takes the caltrop and then runs off. 


The cleric has bought us some time. 


We jump into a large boat and head out. As we head out we ponder what we have accomplished. We came to find equipment, and we did that. And as Daz said, we betrayed many people. 


But the other truth is that we didn’t betray the city of Gracklstugh. The secrets we carried - of the Deep King’s plots, the corrupted dragon egg, and the lurking demonic plots - could have provoked mass death and destruction. And we took those secrets with us. The people of Gracklstugh owe us, even if they are unaware of it. 


I find it comforting to know that. 


As we leave Grackstugh, we debate where to go next. 


Rump-a-dump and Stool want to go to the Neverlight Grove. I explain that there is a very dangerous and mighty demon there, and that we might not want to go there at all. 


Rump-a-dump looks at me, or at least I think he does, “Zalthir, the circle cannot be corrupted. “Our sovereign would never let that happen.” 


I want to explain to him how wrong he is, but then I remember he is a child. 


Serith insists that we must go there as well. The strange compulsion that drew him to the dancing Myconids in the Whorelstone Caverns draws him to the grove. 


Thorin, having avoided one gift from a demon, seems to want to go again. I shake my head, “You had your chance, don’t you think we shouldn’t try again?”


But then it struck me that Thorin will roll the dice and make strange decisions. And I grit my fangs and mutter, “Perhaps we could first go to the Lost Tomb of Khaem, secure whatever weapon it has, and then go?” 


They all nod. 


Just as we are about to set sail, Jimjar says something bizarre - "I'll bet you an empty shell gem that this circle of joy will reveal itself to be a circle of unwilling vows before you leave it.”


Great, a wedding involving demons and mushrooms. 


I hope no one will take him up on his weird bet, but Grygum does. 


## 4th-6th day of the 2nd tenday of Myrtul 1493


### Thorin 


The first two days are uneventful. There is the usual tedium of the rowing and the darkness and the strange sounds and cries. 


The third day brings excitement when some bloodsucking giant mosquitoes fall from the roof. 


They are killed very quickly. 


I like giants, but not giant mosquitoes.


## 7th day of the 2nd tenday of Myrtul 1493


On the fourth day, Serith announces that we must get out on a beach and head deeper into the Underdark on foot. 


He explains, “The path to the Neverlight Grove goes past the Lost Tomb of Khaem. But we must leave the boat here.” 


Errde will have probably told the Drow that we came through her city, and they will once again be pursuing us. 


Leaving the boat is like leaving a sign. But we might need it later. 


Gyrgum shouts, “We could scuttle it.” 


I stare at him, perplexed. 


“I can cast mending.” 


Eldeth looks at him, “Really?” 


I look at her, confused. 


“Well, spell casters who could cast mending were in high demand by the navies. And so spellcasters tended to avoid learning that spell. See, in naval combat, the first person you kill is the mender. Because until you kill him, you can’t sink the ship. So finding a spell caster who can cast it is rare.” 
# Chapter 26 Journey to and into the Lost Tomb of Khaem. 
## 7th day of 1st tenday of Myrkhul, 1495 
### Grygum 


The boat is sunk. My mending skills are in high demand. And if I want to not end up on a ship, it's best to keep it secret from myself. 


## 9th day of 1st tenday of Myrkhul, 1495
### Daz


At first, I thought this adventure was about escape. About finding a way home. But now that we have been wandering through the world, I realize it’s an opportunity to learn and explore. 


My whole life, I was a Drow of Menzoberanzaan. Trapped in the formalities of ritual and expectations, trying to avoid the predations of the Cult of Lolth and the machinations of the Noble Houses. 


I never saw the Underdark for what it is, a place to explore and learn. And now I know this journey not as an escape to another place, but instead as an escape from a previous worldview. My journey is about discovery, appreciating the diversity of ecosystems, life forms, and civilizations, and learning. 


For two days, Eldeth has been hiding our tracks for two days, where all we could see when we could see was the dark passages. Serith insisted he knew where we were going. I was hoping to see new things. 


We turned down yet another passageway, and the air grew thick with a familiar, subtle hum, the Faerzess. 


Ahead, there was no longer the rough-hewn stone, but an area suffused with the arcane glowing magic of the Faerzess. Fist-sized chunks of quartz crystals erupted from the wall, shedding a dim ten-foot radiance. 


Before, this would have been yet another obstacle, another exotic backdrop to our desperate flight to safety, but now I wanted to experience and explore. 


“Let’s collect some of these crystals and look around.” 


In a corner were two desperate humans. I stare at them and quickly surmise they are escapees from the Drow. 


“Who are you? And back off!” shouts a male human. He holds a crystal as a weapon. It’s too pathetic. 


They insist they are escapees of the Drow; I concur, but Zalthir, who is curiously unobservant, scoughs.


The male, dressed in rags and starving, explains that his name is Fuurm Coppernose, or Copper to his friends, who had lost his sister and went looking for her in the Underdark. 


I look at him and wonder if he has any skills as a rogue, a fighter, a wizard, or a cleric, but he explains that he is just a farmer. 


I am astonished that he is alive and question how he escaped. 


Baedora, the woman who is dressed in rags as well, and is equally starving, explains, “That it was demons that attacked. The Drow fought back. We ran. Figured we were more likely to stay alive away from Drow and Demons.” 


We have collected so many strays that one more won’t harm us. 


And so I invite them to join our group. 


Before we leave the cave, we take as many crystals as we can. To hide our tracks, we smash the cavern and the crystals, as if some monster had attacked, not escaped slaves who took crystals that shone in the darkness. 
## 2nd day of the 2nd tenday of Myrkhul, 1495


### Grygum 


Three more days in the dark. Was it three more days? I think it was. And finally, the winding passageway opened, and the air grew heavy with the subtle, earthy scent of the damp loam and something indescribably sweeter. 


There were the towering stalks and caps of fungi, a veritable forest of the subterranean. Mushrooms of all kinds and of all types, stretching up into the unseen ceiling, some glowing faintly with a soft, bioluminescent light, others a muted, earthy brown. We were making good progress, moving at a steady pace since Eldeth had done well to hide our tracks in the faerzress crystal cave we'd just left. Stool, my new myconid friend, was curled up contentedly against Thorin's back, probably still reliving his 'good idea' to ride on the dwarf. It was, for a moment, almost peaceful.


Then, it hit. A sudden, piercing shriek that ripped through the heavy air and vibrated through the very rock beneath my feet. Not one, but many. Shriekers. The kind of noise that sends a jolt of adrenaline through any sane creature, screaming "danger!" and "dinner is served!" to anything else that might be lurking in the tunnels. My first instinct, honed by years of getting into and out of trouble, was to find cover or to run further into the fungal maze.


But then a thought sparked, a mischievous, practical thought. We had just gathered a small collection of those glowing quartz crystals from the previous chamber. I half-expected a surge of spores, some defensive blast, or perhaps even a confusion spell, something bizarre and dangerous to grapple with. For a moment, I even thought, "I was gonna have to survive throwing a crystal at the shrieker".


But no. The crystal sailed through the air, a small, glowing arc, and clattered against a broad fungal cap. And the shrieking... didn't change. It was a bit of an anticlimax, really. Just shrieking. No grand magical effect, no sudden silence. Just continuous, irritating noise. Still, at least it meant the fungi weren't actively harmful themselves, just loud alarms for bigger, hungrier things. 


## 3rd day of the 2nd tenday of Myrkhul 
### Grygum 


Another cave full of crystals. And we collect more. Eldeth is worried; she’s reasonably convinced we have thrown the Drow off our tracks, but every time we mess with the environment, we make it easier for them. 


I tell her not to worry. 


Jimjar shouts, “Want to make a bet?” 


And so I turn to him, “Wanna bet that these crystals will be useful?” 


He looks at me, confused. He’s not used to other people making the bet. 


But he smiles and says, “Yes, I do.” 


## 5th day of the 2nd tenday of Myrkhul 
### Zalthir


My dragonborn scales feel rough against my skin, constantly reminded of the grime and the chill that permeates everything. We've evaded the Drow, thanks to Eldeth's shrewdness, reducing their pursuit to a mere whisper behind us. Fuurm and Baedora chat nervously, their bellies full and their spirits somewhat lifted. Jimjar, of course, has already started a new round of bets, probably on how many steps Thorin takes before tripping. My vow of silence, of speaking only when there's truly something to say, feels easier with each passing mile.


Then, it happens. A soft, feminine voice, distant yet clear, rings out in my mind, "Hello? Is someone there? Oh, please, I need your help! I have been trapped in the dark for so long... so very long. Please, won't you help me? Won't your help to free me?"


My senses immediately sharpen. This isn't the first time strange voices have echoed in these depths, but this one carries a distinct plea. It’s also unnervingly direct, pinpointing the direction of a tomb entrance. I glance at the others, confirming they've heard it too. "Is that the direction we were going anyway?" I ask, my voice a low rumble, ever the pragmatist, seeking confirmation that this isn't some new diversion. 


Serith nods yes, this is the way. Of course, it does. Nothing in the Underdark is ever truly straightforward, yet here, a trapped voice leads us exactly where we intended to go, The Lost Tomb of Khaem.


We arrive at a large double door. The stone is ancient, hinting at a lost era, a common theme in this alien landscape. Inside, a chill descends, and my eyes adjust to a faded grandeur. A stone diorama stands to the right, depicting a Netherese noble, Brysis of Khaem, surrounded by her retinue, flaunting wealth and power. To the left, a sprawling mural covers the wall, illustrating fantastic floating cities.


I know the lore of the Netheril Empire – a civilization of immensely powerful magic users, whose cities defied gravity, only to fall catastrophically when one of their leaders tried to seize all magical power, tearing the very fabric of reality. It's a stark reminder of unchecked ambition, a cautionary tale against hubris. My monastic training emphasizes balance and inner peace, not the dangerous pursuit of absolute external power. It makes me wonder what kind of sorceress Brysis was to be buried here. 


We descend a dusty staircase. Grygum, with his keen perception, takes the lead, carefully testing each step. On one landing, I note a Netherese Calendar Stone, a relic of a time long gone, its purpose unclear. The stairs finally give way to a shrine, its floor littered with shreds of dusty tapestries.


I focus, drawing on my monk's discipline, seeking patterns, anomalies in the dust, and then I speak, "Proof here of a lower power." 


What an absurd conclusion that immediately grates on my own rational mind. How dangerous to be so easily misled by my own mind, in a place where observation is key to survival.


Grygum, thankfully, is more successful. He notes recent damage but no tracks in the thick layer of dust. He then recalls old tales of “floating undead creatures that typically rest in tombs”.


Yes, I agree, a "lost tomb" implies something more than just undisturbed dust and cobwebs. It implies guardians, dangers, and perhaps, the very undead Grygum speaks of. I remember Fargus Rumblefoot's warning about a "secret room" or "false tomb" here, adding another layer of treachery to this place. Daz checks an altar, finding nothing of arcane significance, another dead end for now.


There is a passageway south and one going east, so we proceed East. The room we enter contains four stone sarcophagi. Markings of robed human figures in repose adorn their lids. We inspect them, looking for traps, for anything unusual. And then, Grygum points it out: the northeast sarcophagus rests on hidden stone rollers. A possible secret, a hidden passage. This is it.


I move into position, my hands forming the familiar gestures. I call forth the shadows, plunging the area around the sarcophagus into a sphere of magical darkness. Daz won't be able to cast Magic Missile within it, but that's a calculated risk. Thorin, strong as an ox, leverages the darkness, pushing the heavy sarcophagus aside. The stone grinds, revealing... a hole. The true tomb, perhaps. We are finally here. My instincts prickle.


A chill emanates from everywhere at once. Rime creeps across surfaces, and my breath plumes before me in the suddenly frigid air. A moan, pained and distant, rises with the wind, and I see a figure detach itself from the shadows and glide toward me—weightless, formless, undead.


Daz


The sarcophagi stand, silent and imposing, lining the room like morbid sentinels. Zalthir, ever the master of shadow, had just blanketed the area in his magical darkness. I appreciate the tactical advantage it offers, though it always makes me momentarily blind until my own Drow eyes adjust to its particular brand of void. Thorin grunts, a familiar sound of effort, as he shoves the heavy northeast sarcophagus lid aside.


A gasp from someone, then a sudden, chilling presence. From the newly opened space, a form coalesces from the gloom – translucent, malevolent, undeniably undead. A Spectre. My instincts, sharpened by a lifetime of navigating the treacherous currents of the Underdark and the fleeting horrors of Velkynvelve, scream danger. Then, another, and another. My mind quickly registers the threat: four Spectres now hover, incorporeal and menacing. "No, you must save me!" a soft, feminine voice cries out in my mind. It's the same voice from when we entered the tomb, trapped, pleading. It adds another layer of urgency, a distraction from the immediate threat before us. These are Brysis's retainers, then, still bound to her ancient tomb.
It's my turn. I assess the swirling forms, their spectral claws already reaching. With a familiar incantation, I conjure the shimmering darts of pure force. Magic Missile. Two bolts streak through the darkness, finding their mark on one Spectre. Another bolt follows, striking a second Spectre. Each hit is satisfying, a clean impact on an ethereal foe. They might be immune to a host of things, but raw magical force isn't one of them.


Then, their icy touch. One Spectre lunges at me, its chilling form passing through my defenses. A jolt of cold, raw energy courses through me, necrotic damage, and I feel my very life force diminish. Before I can fully process it, another Spectre attacks, a more potent drain this time, twice as much necrotic damage, and my strength wanes further. My body screams for respite. "I'm gonna need a long rest here pretty soon," I mutter, the words barely audible, a desperate plea for recovery. This is not the clean, surgical combat I prefer. This is a battle of attrition, and my life force is the price I pay.


Grygum, in his devotion, tries to turn them, his holy symbol raised, but the Spectres resist, their wills too strong, or perhaps their existence too ancient to be swayed. Zalthir, ever the whirlwind, moves his sphere of darkness, then his fists become blurs in the gloom, punching and pummeling. He kills one, then another. "I will punch the ghost!" he declares. I can almost hear Pelek, our ghost, correcting him. 


With the last Spectre vanquished by Zalthir's relentless strikes, a momentary quiet descends, broken only by our heavy breathing. My mind is already racing, calculating. "Is this, would this be a good time for us to take a… Long rest. By chance?" I inquire, hopefully.


My mind races through tomes I studied, drawing on my arcane knowledge, and I remember that many such creatures will return after being destroyed when the central evil force that created them remains.  


If we rest, we will find them here when we come back. 


And although they may just stay here, they may also pursue us. 


Before we go down the dark passageway, we open the sarcophagi. Each sarcophagus contains mummified remains, the tattered remnants of ancient burial garments, and treasure of Netherese origin.  


They are worth a great deal as gold, and perhaps even more to the right collector. 


### Grygum


We descend, Thorin taking the lead, his broad shoulders easily pushing through the confined space. The air grows heavier, thick with an ancient stillness. We enter a new chamber, and the faint light catches murals on the walls, depicting grand scenes, probably of the Netherese sorceress Brysis of Khaem and her lost cities. A gilded sarcophagus gleams against one wall, clearly the focal point, and I notice the subtle shimmer of an invisible stone chest near its foot. Predictable. An actual tomb wouldn't be without its grand pronouncements and its hidden treasures.


Then, a cold, empty feeling washes over me, a familiar touch of undeath. From the sarcophagus, a figure rises, ethereal and malicious. A Wraith. Its voice, resonant with ancient menace, fills our minds, not with the pleas of the previous Spectres, but with a chilling declaration: "Your deaths will free me from this prison, and how my victims will serve me even in death!”


I remember that a wraith, when it kills, turns its victims into specters, and I shudder. 


Daz contemplates a Fireball, but then remembers that they are resistant to fire. “Magic missiles it is,” and the bolts of power are precise and undeniable, but the spectral form endures.


The wraith glides forward, a silent, menacing presence, and attacks Thorin. But the dwarf's armor and the grace of Bahamut protect him; the attack misses. Then, in a move I find utterly infuriating, the Wraith hovers back into its sarcophagus. "Coward," I think, a dry amusement stirring within me. Retreating into a stone box is hardly a display of power.


Zalthir moves. Ever the tactician, he casts his magical darkness, spreading it to cover the entire room. The already dim tomb plunges into an even deeper, magical gloom. I hear him move, and then move the sarcophagus. Just as the lid creaks aside, the soft, feminine voice from earlier, the one that first called to us, speaks again, "In the sarcophagus! I can help you!" 


So, the trapped entity, the true owner of the voice, is inside this sarcophagus.


Is it the Wraith or is it something else? 


Zalthir looks in. 


# Chapter 27 The light of the Dawnbringer, and the Two in a Box 


## 5th day of the second tenday of Myrkhul 1495
### Zalthir


As I stare into the sarcophagus, I see what has been speaking to them - “It’s a talking sword. More like a talking sword hilt.” 


The sword hilt sits on top of the mummified corpse, held tight by its withered hands. 


“Please, help me.” 


Grygum shouts, “Not a talking sword.” 


I groan. 
The sword hears that and exclaims, “I can help you! Please don’t let me go.” 
Then it must have figured out that I am a monk, and it can’t help me. 
"You're a monk! Get the fighter over here!”

Grygum mutters, “A talking mace would have been nice.” 


I nod and think, “A silent glove would have been better.” 
But enough of that, time to attack. And I focus my mind and strike the wraith with my hands. The creature is in shock. 


And then I hear the belching sound that Grygyum makes just before acid spews from his mouth, I move out of the way, and watch as the Wraith is covered in the slime.  
Thorin, whose choices are always interesting, decides to drop his sword and pick up the magical hilt. The sword rejoices, and then, where there is no blade, a shimmering blade of light appears. 


The wraith, whom I assume is Brysis, screams, “Not Dawnbringer!” 
The sound of scorching heat penetrates my sphere of darkness; it’s the spells of Daz who strikes the undead monster. The creature howls in pain and screams, “I have been waiting for millennia to be free, and I won’t be denied now!” 


Daz takes no chances and climbs out of the room into the passageway that we took from the room full of sarcophagi. 


And then the creature howls in pain and disappears. 


Killed by barf. What an odd way to go. 
### Daz 


The sword introduces itself as Dawnbringer. A powerful sunblade that can read and write, and can cast lesser restoration. 


Grygyum is surprised it can read and write. The orc is confused that the creature can read without eyes. 


I roll my eyes. He has never seen the eldritch horrors that exist here in the realms.

As we look around for treasure, we stumble on an invisible chest. Using fairy fire, I outline the box, and Zalthir opens it. 


Inside, we find even more treasure: a necklace of fireballs, a potion of greater healing, and some gold. 


Once we have collected the treasure of Brysis, we climb out of the real tomb and finish our exploration in the room we skipped.


And a good thing indeed, for this was the false tomb, complete with a sarcophagus that was very easy to open. This was the place that Fargas Rumblefoot warned us of. 


I sense some kind of magical trap that was tied to this place. And now that Brysis is dead, this trap is gone as well. 
## 8th day of the second tenday of Myrkhul 1495
### Daz


The last three days were uneventful as we trudged through the underdark. Our band had grown larger with the addition of the two new members and Dawnbringer. 


After millennia, the sword refused to extinguish its light. And Thorin, who is too compassionate, would keep it lit, even at night, when many of us wanted to sleep. 


As for our pursuers, Eldeth told us this morning that she believed we had lost them. They were no longer on our trail. 


Grygm chortled, “I guess they didn't like the tomb.” 


Today,d we arrive at Neverlight Grove. 


As we enter the cave, the beauty overwhelms Grygum, who shouts, “Wow, this place is incredible.” 
### Grygum
![image]()
Wow, this place is incredible. My jaw hangs open, and I feel a shiver of awe run through me. We've been tramping through the Underdark for what feels like an eternity, and every twist and turn has brought more of the same—darkness, danger, and the constant, nagging feeling that something is about to jump out at us.
But this is different. It's a vast cavern, but instead of being a dark, oppressive void, it's a living, breathing landscape of impossible color. The cave walls shimmer with a soft, bioluminescent light, casting a gentle glow on everything. The light is a beautiful mosaic of blues, greens, and purples, like a nebula trapped underground. Myconids, the mushroom folk we're traveling with, are everywhere, and they seem to be a part of this vibrant world, glowing with the same otherworldly light.
For a moment, all the dangers and all the worries just vanish. I forget about the Drow pursuers we just shook, the grumpy talking sword that's been driving Daz crazy, and the mysterious disease affecting the Myconids. It's not a scary, alien place; it's a work of art, and I am standing right in the middle of it. This isn't just a cave; it's a cathedral of light and life. It reminds me that even in the deepest, darkest places of the world, there can be something truly beautiful and amazing waiting to be found.
Daz turns to me, “It’s a good thing I left my mushroom recipe book at home.” 


I laugh. 


We have just entered this magical place from a natural tunnel that was formed by a drying underground stream, and that is dimly lit by lichen. 


The access tunnel opens above the grove’s main floor. It gives us a panoramic view of the mushroom forest that covers every surface, including the ceiling, and illuminates the darkness with brilliantly colourful patterns made from the living light of the fungi. 


Beyond the exotic forest, the cavern narrows into a ravine. And beyond the ravine, I catch a glimpse of a majestic mushroom, but it’s too far away for me to see any details. I look at Daz, who shrugs. 


And then I hear Rump-a-dump's delight and Stool’s happiness as they run into the cavern shouting, “We’re home!” 


Sarith, our drow guide, looks unhappy and serene but follows the myconid’s. Jimjar smiles at me and says, “Remember my bet,” as he races after the two myconids and Sarith. 


Zalthir, who finds the idea of mushrooms that turn you into zombies very creepy, covers himself in his orb of darkness and hangs back. 


Thorin and his sword race down with the rest. And the rest of our followers, Eldeth, the goblin, and the humans follow him. 


I shrug and follow. 


We go through a large fungal forest and descend into a central basin. Beyond the mud and mushrooms of the fungal forest, a large, clear pool sits in the midst of the fungal grove. A central mound is the only dry spot in sight, though a small cliff rises above the cavern floor far across the clearing with giant mushrooms visible in the distance. 


On the ceiling, I notice how the living light of the fungi trace strange constellations along the cavern’s ceilings and walls, showing the darkness of the ravine and mist-shrouded smaller cavern beyond. 


I see Rump-a-dump and Stool chatting with two very large mycondis. One of them spreads spores that allow us to talk. 


The creature introduces itself as Phylo and is genuinely happy to see us. 


Stool interrupts the creature to explain how Thorin carried him when he was tired, and that Zalthir was always grouchy but a really nice softer, and saved Rump-a-dump. 


Phylo waves his hand, and the two sprouts are silenced, “You are safe, friendly softers! You arrive at a wondrous time, for Neverlight Grove is on the verge of something great, something marvelous! Celebrate as the day of joy is nigh!”


I thank him. They smile, or at least that is what I feel they do. And then they say, “You should visit and explore our cave and see the wonders of the Neverlight Grove. But please, don’t visit the eastern plateau because the Circle of the Masters is preparing a wondrous and glorious surprise in the Garden of Welcome. Tomorrow, I can give you a peek, if you want.” 


I try to ask any questions but Phylo says we should direct our questions to the Great Seeder. I don’t recognize this god. Phylo says, “She lives beyond the Garden. She is a wonderful entity who will help all of us get closer to her beauty!” He keeps talking about this creature. 


Daz turns to me, “How odd. Myconids have no gender, and in general get confused about the topic. The sovereign’s use of a specific gender and consistent use of one particular gender is quite peculiar.” 


And then I remember that Zugtomy is often referred to as she. And I worry. 


### Daz


The other sovereign looks uncomfortable, as if it feels that there is something off. 


And I think there must be a way to stop whatever madness has taken over Phylo. If only we could talk to the other Sovereign. 


We owe Stool that much. 


The other sovereign introduces itself as Basidia and says to Phylo, “I can take them on the tour of the gardens, co-sovereign.” 


I stare at them, dumbfounded. In Menzoberanzan, there were tales of two rulers who shared power. We used the term, ‘two in a box’ to describe this power sharing. It wasn’t power sharing; it demonstrated a lack of will on the part of someone. Some other ruler could not choose who to kill and who to promote. So they would make the two drow co-rulers. And before long, one or both would be dead. The box from our saying was a metaphor for a tomb. 


My thoughts are interrupted by Phylo, who says, “ You are my sovereign and co-equal in all things. And I shall stay here for tomorrow, I shall take them to the great circle of the Masters.” 


And so we leave, 


As we enter the forest, Basidia turns to us and says, “The grove is not safe. Another group of 'softers' arrived not too many cycles ago and accepted Phylo’s offer. They were taken to the Garden of Welcome. I haven’t seen them since, nor has Phylo made any further mention of them.” Basidia then whispers, even though we can only hear her in our heads, “the Circle of Masters is taking most of the carcasses the Circle of Hunters bring in, and are sending groups of myconids outside the grove without telling anybody.”


Grygum, nervously, asks, “Are we seeing the Garden of Welcome today?” 


Basidia laughs, “No. Today we shall the circles.” 


A few minutes later, Basidia turns to us, “I do not recognize the spores of this drow.” I stare at them, confused, “Every myconid sovereign can recognize the spores of any other sovereign in the Underdark. This is strange.”  


Poor Sarith has been affected by Zugtomy. 


### Zalthir


Has Basidia just seen the demonic spores that have infected poor Sarith? Are they different from the ones that infect the Circle of Masters? And what is the Circle of Masters. 


As we walk towards wherever Basidia is taking us she tells about her worries, “I fear Phylo has contracted some kind of diseased spore. We used to work so well together.” 


“Is it the same spore that infects Sarith?” 


“I cannot tell. Perhaps there is a clue in the Garden of Welcome?” 


“The same garden you told us not to go to?” 


“I know it’s dangerous, and I will give you this and more if you find out what’s going on.” 


They hands us a moldy scroll case, and inside is a scroll containing a scroll of protection against fiends. 


Convenient. 


They sense my hesitation, “I would go, but I worry I would succumb to the same disease that has affected Phylo. I will give more treasures we have collected if you bring back my sovereign.” 


Daz mutters, “I have seen this before. There is no mystery what this diseased spore is, its power.” 


Basidia turns to us, “I can also brew many potions of various potency.” 


We might save Phylo by destroying the demon, and then Phylo will explode, and then Basidia will be upset. 


They hear my thoughts and say, “Oh no. Phylo would enter the great circle and all would be well.” 


And then Basidia explains what has worried them. Apparently, Phylo has changed the social order of the community. There are many circles in the Neverlight Grove, and each circle serves a function. Each circle gathers around a circle mound, which they describe as a pile of rocks and soil upon which mold, lichen, and mushrooms grow. Each circle gathers around its mound to sleep. 


Basidia then expresses in horror, “Phylo decided that each circle would meld exclusively with its circle, and only the circle leaders would meld with other circle leaders and the sovereigns. Phylo said that everything would be more efficient and better. Many of the myconids have followed Phylo and his new ways.” 


They stop, and if they could scream, they scream, “I believe this is contrary to the unity and harmony of our way of life. This separation isolates individuals from experiences from others outside of their circle. And then there is the Inner Circle and the Circle of Masters.” 


I look at her, and she explains, “The Inner Circle of all of the circle leaders and the Circle of Masters is a circle of those who are closest to Phylo.” 


I worry that we might be attacked unintentionally. “Can you give us some kind of spore, so other myconids will know we work for you?” 


Basidia laughs, “Don’t worry, they all know.”  


And soon enough,we arrive at one of the mounds. And there is a myconid who seems happy enough to see us. 


Basidia tells us that this is one of her followers, “Loobamub. “ 


Loobamub listens to Basidi, and then he turns to me and asks if we could help him deal with a grick. As he explains, Phylo insists that all dead creatures must be brought to the Circle of Masters. 


“To eat?” 


He laughs, “No to reanimate. If you could bring this creature to Basidia, she could reanimate it, and it could help you.”  


And then it hits me, “Why are you sending us to hunt? Aren’t you hunters?” 


The walking mushroom looks at me and says, “We bring back the dead. We do not kill.” 


I think to myself of the reanimated creatures I saw in the Whorelstone Caves and shudder. “Well I suppose it couldn’t hurt.” 


Grygum looks uncomfortable, I turn to him and say - “What, you don't want a zombie grick joining our team? That sounds so fun.” 


A deadly game of K’tharr-li
### Daz


Basidia has offered to animate a Girk if we can find it. 


The Myconid, Loobamub, the leader of the Circle of Hunters, tells us as we leave that a Shambling Mound is concealed nearby, lurking like mossy camouflage within the swampy ground. 


Engaging the immediate target while allowing an invisible, grappling threat to remain poised to strike is a lapse in security that any house in Menzoberranzan would never permit.


We could proceed with the blunt approach favored by overbrighters and Duergar alike—charging in and hoping luck prevails—but I will not. 


I tell The Ember Vanguard that I have a plan to neutralize the creature’s ability to hide. I explain that I visualize the terrain as a precise grid, and intend to freeze five-foot cube sections of the moss and water using Shape Water. “If a square refuses to freeze, we have found the creature.” 


They look at me funny, and I explain that when I was a child, there was a game we played called K’tharr-li. Each player would be a noble house. And each player had a set of pieces that the other player had to destroy. As this was Menzoberanzan, if neither player had won by some pre-agreed time, both players lost. 


Much like K’tharr-li, we only have so much time. And unlike K’tharr-li, losing can be deadly. 


### Grygum
Daz is using the kinds of tactics the Drow are famous for.  He is casting Shape Water, trying to freeze sections of the water and moss in a checkerboard pattern, playing a game he calls K’tharr-li to locate the monster. 


And he succeeds. The Grik hisses. 


Zalthri immediately covers the Grick in magical Darkness. Brilliant. 


Daz incinerates the area with a Fireball. The Grik is naturally resistant to fire, but the blast hurts. 
Next is Thorin, who rushes into the magical blackness, wielding Dawnbringer. He lands two heavy strikes, leveraging the advantage Zalthir afforded us. 


Finally, my turn. I cannot use Guiding Bolt because Zalthir's spell hides the creature. So, I resort to my secondary option: Tasha's Caustic Brew. It’s essentially projectile acid, hardly glamorous work for a cleric of Bahamut, but necessary to fulfill the mission.
But is it?


Bahamut’s blessed creatures, the Brass Dragon, breathe acid. And the black dragon, which he teaches us is also a holy creature, breathes acid. So am I not, in a curious way, honoring my god in this way?


As I prepare to spew the caustic solution in the general direction of the creature, I note to Zalthir, "One of the material components is a toothbrush, you know, for afterward.” You must keep your humor, even when covered in your own corrosive vomit.


I cast the spell, attempting to burn the creature, but alas, it dodges. 


The blinded Grick misses all three of its subsequent attacks against the Ember Vanguard. It then decides to flee. Predictable. A cornered creature chooses survival.


Thorin delivers the killing blow, and as it dies, I observe, "Should have fled faster.” 


Looking at Zalthir, I pretend to brush my teeth. 


After retrieving the corpse for the Basidia, Zalthir notes that we have completed the quest. I agree, but think that this “mossy swamp”, if left alone, could threaten us later. Furthermore, the vines from these constructs are useful for crafting magical items and are valuable. 


We agree. 


So Daz continues his game of K’tharr-li and finds the creature. 
### 
Zalthir
The creature is near the shore of a lake that is more than 10 feet deep. Recalling how it can grapple, I decide that I do not wish to be drowned, so I circle the lake and attack it from the shore. 


Focusing the force of my strike into its core, I execute a Stunning Strike. The creature attempts to resist, but my timing is precise, and it is stunned. Excellent. A momentary incapacity is a massive tactical advantage.


Daz proceeds, launching Scorching Ray attacks. He hits, but the creature is a swamp creature, and the fire is squelched. But still, I can see it is hurt. 


Grygum casts Spirit Guardians. I note immediately that this spell creates a persistent zone of damage and that I can move creatures into this zone of damage. 


The creature is stunned, and its speed is drastically reduced. Now, I must keep it anchored within the zone of damage created by the cleric. I think, "I have a reason to grapple.”


I use my second strike to initiate a grapple. I am successful. The Shambling Mound is now trapped, immobilized within Grygum's radiating divine energy.


Daz, despite the halved damage output, reinforces his attack with another Fireball.


The creature's turn arrives. It is trapped by my grapple and confined within the Spirit Guardians. 
It thrashes, using its tendril in an attempt to attack me, and succeeds. However, I use my monastic deflection technique, absorbing a portion of the bludgeoning force and limiting the pain. 


It then attempts to escape my hold and engulf Thorin. The image is strange—I hold it, yet it tries to consume another. The grapple remains intact, but Thorin is caught, but not for long. He strains and escapes.


The inevitable happens, the creature is felled not by a final weapon strike, but by the relentless, quiet efficacy of persistent magic.
### Daz
We return to the Neverlight Grove, the corpse of the Grick dragging slightly.


The Sovereign, Basidia, accepts the Grick. We had stripped the Grik for its head. Basidia is concerned, but then sighs. The animation will continue and be successful. 


Basidia then leads us toward the next segment of this bizarre cultural tour: the Circle of the Builders.


As we are about to leave, Grygum asks if Rump-a-dump and Stool would like to join us. Basidia assures that they are pretty happy among their kind. Grygum persists, and he tells Basidia that he would be thrilled to have them come along. 


I sense Grygum is worried. I don't know what. 


We arrive at the Northern Terraces of the Neverlight Grove. The terraces lining the northern walls are suffused with faerzress, and I notice that this place is filled with vegetation. As I draw closer, I see water trickling from the walls of this vast cavern being channeled into a crude yet effective terraced irrigation system. A thick, sweet smell fills the air from the thousands of fungi of all colors and sizes, many glowing with a strange, inviting light.
As we arrive, a new Myconid, Gasbide, approaches us immediately. He is a 'Builder' and, according to Basidi, a "supporter of Sovereign Philo.” He scrutinizes us with undisguised curiosity.


"You are new to this area!" he exclaims.


Grygum, ever the one to leap at a conversational opening, replies simply, "Yes, we are".


Gasbide presses, "And... and are you from, from above?”.


Grygum confirms with a touch of performative pomp: "Yes, we are from the Great Bright.


The builder is immediately obsessed, ignoring the potential dangers lurking outside the Grove. "I must learn about all of your... your... describe to me your buildings," he pleads.


Grygum attempts to satisfy him with the most basic, unhelpful generalizations: "Well, we have some that are tall, and some that are big". This is precisely the type of generalized, imprecise data the Drow abhor.


Gasbide quickly cuts through the fluff: "No, no, no, no, no, like, how are they built? I want you to... is it, like, what shape do they have? What materials do you use? How many windows? How many doors? I've heard the word 'windows'. What is a window?".


This creature is an engineer, captivated by the foreign concepts of surface architecture. Zalthir, seeing an opening to secure an advantage, focuses and conjures a small-scale structure using Minor Illusion. 


"That’s impressive," Grygum notes, appreciative of the display.


Gasbide examines the illusion, calculating rapidly: "Is this to scale? But you don't fit in those buildings. Is it for small people?"


Zalthir calmly explains, "They're usually larger. This is scaled down so you can see it."


Gasbide gasps, Zalthir's status instantly elevated in his eyes. "Oh! And he goes, are you an architect?".


Zalthir, committed to tactical deception, agrees: "Let's go with that."


Gasbide's excitement is now unbridled. He begins detailing the outlandish, bizarre structures he dreams of constructing, clearly a symptom of the chaotic influence surrounding Philo.


"I dream. Do you want me to tell you what I dream of?"


"Sure," I respond.


"I dream of building a fungal tower even greater than Yggmorgus... I hope to use it to break through the Underdark to the surface world, possibly with the aid of Aromikos," he reveals.
The questioning then quickly spirals into exhaustive engineering minutiae: "How big should it be? How many pieces of wood are required? Can... this zurkhwood mushroom be used as an equivalent?".


The creature doesn’t understand that the overbrite has sun and will harm the myconids. They are distraught and ask how they can build things that will protect them from the thing I call a sun. 


And then we get into more technical discussions.  Finally, a creature that can discuss the final points of construction and design with me.


"I'll nerd out with them for a little while," I tell everyone. 


As I engage in the technical discussion, Gasbide reveals a crucial piece of the larger puzzle: he has no clear understanding of what Araumycos is, only that "it is part of a great celebration to come," promised by Sovereign Philo. The impending "great awakening" is tied to this mythical "great celebration".


I wonder if this has anything to do with the celebration promised by Philo tomorrow. 
# Chapter 28 The Wedding Feast. 
### Thorin


Dawnbringer has been quite chatty of late. She enjoys the open air of the Neverlight Grove, with its bright, cheery light and vibrant colors. As for me, I find the cave poorly excavated and lacking several key structural elements that would both enhance and protect it, never mind the need for defensive structures.


As we approach, Basidia releases their spores and speaks to us. They say, “Phylo is changing our society. I believed that the best way for us to work together was to participate in a group meld where everyone could hear from everyone. But Phylo convinced some of the circle leaders that the Great Seeder told them of another way. That instead of one big circle, each circle leader would have a melding with their group, and then with the leaders.” Basidia sighed, “Phylo said strange things like the need to eliminate cross-functional groups and instead have teams focused on the task at hand. Phylo said that by having that focus, and more narrowly, they would be more productive.” 


This sounds like utter madness. 


Zalthir looks at Basidia and whinces, as if he understands all too well what Basidia means. 


Basidia continues, “So now we have two inner circles, the circle of leaders and the circle of masters. The circle of those closest to them.” 


Basidia sighs and then points ahead to another Myconid, “They is Hepbode, and they are the grower. They are friends of Phylo, not of mine.” 


As we approach, Hepbobe starts talking to us once the Spores of Raport connect with our mind. “We are in charge of growing food for the colony.”


Grygum awkwardly asks, “So wait, you are mushrooms, like the food, and you eat other mushrooms?” 


I blush in shame. 


But Hepbobe acts as if they have seen this before, “It’s a typical misconception of softers who think all mushrooms are just that, mushrooms. We are a special kind of mushroom, or more precisely, we are not mushrooms because we are a sentient species.” 


Hepbobe sensing someone who wishes to learn continues, as if he were explaining something to a small child. “Myconid’s are herbivores.  Much like other creatures, we have particular preferences and cooking styles and ways of meeting, producing, and consuming the food that reflect the wide variety of tastes and pellets of the individual myconids.” 


I think I got it and ask, “So you are a fungus and eat fungi, just like I am a mammal and eat animals.” 


“Exactly.” 


“Gotcha!” 


Hepbobe then seems to be lost in his own tour. He shows the irrigation tunnels and the various kinds of fungi that are grown, “To continuously feed and delight the Myconids that live in this community.” 


I am bored, and he notices that and mutters, “I could give you a detailed analysis of our crop yields and growth, but perhaps another time.” 


Basidia prods us to ask Hepbobe about Phylo. 


Hepbobe must have overheard Basidia because he first stares at Grygum, then Basidia, and then Grygum, and then seems to sigh. “Basidia is concerned that Phylo is doing something that is going to irreparably harm Myconid life. I, on the other hand, believe that these organizational constructs, whether it's one or many, are things that only Sovereigns care about. Those of us who have a job to do to maintain the farming supply do not think that this is meaningful one way or another.” 


The words they say are meaningless. They must be mad. 


However, Grygum seems to be nodding. 


“Basidia believes that if we’re all together, everybody knows what’s going on, but does everybody need to? By focusing, we can deliver better mushrooms, higher quality mushrooms, and not get distracted by the concerns of the various groups. And frankly, there are some members of the group who will just talk endlessly about that topic that nobody cares about. For example, I care about this particular fungus, and other members of the circle of farmers care about it. But when we are in the circle, I start talking about it, and my circle cares, but everyone gets bored. And then I am told to be quiet. And I ask, Thorin, when are we supposed to have our internal conversations?” 


Grygum and Zalthi nod. 


And then Hepbobe becomes quite animated, “I think Basidia is exaggerating their concerns. And frankly, what is wrong with Phylo’s proposal, and that we’re going to head to a better day? Does it always have to be doom and gloom? What if there is a better day for Myconid Kind?”


I ponder that. 
### 


Grygum 


The organizational disputes of the Sovereings remind me of the preachings of the clerics of Bahamut. Much like we would spend days wondering which exact prayer would get Bahamut’s attention and please him most, they spend their days pondering how best to organize. 


To be a mushroom is to be connected. To be a sentient mushroom is to be an individual and connected. And surely there are a thousand different ways to connect. 


As we leave the Circle of Growers, Zalthir asks Basidia whether Hepbope’s food supply has the evil spores, and they say no. 


Soon, we arrive at another circle, where a Myconid appears to be dancing. 


When it sees us, it releases spores and they reach our minds. 


Zalthir notes how curious it is curious to see a Myconid dance. I agree. 


The creature, in a sing-songy voice, as if it is in some kind of ecstasy, and then declares, “Welcome, have you come to see the all that Myconids that will be? They are all necessary for Phylo’s great plan and the Greet Seeder who is coming!” 


I notice the fields of myconids that have not yet sprouted. Apparently they grow their kind. 


As he dances, Thorin and I hear the music. I don’t recognize it. But Thorin does, it’s the same melody that we heard when we saw Zuggtomy in his dream. It has no rhythm, no beauty, it revels in a symphony of chaos and evil. It hurts. 


The creature smiles at us and says, “Have you heard of Gasbide’s plan to send us to the Overbright to share our stories?” 


Thorin turns to me, “This is a death cult.” 


I shrug and wonder why is it that there are so many death cults. And then I remember that they don’t think it is a death cult, instead they assume it is a cult that will bring them some great joy.


Like Severin. 


The Circle Leader walks away and heads towards a field of tiny sprouts. I approach.


And then Thorin stops and tells us, “I can hear the music.” And we worry, “No the lyrics. Yrberop, that’s the Myconid’s name, is singing about some Great Seeder, and her “wedding” to the Great Body and how every Myconid is invited bringing joy to all in the world below and above.” 


The infested Myconid is singing to her new sprouts. 


### Zalthir


Spores infecting my mind. And madness is everywhere. 


I will not have my mind infected by these things. I will not become a zombie … 


And then I notice that Jimjar has not made a bet in some time. I ask Basidia if he has been infected and they say no. 


Jimjar must have overheard me, “I don’t see the point in making a bet. Everyone is so happy about this wedding.” 


And I wonder why he must have known about this wedding. And he does look worried. 


And we cross the grove one more time on this tour. And arrive at another of the many myconid circles. 


“Rusharoo is a friend of mine and a leader of the Circle of Explorers.” 


The Myconid enters Basidia’s cloud of spores and starts talking. I notice that there is some nervous energy, a hastiness about them. There is something different. His voice is frantic and full of speed. 


“We are the few, the proud, the explorers, and the pathfinders. We are the ones who scout and see the world beyond the grove.” 


“And what have you seen lately?” 


“I have noticed, as has Basilia, that the Grove is not well. Every time I come back, it changes, and its changes are not for the best.” 


There is a pause. 


“Basidia says I should trust you. I have a few escape routes and nutrient caches should we ever need to flee.” 


He looks at Basidia as if pleading with them to leave now. 


“I have felt that the right way for a Myconid to live is traveling, instead of sticking in one place. The myconid is a nomad.” 


I am surprised and ask, “Ignoring Philo, are you saying that the natural state of a Myconid is nomadic? And that the Sovereigns agree?” 


Basidia, if they could roll their eyes, would. “No, Rusharoo is one of our kind who is always exploring. That is why they are exploring. Myconids stay in one place and cultivate their gardens.” 


“And what about the plans to visit the Overbrite?” 


Rusharoo is disgusted, “That would be a terrible idea. Myconids thrive in the dark. Why would we go into the light of the Overbrite? There is so much more for us to explore in the Underdark. So many tunnels and caves. I think the caves and tunnels are really another Myconid that connects everything. And that we are messages for that myconid.” 


Basidia sighs and then whispers to Rusharoo.


Rusharoo leans in, “If you wish, I could send you into the Circle of Welcome through a secret passageway.” 
### Daz


Gathering intelligence is the Drow way.


The path leads up to a plateau, and beyond that lies a strange garden. We approach it. And as we get closer, we hear strange mutterings. As we get closer, the mutterings turn into a cacophony of moans and hisses. The only thing in this place comes from a few glowing mushrooms, but even in the gloom. I stare in shock. The heads of dozens of underdark creatures peek from the ground. Mold and fungi grow on them, and through them. 


And then a voice, a Drow voice, yells out loudly and in common. She is fighting to speak, “Please, for the love of your gods of light, kill me.” I stare at her some more. She starts to move, I think to prepare a spell, but notice that half her face is rotten and postulated, a bed for the sprouting of mushrooms. She raises what I think is a hand, and it is a spider medallion covered in fungi that have fused the medallion with her body. She moans, “The Great Seeder is here. The Lady of Decay took me.” 


Thorin wants to do as she asks, but Zalthir shows true Drow instincts when he wants to ask questions. 
Thorin asks, “How do we avoid your fate?” 


The thing that was once a drow laughs. “My name is Xinaya, and I was sent to find you. Ilvara thought you would come here.” She cackles, “Who would have thought that I would be begging you to kill me?” 


Zalthir asks if she was here to kill us. 


I stifle a laugh. 


The female Drow coughs, “No, to capture you. Ilvara wanted to kill you herself. I was given orders to capture you. I came here, thinking you would seek refuge amongst the Myconids. But I made the mistake of accepting Phylo’s invitation to see the Circle of Welcome. My squad and I become victims of the madness.”


And then she notices me, perhaps for the first time, and takes the haughty tone of a female Drow follower of Lolth towards any male, “You are from Menzoberanzaan. You must warn the other Drow of the presence of the Demon Queen of the Fungi in the Underdark.” 


The Demon Queen and Demogorgon are here, in the Prime Material Plane and in the Underdark. 


And then I notice a shift. The moans of the victims take on a new tone, a fear of something that moves across the foul ground. 


A disgusting larval creature rises before me. I notice some vestigial fungal growths. I wonder if this might have once been a myconid. 


“Welcome, travelers.” The aberrant myconid’s voice gurgles and spits as it speaks both aloud and in my mind simultaneously. 


“Are you here for the wedding rehearsal? Friends of the bride or her intended? No matter! Let the love of the Great Seeder embrace you as you become one with her chosen, the Great Body!”
### Thorin


Dawnbringer really doesn’t like the dark. And I really don’t like fungal growths that can turn you into abominations. 


We’re all here: Spiderbait, Jimjar, Eldeth, Sarith, Furuum, and the other woman, Aliza Argot, whom we found in the caves. Two Myconids now surround us, along with this fungal abomination and two Drow who have been turned into slaves. 


And it’s a good thing I am carrying Dawnbringer, because the sunlight hurts these creatures. And the bright light emanating from the shift hurts the creatures as if it were from the sun itself. 


I see to my left Jimjar covered in spores, and then he stops moving.  


Grygum approaches the creature to touch it. Is this thing the source of the harmful spores?


The orc cleric of Bahamut approaches the creature gingerly, invokes the power of his god, and inflicts wounds on it. 


Daz shouts, “If you can get out of the way.” 


I can see him calculating. I know what is coming next. “Boom.” 


Just then, a corpse explodes, and the bloody parts somehow cure the abomination. 


“Exploding corpses?” shouts Zalthir. I shrug. “How many do you think there are?” he adds. 


“Enough?” I answer. 


And then boom, as the fire mote flies from Daz’s hand and explodes in a conflagration of fire. 


And then another corpse explodes, drenching us all in acid. 


The creature cackles and shouts, “You’ll now join my mistress!” 


And a spore cloud covers us all.  


Then another one of the Drow spore servants attacks Jimjar. 


And to my horror, Sarith’s head explodes and turns into yet another Drow spore servant. 


I think to myself that I dodged a bullet there with Z. 


Zalthir strikes the fungal abomination, killing it. 


### Grygum 


I look at Xinaya and notice that she is crying. So close to liberation and yet so far. And scream about how life sucks. She does a lot of that. 


Using a guiding bolt, I wound one of the remaining Myconids. And watch as Daz’s bolts kill them. 


Meanwhile, Jimjar kills poor Sarith. 


And then I distinctly notice Daz giggling.  


Zalthir kills the last of the Myconid creatures. Then he rushes to Xinaya. She is still alive. I am confused. 


Thorin marches up to her, talks to Dawnbringer about the kindness of the gesture, Dawnbringer agrees, and Xinaya is killed. 


Zalthir looks confused, “Is she okay with it?” 


Thorin laughs, “I asked, and she said okay. We’re an arranged marriage.” 


I nod, “Arranged marriages can work very well!” 


We look around and collect what treasure we can. 


Up ahead, we see a path that leads to the giant mushroom, and I think, why not? 


Echoes spill from the misty cavern beyond, a cacophony of wheezing voices that wrap together like some kind of discordant music. The remaining heads planted in the Garden of Welcome begin to croak and groan, joining the horrible song.


Through the mist that shrouds the smaller cavern, I see the parade of creatures responsible for the melody. Their bodies are only vaguely humanoid, with clusters of luminescent lichen and tumescent growths forming chaotic patterns on their decaying flesh, their voices stabbing into my mind, both insane and gleeful in equal parts.
