The ground rumbled with a deep, soothing vibration, and they felt an ancient wrongness in the stone being set right. They had successfully released Entemoch's boon, gaining the ability to summon Earth Elementals and receiving a protective blessing that would allow them to turn their skin to stone once per day when struck in battle.


The victory brought unexpected complications when the party learned that the gnomes of Blingdenstone intended to use the newly available Earth Elementals for mining labor. Thorin expressed deep discomfort with this plan, arguing that subjugating these elemental beings as unpaid workers was morally wrong and risked provoking an uprising. The party decided to take a stand, meeting with Blingdenstone's leaders including Senni Diggermattock, Chief Dorbo, and Chipgrin. Thorin passionately argued that asking the elementals for help in defending the realm and then forcing them into hard labor was unconscionable. Grygum supported this position from a religious perspective, invoking the will of the Gnomish gods, while Zalthir spoke of peace and harmony from his monastic training.


Daz delivered perhaps the most cutting argument, drawing a parallel between the proposed elemental labor system and the slave society of Menzoberranzan, asking whether the gnomes truly wanted to become like the Drow they had just freed themselves from. The arguments proved devastatingly effective, with Senni seizing control of the meeting and the religious leaders agreeing that enslaving summoned creatures violated their deepest beliefs. Senni, as a leader of the labor groups, not the business leaders, shouted - "Gnome Labor, not Summoned Labor!" The party successfully convinced Blingdenstone's leadership that Earth Elementals could be summoned for defense and warfare, but not for labor in building or mining, fundamentally disrupting the city's economic plans while earning the gratitude and admiration of the working gnomes.


As Blingdenstone prepared for the impending battle against the Pudding King and his oozes, a traveling merchant named Starlace arrived with a shop full of magical wares. The party took the opportunity to upgrade their equipment before the coming conflict. Zalthir purchased spectacles crafted from glowing crystal that would allow him to see invisible creatures and peer through magical darkness. Grygum had both his mace and shield enchanted with protective magic, significantly improving his defensive capabilities. The party also sold some excess armor to Starlace, with both sides feeling satisfied with the negotiation.


Finally, the party sought out Valimor Brightgem at The Gilded Sheath to commission a proper scabbard for Dawnbringer, the sentient glowing sword that had been attracting attention from local children with its flaming appearance. Valimor offered either an expensive gem-encrusted showpiece or a more practical locking scabbard that would prevent theft. During the discussion, Thorin casually suggested product naming schemes like "Vaultmaster 9000" and the concept of tiered models with replaceable components. Valimor's eyes lit up with excitement at these marketing concepts, his mind racing with possibilities of platform-based business models and upgrade paths. Feeling generous and inspired, he offered the practical locking scabbard at a reduced price, and Dawnbringer was finally pleased to have a proper home that would keep the sword secure and presentable.


# Chapter 42 Zalthir's Daring Grapple


Chief Dorbo Diggermattock stood before the assembled forces, his voice ringing with conviction as he declared that today would be the day of victory against the Pudding King. He pointed to Daz, proclaiming that the dragonborn would lead them to triumph. The chief then unveiled a battle plan: the party would break through a wall cleared by the Galeb Duhr and infiltrate the Pudding King's court from the south, while his forces attacked from another direction to create a diversion. To aid in this assault, he offered three groups of allies—an elemental imbued with Entemoch's power, wererats led by Chipgrin, and the Pickshine Miners under their enthusiastic owner of Pickshine Mines.


The party questioned whether sending troops into the heavily ooze-infested purple area was truly necessary. Senni Diggermattock, her face etched with concern, explained her fears for the civilian areas of Blingdenstone and worried that without a proper diversion, the party's failure might go unnoticed until the town was already overrun. It became clear that while Chief Dorbo was profit-motivated and focused on protecting the mines, Senni cared deeply about the people and the community they had built. After much discussion, the party proposed a minimal distraction rather than a full assault, which pleased many who had been dreading a large-scale battle.


Dasco Pickshine, the owner of Pickshine Mines for Dasco Pickshine Mines, seized every opportunity to promote his brand. He offered "branded tea" and explained his holistic approach to marketing the mining operation. When the party showed interest in branded items, he personally sewed a Dasco Pickshine patch onto Daz's clothes, standing proudly beside the much taller dragonborn. Every piece of Dasco Pickshine's clothing and equipment bore his company's logo, demonstrating his unwavering commitment to brand promotion.


The party established terms with their allies, deciding on a reconnaissance-first approach. Chipgrin and his wererats, taking offense at any suggestion they might be noisy, emphasized their stealth capabilities and agreed to scout ahead while the other allies waited in reserve at area twenty-two. Daz was formally recognized as the general in charge, with Grygum and Zalthir serving as lieutenants who could also give orders. The plan was set: the main distraction force would only begin their attack when the party sent the signal.


A wererat scout ventured ahead and returned with troubling news. A twenty-foot stretch of passageway had been hollowed out into a pulsating pit of black pudding, with an acid-dripping ceiling above. The scout noted grimly that if he could get through the rubble, the oozes could get through the other way. Dasco Pickshine immediately offered a solution: his miners could bridge the pit using mithril braces and salt neutralizers. However, he explained that if they built the bridge, they would need to stay behind to maintain it against the acid, meaning they couldn't back up the party at the Pudding King's doors. Daz accepted the offer, and the Pickshine Miners enthusiastically set to work, completing the bridge in about twenty minutes while singing cheerful songs.


As the bridge neared completion, Jimjar made a bet that Thorin couldn't clear the gap with his pack on. Grygum, with a flash of insight, realized that Jimjar hadn't specified how Thorin should cross and persuaded the dwarf that he could simply walk across the bridge once it was built. Thorin initially considered the more dramatic option of jumping, but his sentient sword Dawnbringer argued against getting stuck in acid. After a brief dialogue between dwarf and blade, Thorin agreed that walking would be just as satisfying.


The second wererat scout ventured further ahead but didn't return. After ten anxious minutes, Chipgrin went to investigate and found the scout caught and terrified, unable to move. He reported that the tunnel walls had transformed into sheets of gelatinous slime acting as dark, weeping mirrors with psychic effects. A "brain slime" in the ceiling emitted a rhythmic, wet clicking and sang a psychic song that turned minds into puddles. Chipgrin offered two options: his pack could howl at a frequency that would drown out the psychic effect, allowing the party to walk through safely, but this would draw all the oozes to attack the wererats, leaving the party without scouts or backup. The party chose this loud path, and Jimjar made a joke about Daz's reflection being better looking than the real thing, though Daz refused to engage with such parlor games.


Daz sent his bat familiar ahead to scout further, and it discovered a grand vaulted corridor barred by a massive, quivering wall of translucent ochre jelly. The creature filled the hallway from floor to ceiling, pulsing with a rhythmic thrum that matched the Pudding King's own heartbeat. Thick pseudopods lashed out from the jelly, attempting to pull intruders into its acidic mass, though the bat navigated through them successfully. The heavy stone doors to the throne room were visible through the jelly's semi-clear body. Glabbagool suggested getting inside him to pass through safely, though this would cause acid burns and oxygen deprivation. The Earth Elemental indicated it could smash through the jelly, as it wasn't affected by acid.


The party asked Glabbagool if the Pudding King could control him, and the intelligent ooze promised he would never hurt his friends. However, he recalled an earlier incident where he had heard a voice calling him from a large pool of slimes, suggesting the Pudding King might have some influence over him. The party learned that the Pudding King had made an alliance with the demon lord Juiblex and was trying to convert Blingdenstone's biomass into ooze biomass by having his creatures consume everyone. They debated what to do with the King once captured, realizing they hadn't established a clear plan beyond the initial snatch-and-grab.


Through the ochre jelly, the party observed the Pudding King monologuing to his two ooze henchmen, Princess Ebonheir and Prince Livid. He gloated about the impending defeat of Blingdenstone, periodically cheering as he described members of the Blingdenstone army being consumed by oozes. He also ranted that Zuggtmoy, the Queen of Rot, thought she could take his kingdom, but Juiblex had promised it to him. The party noted green slime patches on the ceiling throughout the throne room that could drop on anyone standing beneath them.


The signal was sent, and the main distraction force began their attack. Zalthir manifested his tentacles and prepared to fly as the Earth Elemental smashed through the ochre jelly barricade. The elemental then hurled Zalthir thirty feet into the throne room, and the dragonborn teleported an additional sixty feet closer to the Pudding King before walking the final forty-five feet to reach him. Zalthir struck the gnomish villain and successfully wrapped his tentacles around him in a grapple.


In response to being grappled, the Pudding King transformed into an ooze form, his body becoming a shifting, amorphous mass. Despite the transformation, Zalthir maintained his grip and used his remaining movement to drag the Pudding King fifteen feet south, away from his ooze allies. The villain's new form meant he could strike at Zalthir with deadly certainty, but the dragonborn had successfully isolated him from his henchmen, setting the stage for a desperate confrontation.


# Chapter 43 The Fall of the Pudding King
## Summary
The party stood at the entrance to the throne room, having breached the walls with the help of an Earth Elemental that carved a passage through the stone. As they entered, Zalthir made a bold move to grapple the Pudding King, hoping to seize him and end his reign of terror. But to their horror, the Pudding King transformed before their eyes, shedding his humanoid form and becoming a sentient, telepathic ooze—a manifestation of his complete embrace of Juiblex, the demon lord of oozes. His telepathic voice screamed through their minds, declaring his intention to reduce all of the Underdark into nothing but ooze, though the party quickly asked him to lower his mental volume.


Despite the Pudding King's new form, Zalthir maintained his grapple, wrestling with the acidic creature as it oozed around him. The party discussed using their Bag of Holding to contain the ooze, but realized that while they could temporarily shove him inside to deprive him of action, a sentient ooze could simply ooze back out through the opening. The throne room itself proved treacherous, with green slime hanging from the ceiling ready to drop on anyone who passed beneath it, and the Pudding King's lair actions giving him additional power within his domain.


The battle began in earnest as Daz launched magical missiles at the Pudding King while Prince Livid, one of the ooze king's allies, retaliated with psychic blasts. Thorin carefully navigated around the green slime hazards, and Princess Ebonmire hurled blobs of acidic ooze at the party. The Pudding King then unleashed a devastating slime wave that crashed over multiple party members, forcing them to dive out of the way or be knocked prone and covered in corrosive slime. Those who fell were further assaulted by green slime dropping from above, though most managed to roll clear of the worst effects.


Recognizing that the Pudding King's lair was giving him too much advantage, Zalthir made a tactical decision that would prove crucial. Using his monk abilities to dash at incredible speed while maintaining his grapple, he dragged the struggling ooze out of the throne room entirely. In a bizarre moment, he pulled the Pudding King directly through Glabbagool, their gelatinous cube companion, who remarked that it tickled. Zalthir took damage from being inside Glabbagool's acidic body, but his magical protections helped him resist the worst of it.


As Zalthir passed through the body, he thought that Glabbagool should have the mental discipline to control his body and how the acidity affected anyone inside. He took a mental note to suggest that Glabbagool begin the training to become a monk.


As the battle continued, something strange occurred that threw the party into confusion. When Thorin struck what he thought was the Pudding King with his darts, a familiar voice cried out asking why they were hurting him. The party quickly realized that somehow, impossibly, Glabbagool and the Pudding King had swapped positions or bodies. Thorin tested this by asking where they first met, and the ooze near him responded that they had met in a cave—confirming it was indeed their friendly gelatinous cube ally. The real Pudding King was now a Gelatinous Cube and Glabbagool's was an ooze.


Once the confusion was sorted out, the party coordinated a devastating assault. Daz channeled powerful magical energy into missiles that unerringly struck the Pudding King, while Grygum called upon dark powers to inflict necrotic wounds that caused the ooze to writhe in pain. The Pudding King fought back desperately, unleashing more slime waves and trying to use his lair's green slime against them, but he had been separated from his throne room, and his power was waning. Thorin struck with his radiant sword Dawnbringer, its holy light searing through the corrupted ooze.


Zalthir delivered the final assault, teleporting through shadows to close the distance and unleashing a flurry of strikes enhanced by eldritch energy channeling through his tentacles. Each blow caused the Pudding King's form to destabilize further, his ooze body unable to maintain cohesion under the relentless assault. With a final telepathic scream—"Behold the true feast, the soul's final blend!"—the Pudding King dissolved completely, his consciousness dissipating as his physical form melted into inert puddles.


With their leader defeated, Prince Livid and Princess Ebonmire fought on, but they stood no chance against the party's combined might. Daz called down a massive explosion of fire that engulfed both ooze creatures, though Prince Livid's resistance to flames allowed him to survive with grievous injuries. The party quickly finished off both minions, with Princess Ebonmire falling to a combination of necrotic magic and physical strikes, while Prince Livid was destroyed by another volley of magical missiles.


As the last enemy fell, the party felt a palpable shift in the atmosphere around them. The toxic, oppressive presence of Juiblex's demonic power began to recede from the stones and air, seeping away like water draining from a basin. However, they noticed that the fungi growing throughout the cavern were becoming more twisted and malevolent in appearance, suggesting that Zuggtmoy, the demon queen of fungi, was already moving to fill the power vacuum left by the Pudding King's defeat. A demonic voice echoed through the chamber, possibly Juiblex himself, declaring that he would be reborn and consume the banquet of the queen of fungi to grow even stronger.


Glabbagool, now an Ooze, seemed remarkably cheerful about the entire experience. He explained that being a sentient gelatinous cube had always been somewhat inconvenient—he moved slowly and people had to wait for him constantly. But now, having experienced being a smaller, more mobile ooze, he saw new possibilities. He suggested enthusiastically that the party could carry him in a jar or even in their Bag of Holding, allowing him to travel with them and see the world while serving as the ultimate garbage disposal. The party discussed the logistics of this arrangement and even mentioned beginning his training as a monk, teaching him to control his form with precision.


Searching the aftermath of the battle, the party discovered treasure that had been consumed by Princess Ebonmire—a spellbook containing numerous magical formulas that would greatly expand their arcane capabilities. More importantly, they had achieved their primary objective: securing a way out of the Underdark. Though the demonic forces of the Abyss still churned in the depths below them, and though Zuggtmoy waited to claim what Juiblex had lost, the party had won a significant victory and earned their ticket to escape the endless darkness beneath the world.
## Memorable Moments
"I have shed my humanoid form for the supreme power! I shall reduce all of deep known kind into nothing but ooze!" — Pudding King


*The Pudding King reveals his transformation into a sentient ooze, telepathically screaming his intentions*


**Zalthir grapples the Pudding King in ooze form and drags him into Glabbagool, prompting the gelatinous cube to say 'this tickles'**


*An absurd tactical maneuver during the heat of battle*


"Why are you hurting me?" — Glabbagool (in Pudding King's body)


*The party realizes Glabbagool and the Pudding King have swapped bodies when a familiar voice comes from the wrong ooze*


"Behold the true feast, the soul's final blend!" — Pudding King


*The Pudding King's final telepathic scream as he dissolves and dies from Zalthir's attacks*
## Scenes
### Breaking into the Throne Room
#### The party breaches the throne room entrance using an Earth Elemental and prepares to confront the Pudding King.
- The party enters the throne room through a hole created by an Earth Elemental.
- Zalthir attempts to grapple the Pudding King.
- The Pudding King transforms into a sentient, telepathic ooze, revealing he has embraced his connection to Juiblex.
- The Pudding King telepathically screams about shedding his humanoid form for supreme power and his intention to reduce all of the Underdark to ooze.
- The party discusses the mechanics of grappling an ooze, noting its acidic properties.
### The Bag of Holding Gambit
#### Zalthir considers using a Bag of Holding to contain the ooze form of the Pudding King, leading to a discussion of the item's mechanics.
- Zalthir proposes shoving the Pudding King into a Bag of Holding.
- The party discusses the rules about living creatures in Bags of Holding, including suffocation and size constraints.
- The DM rules that while a normal creature could be sealed in the bag, an ooze could 'ooze out' of it.
- The DM allows the bag to be used to temporarily deprive the Pudding King of an action, but not to contain him permanently.
### Initial Combat Exchanges
#### The party begins their assault on the Pudding King and his allies with ranged attacks and positioning.
- Daz casts Magic Missile at the Pudding King, dealing six points of damage.
- Prince Livid attacks Zalthir with a psychic blast, dealing fourteen points of damage reduced to seven by a successful intelligence saving throw.
- Thorin dashes forward, carefully avoiding the green slime hazards in the lair.
- Princess Ebonmire throws a blob at Thorin, but it misses.
- Grygum casts Guiding Bolt at the Pudding King, but it misses.
### The Pudding King's Slime Wave
#### The Pudding King retaliates with a devastating slime wave attack, affecting multiple party members.
- The Pudding King unleashes a slime wave, forcing Zalthir, Thorin, Daz, and Grygum to make dexterity saving throws.
- Zalthir takes eleven points of acid damage, using Stone Skin to reduce it to five.
- Daz and Grygum fail their saves and are knocked prone, taking damage.
- The Pudding King uses his lair action to drop green slime on Grygum.
- Grygum makes his dexterity saving throw against the green slime and avoids damage.
### Dragging the Ooze King
#### Zalthir successfully grapples the Pudding King and drags him out of his lair to neutralize his lair actions.
- Zalthir uses Steps of the Wind to dash, moving a significant distance while grappling the Pudding King.
- Zalthir drags the Pudding King out of his lair and into Glabbagool's position.
- Glabbagool reacts to having both Zalthir and the Pudding King inside him, saying 'this tickles'.
- Zalthir takes acid damage from being inside Glabbagool but uses Stone Skin to resist it.
- Zalthir attempts a stunning strike on the Pudding King but misses.
- Zalthir moves through Glabbagool, dragging the Pudding King with him.
### The Ooze Swap Revelation
#### The party discovers that Glabbagool and the Pudding King have somehow swapped bodies or identities.
- Thorin attacks with darts, dealing six points of piercing damage.
- A voice resembling Glabbagool emanates from the ooze near Thorin, asking 'why are you hurting me?'
- Thorin asks the ooze where they first met, and it responds 'we met in a cake', confirming it is Glabbagool.
- The party realizes that Glabbagool and the Pudding King have swapped positions.
- Thorin attacks the correct target (the Pudding King in Glabbagool's body) with Dawnbringer, dealing twelve points of radiant damage.
- The Pudding King attempts to move under the slime, but Thorin hits him with an opportunity attack, reducing his speed to zero.
### Coordinated Assault
#### The party coordinates their attacks against the Pudding King and his remaining allies.
- Daz casts a third-level Magic Missile at the Pudding King, dealing twenty points of damage.
- Prince Livid and Princess Ebonmire charge toward the party.
- Grygum casts Inflict Wounds on the Pudding King, dealing twenty-three points of damage.
- The Pudding King unleashes another slime wave, affecting Thorin, Daz, and Grygum.
- Thorin makes his save and takes reduced damage; Daz and Grygum use Stone Skin to resist the damage.
- Daz is covered in green slime but avoids immediate damage.
### Defeating the Pudding King
#### Zalthir delivers the final blows to the Pudding King, causing him to dissolve and die.
- Zalthir uses Shadow Step to teleport near the Pudding King.
- Zalthir attacks the Pudding King with advantage, dealing damage and grappling him.
- Zalthir attempts a stunning strike; the Pudding King fails the save, halving his speed and granting advantage on the next melee attack.
- Zalthir continues attacking with punches and Eldritch Claw damage from his tentacles, dealing a total of thirty-seven points of damage.
- The Pudding King dissolves, screaming telepathically: 'Behold the true feast, the soul's final blend!'
- Glabbagool, now in his original gelatinous cube form, expresses confusion about what happened.
### Mopping Up the Minions
#### The party quickly dispatches the remaining enemies, Prince Livid and Princess Ebonmire.
- Thorin uses Second Wind to heal himself.
- Daz casts Fireball, dealing twenty-nine points of damage to both Prince Livid and Princess Ebonmire.
- Prince Livid, resistant to fire, takes fourteen points of damage and is reduced to eight hit points.
- Princess Ebonmire takes full damage from the Fireball.
- Princess Ebonmire charges at Thorin.
- Prince Livid uses a psychic attack on Daz, dealing five points of damage.
- Grygum stands up from prone and casts Inflict Wounds on Princess Ebonmire, dealing eighteen points of damage.
- Zalthir uses Shadow Step to teleport and attacks Princess Ebonmire, grappling her and dealing damage.
- Thorin attacks and kills Princess Ebonmire.
- Daz casts Magic Missile at Prince Livid, killing him.
### Victory and Aftermath
#### With all enemies defeated, the party experiences the aftermath of their victory and discovers treasure.
- The party feels the toxic flow of Juiblex's power receding from the area.
- The fungi in the area become more twisted, suggesting Zuggtmoy is waiting to seize power.
- A demonic voice, possibly Juiblex himself, declares: 'You haven't won. I will be reborn. I will consume the banquet of the queen of the fungi, and I will grow.'
- The party finds a spellbook containing many spells, which was in Princess Ebonmire's stomach.
- The party levels up.
- Glabbagool expresses excitement about his new ooze form, seeing it as an opportunity to be carried and experience the world differently.
- Glabbagool suggests he could be carried in a jar or the Bag of Holding and serve as a garbage disposal.
- The party discusses Glabbagool's potential monk training.
## NPCs
### Pudding King
A former humanoid who transformed into a sentient, telepathic ooze after embracing his connection to Juiblex, the demon lord of oozes. He commanded an army of oozes and possessed powerful abilities including slime waves and green slime attacks. He was grappled and dragged out of his lair by Zalthir, and at one point swapped positions with Glabbagool. He was ultimately defeated and dissolved, screaming 'Behold the true feast, the soul's final blend!' as he died.
### Glabbagool
An intelligent gelatinous cube who was previously affected by demonic power. During the battle, he somehow swapped positions with the Pudding King, causing confusion for the party. After the Pudding King's defeat, Glabbagool returned to his original form and expressed excitement about potentially being carried in a jar or Bag of Holding, viewing his new mobility as an opportunity to experience the world differently. He sees himself as a potential garbage disposal and is interested in monk training.
### Prince Livid
An ooze ally of the Pudding King who attacked with psychic blasts. He was resistant to fire damage, which allowed him to survive Daz's initial Fireball with only eight hit points remaining. He was ultimately killed by Daz's Magic Missile.
### Princess Ebonmire
An ooze ally of the Pudding King who attacked by throwing blobs and charging at the party. She was killed by the party's combined efforts, and after her death, a spellbook containing many spells was found in her stomach.
### Juiblex
The demon lord of oozes, whose power was channeled through the Pudding King. After the Pudding King's defeat, his infernal influence receded from the area, but a demonic voice claimed he would be reborn by consuming the Queen of Fungi.
### Zuggtmoy
The Lady of Rot and Demon Lord of Fungi. After Juiblex's defeat, the fungi in the area became more twisted, suggesting she was waiting to seize power in the vacuum left by the Pudding King's death.
## Locations
### Throne Room
The Pudding King's throne room, accessed through a hole created by an Earth Elemental. The room contains green slime hazards on the ceiling that can drop on those beneath them. It served as the Pudding King's lair, granting him special lair actions until he was dragged out of it.
## Items
### Bag of Holding
A magical bag capable of storing vast amounts of items and potentially creatures. The party discussed using it to contain the Pudding King, but the DM ruled that while it could temporarily deprive an ooze of an action, a sentient ooze could 'ooze out' of it and escape. Glabbagool later expressed interest in being carried in it.
### Dawnbringer
A magical weapon wielded by Thorin that emits light in a twenty-foot radius and deals radiant damage. It was used to attack the Pudding King after the party realized he had swapped positions with Glabbagool.
### Spellbook
A spellbook containing many spells, found in Princess Ebonmire's stomach after her death. It significantly expanded the party's magical repertoire.
## Spells
### Magic Missile
A reliable force damage spell cast by Daz multiple times during the battle. It does not require a roll to hit and has a range of 120 feet. Daz used it at both first and third level, with the third-level version dealing twenty points of damage to the Pudding King. The final Magic Missile killed Prince Livid.
### Guiding Bolt
A spell cast by Grygum early in the battle that missed its target.
### Stone Skin
A temporary magical effect that grants resistance to a chosen damage type for one round, usable once per long rest. Multiple party members used it to resist acid damage from the Pudding King's slime wave attacks.
### Inflict Wounds
A necrotic damage spell cast by Grygum that requires the target to make a constitution saving throw. It was used successfully against the Pudding King for twenty-three points of damage and against Princess Ebonmire for eighteen points of damage.
### Fireball
A powerful area-of-effect spell cast by Daz that deals fire damage in a large area. It dealt twenty-nine points of damage to both Prince Livid and Princess Ebonmire, though Prince Livid's fire resistance reduced his damage to fourteen points.
### Shadow Step
A monk ability used by Zalthir to teleport short distances, allowing him to quickly close the gap to enemies. He used it to reach the Pudding King and Princess Ebonmire during combat.
### Second Wind
An ability used by Thorin to heal himself during the battle.
### Eldritch Claw
An ability used by Zalthir that adds force damage to his melee attacks, manifesting as damage from his tentacles. Each hit adds 1d6 force damage.
### Revivify
A resurrection spell mentioned by Zalthir as a potential option to help Glabbagool, though it was not cast as Glabbagool was not dead.


# Chapter 44 The Knucklebone of Truth
Date: Mar 12th, 2026
## Summary
In the aftermath of the Pudding King's defeat, the Ember Vanguard found themselves far from finished. The Earth Elemental that had held the throne room's passage open was beginning to crack under the strain, its elemental energy leaking through fissures in its ancient stone body. Grygum called upon his divine gifts to mend the elemental's wounds, and with a long, relieved stretch — like Atlas finally setting down the world — the great being sighed, dropped a small glowing geode at the party's feet as a token of its favor, and dissolved back into the earth. As the dust settled, the party noticed the fungi scattered throughout the chamber were growing faster than they should have been, a quiet and unsettling reminder that though Juiblex had been driven out, Zuggtmoy's influence still crept through the dark like roots through stone.


The party pressed on to the Hall of Melting Mirrors, where Chipgrin and his wererats had been maintaining a chanting vigil to suppress the lingering psychic static left behind by the mirrors. Chipgrin turned to the party's spellcasters, hoping one of them could locate the harmonic center of the room and silence the noise for good. Daz and Grygum both reached deep into their knowledge and intuition, but the answer eluded them. It was Thorin — the party's most reliably stabby and punchy member — who paused, looked around, and simply pointed. Chipgrin stared at him for a long moment before muttering that he probably should have asked the dwarf first, then caught Zalthir's eye and hastily clarified that he meant no offense by that.


From there, the Ember Vanguard made their way to the support beams, where Gnomish miners were locked in a heated debate over construction materials and methods, arguing with the passionate conviction of people who had very strong opinions about zurkhwood versus steel. Grygum tended to the miners who had suffered burns, while Thorin threw his considerable strength into winching a critical support beam into place, aided by Daz's tactical guidance. The effort was a success, and Diggermattock was so moved that he personally threaded a needle and sewed a Diggermattock Miners patch onto Thorin's gear, declaring him an honorary member of the crew. Grygum, not to be outdone, used a cantrip to attach the patch with such precision that everyone present was briefly more impressed by the needlework than by the feat of engineering.


The relative calm shattered when the party emerged into the farming area beyond the tunnels and found a panicked gnome farmer warning them that the city was under attack. At the Trader's Grotto, they found a large Gnomish army standing before a breached wall, and beyond it — a writhing, churning mass of oozes, jellies, and black puddings, no longer bound by the Pudding King's will and very unhappy about it. Chief Diggermattock and Chipgrin were already arguing about how to divide the newly opened territory, seemingly unbothered by the fact that said territory was currently full of ooze. Thorin attempted to redirect their attention to the more immediate problem, but the argument rolled on like a gelatinous cube down a corridor.


It was Jimjar who cut through the chaos, as he so often did, with a casual wager. He approached Grygum and offered a bet of ten platinum pieces, claiming that Glabbagool — the party's intelligent gelatinous cube companion — had more sense than the Pudding King ever had. Before anyone could fully process what was happening, Jimjar tossed a small bone die onto Glabbagool. A strange blink rippled through the air, and then something extraordinary happened: Glabbagool briefly became a bridge between every ooze in the cavern, a single vast mind connecting jellies, puddings, and cubes alike. He told them, in his gentle and earnest way, that the world was fine, that everyone could get along, and that there was really no need to kill anyone. The oozes, apparently persuaded, went mindless and peaceful, slithering away into cracks and stonework until the threat simply dissolved.


When the party pressed Jimjar on the nature of the die, he explained that he had won it off a blind Duergar in Gracklestugh, who claimed it had been carved from the knucklebone of a saint who never told a lie — a die with a memory for the truth. Jimjar shrugged and said he had figured that in a place where the blink had turned the world's math into a bad joke, a little uncertainty could go a long way. The die rolled out of Glabbagool a moment later, spent and inert, and Jimjar handed it to the party as a keepsake. Grygum paid the ten platinum pieces without complaint, and the party quietly agreed it had been the best investment they had ever made.


With the ooze crisis resolved, the Ember Vanguard was ushered into a council meeting where the various factions of Blingdenstone — miners, wererats, ghosts, and spiritual leaders — were already at each other's throats over the future of the city. Daz stepped forward and delivered a passionate appeal for unity, urging the assembled leaders to set aside their egos and build an alliance strong enough to outlast the demons. The party worked the room with careful insight: they brokered a wage agreement between the miners guild and the working class, proposed that the Gold Whisker wererats take control of the upper boroughs as a self-funded defense force, and helped broker a compromise on sustainable mining practices that satisfied both the Miners Guild and the ghosts who considered the sanctum sacred ground. One by one, the arguments quieted, hands were shaken, and a fragile but genuine peace began to take shape.


The next morning, as the party prepared to leave for the surface, the city sent them off with ceremony. Working-class gnomes lined the tunnels chanting their new rallying cry, the Burrow Warden ghosts dipped their spectral banners in salute, and Chief Chipgrin pressed a braided rat's foot into Daz's hand — the Voucher of the Varmint, he called it, a token recognized by wererats and outcasts from Blingdenstone all the way to Menzoberranzan. Legends of the Ember Vanguard were already spreading through the tunnels, growing wilder with each retelling: Daz casting storms of meteors, Grygum shattering mountains, Zalthir cutting through enemies at blinding speed, and Thorin smashing solid rock with his bare hands. The party listened to these stories with a mixture of pride and mild alarm.


It was Jimjar who delivered the final, ominous note before the party departed. He pointed to a pale white puffball mushroom growing at impossible speed from a crack in the wall, its scent cloyingly sweet, like a feast left to rot in a hothouse. He remarked that Juiblex had been a loud and messy neighbor, but that this sister — Zuggtmoy — preferred to move in while you were sleeping. Then he turned and walked back toward Blingdenstone. Zalthir, long suspicious of the little gambler, reached out with a focused awareness and discovered that Jimjar was immune to poison and psychic damage, could not be charmed or frightened, and shrugged off radiant energy and mundane weapons alike — a profile that matched no ordinary gnome, and bore a striking resemblance to something far more divine. Jimjar noticed the scrutiny, offered a knowing wink, and vanished entirely from existence, leaving only the faint metallic clink of platinum coins echoing in the tunnel behind him.
## Memorable Moments
**Thorin, the least magically inclined member of the party, succeeds where all the spellcasters failed — correctly identifying the psychic center of the Hall of Melting Mirrors using a lucky roll and dwarvish intuition.**


*Chipgrin remarks he should have asked the dwarf first, before awkwardly clarifying to Zalthir that he meant no offense by calling them a 'surface dweller'.*


"The old mule swore it was carved from the knucklebone of a saint who never told a lie, said it had a memory for the truth. I thought he was just trying to cover his losses." — Jimjar


*Explaining the origin of his mysterious bone die after using it to pacify an entire army of oozes through Glabbagool.*


**Zalthir uses a special ability to inspect Jimjar and discovers he possesses divine-level immunities and resistances. Jimjar notices, winks, and vanishes into thin air — hinting the party will meet again.**


*The party had long suspected Jimjar was more than he appeared; this confirmed it, with his stat block resembling that of an angel or deity.*


"Juiblex was a loud, messy neighbor, but this sister, she prefers to move in while you're sleeping." — Jimjar


*Pointing ominously at a pale mushroom growing at impossible speed from a crack in the wall, foreshadowing Zuggtmoy's encroachment, just before casually walking away.*
## Scenes
### Stabilizing the Earth Elemental
#### Following the defeat of the Pudding King, the party assists a straining Earth Elemental in holding up the throne room's structure.
- The party finds an Earth Elemental struggling to keep the throne room from collapsing, leaking elemental energy through cracks in its form.
- Thorin attempts to use brute strength to set the cracks but fails to make an impact.
- Grygum casts a powerful healing spell that restores the elemental's structural integrity.
- Rejuvenated by the magic, the Earth Elemental stretches and disappears into the dirt, leaving the passage stable.
- Before departing, the Earth Elemental drops a small glowing geode as a token of favor.
- The party notices fungi in the area beginning to grow at an accelerated rate, foreshadowing the lingering influence of Zuggtmoy.
### The Harmonic Center of the Mirror Hall
#### The party encounters Chipgrin and the wererats in the Hall of Melting Mirrors and attempts to neutralize the psychic noise.
- Chipgrin asks the magic users of the party to find the harmonic center of the room to stop the lingering psychic static.
- Daz and Zalthir attempt to use their arcane knowledge and insight to locate the center but are unsuccessful.
- Grygum tries to tune into the spheres to find the source of the noise but also fails.
- Thorin, using a bit of luck and unexpected intuition, successfully points out the exact location of the psychic center.
- Chipgrin is impressed by the dwarf's success, noting that he should have asked the dwarf first.
### Repairs and Reinforcements at the Support Beams
#### The party assists Gnomish miners with structural repairs and medical aid near the black ooze-infested support beams.
- The party encounters Gnomish miners arguing over construction methods and materials for over-engineered temporary bridges.
- Grygum uses magical healing to treat miners suffering from burns.
- Thorin uses his physical strength to winch a critical support beam into place, aided by Daz's tactical advice.
- Diggermattock rewards Thorin with a 'Diggermattock Miners' patch, which is magically mended onto his gear.
- Jimjar appears and comments on the party's knack for fixing things before they depart.
### The Ooze Breach at Trader's Grotto
#### Exiting the tunnels, the party finds the Gnomish army struggling to contain a massive breach of uncontrolled oozes.
- The party emerges into a farming area where a panicked gnome farmer informs them that the city is under attack by oozes.
- The party reaches the Trader's Grotto and finds a large Gnomish army standing before a breached wall.
- A massive swarm of uncontrolled oozes, no longer under the Pudding King's command, threatens to overrun the Gnomish defenses.
- Chief Diggermattock and Chipgrin begin arguing over how to divide the territory even as the oozes threaten to overrun them.
- Thorin attempts to persuade the leaders to focus on the immediate threat, though the argument initially continues.
### Jimjar's Bet and the Bone Die
#### Jimjar proposes a wager and uses a mysterious bone die to pacify the entire ooze army through Glabbagool.
- Jimjar approaches Grygum and proposes a bet of ten platinum pieces that he can stop the 'noise' of the oozes using a special die.
- Jimjar tosses a bone die onto Glabbagool, triggering a mysterious 'blink' that causes the oozes to become mindless and peaceful.
- Glabbagool briefly connects with the entire ooze horde telepathically, telling them to calm down, leading the mass of jellies and puddings to slither away into the stonework.
- Grygum pays Jimjar the ten platinum pieces from the party funds for successfully neutralizing the threat.
- Jimjar explains the origin of the bone die, claiming he won it from a blind Duergar in Gracklestugh and that it was carved from a saint's knucklebone.
- The party asks Glabbagool about the experience; he describes briefly being part of one big mind with all the oozes before they returned to their mindless states.
- The party observes the oozes dispersing naturally — gelatinous cubes consuming other oozes, black puddings slipping through cracks, gray oozes going still.
### The Council of Blingdenstone
#### The party mediates a complex political dispute between the various factions of Blingdenstone to ensure a lasting peace after the Pudding King's defeat.
- The party attends a council meeting where Dorbo Diggermattock expresses concerns about the city's economy, labor shortages, and defense.
- The wererats demand the upper boroughs as their own territory, while spiritual leaders object to the Miners Guild's plans to strip-mine the sanctum.
- Daz delivers a motivational speech urging the factions to set aside their egos for a mutual alliance and economic renaissance.
- The party uses insight to identify key leverage points, including suggesting a wage increase for the working-class gnomes to settle labor disputes.
- The party proposes that the Gold Whisker wererats take control of the upper burrows to serve as a defense force, removing the need for Diggermattock to pay for military protection.
- A compromise is reached regarding the mining of the throne room, establishing sustainable mining practices to respect the burial grounds of the ghosts.
- The various factions agree to a peace arrangement, and Dorbo Diggermattock prepares to reopen Blingdenstone for trade with the surface world.
### Departure and the True Nature of Jimjar
#### As the party prepares to leave for the surface, they receive tokens of gratitude and Zalthir's inspection of Jimjar reveals he is far more than a simple gnome.
- Chief Chipgrin presents Daz with a braided rat's foot Voucher of the Varmint as a sign of friendship with the wererats.
- The party overhears exaggerated legends of their exploits being told by local gnomes, including tales of Daz casting meteor swarm and Thorin smashing rocks with his biceps.
- Jimjar returns Grygum's ten platinum winnings and warns of a new fungal threat — a pale white puffball mushroom growing at impossible speed from a crack in the wall, smelling sweetly of rot.
- Zalthir uses a special ability to discern Jimjar's resistances and immunities, discovering he is immune to poison and psychic damage, cannot be charmed or frightened, and is resistant to radiant damage and non-magical physical attacks.
- Realizing he has been scrutinized, Jimjar winks at the party and vanishes into thin air, heading back toward Blingdenstone.
- The party discusses the possibility of Jimjar being a deity or celestial being, noting his stat block resembles that of an angel.
- The session concludes with the party preparing to finally exit the Underdark and see the sun.
## NPCs
### Earth Elemental
A massive being of stone that sacrificed its energy to hold open a breach in the throne room. It was healed by Grygum's magic before merging back into the earth, and left behind a glowing geode as a token of favor.
### Chipgrin
A wererat leader encountered in the Hall of Melting Mirrors who sought the party's help neutralizing psychic noise. He later negotiated for wererat control of the upper boroughs during the council meeting, and gifted Daz the Voucher of the Varmint upon the party's departure.
### Glabbagool
An intelligent gelatinous cube and ally to the party, currently carried in a bag of holding. He briefly acted as a telepathic bridge for the ooze horde when Jimjar's bone die was tossed onto him, allowing him to calm the entire swarm.
### Jimjar
A mysterious deep gnome with a penchant for gambling who used a bone die carved from a saint's knucklebone to pacify the ooze army. He revealed a philosophy of 'world math' and probability before departing. When Zalthir used a special ability to inspect him, he was found to be immune to poison and psychic damage, resistant to radiant and non-magical physical attacks, and unable to be charmed or frightened — before winking and vanishing entirely.
### Chief Dorbo Diggermattock
The leader of Blingdenstone who argued for aggressive economic recovery and mithral extraction. He rewarded Thorin with a miners patch and ultimately agreed to a peace arrangement, announcing plans to reopen Blingdenstone for trade.
### Senni Diggermattock
Dorbo's wife and a member of the Gold Whisker clan who advocated for a functional alliance between the gnomes and the wererats, and whose support was noted as helpful to Dorbo's decision-making.
### Burrow Warden Jadger
A spectral leader of the ghosts who observed the party's departure and dipped his spectral banner in salute as they left Blingdenstone.
### Dazco Pickshine
A representative of the Miners Guild who initially pushed for immediate strip mining to fund city repairs before agreeing to a sustainable mining compromise.
### Entemoch
The Prince of Good Elementals, mentioned as feeling favorably toward the party after they assisted the Earth Elemental.
## Locations
### Throne Room
The site of the Pudding King's defeat, where an Earth Elemental strained to prevent the ceiling from collapsing. Fungi in the area were observed growing at an accelerated rate after the battle.
### Hall of Melting Mirrors
A chamber filled with psychic static where Chipgrin and his wererats were maintaining a chanting vigil to keep the lingering psychic noise at bay.
### Support Beams
An area featuring over-engineered temporary bridges and structural beams being maintained by Gnomish miners amidst black ooze residue, where several miners had suffered burns.
### Trader's Grotto
A Gnomish defensive position in Blingdenstone where a large gnome army gathered at a breached wall to face an encroaching army of uncontrolled oozes.
### Blingdenstone Council Room
A meeting hall where the leaders of the deep gnomes, wererats, miners guild, and spiritual enclaves gathered to debate the future of the city and negotiate a lasting peace.
### Northern Exit Tunnels
The set of tunnels leading out of the Underdark toward the surface world, where the party was escorted by a Gnomish honor guard as they prepared to depart.
## Items
### Glowing Geode
A small, luminous rock gifted to the party by the Earth Elemental as a token of favor before it disappeared into the earth. It is valued at 100 gold pieces.
### Diggermattock Miners Patch
A commemorative patch given to Thorin by Diggermattock as recognition of his work helping with the support beams, signifying his status as an honorary member of the mining crew. It was magically mended onto his gear.
### Bone Die
A 20-sided die carved from the knucklebone of a saint who never told a lie, won by Jimjar from a blind Duergar in Gracklestugh. When tossed onto Glabbagool, it triggered a mysterious 'blink' that pacified the entire ooze army by correcting the 'world's math.' It is now considered spent and was given to a party member as a keepsake.
### Voucher of the Varmint
A braided rat's foot given to Daz by Chief Chipgrin upon the party's departure. It serves as a mark of friendship recognized by wererats and outcasts throughout the Underdark, from Blingdenstone to Menzoberranzan.
## Spells
### Mass Healing Word
Cast by Grygum to restore the party's vitality and, more significantly, to repair the physical cracks in the Earth Elemental's stone body, allowing it to relax and eventually depart peacefully.
### Lesser Restoration
Used by Grygum to treat the burned and wounded Gnomish miners at the support beams.
### Mending
A cantrip used to magically attach the Diggermattock Miners patch to Thorin's clothing with expert precision.
### Motivational Speech
Employed by Daz during the council meeting to inspire the bickering factions of Blingdenstone — including the labor unions and the mining guild — to seek a peaceful compromise and common ground.


# Chapter 45 The Wreckage of a Lie


## Daz — The Deception Completed
The spider was already back on my wrist before Asha had finished watching the light die. That part had gone well — the Dancing Lights threading down like a column of divine attention, absorbed into the familiar, absorbed into me, blinking out. Clean. Considered. I'd been genuinely pleased with myself.


Then she spoke.


"You're a wizard. A wizard… a wizard who prays to Lolth?"


Not wonder. Appraisal. The flat, practiced appraisal of someone who has lived her entire life in a society that treats information as currency and lying as a primary language, and who has therefore developed, out of sheer professional necessity, an excellent ear for both. I filed the tone away. She wasn't convinced. She wasn't unconvinced. She was running the numbers.


So I leaned in.


"I am… you are not speaking to the wizard of this body. I… he… this body has communed with Lolth. And I… I am speaking through this body."


I shifted registers. I let the sentence stumble, then recover. I was trying to sell her something a drow cleric would recognize — the specific texture of divine intrusion, the grammar of a body that is briefly not its own. I've read enough. I've observed enough. Being a drow, you pick some stuff up.


It didn't work.


"Aha," she said. "You are trying to test me, to see if I was one of those fake followers of Lolth, who are willing to believe every charlatan magic user that is somehow being possessed by the power of Lolth."


She hadn't disbelieved me because the illusion was poor. She'd disbelieved me because she had seen this exact con before — probably multiple times, probably from people more practiced than I am, probably in considerably higher-stakes circumstances. I felt something I will not call embarrassment. I will call it a recalibration event.


The divine possession angle was closed. I pivoted.


"There are many imitations," I said, "but as you saw, I came to you in my smaller form, and led you here. You should know the truth."


I was threading a needle — the familiar's earlier appearance as the spider, reframed. Not fraud, but mystery. Not possession, but presence. If she couldn't accept what I was claiming, perhaps she could accept that something strange was happening, and that strange things sometimes arrive in wizard-shaped containers.


She was quiet for a moment. And then she began building her own frame.


"Oh, dear goodness, have you two been infected by the spores, possessed by the crazed magic of Zuggtmoy? Convinced of the bride's power? Is this another trick of Elvara's?"


I want to be precise about what happened in that moment: she had discarded my lie and replaced it with a different explanation that she found more coherent. The divine claim was dead. But Asha Vandree was not walking away. She was doing what intelligent people do when confronted with something that doesn't fit — she was finding a frame that let her keep the useful parts and discard the implausible ones.


A deluded magic user was more believable to her than a divinely-touched wizard. Fine.


I could work with deluded.


"Perhaps my prayers have been answered through this… confused vessel," she said — almost to herself, the way people do when they're granting themselves permission to proceed.


She'd seen through me and chosen to keep me anyway. In drow terms, that is more or less a letter of reference.


"I really do believe that I have," I said. Leaning into it now. "Perhaps there are some spores within me, but I… it feels… I feel it. And by the way, I've convinced others to join me."


I brought the party forward. Madness with followers is not simply pathetic — it is tactically interesting. It suggests either genuine power or a sufficiently compelling delusion, and from Asha's position, the practical difference between those two things was probably small.


It was at this point that Glabbagool attempted to pass for a rock.


The eyes gave him away. They drifted left. They drifted right. They did this with the unhurried curiosity of a creature that has never needed to pretend to be geological before and doesn't fully understand why it's being asked to start now. I looked at him. He looked at me. Or at least, several of his eyes moved in my general direction.


"Glabbagool," I said, with what I hope was a tone of patient authority rather than suppressed desperation, "I'm taking care of this. It's fine."


No deception manual I have ever studied contains a chapter on managing an ooze during active negotiations. I am adding one mentally, in real time.


Asha, to her credit, did not run. She assessed. She accepted Glabbagool as a bound familiar — the grey-ooze creature, strange and drifting and thoroughly uncategorizable, fitting quite neatly into the profile of a deluded mage who nonetheless had genuine and unusual power. It may have helped more than the Dancing Lights. I will not dwell on this.


Then she began to talk about Ilvara, and the information was worth everything the con had cost.


The hatred in it was real. Not political calculation. Not tactical positioning. Something that had been building for a long time in close quarters with a corrupted superior, and was now coming out in full.


"Ilvara, who was once a high priestess of Lolth, has become seduced by this abomination, this idea that Lolth wishes to be married. There is something foul and stinking about her, and then all of those allies she seems to covet have turned into fungal creatures that are mindless. We need to kill her. We need to butcher her! We need to send her to an unearthly grave! I fear that her disease will spread."


I listened. Only she and Jorlan remained uninfected — Asha through devotion, Jorlan through hatred, which is its own kind of immunological theory. Twenty feet of maintained distance. Separate food. The mushroom artifact from Neverlight Grove was the mechanism of corruption. The Big Heart Fungus was the primary weapon, would need sustained damage, would not die quickly or easily.


Then, because I am who I am:


"How do you propose to kill her if you're not gonna to get within 20 feet of her?"


A fair question. Asha had a ready answer.


"I was going to kill her. That is what you… where you come in."


The plan, such as it was, had always required someone else to do the lethal part. She had survived long enough to find useful lunatics willing to close that distance for her. I could not fault the logic.


"If I and the crew that is with me were able to take care of this small problem for you," I said, "what would be in it for us?"


"The gratitude of Lolth."


"I already feel the gratitude of Lolth. I have that."


I delivered it without a beat's pause. The dryness of it, I think, may have done more for the deluded-believer angle than anything else I'd attempted — it had the specific texture of a man who genuinely believes his spiritual compensation is already sufficient and is asking a practical follow-up question. Which, I realized afterward, was the most accurate version of the character I had played all evening.


She pushed back.


"That is not the kind of conviction a follower of Lolth shows."


"It's the kind of conviction this follower of Lolth shows."


I didn't flinch. Didn't qualify. Didn't offer an explanation. Steadiness, in my experience, does more work than eloquence — eloquence suggests you've been thinking about what to say, and steadiness suggests you've never needed to. The negotiation stayed alive.


She offered Ilvara's magical items as additional payment, with the caveat that they might be contaminated. I noted that caveat. I filed it.


The intelligence was solid. The alliance was provisional but real. Asha Vandree had seen through my lie, built her own explanation out of the wreckage, found it workable, and decided that a spore-maddened wizard with followers and a gelatinous familiar was, on balance, the best available instrument for killing someone she needed dead.


She wasn't wrong.


## Thorin — Tactical Preparations
The mushroom thing — I want to be clear about the mushroom thing — the fates looked at Grygum and looked at me specifically. Both of us. The artifact sitting there like a dare, and the warning coming down with actual gravity: *do not touch it*. Grygum and I had both been where that road goes. I didn't need the long version. Neither did he. We both just said nothing, which for us was the equivalent of a blood oath.


So I watched the others work through the plan instead.


The crossbow came first, because I'm not going into something like this with nothing that reaches past ten feet. Grygum had a light crossbow. I asked him for it. Simple transaction, no drama — he handed it over and I checked the mechanism the way you check anything borrowed before a fight: pull the string, sight down it, make sure the person who owned it before you wasn't sloppy. He wasn't. That dwarf is okay.


Then the party spread out the options on the table, or whatever the Underdark equivalent of a table is when you're crouched in the dark with a drow informant and a borrowed crossbow. Glyph of Warding. Dust of Suleiman. Phantasmal Killer. Fireball. Grygum had one 4th-level slot. Daz had one 4th-level slot. Those are not renewable resources in the next twenty minutes, so every piece of this had to land somewhere it mattered. I listened. I watched who spoke with certainty and who spoke with hedging. Zalthir said he could teleport directly to Ilvara — or grab her and move her somewhere unpleasant. I stored that. Teleportation as a weapon. Thorin files that away in the part of his brain labeled *useful people.*


Asha laid out her terms, and I heard them clearly. She would not come in at the start. Once we initiated, she would hold the perimeter — anything coming from outside, she handles it. Which is fine. It's useful. But I know what it is. She's drow. She's going to fight this fight on her own schedule, at the angle that suits her. I don't hold that against her. I'd be lying if I said it didn't register.


Then Grygum took the bridge.


Jorlan's side. He moved to the crossing and started inscribing the Glyph of Warding into the stone itself, and I watched the whole process with the specific attention of someone who needs to *not step in that spot* when things start moving fast. The trigger: any hostile creature crossing. Invisible once finished. Patient in the way only traps can be patient, because they don't get tired. It went down into the rock and disappeared, and the bridge looked like a bridge again.


I noted the position. I noted it carefully.


And I looked at Jorlan across that bridge, and I thought about weight and leverage and who in this room can be trusted to act predictably. Jorlan is not complicated. Jorlan is a threat with a location, which is the best kind of threat because it tells you exactly where to aim.


I have a borrowed crossbow. I have a position. He doesn't know we know he's there.


*The goal the whole time*, I thought. *Eyeing the prize.*


## Zalthir — Zalthir Opens the Fight
The distance across the cavern was a problem. Then it wasn't.


One moment I was reading the geometry of the space — the elevated platform, the sightlines, the gap between us and her — and the next I was already there, adjacent, inside the radius where a priestess stops being an authority and becomes a target. She hadn't called that. She hadn't dictated anything. I stepped through the dark and arrived before she'd finished deciding what to do, and that moment of her not-deciding was exactly what I needed.


I drove the weapon in. Sixteen. The grip locked.


Grabbing a drow priestess of Ilvara's caliber felt like grabbing a live coal — you know going in that it's going to cost you, you do it anyway because the alternative is worse. But the grapple held. She was in my hands, her movement mine to constrain, and suddenly the battlefield looked different. Not good. But different in a way I could work with.


The second strike came with her pinned and her options narrowed. Advantage. Fifteen more. Thirty-one total. She was hurting and she knew it and I could feel that knowledge in the tension of the hold — the way resistance shifts when something goes from confident to afraid.


Then I looked at the cavern floor. At the Dust of Suleiman area. At the rough arithmetic of: priestess plus that zone equals someone else's problem.


It was a brutal plan. It was also economical. You let the battlefield do the killing when you can. I'd spent enough — I wanted to spend her.


I started moving her toward it. Fly, carry, drag if I had to.


She screamed.


Not at me. The GM's exact words: *at herself.* And I caught that — I filed it, the way you file things that tell you something true. She was furious at herself. Which meant I'd actually hurt her, actually threatened something she thought couldn't be threatened, and the scream was the sound of that particular illusion breaking.


Then she was gone.


Between one heartbeat and the next, she came apart into the fungal matter beneath her feet — flowed through it like water pouring into a crack, like smoke running back into the dark — and reappeared somewhere else on the cavern floor. The grapple didn't break. It simply stopped having anything to hold. My hands closed on nothing. She was out of reach and already putting distance between us, and the scream still echoed off the cave walls like she'd left it there on purpose.


I hung in the air.


Out of actions. Out of bonus actions. Out of everything I'd had when I arrived on that platform thirty-one damage and one tactical calculation ago.


Below me, the battlefield was still happening. People were still fighting, or dying, or doing things that required me to have something left to give, which I didn't. I had altitude and a view and the specific exhaustion of a plan that almost worked.


*She's angry at herself,* I noted, and filed it away, and watched.


## Grygum — The Heart Fungus Retaliates
The cloud didn't drift. That was the first thing I noticed. Normal smoke drifts. Normal gas disperses. This hung in the cavern air like it had decided to stay — twenty feet of spore-thick poison, sitting in the middle of the battlefield as if it belonged there, as if it had always belonged there, as if *we* were the interlopers in its home.


Which, to be fair, we were.


I'd been watching the Big Heart Fungus since we entered this chamber. That's not a metaphor. I took notes. It's what I do. And what I had written in my head about that particular organism was: *not scenery*. The moment it detonated that cloud across the cavern floor, every instinct I had confirmed the notation.


Zalthir took the full brunt of it. I watched the dragonborn's body register the toxin — not a dramatic collapse, nothing so clean as that — just a subtle wrongness in how he moved, a falter in the stride of someone who had been, until thirty seconds ago, pressing a meaningful advantage over Ilvara. The poisoned condition settling over a person looks different depending on who they are. On Zalthir it looked like frustration wearing a physical costume.


He disengaged and went straight up. Ten feet. Clear of the worst of the cloud, hovering in that particular way of someone who has made the tactically correct decision and is not happy about it.


"I'm out of actions and bonus actions," he said, from somewhere above the spore line, "so I guess I'll just kind of look on and be confused."


The dry resignation in his voice said everything. I didn't laugh, but I noted it. The battlefield had fragmented faster than any of us had planned for, allies pulled in three different directions by pressure we hadn't fully mapped before we walked in. That's how these things go. You plan for the drow commander. You don't always plan for the floor itself to become an enemy.


And then Ilvara called them up.


Four shapes. Rising from the cavern floor with the patient, purposeless movement of things that are no longer choosing to move — they are simply directed. Former Velkynvelve guards. I recognized the posture of soldiers whose bodies had been repurposed, the fungal colonization of Zuggtmoy's influence made visible through Ilvara's particular corruption. These had been drow with names and duties and probably opinions about their assignments. Now they were just pointed at us.


Zalthir said, from his aerial vantage point, "Those poor guards. They've been through quite a lot."


Then he reflected on Valen. Not out loud, really — it was more in the quality of the silence that followed. I felt the thought land in the room anyway. Valen, who had been one of them. Who could have been one of them, differently categorized. These bodies on the cavern floor had once been exactly what Valen was, and somewhere between then and now, they had lost the thread entirely.


Soldiers. Now weapons. The difference between the two is sometimes just time and circumstance, and I filed that thought away under *things not to dwell on mid-combat*.


Jorlan was moving, and I saw the angle.


The Glyph of Warding on the bridge was still live. We'd placed it with exactly this kind of chaos in mind, and Jorlan was close enough, distracted enough, *angry* enough that he might not be tracking the floor carefully. I calculated this in approximately one second, which is about as long as tactical decisions get in a room that is actively trying to kill you.


"Come get it, idiot," I called across the chaos.


He ran toward the trap.


The glyph detonated. One spore servant ceased to be a problem. The others staggered in a way that suggested they had not enjoyed the experience. Jorlan himself was not having his best moment.


"Kaboom," I said, because it seemed warranted. Then: "I didn't expect it to work."


That last part was honest. The tactic had been a gamble — you call a man an idiot and invite him toward an explosive ward and you are making a bet on ego overriding tactical awareness, which is sometimes a safe bet and sometimes gets you killed. This time it paid. I took note of the conditions that made it pay, in case they became relevant again.


With the servants disrupted and Jorlan compromised, I turned my attention back to the thing that had started all of this. The Big Heart Fungus. Still standing. Still anchoring the far end of the battlefield. Still the reason Zalthir was hovering above the fight instead of in it.


I committed the Dust of Suleiman and cast it directly onto the fungus. This was not a small resource. I made the decision anyway, because the creature had already demonstrated what it was willing to do to us and I had no interest in finding out what it would do next if left unaddressed.


Then Daz's shaped Fireball hit — Ilvara and the Zuggtmoy icon both, simultaneously — and the two effects overlapped in a way that exceeded what either spell would have done alone. The cavern went briefly and magnificently wrong in all the right ways.


"That worked better," I said, surveying the damage — servants staggered, Jorlan reeling, Ilvara absorbing punishment she hadn't budgeted for, fire and spore and disruption filling a space that had, ten minutes ago, been merely dangerous — "than I had any right to expect."


The fungus was still standing. The fight was far from over. But the battlefield had shifted in our favor, and I noted the specific combination of factors that had produced that outcome: bait the ego, trust the glyph, commit the resource, let Daz do what Daz does.


Bahamut may or may not have been watching. I took notes either way.


## Thorin — The Glyph Detonates
The Glyph was Grygum's idea, or at least Grygum's mouth. The placement was all of us. We'd laid it on the bridge like a welcome mat, and then the whole job was just: don't stand on it yourself, and wait.


Grygum called out. "Come get it, idiot."


I will say this for Jorlan: he committed. The drow didn't hesitate, didn't slow — he came across that bridge like a man who had already decided the outcome. You have to respect that, a little, even when the outcome is about to be wrong for him. There's something almost giant-brained about that kind of certainty. Giants move like that. Big, direct, total confidence in the thing they've already decided. The problem is, giants are usually right about the terrain.


Jorlan wasn't right about the terrain.


The Glyph fired.


Force and light erupted outward in a sphere, the kind of detonation that doesn't care who's in the way. Twenty-one damage blooming through the cluster all at once — through the spore servants he'd brought across with him, through Jorlan himself. One servant came apart completely. Just gone. The others staggered; I watched one barely hold together, listing like a wall with one stone pulled from its base. And Jorlan took the full force. He hadn't cleared it in time, hadn't been fast enough, hadn't seen it coming the way you can't see it coming when you're already running at what you think is your prize.


Grygum said, "Kaboom!" And then, with something like genuine surprise underneath it: "I didn't expect it to work."


That's the thing about a plan that comes together. You stop expecting it, almost. You get tactical, you do the work, you lay the trap in exactly the right place — and then somewhere between placing it and watching it detonate, you forget to believe in yourself. Or maybe you just don't want to be disappointed. I understood it. I felt the same flicker of it, the half-second of *oh. Oh, that worked.*


It worked.


I didn't stand there appreciating it. I was already closing on Jorlan. The explosion was still ringing through the cavern when Dawnbringer came down — crit, the blade's light cutting into him hard and clean, 14 damage landing exactly where it needed to. He'd taken the full force of the Glyph and now this. The second swing went wide; he shifted at the last moment and I carried past him. Doesn't matter. I pressed the Sap after it, using the momentum wrong to do something right — shoving him off-balance, leaving him on the back foot, disadvantage waiting for him the next time he tried to hit back.


One of the servants wasn't finished with me. Legendary action, a swing that went so wide it almost circled back around to being impressive — natural 1, nothing — and then the follow-up connected for 5. Glancing. A reminder.


Fair enough. I noted it. We weren't done.


## Daz — Concentrated Fire
The Dust of Suleiman lands and the battlefield reorganizes itself in my head.


This is the part I'm good at. Not the talking, not the diplomacy, not whatever Thorin does when he walks directly into the emotional centre of a conflict and somehow makes it worse and better simultaneously. This part. Reading the board. Identifying the highest-value targets. Calculating acceptable losses against projected return.


The priorities are clear: Ilvara, and the icon. In that order, or really in no particular order — they're the same problem wearing different faces. Asha was explicit enough about what's riding on this that I haven't been able to fully file it away the way I prefer to file things. It keeps surfacing. The stakes are not abstract. The stakes are Asha, and everything she told me, and the fact that a Zuggtmoy-aligned symbol of office left standing is not a symbol — it's a seed. You don't leave seeds.


So. Fireball. Cast at fourth level. Eight dice.


I have used Fireball the way some people use a favourite coat — comfortable, reliable, something I reach for when precision matters less than coverage. But coverage is not what I need. I need placement. Ilvara is elevated, which is poor positioning on her part and convenient positioning on mine. The icon is beside her. Both targets, one sphere, and the geometry cooperates if I'm exact.


Zalthir and Thorin are inside the problem zone.


This is what Sculpt Spells is for. I carve them out. The fire will know the shape of them by the time it arrives and it will go around — not because fire cares, fire doesn't care about anything, but because I told it the shape of what it cannot touch. It is perhaps the most useful thing I know how to do. Precision is not the opposite of force. It is force, directed.


The sphere lands where I placed it.


Ilvara is quick. She half-saves, which is professionally irritating but not unexpected — she did not survive this long in Menzoberranzan's social ecosystem by being slow. She takes twelve. The icon takes twelve. The fire roars around Zalthir and Thorin and doesn't touch them.


Both targets absorb the blast.


I have found purpose. I am the feared mage of the Ember Vanguard.


The irony is almost invisible, even to me.


Grygum's voice cuts through the settling heat: *"That worked better than I had any right to expect."*


It's an honest assessment, and I appreciate honesty in tactical partners. Two spells, two priority targets hit, the fight still live but the math changed in our favour. Not a perfect outcome. The icon is still standing. Ilvara is still standing. But twelve points is twelve points and the board looks different than it did thirty seconds ago, and that is the only metric that has ever mattered.


I note that Zalthir is unsinged. I note that Thorin is unsinged.


I don't say anything about it. It was the plan. Plans working is not remarkable.


But I notice.
# Chapter 46 Fungus Among Us


## Daz — The Spider's Blessing
The plan had three moving parts.


First: my familiar. A small spider, real enough, convincing enough if you don't look too hard at the absence of divine ichor. Second: Dancing Lights, shaped not into floating globes but into something grander — a silhouette, towering and feminine and terrible, the suggestion of eight eyes and infinite patience. Third: my nerve.


I've run more complicated cons with worse materials.


The spider scurried back across the fungal floor toward me on cue, and I was already weaving the lights around it — not frantically, not with the showy flick of wrists that amateur illusionists love, but with the quiet precision of someone who has thought this through to the fourth step. The luminescence built. Condensed. The shape of the Spider Queen herself, reduced and reduced and *reduced* until it shrank into that small skittering body and seemed to pass directly into mine. Then: darkness. The performance was seamless.


I know what I'm doing.


Behind me, somewhere in the fungal shadows, Glabbagool was doing what Glabbagool does. Which is to say: failing at the very simple task of being a rock.


I had given him clear instructions. Motionless. Silent. A feature of the cavern. And he had, apparently, decided that rocks sometimes needed to narrate their own invisibility, because he started *talking*. I heard the reminder that invisible rocks do not speak. I heard — I am fairly certain I heard — the small wet sound of him opening his eyes, which then began tracking left and right with the particular energy of someone who absolutely cannot help himself.


"Glabbagool," I said, without turning around, without breaking the posture of a man recently vacated by a goddess, "I'm taking care of this. It's fine."


It was fine. It had to be fine.


Asha Vandry was watching me with those wide, fractured eyes — the look of someone who has spent so long in paranoid devotion that suspicion has become its own kind of faith. The spectacle had landed. I could see that. What I could not yet determine was exactly *which* way it had landed.


She spoke.


"You're a wizard. A wizard… a wizard who prays to Lolth?"


Not awe. Suspicion, clean and immediate. The question of someone who has been deceived before and has filed the memory carefully. I felt, for a fraction of a second, the specific sensation of a gamble that could go either way.


I leaned in. Not physically — just into the role, into the space the performance had opened.


"I am… you are not speaking to the wizard of this body. I… he… this body has communed with Lolth. And I… I am speaking through this body."


Conviction carries what evidence cannot, if you commit to it fully enough. I committed.


Then she surprised me.


"Aha," Asha said, and her voice had the bright, brittle quality of someone who has just solved a puzzle, "you are trying to test me, to see if I was one of those fake followers of Lolth, who are willing to believe every charlatan magic user that is somehow being possessed by the power of Lolth."


I took a moment to process that.


She had not seen through the deception. She had reframed it entirely — had taken my con and reclassified it as a *divine test of her discernment*, which she believed she had now passed. The paranoia hadn't broken my gambit. It had built her a completely different story in which she was the clever one.


There are players who don't know they're at the table. There are players who think they're winning. And then there is Asha Vandry, who had somehow managed to be both at once.


I recovered. This is what you do. You don't argue with the story someone has already decided to believe — you find the thread that connects their version to yours and you pull it.
